# Decision log — running paper trail

> **Purpose.** An append-only, chronological record of every **decision / issue / bug / fix / pivot** so that a future session (after auto-compact or a premature end) can reconstruct *what was decided and why* without re-deriving it from faded context. This file exists because on 2026-05-30 the assistant recommended re-opening an **already-settled** decision (build v0.2 vs. a v0.1.3 patch-sweep) — reasoning from in-context memory instead of the durable record. The user: *"we will not have this problem again that you decide something against an already decision line we are already into."*
>
> **Binding usage (see CLAUDE.md "Decision-log discipline"):**
> 1. **Before re-opening ANY decision** — search this file + [`v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md`](v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md) + tasks.md for it. If it's here marked **SETTLED**, do not re-litigate it; execute it. Surface a change only if you have *new* evidence, and say explicitly "this revisits SETTLED decision D-N because <new evidence>".
> 2. **After making/learning anything durable** — append an entry in the SAME batch as the work. Decisions, issues found, bugs, fixes, design choices, pivots. Newest block at the TOP.
> 3. Entry types: **DECISION** (a choice + why), **PIVOT** (a previously-documented choice changed — preserve the old per decision-trail rule), **ISSUE** (a problem noted, maybe not yet fixed), **BUG**, **FIX**, **NOTE**.
> 4. This is the running paper trail. Stable rules still graduate to CLAUDE.md; task state still lives in tasks.md; per-PR narrative still goes to the build log. This file is the chronological spine that ties them together.

---

## 2026-07-07 — D-289: Task 192 shipped — the Stop-hook JUDGE closes the learn-loop's Phase 1 (ADR-0017 1c); v0.5.0's headline is CODE-COMPLETE

- **✅ BUILD (TDD, 14 tests):** `judge-signals.mjs` — the full oracle-free passive-signal portfolio as FOUR deterministic detectors (no LLM, no new spawn, no ritual): **tool-result ±** (turn-tools now exposes `extractTurnToolCalls` with the JSONL `is_error` flag — one parse, two consumers; failures DAMPEN, an all-success tool turn weakly REINFORCES — attributed to the turn window's SEARCHED ids from the 190 recall-log, deliberately NOT the whole inject snapshot: a fact the model never engaged with shouldn't eat a tool failure); **user-correction −** (start-anchored patterns on the prompt hook — a mid-sentence "no" is not a correction; revert-phrasing = REVERSAL, the strongest single-user causal signal); **re-ask −** (a search returning ONLY already-injected ids = the injection failed the model; **polarity per D-246, pinned by test: a re-surfacing fact is DAMPEN, never reinforcement**); **silent-success weak-+** (a pending expectation surviving TURN_WINDOW_MS with nothing fired resolves WEAK-POSITIVE — a nudge, never a replication, per 191's evidence rules). Attribution joins by TIMESTAMP window, not session id (production search entries carry session:null — the 190 design note, honored).
- **The loop is CLOSED through the guardrails:** every delta routes through `applyTrustSignal` = the 193 FEEDBACK-SCREEN (rate-limited, burst-held, audited) — a misfiring detector cannot mass-dampen; expectations resolve through 191's B2-guarded `resolveExpectation` (no replication inflation). 190→193→191→192: all four organs shipped in sequence, each inheriting the prior's protections.
- **Wires (the automatic path, pinned by tests):** `captureTurn` runs `judgeTurn` on the SAME JSONL tail read 104.1 already does (zero extra I/O); `capturePrompt` runs `judgeUserPrompt` on the sanitized prompt. Both best-effort — the judge can never break capture.
- **⚠️ HONESTY FLAG (D-84):** the done-when's "live-tested on a real session" is NOT claimed — the hook wires are unit-driven (real captureTurn/capturePrompt calls, stubbed spawn). The v0.5.0 cut-gate's live half must drive a REAL session (a genuine tool failure + a genuine correction) and check `.locks/trust-signals.log` for the deltas. Flagged in the tasks.md entry. _Relates ADR-0017 (Decision #2), D-246 (the polarity rule, now pinned in code), D-286/287/288 (Phases 1a/1d/1b), the 2026-07-01 failure-learning survey (the portfolio). D-289._

## 2026-07-07 — D-288: Task 191 shipped — expectation pre-registration + judgment_*.md (ADR-0017 Phase 1b); the earned-judgment wedge is real

- **✅ BUILD (TDD, 12 tests):** two modules + one wire. **judgment.mjs** — `writeJudgment` routes through the writeFact SAFE PATH (Poison_Guard screened a planted secret in the test; INDEX + audit ride along): `VALID_TYPES` gains **'judgment'**, a LOOP-BORN type the remember/mk_remember dictation enums deliberately exclude (a judgment must be EARNED, not asserted); the filename convention `${type}_${slug}.md` gives the study's `judgment_<slug>.md` for free. Frontmatter = the study schema verbatim (claim/baseline/prefer/over/status/n_episodes/direction_consistent/confounds/outcome_horizon/decays_after) + **decays_after maps onto 66.1's `expires_at`** so a decayed judgment hides from search with ZERO new plumbing. `appendJudgmentEvidence` implements the nudge-vs-lock asymmetry: HIT bumps n_episodes (corroborated only at >=3 consistent), **MISS/REVERSAL set direction_consistent:false — a STICKY lock later HITs cannot undo**; WEAK-POSITIVE appends evidence only (silent success is a nudge, never a replication). **Cycle detection** (A>B,B>C,C>A) marks EVERY judgment on the cycle contested — surfaced, never auto-picked. **expectations.mjs** — `PREDICTION: <text>` scan with the vague-doesn't-count gate (>=4 words), event-sourced pending log at `context/.locks/expectations.log` (the EIGHTH NDJSON log — design table updated), `resolveExpectation` appends the resolution + optionally routes it into a judgment's evidence (the earn step). **The wire:** `captureTurn` calls `capturePredictions` on the SANITIZED turn (privacy first) — automatic, no new spawn, no cmk command, M8-gated (never scaffolds a non-kit project).
- **Honest split with 192:** 191 ships capture-automatic + the resolution PRIMITIVES; the resolution AUTOMATION (detectors deciding HIT/MISS from next-turn signals) is Task 192's wire — per 191's own done-when text. _Relates ADR-0017 (Decision #1), the 2026-07-01 comparative-judgment study (schema adopted verbatim), D-286/D-287 (Phases 1a/1d, same push), Task 192 (the judge that closes the loop). D-288._

## 2026-07-06 — D-287: Task 193 FEEDBACK-SCREEN shipped (ADR-0017 Phase 1d) — the loop's Poison_Guard; trust mutations are now rate-limited, burst-held, and audit-logged

- **✅ BUILD (TDD, same-evening as 190):** the screen lives INSIDE `applyTrustSignal` (`trust-signal.mjs`) — the verified single trust_score mutation gate (4 callers, zero bypass writers) — so every present AND future signal (Task 192's judge) inherits it. New module `feedback-screen.mjs`: `screenSignal` (pure verdict over today's `context/.locks/trust-signals.log` entries) + `logSignal` + `readSignalLog`; exported constants `RATE_LIMIT_PER_FACT_PER_DAY=5`, `BURST_MIN_SIGNALS=10`, `BURST_NEGATIVE_FRACTION=0.8`.
- **The three rules:** (1) rate-limit — max 5 APPLIED deltas per fact per UTC day (refusals don't consume budget, so a storm can't freeze a fact forever); (2) burst-hold — ≥10 same-day applied signals with >80% dampens → further DAMPENS quarantined (`applied:false, reason:'burst-hold'`), reinforces pass (positives aren't the attack surface; A-MemGuard set-level-defense precedent); (3) every applied Δ ALSO lands in the canonical audit.log (`action:'trust-signal'`, tier/id/reasonCode per schema) in an ISOLATED try/catch — a post-apply bookkeeping failure must not make the outer catch falsely report `skipped` after the UPDATE ran (a real hazard caught during the build: `appendAuditEntry` THROWS on missing fields).
- **Caller-map executed:** the 3 shared-db call sites (conflict-queue ×2, merge-facts ×2, validity-window ×1) passed `db` WITHOUT `projectRoot` — they all HAD it in scope (they open `sigDb` with it); now they pass both, so the screen sees state on every production path. FAIL-OPEN posture: no `context/`/unreadable state → the signal applies unscreened (the pre-193 contract, preserved — a broken diagnostic never breaks the primary write).
- **POSTURE DECISION (skill-review I1 — recorded, not deferred):** all 7 production emitters today send `dampen` (no production `reinforce` until 192's judge), so burst-hold currently = a daily dampen THROTTLE (>=10 applied/day, rest quarantined till UTC midnight) rather than a fraction-anomaly detector. ACCEPTED as fail-PROTECTIVE: a legit bulk day loses late-day dampen signal, but no memory is wrongly dampened (the failure mode the screen exists to prevent); the first-N prospective leak (~10 dampens apply before the gate closes, each fact capped at 5 by the rate limit) is named and accepted. Both constants revisit at Task 192 when reinforces make the fraction meaningful. All other findings fixed in-branch: budget-registry entries + under-threshold/boundary tests (I2), JSDoc contract (I3), null-line filter (M4), audit tier comment + REASON_CODES registration (M6), unknown-event inert guard (M7), no-scaffold gate on BOTH bookkeeping writers incl. appendAuditEntry — which mkdirs .locks and was the hidden scaffolder the fail-open test caught (M8).
- **Tests:** 8→12 (five doors; the burst-storm over-mutation scenario — 10 distinct-fact dampens, then a dampen against a GOOD memory is quarantined with its score untouched; per-fact isolation; floor-through-screen; projectRoot-only composition; fail-open). One test-fixture bug fixed during RED→GREEN (the composition test seeded a custom dbPath the internal open can't see — test setup fixed, not the code). Touched suites 129/129; full suite exit 0. Docs walked proactively (the 190 skill-review lesson): design §"seven log files" table row + §16.13 rotation scope + §20.2 "screened" bullet, SYSTEM-MAP Phase-1d marked shipped, CHANGELOG, tasks.md. _Relates ADR-0017 (Decision #4 — "a prerequisite, not an option"), D-286 (Phase 1a the same evening), Task 192 (the judge this pre-screens), NFR-9. D-287._

## 2026-07-06 — D-285: LIVE INTERACTIVE re-test (the user drove real `kiro-cli chat`) OVERTURNS part of D-284 + finds the MCP-prompt root cause — automatic CAPTURE does NOT need the global default; the global default buys PROMPT-FREE, not memory-at-all

- **⚠️ D-284 PARTIALLY OVERTURNED (by the user's insistence on a real interactive run — my headless `--no-interactive` tests hid the truth).** D-284 concluded "automatic memory needs the global `chat.defaultAgent`." **A live interactive re-test (clean folder `C:\Temp\kiro-retest-clean`, global default CLEARED, global cmk REMOVED, `kiro_default` the active agent) proved that WRONG for capture:** the user typed a preference, and the project-level **`.kiro/hooks/cmk-capture.json` (trigger `Stop`, `cmd.exe /c cmk hook stop`) FIRED** (the cmd popup) → `now.md` written with the real turn, the extract child ran. **The project `.kiro/hooks/` IDE-style hooks fire on kiro-cli REGARDLESS of the active agent** — because they're PROJECT-scoped (`.kiro/hooks/`), not agent-config-scoped. So a user WITHOUT the global default still gets automatic capture. The corrected, tested split:
  - **project `.kiro/hooks/` (capture/inject)** → fire on ANY agent (kiro_default included) ✅ — automatic, no global default needed.
  - **project `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` (MCP tool availability)** → any agent ✅ (kiro_default offered `mk_remember`).
  - **project `.kiro/steering/` + skills** → any agent ✅.
  - **agent-config hooks (inside `~/.kiro/agents/cmk.json`)** → only if cmk active (needs the default). REDUNDANT with the project hooks for capture/inject — the project hooks are the load-bearing ones on kiro-cli.
  - **MCP tool AUTO-APPROVE (prompt-free)** → needs cmk active (agent trust). ❌ on kiro_default (see below).
  - **NET: the global default buys PROMPT-FREE + full automation; it is NOT required for memory to WORK.** A no-global-default user gets automatic capture + working saves, with a one-time approval click on explicit MCP saves. This is a MUCH more favorable Kiro-cli story than D-283/D-284 told, and it means the global default could be OPTIONAL/opt-in rather than always-set (a real design consideration — parked, not decided).
- **🐛 THE MCP-PROMPT ROOT CAUSE (the user's pic-2 catch: "didn't we make it not ask?") — FOUND, and it advances the parked Task 165(a).** On the `kiro_default` session, `mk_remember` popped "requires approval" despite the kit's D-196 auto-approve work. Root cause (code + live confirmed): the cmk agent ships **`includeMcpJson: false` and NO `allowedTools`** (a deliberate D-198 choice — when cmk is active the model uses the pre-trusted `cmk` SHELL commands, never MCP). But `kiro_default` (active here, since no global default) DOES load the project `mcp.json` (with its 11-tool `autoApprove`), so the model reached for `mk_remember` (MCP) — and kiro-cli does NOT honor `mcp.json`'s `autoApprove` for trust (that's the IDE-only mechanism). So the prompt is the MECHANISM SPLIT (shell-trust-for-cmk-agent vs MCP-autoApprove-for-IDE), not a wrong format. The kit optimized the cmk-agent-active path and left the any-other-agent-but-MCP-still-loads path prompting. **Filed into Task 165(a)** (the pre-existing parked D-196 follow-up) with the new root cause + revised done-options + a v0.4.6 lane (root cause found → graduates from "diagnose" to "fix or document"). The fact still SAVED (`P-2Y9KMMVK`, Black-only pref) after the user's one approval click — so it's a friction bug, not a data-loss bug.
- **META (the honesty lesson, on ME):** I stated the "needs global default" conclusion THREE times from headless approximations; the user corrected it by running the real interactive session and reading the cmd popup + the on-disk `now.md`. Headless `--no-interactive` blocks tool approval AND doesn't exercise the interactive hook path the same way — it is NOT a valid proxy for "does automatic memory work in a real kiro-cli session." The D-84 live-test rule, applied to MY OWN test method: a headless probe of an interactive surface is unit-green-≠-works-on-real-input one level up. _Relates D-283/D-284 (the conclusion this corrects — project hooks fire on any agent; global default = prompt-free not memory-enabling), D-196 (the auto-approve mechanism split this explains), Task 165(a) (the parked follow-up this advances with the root cause), the D-84 live-test rule (applied to my headless method). D-285._

## 2026-07-06 — D-284: EMPIRICAL TEST RUN + COMPLETE — "can the Kiro CLI agent work project-local like Claude Code?" → **NO.** Local agents do NOT auto-activate; the global `chat.defaultAgent` is REQUIRED for automatic memory. D-283 experimentally CONFIRMED.

- **RESULT (every combination tested live on kiro-cli 2.10.0, sentinel-hook-on-disk methodology; system fully restored after):** dropping a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` in a repo does **NOT** make it active — kiro-cli falls back to the built-in `kiro_default` and the agent's hooks never fire. **∴ Kiro CANNOT work like Claude Code** (where a project file "just works"); automatic memory REQUIRES the global `chat.defaultAgent: cmk` (or a manual `--agent cmk` every session). The current kit design (global agent + global default) is VINDICATED by experiment, not just docs.
- **THE MATRIX (⭐ = the key case):**
  - **⭐ Case A** — no global default, local cmk only, no flag → resolved `* kiro_default`, probe **EMPTY**. **Local does NOT auto-activate.** THE answer.
  - **Case B** — no default, local cmk, `--agent cmk` → LOCAL fired. Explicit flag activates a local agent (no global default needed).
  - **Case C** (control) — no default, no cmk, no flag → kiro_default, EMPTY. Baseline.
  - **Case D** — default=cmk, BOTH local+global cmk → **LOCAL won** (`WARNING: Agent conflict for cmk. Using workspace version.`). Precedence-local-wins CONFIRMED — but only because the name already resolved to `cmk` via the global default.
  - **Case E** — default=foreign agent, local cmk present → FOREIGN fired (local ignored). **E2** — default=a named global agent, local cmk present → that GLOBAL fired. Local only wins when the RESOLVED NAME matches a local agent.
  - **Case F** — `--agent foreigntest` → FOREIGN fired. Flag beats default beats everything.
  - **Case G** — default=cmk, global cmk only (today's kit shape) → GLOBAL fired. ✅ what ships.
  - **⭐ Case H** — Case A repeated INTERACTIVELY (piped, not `--no-interactive`) → `kiro_default`, EMPTY. **The negative result holds interactively too** (headless≠interactive was a real risk; here they agree).
  - **Case I** (bonus) — a BOM'd local cmk → `Error: Json ... invalid: expected value at line 1 column 1`, kiro-cli REJECTED it and fell to global. **D-187 CONFIRMED empirically**: kiro-cli's JSON reader is NOT BOM-tolerant — if the kit ever writes a project-local agent it must be BOM-free.
- **MECHANISM (now proven, not inferred):** kiro-cli resolves the active agent from `chat.defaultAgent` (global-only setting) or `--agent`; a name that resolves to `cmk` THEN prefers a local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` over the global one ("workspace version", with a warning). So local precedence is real but DOWNSTREAM of a global/flag activation — merely having the file activates nothing.
- **DECISION IMPACT — the D-283 "open follow-up" is NARROWER than hoped, but still valid:** the kit COULD write the agent FILE project-local (it'd win precedence per Case D) WHILE keeping the global `chat.defaultAgent: cmk` — giving repo-scoped, git-committable agent definitions that match the other surfaces. BUT: (a) the global default is STILL required (no Claude-Code-style zero-global-footprint), so it's a smaller win than "make it like Claude Code"; (b) a global default naming `cmk` would then WARN/fall-through in any project WITHOUT a local cmk copy — so the kit would still need a global cmk as fallback, meaning BOTH files, not fewer. Net: moving the file local ADDS a per-project file without removing the global one — arguably MORE footprint, not less. **Recommendation: KEEP the current global-only agent** (simplest, one file, works everywhere); the project-local-file idea is not worth the added complexity given it can't remove the global default. Re-open only if a user needs a per-project DIFFERENT memory agent. This CLOSES the D-283 open follow-up as "considered + rejected on the evidence."
- **STATUS: test COMPLETE, system RESTORED** (real `chat.defaultAgent: cmk` + real `cmk.json` back; test sentinel agents removed; test dir cleaned). The real user-tier restore from `20_v0.4.5_gate` is STILL PENDING (separate from this — see below). D-284.

### (original resume-point block, kept for the decision trail — the test was designed here, then run above)

- **STATUS (pre-run): test harness BUILT, NOT YET RUN.** The user asked to test every combination of Kiro agent activation, then paused to drive home. Nothing on the system was mutated — the global `chat.defaultAgent: cmk` was UNTOUCHED (backed up, never changed).
- **THE QUESTION the test answers (the one thing the Kiro docs do NOT state, verified by reading every relevant page directly 2026-07-06):** when `kiro-cli` launches in a directory containing a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` but **`chat.defaultAgent` is UNSET (or names another agent)** — does kiro-cli **auto-activate the project-local agent** (→ hooks fire → we CAN work like Claude Code, repo-scoped, zero global footprint), or fall back to the built-in `kiro_default` (→ a global default is REQUIRED for automatic memory → current design forced)? Docs are silent; only an experiment decides.
- **DOC FACTS ESTABLISHED (read the actual pages, not sub-agent summaries):** hooks live ONLY inside an agent config — no project-level hook file exists (`/docs/cli/hooks/` + config-reference `#hooks-field`; events: agentSpawn/userPromptSubmit/preToolUse/postToolUse/stop; fields: `command` required, `matcher` optional). Agents live at `.kiro/agents/` (local, via `--directory workspace`) OR `~/.kiro/agents/` (global); **local WINS precedence over same-named global "with a warning"** (config-reference "Agent precedence", verbatim). Activation = `--agent` flag | `/agent swap` | global `chat.defaultAgent` (global-only setting) | default `kiro_default`. Headless `kiro-cli chat --no-interactive` fires hooks + works on the user's SUBSCRIPTION (no API key — user live-proved it; the earlier sub-agent claim that headless "requires KIRO_API_KEY" is CONTRADICTED by the user's real run, `▸ Credits: 0.04`). NOTE `timeout_ms`/`cache_ttl_seconds` appear in the examples page but the config-reference omits them — verify they're honored if used.
- **THE TEST MATRIX (run each as a real `kiro-cli chat --no-interactive` FROM the test project dir; the sentinel = an `agentSpawn` hook that appends a unique string to a probe file, so "did it fire + WHICH agent" is unambiguous ON DISK):**
  - **Harness already built at `C:/Temp/kiro-agent-activation-test/`**: a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` whose agentSpawn hook runs `cmd.exe /c echo LOCAL_AGENT_HOOK_FIRED >> "C:\Temp\kiro-agent-activation-test\probe.log"` (valid JSON verified; probe.log empty). Extend with a GLOBAL sentinel agent writing `GLOBAL_AGENT_HOOK_FIRED` to tell precedence apart.
  - **Case A (THE KEY CASE):** global default UNSET, project-local cmk present, NO `--agent` → run headless in the dir → probe shows LOCAL_FIRED? ⇒ project-local auto-activates ⇒ **YES, Claude-Code-like is possible.**
  - **Case B:** global unset, local present, `--agent cmk` → does explicit selection of a LOCAL agent work?
  - **Case C (control):** global unset, local ABSENT, no flag → expect kiro_default, NO sentinel (baseline).
  - **Case D:** global default = cmk (global copy present) + local copy present, no flag → which sentinel fires? (precedence + the "warning" — does local win as the config-ref claims?).
  - **Case E:** global default = a FOREIGN agent, local cmk present, no flag → does the foreign global default block the local agent, or does local override?
  - **Extra combos to cover "every combination" (the user's ask):** (F) local present + global cmk present but `--agent <foreign>` (flag beats default?); (G) `/agent swap cmk` mid-session interactive; (H) INTERACTIVE (not headless) Case A — headless≠interactive proven already (the user's `fs_write`-rejected-in-non-interactive run); (I) local agent with a BOM (D-187: kiro-cli's reader is NOT BOM-tolerant — does a BOM'd local agent silently fail to load?); (J) local + global BOTH named cmk but DIFFERENT hook sentinels → confirm the "warning" text + which wins.
- **SAFETY / RESTORE (all backed up, restore at the very end):** global default+agent snapshots at `C:/cut-gate-backups/21_v0.4.5_kiro/*.pretest-backup`; real user tier at `C:/cut-gate-backups/20_v0.4.5_gate/`; real `~/.kiro` at `21_v0.4.5_kiro/`. The test mutates `~/.kiro/settings/cli.json` (default-agent) + adds a global sentinel agent — RESTORE both after. **The real user-tier restore from `20_v0.4.5_gate` is STILL PENDING** (do NOT forget — the user's real cross-project memory lives only there now; `~/.claude-memory-kit` is currently the moved-aside claude-gate test output at `C:/cut-gate-backups/claude-gate-testoutput_2026-07-06`).
- **DECISION IMPACT:** if Case A fires LOCAL ⇒ file a real task to move the kit's kiro-cli agent project-local (the D-283 "open follow-up") — repo-scoped, matches every other surface, no global footprint. If Case A does NOT fire ⇒ D-283's "activation is necessarily global" is EXPERIMENTALLY confirmed (not just docs-reasoned), and the design is vindicated. Either way, replace D-283's docs-only reasoning with the tested result. D-284.

## 2026-07-06 — D-283: the Kiro CLI agent ACTIVATION is global (~/.kiro `chat.defaultAgent`) — SETTLED, now EXPERIMENTALLY confirmed by D-284 (the agent-file-project-local idea was considered + rejected on the evidence)

- **DECISION (SETTLED) — the kiro-cli agent-config stays GLOBAL; this is correct, not the design-inconsistency it appears to be.** During the v0.4.5 Kiro cut-gate the user asked why the kit writes `~/.kiro/agents/cmk.json` (user-global) when every OTHER Kiro surface (mcp.json, steering, IDE hooks, skills, AGENTS.md) — and every Claude Code surface — is PROJECT-local; their expectation (reasonable) was per-project like Claude Code. **Investigated against the PRIMARY docs (kiro.dev/docs/cli/…) before touching code — and the global path is FORCED by a hard Kiro constraint the other agents don't have:**
  - kiro-cli DOES support a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` (kiro.dev/docs/cli/custom-agents/creating — `--directory workspace` saves to `.kiro/agents/` in the cwd; default with no `--directory` is global `~/.kiro/agents/`) — so project-local *looks* cleaner. BUT: the **`chat.defaultAgent` SETTING is global-only.** kiro.dev/docs/cli/chat/configuration's scope table (READ DIRECTLY 2026-07-06) lists **`Settings | User: Yes | Project: N/A | Agent: N/A`** — i.e. Settings exist at global/user scope only, with no project or agent scope. There is NO project-local default-agent.
  - **Precedence IS documented** (kiro.dev/docs/cli/custom-agents/configuration-reference, "File locations" / "Agent precedence", READ DIRECTLY 2026-07-06): "1. Local first: Checks `.kiro/agents/` in the current directory. 2. Global fallback: Checks `~/.kiro/agents/`. If both locations have agents with the same name, **the local agent takes precedence with a warning message.**" So a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` WOULD win over the global one.
  - **BUT a local agent does NOT auto-activate by merely existing.** Same page: local agents are "only available when running Kiro CLI from that directory" — that is DISCOVERABILITY/selectability, not activation. The page has NO statement that a local agent becomes the workspace default on its own. Activation still requires either the global `chat.defaultAgent` OR an explicit `--agent cmk` / `/agent swap`.
  - Automatic memory = the agent's `hooks{}` firing every INTERACTIVE session with no per-session flag = `cmk` must be the ACTIVE agent = (since local-file-alone doesn't activate, and users don't pass `--agent`) a **global `chat.defaultAgent: cmk`**. That default is global-only (scope table above). **∴ activation is necessarily global.** The agent FILE could be local (it'd win precedence) — but a local-only file leaves the global default dangling in projects without a copy, so the kit writes the agent globally too. The clean-but-heavier alternative (global default + a per-project local agent file that wins precedence, matching the other surfaces) is a REAL open option — see the OPEN FOLLOW-UP below; it was NOT adopted for v0.4.5, but it is not refuted by the docs.
- **What about HEADLESS mode? (checked — doesn't rescue the surface.)** kiro.dev/docs/cli/reference/cli-commands confirms `kiro-cli chat --no-interactive [INPUT]` (one-shot, print-to-STDOUT) AND a per-invocation `--agent <name>` flag that selects an agent INDEPENDENT of the global default. So headless CAN pick a project-local agent per call. But this splits into two cases and only helps the one that doesn't need it: (a) **the kit's automatic ENGINE** (the v0.4.5 backend's compression/auto-extract LLM call) ALREADY uses `kiro-cli chat --no-interactive` — and deliberately passes **NO `--agent`** (0 occurrences in `kiro-backend.mjs`), using the built-in `kiro_default` as a plain LLM; it doesn't want the cmk memory agent, so headless-`--agent` is irrelevant here. (b) **the user-facing memory SURFACE** (inject/capture via the agent's `hooks{}`) needs cmk to be the ACTIVE agent in the user's **INTERACTIVE** session — and users chat interactively, not headless one-shot. `--no-interactive` is a scripting mode, not where capture happens. So headless `--agent` gives per-project selection only for the backend (which the kit already drives with its own argv, agent-less) and NOT for the interactive surface (which still needs the global default). Conclusion stands.
- **Was this changed in v0.4.5? NO** — git-proven: v0.4.5 (Tasks 200/201/202) never touched `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` / `install-kiro.mjs`. **Was it always global? YES** — since Task 50 (D-198 moved it from the WRONG `~/.aws/amazonq/` to the right `~/.kiro/agents/`, keeping it global). D-198 had the reason but never spelled out the settings-are-global-only constraint, so it kept reading as a bug.
- **Cursor checked for the same class — CLEAN.** The Cursor installer writes ONLY project-relative surfaces (`.cursor/hooks.json`, `.cursor/rules/*.mdc`, `.cursor/mcp.json`); no homedir/global write. The global-agent issue is **Kiro-only** (its Amazon-Q lineage + the global-settings constraint), not a cross-agent pattern.
- **ACTION for v0.4.5: documentation-only, NO code change.** The ACTIVATION being global is forced (verified above); v0.4.5 ships the current behavior (global agent file + global default) with a primary-source-cited comment in `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` so it stops reading as a bug. The default-agent write remains GUARDED (a user's foreign existing default is never clobbered → `skipped-existing`).
- **OPEN FOLLOW-UP (a real option the docs do NOT refute — surfaced by the user's persistent "check the docs" 2026-07-06): move the agent FILE project-local while keeping the global default.** Because a project-local `.kiro/agents/cmk.json` WINS precedence (verified), the kit COULD write the agent definition into each installed project's `.kiro/agents/` (travels with the repo, git-committable, matches every other Kiro surface) AND still set the global `chat.defaultAgent: cmk` for activation. Trade-off to resolve: the global default would then "dangle" (warn/fall-back) in projects WITHOUT a local cmk agent — so the kit likely still needs a global fallback agent, OR accepts the warning in non-installed projects. This is a genuine design question, NOT settled; needs its own task (design + tests + the backup/restore + uninstall implications + gate-guide updates). Trigger: file as a v0.4.x/v0.5 task. **This entry is NOT "do-not-reopen" — the ACTIVATION-is-global fact is settled; the agent-FILE-location is an open improvement.**
- _Relates D-198 (the location root-cause this completes with the WHY), the "check the primary source before implementing/concluding" rule — the user's repeated "did you check the docs?" caught (a) my wrong convergent-evidence claim that kiro-cli agents are user-tier-only (they are NOT — local + global, local wins), and (b) my own flip-flop where I deleted the verified precedence rule as "unverified" because I'd read the CREATING page not the CONFIGURATION-REFERENCE page. Lesson re-underlined: read the SPECIFIC primary page yourself, don't trust a sub-agent's summary of a nearby page. D-283._

## 2026-07-06 — D-280: the code-review-excellence pass CAUGHT a DON'T-MERGE bug — the Kiro D-279 prompt fix only worked for a TOY prompt; against the REAL compression prompt kiro still refused. Fix: all three backends pipe the prompt on STDIN.

- **🐛 BUG (DON'T-MERGE) + 🔧 FIX (2026-07-06) — D-280: the Task-200 pre-PR code-review-excellence pass, probing cross-cutting concern (f) "do the three backends' prompt shapes all work against the SAME real callers?", caught that the D-279 Kiro fix was INSUFFICIENT — verified only against a TOY one-line prompt, not the REAL `buildCompressionInstructions` (a multi-paragraph instruction block + a delimited session buffer). Against the real prompt, kiro-cli with the D-279 colon-join positional STILL REFUSED: "I don't see a session buffer in your message to compress. Could you provide it?" — i.e. the shipped KiroCliBackend would have written REFUSALS-as-memory into every Kiro user's store. The parametric harness's reject-gate would have caught it at live-test time, but the backend itself was broken for the real workload. This is the "unit-green ≠ works-on-real-INPUT" class one level deeper: I live-tested with real INVOCATION but a FAKE (toy) prompt; the real prompt is part of the input.** **The fix (live-verified against the real prompt): pipe the prompt on STDIN, no positional arg** — the SAME channel the claude + cursor backends already use. Piping on stdin makes kiro-cli DO the task and read the delimited buffer correctly (`## Decisions` / `## Active Threads`, no refusal). So the D-279 colon-join is REPLACED (decision-trail: D-279 was a band-aid that only worked for toys; D-280 is the real fix) by the plain two-line `instructions\n\ninput` form delivered via stdin — now UNIFORM across all three backends (claude: stdin two-line; cursor: stdin two-line; kiro: stdin two-line). **Also verified (the "did you check?" rule applied to my own earlier live-tests): the CURSOR backend against the REAL multi-paragraph prompt** — it already used stdin, so it was fine (confirmed: correct summary, no refusal), but I had only toy-tested it too. **The meta-lesson:** a backend live-test MUST use the REAL production prompt (`buildCompressionInstructions` / `buildClassifierInstructions` / `buildJudgeInstructions`), not a hand-written toy — the prompt shape IS part of the input the D-84 rule covers. _Relates D-279 (superseded — the toy-verified band-aid), D-278 (the cursor stdin fix this generalizes), D-84 (unit-green ≠ real-input, applied to the PROMPT), the code-review-excellence two-pass discipline (skill-review caught what self-review + the toy live-test missed — the exact value the second pass exists for). D-280._

## 2026-07-06 — D-279: the agent-parametric backend live-test CAUGHT a real shipped bug — KiroCliBackend has the SAME prompt-shape failure D-278 fixed for Cursor (built earlier, missed the fix)

- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-07-06) — D-279: the new `scripts/live-test-backend.mjs` (agent-parametric — the D-84-gap-closer that runs the kit's REAL backend selection on whatever agent resolves) did EXACTLY its job on its first run: forcing `--agent kiro` surfaced that `kiro-cli chat`, given the KiroCliBackend's `instructions\n\ninput` prompt, REFUSES the task — it replied "I don't have access to any stored durable preferences… could you clarify?" instead of summarizing. This is the SAME prompt-shape failure mode D-278 caught + fixed for Cursor (the two-line form reads as a "workspace question"; the model second-guesses instead of doing the task — the research's "reject-gate" class, D-275). The KiroCliBackend shipped BEFORE this research, so it never got the fix. A live single-line-directive probe CONFIRMED the fix direction: `kiro-cli chat … "Summarize this durable preference in one short sentence, reply with only the sentence: <text>"` returns a correct summary (0.01cr, ~1s).** Two fixes:
  - **KiroCliBackend prompt shape:** join instructions + input as a SINGLE directive line (the D-278 discipline), not two newline-separated blocks. (Kiro takes the prompt as a positional, not stdin like Cursor — but the SHAPE is the fix, not the channel.)
  - **The harness's own weakness (honest):** `live-test-backend.mjs` reported "LIVE OK" on the kiro refusal because it only checked the output was NON-EMPTY — a refusal ("I don't have access… could you clarify?") is non-empty. That's the harness masking the exact failure it exists to catch. Strengthen it: detect refusal/clarification phrasing ("I don't have access", "could you clarify", "I cannot", "please provide") and FAIL on it — the "reject-gate" the research named (claude-remember's `_is_non_summary`), now applied to the kit's own live-test AND worth adding to the backends' result-handling as a follow-up.
  - **Why this matters (the meta-point):** this is the whole thesis of agent-parametric testing, proven on its first run — the OLD `live-test.mjs` (hardcoded `claude` driver) would NEVER have surfaced this, because it never exercises kiro/cursor as the backend. D-270's invisibility class, caught by the harness built to catch it. _Relates D-278 (the Cursor fix this ports to Kiro), D-275 (the reject-gate field pattern), D-270/D-84 (the invisibility class the parametric harness closes), Task 200 (the backend build). D-279._

## 2026-07-05 — D-278: CursorAgentBackend BUILT + LIVE-VERIFIED end-to-end — the live-test caught two real bugs green units couldn't (prompt-via-stdin, and cursor-agent is SLOW: 30–83s)

- **✅ BUILD + 🔬 LIVE-VERIFY (2026-07-05) — D-278: `CursorAgentBackend` ([`cursor-backend.mjs`](../packages/cli/src/cursor-backend.mjs)) built TDD (test-first, 7 tests, RED→GREEN) mirroring `KiroCliBackend`, then LIVE-VERIFIED through the real `cursor-agent` on the user's Windows machine (off their Cursor SUBSCRIPTION, NO API key): a real compression call returned a correct one-sentence summary, exit 0, ~31s. The live-test caught TWO real bugs the 7 green unit tests structurally could NOT — the D-84 "unit-green ≠ works-on-real-input" lesson, fired exactly as designed.**
  - **BUG 1 (prompt shape) — the multi-line positional read as a "workspace question."** The first draft passed `instructions\n\ninput` as cursor-agent's trailing `[prompt]` positional (mirroring the kiro backend). Live, the model IGNORED the task and replied *"There's nothing in this workspace to summarize yet — what should I summarize? Paste the text…"* — it treated the first line as a chat question, not a directive. **Fix: pipe the prompt on STDIN** (like the claude backend does — `child.stdin.write(promptBody)` then `.end()`), which (a) makes the model DO the task (live-confirmed: correct summary), and (b) dodges the newline/quoting hazard of a multi-line positional through spawnBin's Windows pre-quoted command string. This is the field's "reject-gate"/prompt-discipline class the research flagged (D-275, claude-remember's child-model-second-guesses failure mode).
  - **BUG 2 (latency) — `cursor-agent -p` is SLOW: it runs the FULL agent loop even in print mode.** Live timings: ~11s for a trivial reply, **30–83s for a real compression task** (vs kiro-cli's ~1s — a 30–80× difference). The first draft only armed the timeout when the caller passed `timeoutMs`; a ceiling-free caller that omits it would run unbounded, and a hook-ceiling caller (60s SessionEnd) would false-timeout. **Fix: a `CURSOR_DEFAULT_TIMEOUT_MS = 150_000` default** applied when no `timeoutMs` is given. **DESIGN CONSEQUENCE (load-bearing for `makeBackend` + the callers):** a Cursor backend call CANNOT run synchronously inside the 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling — it must route through the ceiling-free/detached paths (daily-distill, lazy-compress at 120s+). This is a per-backend latency PROPERTY that composes with the §8.5/§8.7 timeout family: the same code that's fine on kiro-cli (~1s) will blow the SessionEnd ceiling on cursor-agent. The build must ensure the SessionEnd-synchronous compress path either uses a fast backend or is made async/detached for the slow ones. (Kiro was fast enough that this never surfaced; Cursor forces the issue.)
  - **Confirmed working (the ground truth for the rest of the build):** `agent -p --trust --model composer-2.5-fast --output-format text` + prompt-on-stdin → clean summary on stdout, no ANSI/`> ` strip needed (simpler than kiro), exit 0. Windows bin = `agent.cmd` shim under `%LOCALAPPDATA%\cursor-agent\` (the default bin is `agent.cmd` on win32; a non-interactive shell may not see the freshly-PATH'd dir — the live-test hard-coded the absolute `.cmd`, which is what the `agentCliOnPath` detector must resolve). Recursion guard (`CMK_BACKEND_SPAWN`) carried, same as kiro (agent-agnostic). _Relates D-274 (the raw live-probe this builds on), D-270 (the backend), D-275 (the prompt-discipline field pattern), Task 200 (the build — this is the CursorAgentBackend Done-when item, DONE + live-verified; the latency finding now governs the makeBackend/caller composition), the §8.5/§8.7 timeout family (the SessionEnd-ceiling composition Cursor forces). D-278._

## 2026-07-05 — D-277: no-CLI degrade = warn-and-file-only (settled); + the "split-brain backend" — run automatic memory through a DIFFERENT agent's CLI than the one you code in (new Task 201)

- **⚙️ DECISION + 💡 IDEA (2026-07-05) — D-277, two related backend-config calls the user made while clarifying their mental model of Task 200.**
  - **(1) SETTLED — the no-CLI degrade behavior:** when the kit is installed for agent X but X's CLI is NOT on PATH (e.g. Kiro IDE but no `kiro-cli`) and no cloud key is set, the automatic engine **warns at BOTH `cmk install` (first-touch) and `cmk doctor` (recurring), and degrades to file-only** — capture/search/recall/delete-guard keep working (pure files + SQLite); only the automatic LLM steps are skipped, and the user is TOLD, never a silent no-op (the D-270 bug). Rejected: auto-falling-back to a cloud key silently (can spend money / use an unintended vendor — the cloud-API-key route stays OPT-IN, tier-2, per D-275/D-276). The "offer to install the CLI for the user" enhancement is the later-version upgrade of the parked consent-mode idea (not now). This CONFIRMS the D-272 both-surfaces check + the D-271 honest-floor; nothing new to build beyond what Task 200 already scopes.
  - **(2) NEW TASK 201 — the "split-brain backend" (the user's idea, genuinely good):** decouple "which agent I code in" from "which agent runs my background memory." The user: *"I have claude installed and kiro, I use claude as my main programming aid, but want to use the kiro-cli as the one that does the automatic memory."* This is COST/ROLE SEPARATION — the interactive coding agent (premium, full-context) and the background janitor LLM (cheap, frequent, unattended compress/extract) are DIFFERENT jobs; route the janitor to the cheapest CLI the user has (kiro-cli Haiku on a Google login) and save the premium subscription for coding. **Novel** — none of the 42 deep-read projects (D-275/D-276) let you CHOOSE a non-primary agent for the background call (codemem auto-DETECTS one, never lets you override to a different agent). **Small IF Task 200 builds the factory override-ready** — which it now will: Task 200's `makeBackend` Done-when was amended to read an optional `backend.agent` config key BEFORE `detectInstallKind`, so Task 201 is just a config-key + a doctor line + docs (Estimate S). The backend modules are already agent-independent (they don't care WHY they were selected), so no rework. Filed as Task 201 with a named D-248 trigger ("fires as the immediate follow-on once Task 200 ships the override-ready factory"). _Relates Task 200 (factory built override-ready for this), Task 201 (the new task), D-270 (agent-relative backend), D-271/D-272 (the prereq floor + both-surfaces check this degrade confirms), D-276 (codemem auto-detects but can't override — the gap this fills). D-277._

## 2026-07-05 — D-276: the tail-judgment wave CORRECTS the "0 multi-CLI" claim — `codemem` is a genuine PRIOR-ART reference for exactly Task 200 (auto-detect the agent, shell its CLI, API-key fallback); the kit is not reinventing an impossible thing, and now has a design to validate against

- **🔬 RESEARCH + ✏️ CORRECTION (2026-07-05) — D-276: after the 32 high-relevance reads (D-275) concluded "0/32 do multi-CLI routing," a tail-judgment wave checked the 10 tail projects that could plausibly be a counter-example (the ones naming multiple agents or claiming cross-LLM + a background call). Two flagged — and the honest correction is that the absolute "nobody does it" was slightly WRONG. The precise, better finding:**
  - **`codemem` (kunickiaj/codemem) — a GENUINE counter-example, and the closest prior art to Task 200 in the entire 119-project field.** Its `ObserverClient` (`packages/core/src/observer-client.ts`) has FIVE dispatch paths and `loadObserverConfig()` AUTO-DETECTS the environment to pick one: (1) explicit config wins; (2) inside Claude Code (`CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRYPOINT`/`CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION` set) AND no API key → shell `claude -p --output-format json --permission-mode bypassPermissions` (`_invokeSidecar`); (3) else `codex` on PATH AND `~/.codex/auth.json` exists AND no OpenCode OAuth → shell `codex exec --ephemeral -s read-only` (`_spawnCodex`); (4/5) else API-key/OAuth HTTP. So the SAME background-observer machinery shells a DIFFERENT agent CLI (claude OR codex) based on which the user has authenticated — **exactly the kit's Task-200 goal**, in shipping code, with **native Windows first-class** (`where` vs `which`, an install-matrix doc) and a **pure testable selection function** (`shouldAutoSelectCodexSidecar()`) isolating the PATH/env probes from the decision. **This is a blueprint, not a threat:** it PROVES the D-270 approach works in production, and hands us a design to mirror — an auto-detect selector + a `shouldAutoSelectXSidecar()`-style pure function + an API-key/OAuth universal fallback (the D-275 two-tier shape, confirmed by a shipping peer). codemem does claude+codex; the kit extends the same pattern to **cursor-agent + kiro-cli** (which codemem does NOT cover — cursor/kiro were live-verified by us in D-274/the kiro-backend), so the kit is still novel in its agent COVERAGE, just not in the core technique.
  - **OpenHands — multi-CLI INFRA but NOT a counter-example for our case.** Its ACP provider registry (`acp_providers.py`) has claude-code/codex/gemini-cli as interchangeable CLI backends, but (a) the choice is EXPLICIT user settings, not auto-detect-whichever-is-installed, and (b) it drives the INTERACTIVE foreground agent, NOT the background condenser — the background summarization always goes through a single unified LiteLLM cloud-API call. Still a useful data point: OpenHands deliberately makes its automatic background-maintenance LLM REUSE the same provider config the main agent already has (via LiteLLM) rather than needing its own credential — a design question for us (should our compression call reuse whatever the primary agent is configured with?).
  - **The 8 others confirmed NOT counter-examples** (reinforcing the finding): Supermemory (VC-funded, cross-agent-BY-DESIGN — and STILL chose cloud-API-key + per-native-hook adapters, never CLI-shelling), Honcho / LangMem / TencentDB / hindsight / agentmemory / Axe / codenamev-claude_memory — all cloud-API-key, no-headless-call, or single-CLI. Notably **even the projects explicitly built to be cross-LLM/portable chose the API-key route, not multi-CLI** — which is WHY codemem stands out as the lone peer that took the harder, subscription-reusing path the kit is committed to.
  - **Corrected headline (supersedes D-275's "0/32"):** across 42 deep-read projects, exactly **ONE (codemem)** does auto-detecting multi-CLI routing for the background call, and it covers claude+codex only. **Nobody covers the kit's target set (claude + kiro-cli + cursor-agent), and nobody else even attempts subscription-reuse multi-CLI** — the field overwhelmingly picks cloud-API-key for portability. The kit's thesis holds (automatic + portable is the near-empty intersection), the technique is de-risked (codemem proves it ships), and we have a concrete reference to validate `makeBackend` against. _Relates D-275 (the claim this refines — intellectual-honesty correction, the "did you check" rule applied to our OWN finding), D-270 (the two-tier backend — codemem confirms it), D-274 (Cursor/Kiro coverage codemem lacks), Task 200 (mirror codemem's auto-detect + pure-selector pattern). D-276._

---

## 2026-07-05 — D-275: the D-271 research — Waves 2+3 CONFIRM the kit's shape is novel (0/32 do multi-CLI routing) AND surface real mechanisms the field uses that we did NOT know (the user's catch: "ask it OPEN so you don't only get what you expected")

- **🔬 RESEARCH (2026-07-05) — D-275: the deep research completed 3 waves over the 32 high-relevance projects. Wave 2 answered 4 user-added questions (multi-CLI routing / no-CLI mode / cost / auto-honesty); Wave 3 was an OPEN, non-leading trace of the automatic-memory MECHANISM (the user's methodology catch: my proposed a/b/c question was leading — "what if they do it a way you don't know?" — so the prompt was rewritten to trace the actual chain and flag anything that ISN'T hook→CLI or agent→MCP-tool). ~4.8M subagent tokens across all waves (Sonnet). Two big results:**
  - **RESULT 1 — the kit's shape is genuinely novel (confirmed, not assumed): 0 of 32 projects route the background LLM call through MORE THAN ONE agent CLI (claude OR kiro OR cursor, whichever is present).** Every project is exactly one of: (a) **no-headless-call** (~19 — recall is deterministic search; the LLM is the INTERACTIVE agent via MCP; cross-agent for free but NOT hard-automatic — it depends on the model choosing to call the tool), (b) **single-CLI** (~6 — shells out to ONE specific CLI, almost always `claude -p`; hard-automatic via a deterministic hook but locked to that one agent — claude-remember, memsearch, claude-memory-compiler, Meowary→opencode, Amazon-Q→`q`, Spec-Kit→user-chosen-once), (c) **cloud-API-key** (~4 — bypasses the agent, calls Gemini/OpenRouter/Anthropic directly with a key; claude-mem's fallback, GBrain, MemClaw, mem0, EverOS), (d) **agent-SDK** (~2 — Claude Agent SDK headless, still Claude-only). **Nobody combines "hard-automatic (deterministic hook, not model-discretion)" WITH "portable across whichever agent CLI is present."** The field traded one for the other: the MCP majority got portability by giving up the deterministic guarantee; the CLI minority got the guarantee by giving up portability. The kit's Task-200 goal — a deterministic hook that spawns *whichever* agent CLI the user has — is the unfilled intersection. This VALIDATES the whole premise (and the user's original reason for building the kit: automatic, not "unreliable methods like math").
  - **RESULT 2 — real mechanisms we did NOT have, surfaced ONLY because the question was open (the payoff of the user's catch):**
    - **claude-mem — the "persistent Observer agent" pattern (the most novel).** NOT spawn-per-event. A deterministic hook enqueues events into a SQLite-backed buffer; a long-lived background daemon holds ONE Claude-Agent-SDK conversation open per session, fed by an ASYNC GENERATOR that drains the queue — so a single "Observer" LLM instance stays alive across many hook firings, receiving synthetic templated turns and emitting `<observation>` XML when IT (a second, isolated agent — not the interactive model, not a hard rule) judges something memory-worthy. Three-way hybrid: deterministic trigger → queued batching → LLM-judged extraction → deterministic persist. (We do per-turn spawn; the batched-Observer idea is a scaling pattern worth noting, not adopting now.)
    - **GBrain — extraction as an invisible SIDE EFFECT of a generic write tool, via a bare `queueMicrotask` "queue."** The agent calls `put_page` (generic write), and the handler fires `runFactsBackstop` AFTER the write with zero agent awareness — memory extraction is invisible plumbing behind an unrelated tool, NOT a memory-specific tool the agent chose. The decoupling "queue" is a plain in-process `queueMicrotask` loop (cap 100, in-flight 1) — no Redis/BullMQ. AND it runs BOTH this lightweight eager path AND a heavyweight OS-scheduled (launchd/systemd/cron) durable-Postgres-queue path for nightly "dream" consolidation — two triggers, one shared `runCycle` primitive.
    - **MemClaw — "passive outcome inference from data exhaust," zero write-path hook.** Trust/success signal is computed RETROSPECTIVELY from data that already exists (contradiction state, `supersedes_id`, terminal memory_type like "shipped"/"blocked", git/CI status) — pulled cold on a cron tick, never pushed at write time ("INTENTIONALLY zero-cost on the write path, no producer hooks"). A fundamentally different signal-capture technique than hook-or-tool. (Directly relevant to our trust/persona evolution — signal from exhaust, not from asking.)
    - **Basic Memory + claude-memory-compiler — PreCompact-as-checkpoint + the fast-hook/detached-twin split.** Hook the exact moment the agent is about to DESTROY context (compaction) as the forcing function to write durably — deterministic (zero-LLM parse), "write early enrich after" in case of a kill. And the fast synchronous hook does only a temp-file write then fire-and-forgets a DETACHED background process that does the unbounded LLM work off the hook's clock (satisfies the timeout) — the "response" is just an append the NEXT SessionStart reads. (We already do detached auto-extract; PreCompact-as-checkpoint is a trigger we don't use and could.)
    - **mem0 — memory as a MITM side effect of the chat SDK.** Its proxy wraps the OpenAI-compatible `chat.completions.create`: on a user turn it fire-and-forget threads `add()` AND synchronously injects retrieved memories into the outbound prompt — memory capture with NO hook and NO agent decision, riding the SDK the dev already uses. (Also: mem0's famous "LLM-judged ADD/UPDATE/DELETE" is now DEAD CODE — replaced by additive-only extraction + deterministic MD5/cosine dedup. A training-data-known "fact" that's false in current code — the exact "did you check the primary source" class.)
    - **EverOS — a declarative typed trigger engine (Immediate/Cron/Idle) + a filesystem watcher** that re-derives indexes when a user hand-edits the markdown (markdown-as-truth, indexes derived) — the "someone touched a file" trigger class, decoupling durability from queryability. Several projects (claude-mem, EverOS, Basic Memory) independently ship a filesystem-watcher as a SECOND trigger alongside hooks.
  - **Cross-cutting confirmations for our design:** (1) the RECURSION GUARD is universal — every project that spawns its own agent CLI has one (claude-remember strips `CLAUDE_*` env + a reject-gate regex on the child's output; memsearch uses `MEMSEARCH_DISABLE=1`; claude-memory-compiler sets `CLAUDE_INVOKED_BY` before any import) — our `CMK_BACKEND_SPAWN` guard is exactly the right, field-standard move (D-270). (2) The "reject-gate" idea (screen the child model's output for refusal/clarification phrasing and DROP it rather than writing "I cannot…" into memory) is a real bug others hit — worth adopting in our backend result-handling. (3) markdown-as-source-of-truth + rebuildable derived index is the dominant durable-storage choice (memsearch, EverOS, Basic Memory, GBrain) — our ADR-0002 confirmed again. **The backend-shape DECISION stays deferred per the user** (widen evidence first — now done for the high tier; tail-judgment + synthesis next). _Relates D-271 (the mandate), D-273/D-274 (Cursor), D-270 (backend), Task 200, ADR-0002 (markdown-truth), the persona/trust tasks (MemClaw's exhaust-inference), the §5.1 primary-source rule (mem0's dead-code find). D-275._

---

## 2026-07-05 — D-274: `cursor-agent` headless LLM backend LIVE-VERIFIED on the user's real Windows machine, off the Cursor subscription, NO API key — the last Task-200 open question closed with primary-source proof

- **🔬 LIVE-VERIFICATION (2026-07-05) — D-274: the user installed `cursor-agent` on their Windows box, logged in via browser-OAuth (their existing Cursor subscription — no API key), and we probed the real binary end-to-end. This upgrades D-273's Cursor findings from "doc-confirmed" to "LIVE-confirmed on the user's own hardware" (the kiro-cli-style live-verify), and CORRECTS two doc-based caveats. The `CursorAgentBackend` (Task 200) can now be built against confirmed ground truth, not docs.** **The confirmed invocation (ran live, exit 0, ~11s, clean stdout):** `agent -p --trust --model composer-2.5-fast --output-format text "<prompt>"` returned exactly `cursor backend works` from a throwaway temp cwd. **Ground-truth facts for the build:**
  - **Binary + Windows install shape:** the native-Windows installer (`irm 'https://cursor.com/install?win32=true' | iex`, confirmed native — the user ran `agent` directly in PowerShell, NOT WSL/Git-Bash) drops **`agent.cmd` + `agent.ps1`** shims under **`%LOCALAPPDATA%\cursor-agent\`** and adds that dir to the USER PATH. Version live: **`2026.07.01-41b2de7`**. CRITICAL detfor the `agentCliOnPath` detector: on Windows it is a **`.cmd` SHIM** (like Claude's `claude.cmd` / the claude-remember #120 bug) — a bare-name `spawn('agent', …)` will NOT resolve it; the detector/backend must resolve the `.cmd` via `where`/`process.env.PATH` walk, and a non-interactive shell may not see the freshly-added PATH until a new session (our probe had to hard-code the absolute `agent.cmd` path because Get-Command didn't see it).
  - **Headless one-shot:** `-p/--print` ("for scripts or non-interactive use"), `--output-format text|json|stream-json`. Clean answer on STDOUT with `text` (no TUI-noise strip needed, unlike kiro-cli's ANSI+`> ` — simpler parse than Kiro).
  - **Trust (the load-bearing flag — dodges the interactive `[a] Trust this workspace` prompt the user hit):** `--trust` — "Trust the current workspace without prompting (only works with --print/headless mode)." This is Cursor's exact analog of Kiro's `--trust-tools=`. Also `--sandbox enabled|disabled`, `-f/--force`/`--yolo` (run-everything — do NOT use for the backend; `--trust` is the minimal safe flag).
  - **Cheap background model (the "Haiku role"):** `--model composer-2.5-fast` (Cursor's own fast/cheap tier, the interactive default — the natural Haiku-analog for compression/extraction; `--list-models` also shows `gemini-3-flash`/`gemini-3.5-flash`/`gpt-5-mini`/`gpt-5.4-nano-*` as cheap alternates, and `claude-sonnet-5-*`/`claude-opus-4-8-*` for heavier roles). No literal "haiku"; composer-2.5-fast is the pick.
  - **AUTH — CORRECTS D-273's doc-based caveat (the user: "no api key needed, working with my subscription"):** `--api-key`/`CURSOR_API_KEY` EXIST but are **OPTIONAL** — interactive browser-OAuth login (`cursor.com/loginDeepControl` → "Yes, Log In" → "Authentication tokens stored securely") reuses the user's Cursor SUBSCRIPTION, exactly like kiro-cli reuses the Google login. So D-273's "separate CURSOR_API_KEY required, HARDER friction than Kiro" is DOWNGRADED: for a normally-logged-in Cursor user the backend needs NO API-key onboarding; the key path matters ONLY for headless-CI/no-browser environments. This makes Cursor parity with Kiro (both: use the login you already have, no second paid vendor) — and reaffirms D-270's rejection of a mandatory Anthropic-API-key path.
  - **Recursion guard still required:** same class as Kiro — spawning `cursor-agent` from inside the kit's own Cursor hook would re-fire the kit's hooks; the `CMK_BACKEND_SPAWN` env guard at `dispatchCursorHook` entry (already built for Task 200) covers it. (Not re-tested live here; the guard is agent-agnostic.)
  - **Latency:** ~11s for a trivial call (vs kiro-cli's ~1s) — heavier, but well within the ceiling-free compress budgets (120s). Worth noting for the timeout sizing; not a blocker.
  **Net:** Cursor is now as well-understood as Kiro for the backend. The remaining Task-200 build items (the `CursorAgentBackend` module + `makeBackend` factory + `agentCliOnPath` Windows-`.cmd`-aware detector + doctor/install checks + agent-parametric live-test) are unblocked. _Relates D-273 (the research this live-confirms + corrects), D-270 (the two-tier backend; Cursor tier-1 now proven), D-271 (the OS-coverage requirement — Windows-native Cursor CONFIRMED on the user's box), Task 200 (unblocked), the kiro-backend.mjs precedent (the CursorAgentBackend mirrors it, minus the ANSI strip, plus the `.cmd` resolve). D-274._

## 2026-07-05 — D-273: the D-271 DEEP research — Wave 1 (16 highest-signal projects, code-read) OVERTURNS my 2-search Cursor-on-Windows conclusion + tallies how the field solves the headless-LLM-backend problem

- **🔬 RESEARCH (2026-07-05) — D-273: the ultracode workflow research the user mandated in D-271 is underway; Wave 0 built a 119-project manifest (32 high / 53 med / 34 low; far past the "~70" estimate), and Wave 1 CODE-READ the 16 highest-signal cross-agent projects (15/16 succeeded — mimir hit a StructuredOutput retry cap, Kiro's entry came back partial; both re-run in a later wave). Sonnet-5 agents, ~1.68M tokens. Findings saved to the run's scratchpad + being written to a consolidated `docs/research/` note.** **THE HEADLINE — the Cursor-on-Windows story is RESOLVED, and my D-271 2-search conclusion was WRONG (the exact lazy-framing the deep research existed to correct):** native Windows support for `cursor-agent` shipped ~late-Jan-2026 — cursor.com/docs/cli/installation TODAY gives a Windows-native PowerShell installer verbatim (`irm 'https://cursor.com/install?win32=true' | iex`), presented as a standard option with NO experimental caveat, alongside the WSL/mac/Linux bash line. The community "ports" I cited (gitcnd/cursor-agent-cli-windows pinned to `2026.01.02`, TomasHubelbauer/cursor-agent-windows) are PRE-native historical artifacts, now superseded — NOT evidence of a current gap. **Caveats the code-read surfaced (real, must design around):** (1) it's Node.js-based under the hood (not a compiled native binary like Claude Code), younger/rougher than mac/Linux, with installer-detection bugs the Cursor IDE itself carried into ~May-2026 (a live forum bug: the IDE's own toast ran the Unix installer inside Git Bash → `Unsupported operating system: MINGW64` — the SAME error I hit; a maintainer confirmed a fix merged 2026-05-04) → the kit's doctor/`makeBackend` must probe `agent --version` EXIT CODE, not just presence-on-PATH; (2) `cursor-agent -p` in automation REQUIRES a separately-generated `CURSOR_API_KEY` from the Cursor Dashboard — it does NOT reuse the logged-in desktop session (cursor.com/docs/cli/reference/authentication) — HARDER friction than Kiro (which just worked off the existing `kiro-cli` Google login) → the Cursor-backend onboarding needs an explicit "generate + set CURSOR_API_KEY" step, or the backend silently no-ops (the D-270 bug re-created). The planned `agent -p --output-format json --model <id>` invocation is flag-validated against the official parameter reference; the tool-sandbox equivalent of Kiro's `--trust-tools=` is `--sandbox <mode>` (mode values still need a live `agent --help` probe in the build). **THE FIELD-WIDE PATTERN (15 projects, invocation-mode tally):** per-agent-CLI ×4 (claude-remember, memsearch, Ruflo, Cursor-as-target — all shell out to a specific agent's CLI), agent-own-headless ×2 (claude-memory-compiler + Kiro — via the Claude Agent SDK / the agent's own headless mode), cloud-API-key ×1 pure + inside ×3 hybrids (claude-mem, Taskmaster, agentsys — a configurable provider with an API-key fallback), no-LLM ×4 (mimir, MemPalace, CodeGraph, gstack's /learn — recall is deterministic search; the LLM is the *interactive* agent, never a headless call). **The load-bearing precedent — claude-mem (the closest cross-agent analog):** its answer to "no Claude Code on this machine" is NOT "drive Cursor/Kiro headlessly" (no such mechanism exists in its code) — it's a central worker-daemon with a `CLAUDE_MEM_PROVIDER` switch: default `claude` (Agent-SDK → spawns the installed `claude` CLI), else `gemini`/`openrouter` (direct cloud-API-key `fetch()`); its STANDALONE-SETUP.md tells Cursor-users-without-Claude to set a Gemini/OpenRouter key. **This VALIDATES a two-tier backend for us:** (tier 1) route through the agent's OWN CLI when present (`kiro-cli` live-confirmed, `cursor-agent` doc-confirmed native-Windows) — the D-270 decision holds; (tier 2) a cloud-API-key fallback is what the field actually does when no agent CLI is usable — worth considering as the kit's honest last resort rather than a silent no-op, THOUGH it reintroduces the "2nd paid vendor" cost D-270 rejected as the *primary* path (keep it opt-in, not default). **Windows discipline takeaway (recurring across the bash-first projects — claude-remember's CHANGELOG is the cautionary tail):** projects that bolted Windows onto a bash-first hook layer (claude-remember, memsearch, gstack, mem0-hooks) all require Git-Bash/WSL + earned Windows support through a long tail of one-at-a-time bugs (claude.cmd-shim-not-found, cp1252 mojibake, drive-letter path doubling, CRLF eval-bridge breaks, PowerShell quoting) — the kit's per-agent hook wiring must stay native-PowerShell/Node on Windows (the platform-commands.mjs discipline), NOT POSIX one-liners with a cygpath shim. And claude-memory-compiler's concrete Windows spawn-flag knowledge (`CREATE_NO_WINDOW` for the fast hook vs `CREATE_NEW_PROCESS_GROUP|DETACHED_PROCESS` for the detached child, explicitly NOT combining `DETACHED_PROCESS` with live piped stdio "because it breaks the SDK's subprocess I/O") is worth checking our own Stop→auto-extract detached spawn against. _Wave 2 (the other 16 high-relevance) + the mimir/Kiro re-reads + the tail-judgment pass still pending; the consolidated note + comparison table land when the reads complete. Relates D-271 (the mandate + the 2-search error this corrects), D-270 (the two-tier backend this shapes), Task 200 (the build), the §5.1 + no-lazy-framing rules (the 2-search conclusion was exactly the class both name). D-273._

## 2026-07-05 — D-272: the agent-CLI-presence CHECK belongs at BOTH `cmk install` (first-touch) and `cmk doctor` (recurring), sharing one detector — and recording durable decisions is the standard, not an approval-gated step

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-07-05) — D-272: the D-271 prereq isn't just DOCS — the kit should DETECT a missing agent CLI, and the primary surface for that is `cmk install`, not only `cmk doctor`.** The user, on being asked whether the check belongs in `cmk install`: *"don't we want this check in the cmk install?"* — yes. `cmk install` is **first-touch**: the user is actively wiring the kit into THEIR agent, so a missing-CLI warning there catches the gap at the exact moment it's actionable ("you just installed for Kiro, but `kiro-cli` isn't on PATH — the automatic features won't run until it is"), BEFORE they ever wonder why nothing summarizes. `cmk doctor` is the **recurring** check (the same missing CLI surfaced on every health run). **Both surfaces, ONE detector:** a new `agentCliOnPath(kind)` companion to the existing `detectInstallKind` (doctor.mjs already routes Claude/Kiro/Cursor by install kind; `install.mjs` has ZERO agent-CLI-presence check today — verified). Building them together is cheaper than separately. **Still GATED on the D-271 deep research** — the load-bearing reason: if the detector hard-codes "Cursor → look for `cursor-agent` on PATH" and the research finds Windows Cursor users invoke it another way (WSL bridge, a community binary), the check fires a FALSE "your CLI is missing" on every correct Windows Cursor install — worse than no check, and the exact "concluded from 2 searches" trap D-271 corrected. So the detector waits for the manifest; the DOCS floor (README + QUICKSTART, done 2026-07-05) ships regardless. Folded into Task 200's Done-when at both surfaces.
- **⚙️ META-DECISION (2026-07-05) — recording a durable decision is the WORKING STANDARD, never an approval-gated step.** The user, when asked "should I log this to the DECISION-LOG or is tasks.md enough?": *"you don't need my approval, this kind of thing should be the working standard."* → Do NOT ask permission to append a DECISION-LOG entry, flip a task checkbox, update a single-source-of-truth doc, or otherwise maintain the durable paper trail — that IS the standard already codified in CLAUDE.md ("single source of truth, always-on" + "decision-log discipline"). Asking about it is ceremony (the anti-pattern). Log durable decisions in the same batch as the work, silently, as a reflex. _Relates D-271 (the prereq this operationalizes), D-270 (the backend gap), Task 200 (the build — both check surfaces in its Done-when), the CLAUDE.md "single source of truth, always-on" + "decision-log discipline" + anti-ceremony rules. D-272._

## 2026-07-05 — D-271: the per-agent CLI PREREQUISITE must be documented (the honest minimum) + a DEEP multi-project research is owed on cross-OS headless LLM invocation (the user's correction — I stopped at 2 web searches)

- **📋 DECISION + 🔬 RESEARCH-DEBT (2026-07-05) — D-271: two things the user made binding while building D-270/Task 200.** **(1) The per-agent CLI prerequisite is the non-negotiable floor — document it or we mislead users.** The kit's automatic engine spawns an LLM via a CLI, and that CLI is a SEPARATE install from the IDE, for EVERY agent: **Claude Code** needs the `claude` CLI on PATH even if you use Claude in VS Code; **Kiro** needs `kiro-cli` even with the Kiro IDE (this is why the KiroCliBackend live-test worked — `kiro-cli` is on the user's PATH); **Cursor** needs `cursor-agent` (the CLI, separate from the IDE). The user: *"if we have a prerequisite … like we have to have the kiro cli installed, even if we have the kiro ide … then we have to, minimum, say so in the readme as a note for prerequisites per ide/cli, and that is also true for claude … if we dont do that minimum then we really mislead our users."* → a per-agent **Prerequisites** section in README + QUICKSTART + a `cmk doctor` HC that names the missing CLI. This is TRUE regardless of what the deep research finds — the honest floor. **(2) I jumped to a conclusion — a DEEP cross-project research is owed.** On hitting "cursor-agent has no official Windows build (Linux/macOS installer only; Windows = WSL2 or an unofficial community patch — [gitcnd/cursor-agent-cli-windows], [TomasHubelbauer/cursor-agent-windows])," I concluded from just TWO web searches — the lazy-framing the project's own rules forbid. **The user's directive:** *"i dont believe that there isnt a project out there that didnt solve this, we need to do deep research online and every project we research, i dont care if we have 70 projects, we should check them all, and we should clone them (re-clone if we already did) and check docs AND code to see what they did."* So the real research (owed BEFORE deciding the Cursor-on-Windows story): re-clone the cross-agent memory/tooling projects in our research base + any new ones, read their CODE + docs specifically for **how they invoke an LLM headlessly across Windows/mac/Linux** — do they require a CLI, call an API, use each agent's own headless mode, bridge WSL, or something else? **(3) The OS-coverage requirement (the user): Windows + macOS + Linux ALL required for every agent that has an installer on that OS** — "most people I know are on Windows, I'm mainly on Windows, but there's a huge base on all 3." A Cursor backend that only works on mac/Linux is NOT acceptable if a real Windows path exists (which the deep research must find, not the 2-search conclusion). _Relates D-270 (the backend gap this refines), Task 200 (the build — now gated on the deep research for Cursor + the prereq note as the floor), the §5.1 primary-source + no-lazy-framing rules (both fired against me here). D-271._

## 2026-07-04 — D-270 RESEARCH DONE: the agent-relative backend is FEASIBLE — Kiro live-confirmed, the recursion hazard reproduced+guarded, Cursor doc-confirmed (build must live-probe)

- **🔬 RESEARCH (2026-07-04) — D-270 research phase complete ([note](../research/2026-07-04-agent-relative-llm-backend.md)); no blocker found, the build (Task 200) is a real L but every hard question now has a verified answer.** **Kiro — LIVE-CONFIRMED on the installed `kiro-cli` (primary source):** `kiro-cli chat --no-interactive --model claude-haiku-4.5 --trust-tools=` is a working scriptable one-shot — a 3-word reply cost **0.01 credits in ~1 s** through the user's **Google login** (NO Claude Code, NO `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`); a genuine cheap Haiku (`--list-models` → `claude-haiku-4.5` at 0.40x) maps onto the background role. **Output parse SOLVED:** the interactive TUI noise (ANSI spinners, `N of 1 hooks finished`, credits footer) all goes to **stderr** — **stdout carries ONLY the answer** (`> <text>` + color codes → strip ANSI + the leading `> `). **The recursion fork (#4, the make-or-break one) is REAL and I reproduced it live:** running `kiro-cli chat` in a kit-installed dir FIRED the kit's own `agentSpawn` inject hook (`cmk hook agentSpawn`) → it timed out (`✗ … 10.15 s: command timed out`); spawning `kiro-cli` from inside a Kiro hook would recurse. **Guard designed + verified:** set **`CMK_BACKEND_SPAWN=1`** in the spawned child's env; a one-line check at the `dispatchKiroHook`/`dispatchCursorHook` ENTRY (`if (process.env.CMK_BACKEND_SPAWN) return noop`) makes every inner hook no-op — env-inheritance through the spawn was live-verified. **Cursor — doc-confirmed feasible, NOT live-verified** (`cursor-agent` isn't installed on the dev machine, only the IDE launcher): `agent -p "<prompt>" --output-format json` exists (json is cleaner than Kiro's strip-stdout), auth `CURSOR_API_KEY`; but `--model`/no-tools-sandbox/the `-p`-hang bug are NOT in the docs → **the build must run a live `agent --help`/`-p` probe** (the §5.1 don't-claim-from-docs rule — recorded honestly as a build-probe, not a pass). **Design sketch (design.md §16.50.x at build time):** a `CompressorBackend` per agent (`HaikuViaClaudeCli` = the renamed existing path, + `KiroCliBackend` + `CursorAgentBackend`), selected by `detectInstallKind` (the doctor's existing agent-detect); the 7 `HaikuViaAnthropicApi` sites call a `makeBackend({projectRoot})` factory; a NEW doctor HC surfaces "backend for <agent> unreachable → automatic memory degraded" instead of the silent no-op that IS the D-270 bug; `scripts/live-test.mjs` becomes agent-parametric (it hardcodes `claude` — the harness that would otherwise HIDE this bug, the D-84 class one level up). _Relates D-270 (the gap), Task 200 (the build), ADR-0008 (pluggable backends), the 7 spawn sites. D-270-research._

---

## 2026-07-04 — D-270: the cross-agent LLM-backend gap — a Cursor-only / Kiro-only user has NO working automatic engine (the kit shells out to `claude`, which they don't have); v0.4.5 BLOCKED until the backend routes through the agent's OWN CLI

- **🐛 ISSUE + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-07-04) — D-270: the cross-agent adapters (Kiro v0.4.0, Cursor v0.4.5) shipped the WIRING but not the PROMISE. The kit's ENTIRE automatic-intelligence layer — auto-extract, compression, persona/wedge, temporal-sweep, daily-distill, weekly-curate — runs through ONE backend, `HaikuViaAnthropicApi`, which shells out to the locally-installed `claude` binary (`claude --print`, authed by a Claude subscription; verified compressor.mjs:51/200 + the 7 spawn sites + the D-552-era note "the kit's Haiku backend is `claude --print`"). There is NO API-key path (no `@anthropic-ai/sdk` dep, nothing reads `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`) — the class NAME is a misnomer; it is `HaikuViaClaudeCLI`. So a user who has ONLY Cursor or ONLY Kiro and never installed Claude Code gets: capture/search/inject/delete-guard WORK (pure file-I/O + SQLite), but every LLM step SILENTLY no-ops (spawn ENOENT → best-effort catch) — no extraction, no compression, no wedge, no sweep. The kit degrades to a manual note store, which is NOT the automatic memory kit that is its entire point.** The user's correction (2026-07-04), which reframes the whole cross-agent premise: *"when i said we need the kit to be compatible with other ide/cli i meant that if a user who has only cursor or only kiro installed and never installed claude can use the kit."* The adapters route to a brain that isn't on the machine.
  - **Why it was invisible:** (a) the whole team (dev + cut-gate operator) has `claude` installed, so it "worked" for everyone who tested it; (b) the automated live-test harness (`scripts/live-test.mjs`) HARDCODES `claude` (`:115`/`:148`) and runs on a Claude-equipped machine — it would PASS while hiding this exact bug (the D-84 "unit-green ≠ works-on-real-input" class, one level up: the LIVE test itself can't see the gap because its own environment satisfies the hidden dependency); (c) ADR-0008 deliberately deferred alternative backends "to v0.2," and nobody re-opened that when Kiro/Cursor landed — the v0.1 "Claude Code is the only target" assumption silently persisted into a multi-agent product.
  - **DECISION — the backend must route through the AGENT'S OWN CLI (the user's call, 2026-07-04).** NOT a direct `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` backend (rejected: forces the user to get a SECOND paid vendor account — a Cursor-only user shouldn't need an Anthropic key; the point is they use what they ALREADY have). NOT "document Claude Code as a prereq" (rejected: that is exactly the false promise the user is correcting). The kit's "Haiku call" becomes agent-relative: on Cursor → `cursor-agent -p` (headless CLI CONFIRMED to exist — cursor.com/docs/cli/headless: `agent -p "<prompt>" --output-format json`, auth `CURSOR_API_KEY`); on Kiro → Amazon Q's headless equivalent (UNVERIFIED — research needed); on Claude Code → the existing `claude --print` (unchanged, no regression). This is a `CompressorBackend` per agent, selected by which agent the project was installed for.
  - **v0.4.5 is BLOCKED (the user's call).** Do NOT tag v0.4.5 — shipping "Cursor support" that silently requires Claude Code is a false promise. The Claude-free backend must work FIRST, then cut. (Cursor is already merged to main as unreleased; the tag is what's blocked, not the merge.)
  - **OPEN RESEARCH (before any code — the §5.1 primary-source rule):** (1) does `cursor-agent -p` work as a scriptable ONE-SHOT LLM call (prompt in → text out), and what's the exact invocation + output-parse + auth + the known "-p hangs" bug (forum reports Feb 2026)? (2) can the kit pick the MODEL (a cheap/fast one for background compaction — the "Haiku" role)? (3) Kiro/Amazon Q headless equivalent — does `q chat`/`kiro-cli` have a `-p`-style non-interactive mode, auth, output shape? (4) the composition: these run INSIDE the kit's own hook (`sessionEnd`/`afterAgentResponse`) — does spawning the agent's CLI from within the agent's own hook deadlock/recurse? (5) cost/latency vs the current `claude --print`. (6) does each agent's headless mode even run in the ENV the hook fires in? _Relates ADR-0008 (pluggable backends, deferred — now un-deferred), D-180 (the adapter seam — this extends it from install-wiring to RUNTIME-backend), the 7 HaikuViaAnthropicApi spawn sites, Task 50/196 (the adapters this completes), `scripts/live-test.mjs` (the harness that must become agent-parametric). Filed as a new task in `specs/tasks.md`; the option analysis + the research findings land in a `docs/research/` note. D-270._
