## 2026-07-04 — D-266 SHIPPED: Task 198 per-session temporal sweep merged (the D-266 decision executed)

- **✅ SHIPPED (2026-07-04) — Task 198 (v0.4.5 rider, rode the Cursor lane):** the D-266 cadence re-decision is now code. **198.1:** `temporalSweep` fires from the **SessionEnd** handler (CONCURRENT in `runSessionEndTasks`' allSettled block — the 60s-ceiling composition: a 3rd ~50s Haiku call run sequentially would blow the ceiling, so it overlaps; disjoint inputs verified — compress→`sessions/`, persona→user-tier, sweep→fact-corpus+index) AND the **SessionStart lazy path** (`runLazyCompress`, on `stale-now`/`stale-daily`; `stale-weekly` already routes through `weeklyCurate`'s sweep so no double-run — the Task-105 new-chat-same-window gap is covered). Weekly stays the backstop. **198.1c** pinned end-to-end: an idle lazy session runs the REAL sweep and spawns ZERO judge calls (no-new-facts short-circuit, proven with a two-response backend that would otherwise over-spend). **198.2:** semantic title-embedding KNN candidates at θ=0.80 (Memora's reference) when the project's configured search mode is `semantic`/`hybrid` (gated on `resolveDefaultSearchMode` + the `CMK_DISABLE_SEMANTIC` kill-switch); FTS OR-query stays the always-available fallback; the finder is built only AFTER the no-new-facts short-circuit so an idle sweep never loads the embedder. **Judge/close semantics UNCHANGED** (D-259 untouched — only sites + candidate source evolved), which is why the whole existing temporal-sweep suite stayed green through the change. Docs: design §16.18 shipped-block + memory-lifecycle-map edge 17 + CHANGELOG. **Task 199 (write-time detection) remains deferred** — its D-248 trigger (a live session surfacing a stale-State answer WITHIN the per-session window) has not fired; 198 shrinks the window to a session boundary, and whether that's insufficient is the evidence 199 waits on. _Relates D-266 (the decision), D-259 (semantics preserved), D-166 (the window closed), Task 105 (the lazy gap), Memora App. F (the linear-cost evidence), Task 199 (the still-deferred successor). D-266-shipped._

## 2026-07-04 — D-269: the `cmk hook` INJECT leg emitted EMPTY since v0.4.0 — Kiro sessions never got the memory snapshot; found by the Task-196 Cursor sandbox live-test, fixed for both agents + locked with real-core integration tests

- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-07-04) — D-269: `runHook`'s default inject dep read a NON-EXISTENT field of `injectContext`'s return — `injectContext` has returned `{snapshot, hookOutput, …}` since its first commit (there has never been a `.text`), so `const text = injectContext(...); text?.text ?? ''` normalized every real inject to the EMPTY STRING. Net effect: every Kiro `cmk hook agentSpawn`/`promptSubmit` since v0.4.0 (PR #212) printed NOTHING — Kiro sessions ran without the memory snapshot — while the whole suite stayed green.** The new Cursor wiring (Task 196) copied the same line and inherited the bug; the Task-196 **sandbox live-test caught it** (seeded fact on disk → `cmk cursor-hook` sessionStart returned `{}` → the same probe against `cmk hook agentSpawn` returned empty → `git log -S` proved the shape mismatch was original, not a drift). **Why no test ever saw it:** every dispatcher/bin routing test injects a FAKE `inject` dep — the default dep (the one production runs) was never exercised against the real `injectContext` — the exact cross-module gap the CLAUDE.md **integration-test rule** names (the Task-25 `generateId` precedent, recurred). And the "unit-green ≠ works-on-real-input" clause fired again: this is the live-test rule's poster case — one real command against real input found in seconds what 2,600 green tests structurally could not. **The fix:** both default inject deps read `r?.snapshot ?? ''`; locked by two **D-269 integration tests** (cli-cursor-hook-bin.test.js) that run the DEFAULT dep against the real `injectContext` over a real on-disk `context/MEMORY.md` for BOTH `cursor-hook sessionStart` and `hook agentSpawn`, asserting the fact text lands in the output; re-proven live in the sandbox (both legs now emit the full AUTHORITATIVE snapshot). **Honesty note on v0.4.0's gate:** the Kiro cut-gate recorded inject as live-verified — with this bug present, whatever memory-awareness that gate observed came from the STATIC surfaces (steering/AGENTS.md), not the dynamic snapshot; **the next Kiro gate must re-verify inject explicitly asserting the snapshot CONTENT appears** (a `cmk hook agentSpawn | grep <known-fact>` style check, not "the hook ran"). Also fixed from the same live sweep: uninstall left a frontmatter-only `.mdc` (an always-applied EMPTY rule — kit-shaped residue) → `removeKitOnlyInstructionResidue` deletes a kit-only instruction file, preserves any file carrying the user's own lines. _Relates Task 196 (the finder), Task 50/PR #212 (where the Kiro leg shipped broken), the integration-test rule + D-84/live-test rule (both fired), D-200 (the sibling "wired but silently inert" class), cli-cursor-hook-bin D-269 block. D-269._

## 2026-07-04 — D-268: Cursor memory landscape filed (Task 196 companion) — native Memories REMOVED (no coexistence problem + a real gap), mimir/memex are MCP-only, one watch-item trigger

- **🔎 NOTE (2026-07-04) — D-268: mid-Task-196 the user asked *"did you do research on cursor before you started?"* — the honest audit: the adapter's INTEGRATION surfaces were covered (the Task-50 seam research + fresh primary-source verification of cursor.com hooks/MCP/rules at task start), but the MARKET/COEXISTENCE layer was not checked until the question forced it. Filed as [research/2026-07-04-cursor-memory-landscape.md](../research/2026-07-04-cursor-memory-landscape.md) + SOURCES entries (mimir, memex, the Cursor platform-docs set).** Three durable findings: **(1) Cursor's native Memories feature was REMOVED in Cursor 2.1.x** (late 2025; docs page 404s, forum migration-to-Rules guidance) — static Rules are Cursor's ONLY built-in persistence, so (a) there is NO native-memory coexistence concern on Cursor (no ADR-0011/doctor-check analog needed — same posture as Kiro) and (b) the kit's Cursor adapter restores exactly the auto-capture loop Cursor users lost — positioning, not just breadth. **Watch-item trigger (D-248 style): re-open the coexistence question on the first Cursor changelog entry re-introducing native memory, or on a Cursor-user duplicate-capture report.** **(2) Cursor's "dynamic context discovery" (2026-01-06) is files-first fetch-on-demand** — independent validation of ADR-0002/the kit's files-first thesis; the hook payload's `transcript_path` (full searchable transcript) is a potential future capture substrate, deliberately NOT depended on (format undocumented). **(3) mimir + memex (both surfaced by the user) are the visible memory-for-Cursor competitor class and both are MCP-ONLY** — judgment-gated recall (the 2026-06-14 recall-triggering failure mode); the kit's hook-wired deterministic inject/capture + in-repo committed memory remain the differentiators. Candidate fold-ins noted in the research note without new tasks (per D-248: no trigger, no task): memex's bitemporal edges converge with shipped Task 66; its two-regime decay is noted for Task 190; mimir's recall-usage reinforcement is exactly the signal ADR-0017's two-axis judge governs (the D-253 line holds). _Relates Task 196 (in flight), D-257 (the lane), ADR-0011 (the Claude-side coexistence precedent this finding spares Cursor from), ADR-0002 (files-first, validated again), D-248 (the watch-item trigger), the 2026-06-14 + 2026-06-20 research notes. D-268._

## 2026-07-02 — D-260: the v0.4.4 "141a rider" dissolved — phase (a) had shipped in v0.3.x all along (the stale-entry class, one level deeper) + two Task-66 follow-up notes

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-07-03) — D-267: "lane EVERY task to a version" considered and REJECTED — the lane-or-trigger hybrid stays; the REAL gap was that triggers had no forcing function, closed by adding a TRIGGER-FIRED WALK as the first step of the D-248 minor-cut backlog sweep.** The user asked: *"what about laning every task to a version?"* **Why laning-everything loses:** (1) a lane on CONDITIONAL work (research-then-decide, fires-only-if-evidence tasks like 199/67/the D-260 fork) is a fabricated commitment — "later" wearing a version number; when the condition doesn't materialize the lane slips, and slipping lanes erode what a lane means; (2) **lanes already slip when reality changes — lived precedent:** Cursor was the LOCKED v0.4.1 slot and waited five patches (Task 167 took the slot); a lane is not more durable than a trigger; (3) it fights the one-differentiator-per-minor rule — pre-laning ~39 open tasks means guessing 6–8 minors deep, against the D-157/D-257 posture (digits stamped on cut, order shifts on real signal). **The healthy lifecycle is trigger-then-lane** (Task 196: demand-trigger → the friends-on-Cursor signal fired → D-257 laned it). **The genuine weakness the question exposed:** a lane has a built-in forcing function (the release happens); a named trigger only fires if someone NOTICES — and nothing walked the triggers asking "did any fire?" (196's trigger had in fact fired before the D-257 conversation noticed it — conversational luck, not process). **THE FIX (shipped as process, both homes):** the D-248 sweep now BEGINS with a **trigger-fired walk** — check every named trigger's condition; **fired → lane or explicit re-verdict (never silently deferred); not fired → keep + refresh stale conditions** — added as rule #3 under the CLAUDE.md D-248 rule and as a ★ pre-tag step in cut-gate.md (minor cuts only, with the sweep). Structural-graduation note: if fired-triggers keep getting missed despite the walk, the next step is machine-checkable trigger conditions (e.g. a `fires-when:` token the validator can partially evaluate) — per Prose-vs-enforcement; not built now. _Relates D-248 (the sweep this extends), D-256/Task 197 (the presence validator — this adds the CHECKING half), D-257/Task 196 (the fired-unnoticed precedent), D-157 (assigned-on-cut). D-267._

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-07-03) — D-266: the temporal sweep's WEEKLY cadence is under-ambitious — extend it to EVERY existing Haiku maintenance site (per-session; Task 198) and file write-time detection with in-conversation resolution as the durable design (Task 199). This EXPLICITLY REVISITS the SETTLED D-259's weekly-site choice, with new evidence.** The user's catch (2026-07-03): *"i always had a problem with that we only do it weekly, it's too long no?"* — and the honest audit agrees: the weekly cadence was **inherited from the convenient host site** (weekly-curate had the free Haiku ceiling), never derived from a freshness requirement; the acceptance case D-166 (the snapshot showing a stale state) is precisely about the misleading window a week leaves open. **The new evidence (per the revisit-only-with-new-evidence rule):** (1) **Microsoft's Memora** (ICML 2026; read in full — paper incl. appendices + cloned code, [research note](../research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md)) runs the SAME judgment (similarity candidates ≥0.80 → LLM judge) **at write time**, and its Appendix F shows judged consolidation stays a flat 16.5–22.2% of writes as the store grows — frequent judged consolidation is linear-cost and safe; (2) **the shipped sweep's own properties** (facts that did not exist when D-259 was written — the sweep hadn't been built): marker-incremental + `no-new-facts` short-circuits BEFORE any LLM call, so an idle session costs zero — cadence is ~free; (3) **live evidence from the v0.4.4 cut-gate:** the Vercel→Hetzner State pair sat both-live for days and Session-2 recall surfaced BOTH — the model disambiguated by judgment, not because the engine had resolved it. **What does NOT change:** D-259's judge/close semantics (search-retrieved candidates → one batched judge → event-time window-close) are untouched — only the SITES (198.1: SessionEnd + SessionStart-lazy, weekly as backstop) and the CANDIDATE source (198.2: title-embedding similarity when semantic is enabled, Memora's validated θ=0.80 as the reference; FTS fallback — also kills the D-259 FTS5 version-token-shredding wart). **Task 199** (design-first, D-248-triggered) is the Memora-inspired end-state — deterministic write-time DETECTION + the mention posture (D-215) + Claude-in-conversation as the judge + the user's yes as the gate (ADR-0018 shape): strictly better than Memora's silent write-time merge, which discards the moment of change our window-close preserves. **Also filed from the same review:** cue anchors + the mixed-key theorem + relaxed-frontier params → Task 176; the policy-retriever validation + episodic grouping → Task 149; the title-vs-content embedding bench → Task 178; the Fig-6 judge+merge template + the App-F over-consolidation warning → Task 95; the MemLoop convergence → Task 190 cross-ref. Process note: the first draft of the research note was written from the blog + 9 paper pages; the user's *"maybe you should re-read everything before you decide what is what"* forced the full-appendix + real-code read, which corrected the cue spec (1–3 × 2–4 words, RELATIONAL cues in the code), surfaced the App-F sensitivity table, and calibrated the title-embedding expectation (our rich facts aren't the fragmentation extreme their ablation punishes) — the Task-149 clone-and-read discipline, re-earned. _Relates D-259 (revisited — sites/candidates only), D-166 (the acceptance window), D-215/D-169 (the mention posture 199 rides), ADR-0018 (propose-and-approve), Tasks 66 [x]/198/199/149/176/178/95/190, the Memora research note + SOURCES entry. D-266._

- **🔧 FIX (2026-07-03) — D-265: the post-#253 main push went Sonar-RED (`new_security_rating` B) on `javascript:S4036` (PATH-resolution) at the Task-150 `git status` spawn — an ALREADY-TRIAGED-Safe class (D-128: "PATH is the user's own trust domain"), re-surfaced as new-code because the D-264 fix touched its lines. Encoded the triage durably in `sonar-project.properties`** (`sonar.issue.ignore.multicriteria` for S4036 on `packages/cli/src/**`, with the D-128 justification inline) instead of a per-issue UI review-click — the Task-140 "no token-gated ceremony" philosophy + the prose→structural preference applied to the scanner config. The spawn is a read-only `--no-optional-locks git status` under a 400ms leash; hardcoding git's path would break cross-platform. All other checks on the push were green. _Relates D-128 (the triage this encodes), D-254 (the sibling sonar-config decision-trail in the same file), D-264 (the diff that re-surfaced it), Task 150. D-265._

- **🐛 CUT-GATE FIND + FIX (2026-07-03) — D-264: the MEMORY-COMMIT PROPOSAL (Task 150 / MC1) was DROPPED on an EMPTY memory snapshot — so a brand-new user piling up their FIRST uncommitted `context/` files got no commit proposal, the exact moment it's most needed. TWO root-cause layers; the skill-review caught that my first fix addressed only the second. A v0.4.4 bug in the unreleased Task-150 feature — fixed in-lane.** Same class as D-263 (the wedge), found minutes later in the same cut-gate MC1 probe: **works-with-existing-state, no-ops-from-empty.**
  - **The two layers** (both in [`inject-context.mjs`](../../packages/cli/src/inject-context.mjs)): **(1) the upstream gate — the ACTUAL root cause (skill-review B1):** `commitProposal` was computed only when `rawBlocks.length > 0`, i.e. only when some tier block had injectable content — but the proposal reflects GIT DIRTINESS of `context/`, which is independent of whether memory is injectable; for a truly-empty-memory user the proposal was `''` before any concatenation ran. Fixed: compute it UNCONDITIONALLY (`buildCommitProposal` self-gates on `.git` + zero-dirty-count, so non-git projects still spawn nothing). The `temporalMention` KEEPS its gate (it genuinely needs prior facts to supersede). **(2) the §4 concatenation:** `body === '' ? '' : PREAMBLE+volatile+body` threw the volatile lines away on an empty body. Fixed: with a body → `PREAMBLE + volatile + body` (unchanged); empty body + pending volatile → the action line(s) ALONE, no preamble (a proposal is an action prompt, not an authoritative-memory claim); empty + no volatile → `''`.
  - **The review-caught process failure (recorded honestly):** my first fix was ONLY layer (2) — a correct-but-DEAD branch, because layer (1) forced `volatile=''` in the headline case — and my first regression test **green-passed against the unfixed code** (it blanked 7 of the fixture's 8 files, missing `context.local/overrides.md`, so the body was never actually empty — the same fixture-masks-the-bug class, D-169/D-84, recursing INSIDE the fix for it). The `code-review-excellence` pass (DON'T-MERGE, B1+B2) caught both: it stash-tested my test against main and watched it pass. **Also mine to own:** my own isolated probe HAD shown the truth (empty snapshot with the fix applied) and I waved it off as a harness artifact instead of chasing it — the observe-what-the-tool-does discipline says the probe IS the signal. **Fixed properly:** the gate removed (B1), the test repaired to blank ALL 8 fixture files + dirty via `memory/INDEX.md` (under the `context/` pathspec but never injected, so the body stays genuinely empty) + a no-preamble assertion — and **verified red-on-main** (stash the src fix → `AssertionError: expected '' to match /uncommitted/i` → restore → green), the TDD red step the first version skipped.
  - **Verified:** inject-context suite 59/59; full suite green; cap composition intact (the volatile reserves were already computed independently — §7.1.2 unchanged); the empty-snapshot-stays-empty contract intact (non-git sandboxes have no proposal). Stress 5/5 on the near-final code; final-code stress re-run before merge. Fixed on branch `task-mc1-proposal-empty-snapshot`. _Relates D-263 (the wedge sibling — same empty-state class, same fixture-mask), Task 150 / ADR-0018, MC1 (the cut-gate probe), D-169/D-84 (fixture-masking — now TWICE in one day, once inside a fix), the two-pass-review discipline (the skill pass caught what self-review + a green suite could not). D-264._

- **🐛 CUT-GATE FIND + FIX (2026-07-03) — D-263: the WEDGE could not bootstrap from EMPTY — the Stop-hook auto-extract (and `cmk lessons promote`) silently DROPPED a brand-new user's FIRST cross-project rule because the promote path required the user tier to already exist. Fixed to scaffold the tier on first GATED promote. This is the wedge (B3/B4) — the kit's headline cross-project value — broken for every genuinely new user, surfaced only because the v0.4.4 cut-gate was the first to test the wedge truly from zero.** Two layers, one root cause (`existsSync`-guards-instead-of-ensure), both fixed:
  - **Layer 1 — the bin** ([`packages/cli/bin/cmk-auto-extract.mjs`](../../packages/cli/bin/cmk-auto-extract.mjs) + the plugin twin): `const userDir = existsSync(userDirBase) ? userDirBase : undefined` — the Stop hook passed `userDir` ONLY if `~/.claude-memory-kit/` already existed. A brand-new user has none, so `userDir` was `undefined` → the inline persona-promote block (`if (userDir)` in auto-extract.mjs) was skipped entirely → the first cross-project rule vanished. Fixed: pass `userDir` UNCONDITIONALLY (the comment even said the quiet part — *"skip gracefully on a fresh machine"* — which is exactly wrong for a wedge whose job is to FILL a fresh machine).
  - **Layer 2 — the shared promote fn** (`promoteCandidatesToUserTier` in [`auto-persona.mjs`](../../packages/cli/src/auto-persona.mjs)): even WITH a `userDir`, if the target scratchpad (HABITS/LESSONS/USER.md) didn't exist, `ensureSectionExists` returned `{error:'no-file'}` → routed to `not-promoted-no-file` (queued, never landed). Fixed: `initUserTier({userTier})` right before `ensureSectionExists`, gated behind the confidence/recurrence check that already passed — so the tier materializes EXACTLY when a real durable cross-project fact is landing, never speculatively (the D-74 "don't touch the user's system without cause" posture; the user's design steer — Option "create only when a candidate clears the gate"). One spot fixes all three callers (explicit `cmk lessons promote`, inline Stop-hook, weekly janitor).
  - **Severity + provenance:** NOT a v0.4.4 regression — `git show v0.4.3` has the identical guard; latent since the auto-extract bin was written. **Masked by every prior test AND every prior cut-gate** because they all pre-scaffolded the user tier (the D-169/D-84 "the fixture builds the thing it's checking" class): the existing `weeklyCurate` test *"creates the user tier if absent, then promotes (friend never ran init-user-tier)"* even documented the intended behavior — but the fix lived only in `weeklyCurate`'s own scaffold, never in the shared promote fn, so the inline + explicit paths still dropped it. This cut-gate was the FIRST from-zero test (the user's real `~/.claude-memory-kit/` was moved aside for the wedge check) — the exact D-84 "unit-green ≠ works-on-real-input" gap the live-test rule exists to catch. **Two suite tests that PINNED the old bug** (`not-promoted-no-file → nothing created`) were updated to the corrected contract (genuinely-wrong tests, per the "fix the code not the test — unless the test is wrong" rule). **Verified:** full suite 2573/0 (skip-live) + true-from-empty live on the real bin (user dir ABSENT → promote → CREATED, rule lands trust:high/user-explicit in HABITS/LESSONS § Working Style / Cross-Project Lessons). Stress gate pending before merge. Fixed on branch `task-wedge-bootstrap-from-empty`. _Relates B3/B4 (the wedge cut-gate checks this restores), D-260 (the sibling no-cron userDir-coverage gap — same "userDir only reaches some paths" family), D-74 (don't-touch-system-without-cause, the scoping posture), D-169/D-84 (fixture-masks-the-bug + live-test-every-task), Task 61 (inline promote), Task 45 (auto-persona). D-263._

- **🔎 CUT-GATE FIND + RESOLUTION (2026-07-02) — D-262: the v0.4.4 cut-gate `Use skill /memory-write?` popup that "stuck" in the VS Code Claude panel was caused by UPDATING THE VS CODE CLAUDE-CODE EXTENSION WITHOUT RESTARTING — the running session had the new binary (CC 2.1.198) but a stale/uninitialized `PermissionRequest` hook pipeline, so the auto-approve didn't fire. A full VS Code RESTART fixed it (the panel auto-dismisses). NOT a kit regression, NOT an extension bug, NOT a v0.4.4 blocker. The D-213 auto-approver works in BOTH the terminal AND the VS Code extension — it just needs the session (re)loaded after any change to what provides the hook.** The user hit the sticking `memory-write` skill-approval dialog in the panel during Session 1. **The trigger (the user's own diagnosis, more precise than mine): the VS Code Claude-Code extension had just been UPDATED and the window was never restarted** — so the session was running post-update but with the pre-update/uninitialized hook state. **The RESOLUTION (the user's restart test on `cut-gate-coldopen19`): after fully quitting + reopening VS Code, the SAME folder / SAME config / SAME CC 2.1.198 → the popup AUTO-DISMISSES.** Decisive datum: a genuine "extension never fires the hook" bug would NOT be fixed by a restart. The class is the ordinary "hooks load at session start; after you change WHAT PROVIDES the hook (an extension update, a mid-session `cmk install`), the session must reload before the hook is active" — exactly what the `cmk install` banner means by *"Restart Claude Code to activate."*
  - **SUPERSEDED mid-investigation (kept per the decision-trail rule):** I first concluded this was upstream CC bug **#13203** (*"PermissionRequest hooks do not fire in the VS Code extension"*), reasoning from a terminal-vs-panel A/B that showed panel-sticks / terminal-auto-dismisses on two folders (`coldopen-v043`, `coldopen19`). **That conclusion was WRONG** — the confound was INSTALL-TIMING, not host surface: the terminal `claude` sessions were started FRESH (after install, hook loaded), while the panel sessions predated the install (hook not loaded). Same single cause, mis-read as two mechanisms. The restart test collapsed the A/B. #13203/#31285/#59718 are real tracker items but are NOT what bit this cut-gate (a restart wouldn't fix those).
  - **My process failure (recorded so next-session-me doesn't repeat it):** I answered from ASSUMPTION repeatedly before recalling D-213 + reading the actual files — with the memory-hint literally telling me to recall — and then, once I DID find a plausible A/B, I over-committed to the "#13203 extension bug" story and even researched a non-existent "no kit fix possible" conclusion, when the cheap disambiguating test (RESTART, which the user proposed) settled it in 30 seconds. The lesson is DOUBLE: (1) recall before deriving (the kit's whole thesis); (2) run the cheapest disambiguating experiment BEFORE writing the expensive conclusion — the user drove BOTH corrections (*"you dont remember but we fixed it"*, *"no you are wrong"*, *"it worked in the last cut-gate before this"*, *"maybe do restart?"*).
  - **DECISION:** (a) **NOT a v0.4.4 tag blocker** — the kit ships byte-identical to the working v0.4.3; prompt-free capture works in the panel AND terminal once the hook is loaded. (b) **The real, durable takeaway is an OPERATIONAL one for the cut-gate:** after `cmk install` in a gate folder, **RESTART Claude Code (fully quit the VS Code window) BEFORE running the R2 / prompt-free checks** — otherwise the just-wired `PermissionRequest` hook isn't loaded and R2 falsely appears to fail. This is a cut-gate.md note, not a code change. (c) The D-213 auto-approver is confirmed working on CC 2.1.198 in the VS Code extension (with a loaded session) — no drift, no fix needed. _Relates D-213/Task 172 (the auto-approver — confirmed working on 2.1.198, both surfaces), D-209/D-211 (CC-permission-drift siblings — this was NOT one of those), D-80 (R2 precedent), the recall-before-derive + observe-what-the-tool-does + cheapest-experiment-first disciplines (this entry is a live failure-then-recovery of all three). D-262._

- **📝 NOTE ×3 (2026-07-02) — D-260:** **(1) The D-253a sweep re-laned Task 141 phase (a) as a v0.4.4 rider — but it SHIPPED 2026-06-12 (PR #169, D-134):** HC-8 native-bindings, the install-time ask, the README npm-12 note, the CLI.md doc — all live since v0.3.x; sub-checkbox `141a [x]` the whole time. The sweep read the PARENT `[ ]` (held open by phase (b)'s named trigger) and never checked the sub-entries — the D-253a stale-entry class one level deeper: a parent held open by ONE phase reads as "nothing shipped." Sweep rule addendum: a phase-structured task's verdict must check PER-PHASE checkboxes, not the parent box. v0.4.4 = Task 66 + Task 150 only. **(2) autoPersona-on-the-lazy-path stays a CLOSED fork with a named trigger (D-248):** the Task-66 skill review surfaced that only the cron binary passes userDir to weeklyCurate, so autoPersona/U-drain never run for no-cron users; the Task-66 fix scoped U-tier coverage to the SWEEPS only (`sweepUserDir` seam, `defaultUserDir()` at production entry points). Re-open trigger: a no-cron user reports an empty cross-project persona (the E1 wedge failing for them), OR the v0.5 loop work touches the weekly cycle anyway. **(3) The D-69 hazard near-miss is worth naming:** the first finding-3 fix put a `homedir()` default INSIDE weeklyCurate — every userDir-less test would have walked the maintainer's REAL user tier (damage-checked: none occurred). The rule it re-affirms: `homedir()`/env fallbacks belong at PRODUCTION ENTRY POINTS (CLI actions, hook bins, cron binaries), never inside library functions — now documented on `defaultUserDir()` itself. _Relates D-253a (the sweep class), D-134/PR #169 (the actual 141a ship), D-162 (141b rejected), D-248 (named triggers), D-69 (the test-real-state class), Task 66 review findings 3. D-260._

## 2026-07-02 — D-259: the 66.2/66.4 contradiction-detection design SETTLED BY MEASUREMENT, not interview — the user's "can't you research and test?" executed

- **✅ DECISION (2026-07-02) — D-259: the assistant proposed grilling the user on the 66.2/66.4 forks; the user redirected — *"why do you need to grill me? can't you do some research and test and then see what works?"* — and three experiments on the kit's OWN 1,246-fact dogfood corpus + a live-Haiku judge settled every fork ([bake-off note](../research/2026-07-02-contradiction-detection-bakeoff-real-corpus.md)).** The verdicts, each carried by a number: **(1) lexical pairing is DEAD** — 776k all-pairs Jaccard finds ZERO true contradictions at any threshold (the only 0.4+ pairs are restatements = the 151 recurrence signal); **(2) the real class is state-progression chains** (v0.3.2: 18 facts "scope locked"→"published to npm", none superseded, within-chain Jaccard 0.00–0.21 — subject-shared, word-disjoint, which is WHY (1) is structurally blind); **(3) a ONE-batched-call Haiku judge is reliable and near-free** — 10/10 twice on real pairs, ~$0.004/10 pairs, perfect SUPERSEDES/DUPLICATE/COEXIST separation. **The settled design:** write-time candidates via the kit's OWN search (BM25 OR-query over title tokens; FTS5 shreds `v0.3.2`→`[v0,3,2]`, so query construction is the named build detail) → queue pairs (existing conflicts-queue, new `temporal` kind) → the EXISTING weekly-curate Haiku site judges in one batch (no new hot-path spawn; the auto-extract 60s-ceiling composition stays untouched) → SUPERSEDES closes the old window by EVENT-TIME code (LLM never decides which wins), DUPLICATE routes to the recurrence bump, COEXIST drops → the demo surface is the next SessionStart mention (D-215 heads-up posture). **Two sub-decisions with trail:** `state_key` is DERIVED (search), NOT a declared frontmatter field (the D-169 dead-weight class — same reasoning as D-258's caller-set finding; §16.18's window arithmetic unchanged, only the detection input pivots); **D-221 (captain-claw tension-holding) CLOSED with a negative result** — zero genuine simultaneous-disagreement pairs in 1,246 real facts; latest-wins stands for State facts; re-open only if live judged queues ever produce a real conflicting-COEXIST class. _Relates D-109 (bake-off discipline), D-166 (Bug 2 = the acceptance case, now measured at scale in our own corpus), D-221 (closed), D-258/D-258a, Task 66.2/66.4. D-259._

## 2026-07-02 — D-258a: how "built flagged" was executed for the auto-extract expiry suggestion (NOTE)

- **📝 NOTE (2026-07-02) — D-258a: D-258 prescribed the LLM-suggested expiry be "built flagged + live-validated, never the silent default"; the shipped interpretation is NARROW-SCOPE + PROMPT-GUARD + DOCUMENTED + CUT-GATE-GATED, not a config flag.** Rationale: a config flag nobody flips is the D-169 dead-weight anti-pattern in a different coat — the automatic path would never populate. Instead the suggestion ships ON but quadruple-bounded: (1) the prompt scopes `expires:` to Plan/Event facts whose TURN states a concrete date, with an explicit "NEVER guess or infer a date the turn does not state; when in doubt, omit" rule (Door-3.5-pinned); (2) the parser keeps only strict-ISO values (anything else silently omits — a bad date can't kill a capture NOR write a wrong expiry); (3) the capability is documented (CHANGELOG/CLI.md/MCP.md), not silent; (4) tasks.md 66.3 carries a named CUT-GATE item — live-validate no-invented-dates on real turns before the v0.4.4 tag; if live behavior shows guessing, the fallback is demoting the prompt instruction (or a config-off) BEFORE tag. _Relates D-258 (the design), D-169 (populated-path), Task 66.3. D-258a._

## 2026-07-02 — D-258: Task 66.3's expiry semantics SETTLED from a verified reference set (mem0 + LangGraph checked at primary source; the user's "did you check?" fired again)

- **✅ DECISION (2026-07-02) — D-258: the `expires_at` enforcement design (Task 66.3, v0.4.4) is settled on three convergent calls, each grounded in a primary-source check made AFTER the user asked "did you check how other projects do it so we have a reference?"** (the assistant had stated "mem0 ships TTL" from training memory; the check both confirmed the substance AND corrected a detail — mem0 expired memories are **hidden from retrieval, never deleted** (`show_expired` recovers), not "auto-removed" as first relayed). The reference set: mem0 Platform (`expiration_date`, caller-set, hidden-at-read) + mem0 OSS cookbook (`expires_on` metadata + manual prune) + LangGraph store TTL (`default_ttl` + `refresh_on_read` lease-renewal + background sweeper; no sweep configured = nothing expires) + the in-base graphiti (event-driven invalidation, never-delete, view-filter) + letta (no TTL; sleeptime rewrite). **The three settled calls:** (1) **WHO sets: the caller/writer** — the only precedented path; NO surveyed system lets the LLM set expiry, so auto-extract SUGGESTING expiry for `Plan`/`Event` facts is the kit's unprecedented increment — built flagged + live-validated, never the silent default (and D-169's populated-path criterion binds: the field must demonstrably populate without a human running anything, else it's dead weight). (2) **WHAT at expiry: hide + tombstone, never hard-delete** — mem0/graphiti converge; matches the kit's settled D-163 posture. (3) **WHERE: read-time filter AND curate-sweep, not sweep-only** — LangGraph's nothing-expires trap is the exact failure the read-time half prevents. **Explicitly rejected:** `refresh_on_read` lease-renewal on `expires_at` — that's staleness-TTL semantics (the scratchpad 14-day drop already covers it); conflating would silently extend "demo is Friday" on every recall. Also NOTED (the user, same exchange): zero-code-paths-write-`expires_at` means we're first in OUR repo, not first in the field — absence of local precedent is evidence of neither correctness nor wrongness. _Research note: [2026-07-02-expiry-ttl-precedents-mem0-langgraph.md](../research/2026-07-02-expiry-ttl-precedents-mem0-langgraph.md); relates Task 66.1/66.3, D-163, D-169, D-251. D-258._

## 2026-07-02 — ADR-0017 ACCEPTED: the learn-loop target design adopted (SYSTEM-MAP §6, "our Figure 2") (D-252)

- **✅ DECISION (2026-07-02) — D-252: ADR-0017 finalized Proposed→Accepted; the kit ADOPTS the SYSTEM-MAP §6 target design — the learn-loop closed, every wire research-cited.** **The arc (one sentence):** the user brought ONE paper (U-Mem, D-251) → its system-reading produced the thesis (a session is a bounded agent run; the kit is the cross-session runtime; the learning signal is inherently cross-session) → two research passes (47-system failure survey + 10-system/4-lens comparative-judgment study) earned the constraints → the superimposition ("U-Mem's Figure 2, redrawn as OURS") became SYSTEM-MAP §6 → this decision adopts it. **The deciding criterion, made explicit: HONEST memory — the kit never lies about how much it knows** (of ~57 systems surveyed, every learner cheats with a benchmark oracle and every non-cheater ships an inert utility socket; nobody ships epistemic honesty as a feature — the kit's actual differentiator). **The six load-bearing calls** (full text in the ADR): (1) TWO rankable objects never conflated — fact-utility (`trust_score`) may blend into ranking; method-judgments (`judgment_*.md`, provisional/n_episodes/confounds/decay) NEVER auto-rank; (2) the judge is the per-host adapter — signals are a portfolio, AUTOMATIC-first, human-OPTIONAL, BOTH-polarity, recurrence never read as reinforcement (D-246/Task 181); (3) the blend closes the loop in SEARCH (confidence-gated, facts-only), inject's hot path stays enum — §20.3 revised NARROWLY with new evidence, not reversed; the score also gates SURVIVAL (ExpeL — the inert-socket fix); (4) the FEEDBACK-SCREEN is a build prerequisite — feedback is a second unscreened input channel (Poison_Guard covers writes only); rate-limit + burst-hold (a systemically-wrong judge must quarantine, not dampen good memories) + audit + floor; (5) failures RETAINED as typed anti-patterns, not erased (Memento/REMEMBERER/Negative-Knowledge — demote-not-evict extended to the loop); (6) the RECALL-LOG (memclaw `related_ids`) is the one genuinely-new primitive — the attribution prerequisite. **Build = the §6 phases** (0 shipped in v0.4.3; 1 = the oracle-free wedge on existing hooks; 2 = blend + survival gate; 3 = host-dependent); Task 185 lanes them. **Guards that survive into the record:** the SYSTEM-MAP §5 unsolved region stays BLANK (no small-sample "A>B ranking" may ever be called earned; if it's solved, it's because the HOST changed — Task 50/127); recurrence is the system's fuel (the one variable behind 151/181/U-Mem-r=0.888/the scale floor/189). _Provenance: the 2026-07-01→02 research arc; the thesis and the three load-bearing corrections (system-not-parts, two-axes, both-polarity) were the user's. Relates D-251, ADR-0016/0017, SYSTEM-MAP §§1-8, design §20.3 (amendment lands with Phase 2), Tasks 55/66/95/179/180/181/188/189 + 50/127, the 2 research notes + raw archives. D-252._

## 2026-07-01 — U-Mem (arXiv 2602.22406) VALIDATES the no-score-hot-path-ranking decision + 2 new out-of-the-box ideas (D-251)

- **📚 NOTE + DECISION (2026-07-01) — D-251: the first external-source triage (the user's D-248 ingestion workflow) — "Towards Autonomous Memory Agents" (U-Mem, NUS, arXiv:2602.22406) — surfaced 9 landing spots; its headline idea VALIDATES a decision we shipped 2 days ago, and two out-of-the-box ideas are genuinely new.** **Provenance-corrected first:** a Facebook post attributed it to *Oxford* and framed it as "self-debate / ask other models"; primary source = **NUS**, framework = **U-Mem**, and the post OMITTED the more-novel half (Thompson-sampling retrieval). Read the source, not the post. **The investigation the user asked for (severity-first, not paper-framing):** U-Mem's core retrieval contribution — Semantic-Aware Thompson Sampling — exists to fix "cold-start inequity" (a new fact never surfaces under greedy utility-ranking → never earns feedback → buried forever). I traced our v0.4.3 `trust_score` consumers to check if we have that bug: **we don't.** `cmk search`/`mk_search` rank by `ORDER BY observations_fts.rank` (BM25), `minTrust` filters on the `trust` ENUM not the float; `inject-context` ranks by the coarse enum and its code (L507-510) EXPLICITLY warns that a `trust_score` rank "= the cautionary bug." And **design §20.3 (written for Task 151, BEFORE we saw this paper) already reached U-Mem's conclusion**: *"systems that rank-and-sweep by a score (MemoryOS-LFU, MemOS-top-N) are the CAUTIONARY ones — exactly the Task-151 bug."* So the kit and an independent research group **converged on the same risk and picked opposite sides**: U-Mem "rank by utility, then fix cold-start with Thompson sampling"; us "don't rank by utility in the hot path, so cold-start never arises." **U-Mem is CONFIRMING evidence for §20.3, not new evidence to reverse it** (the "revisit SETTLED only with new evidence" rule — this is validation). **The 9-spot harvest:** (1) cold-start/Thompson → validates §20.3 (trigger-gated: only matters IF §20.3 is ever reversed); (2) advantage-update `Δ=with−without` cancels task-difficulty → enrich Task 66 (our rule is absolute ±); (3) failure→fix Global-Procedural/Local-Corrective types → 3rd source for Task 55's error→fix type; (4) full teacher→tools→human cascade → FUTURE SEED on Task 127 (agent-facing companion, v0.5+; trigger: "a non-interactive/autonomous-agent consumer exists"); (5) **the cascade's user-escalation CUT → NEW near-term idea near Task 55**: when Claude is uncertain → ask the user → auto-capture the resolution so it's never re-asked (the user IS the "teacher trajectory"); (6) their Eliminate/Consolidate/Refine/Retain maintenance prompt (appendix Fig 12) → template for the deferred G5 semantic-dedup; (7) **⭐ NEW: recurrence = memory ROI** (Pearson r=0.888 between task-similarity and gain) — quantifies the kit's whole thesis AND warns value is near-zero for one-off work; a "measure-your-own-recurrence / tell the user how much memory is helping" differentiator no surveyed product ships; (8) **⭐ NEW: "you can't self-diagnose a failure without a correct reference"** — our auto-extract reflects on a session ALONE, the exact naïve move the paper shows hallucinates causes; reframes the user-correction moment as the highest-value capture signal in the kit; (9) marginal-contribution self-pruning → far-future park (trigger: "a measurable per-session outcome signal exists to A/B against"). **Net: no shipped bug — 1 validation, 3 enrichments (66/55/G5), 1 future seed (127), 2 new ideas, 1 far-future park, 1 reference artifact (the appendix prompts are verified primary-source prompt engineering).** All findings feed the Task 185 backlog sweep for final lane assignment. _Provenance: the user brought the paper as an external source to mine ("steal ideas, make tasks better"). Research note: [`2026-07-01-umem-autonomous-memory.md`](../research/2026-07-01-umem-autonomous-memory.md). Relates design §20.3 (VALIDATED), ADR-0016, Tasks 55/66/127, gap G5, D-248 (the ingestion workflow this exercises). D-251._

## 2026-07-01 — SonarCloud analyzer crashes on cli-forget.test.js (flaky-red gate) — Task 187 (D-250)

- **🐞 BUG (upstream, not ours) + SELF-CORRECTION (2026-07-01) — D-250: the v0.4.3 doc-commit's SonarCloud check went red, and my first read of it was WRONG — corrected under the user's "did you actually check the error?" push.** **The failure:** SonarCloud's bundled TypeScript-ESLint analyzer throws `Error: Debug Failure. No error for last overload signature` while linting `tests/cli-forget.test.js:95` under rule `sonarjs/S2699` ("tests should include assertions") — the crash is deep in Sonar's own `server.cjs` `getResolvedSignature` (TS overload resolution), a TypeScript compiler internal-invariant assertion the SonarJS bridge surfaces on certain call-signature shapes. Line 95 is a plain `it(...)` block; **nothing in our code is malformed** — the analyzer is unstable on the file. `cli-forget.test.js` was NOT in the docs commit. **My TWO wrong claims, corrected (the lazy-framing class, caught by the user):** (1) I first guessed it was the D-155 HF-cache coverage-zero flake — WRONG: the HF cache HIT, the semantic tests PASSED, `coverage/lcov.info` WAS written + analyzed. (2) I re-ran it, saw green, and called it "transient — self-cleared" — WRONG: I checked the exit code, not the log. The re-run's log shows the `Debug Failure` **RECURRED (2×, identical)** — attempt 1 ABORTED on the crash (→ red gate), attempt 2 TOLERATED it (analyzed the other files, skipped the unparseable one → `ANALYSIS SUCCESSFUL` → green gate). So the crash is **PERSISTENT + non-deterministic (abort-vs-tolerate)**, NOT transient. **Impact — honest:** v0.4.3 IS correctly published (docs-only commit; all AUTHORITATIVE CI green — suite/coverage/lint/CodeQL/security/cross-OS 14/15; npm 0.4.3 + provenance + GitHub Release live; SonarCloud is ADVISORY, non-gating). But the analyzer will keep flaky-redding future pushes until fixed → a real (minor) infra task, NOT "ignore it." **Fix (Task 187):** exclude the file from Sonar's TS analysis (`sonar-project.properties` `sonar.exclusions` — it already excludes bin/scripts/fixtures; add the crashing test) OR wait for the upstream SonarJS bridge fix + re-include. **Lesson (re-affirms the rule):** "it re-ran green" is not "I checked the error" — a green exit code can mask a recurring crash the tool merely tolerated; read the LOG, not the status. _Relates D-155 (the DIFFERENT Sonar coverage flake I wrongly pattern-matched to), the lazy-framing rule (both wrong claims were it), the "did you check?" load-bearing question, Task 187. D-250._

## 2026-07-01 — ONE doc-drift rule replaces N partial mechanisms (D-249)

- **✅ DECISION (2026-07-01) — D-249: unify doc-coverage into ONE per-change walk over a COMPLETE source-of-truth manifest, replacing the N overlapping partial mechanisms.** **The problem (the user's three-part catch):** (1) *"'because you asked the right question twice' is not how to work"* — the v0.4.3 docs went complete only because the user interrogated repeatedly; (2) *"this is redundant, why don't we have one rule to rule them all?"* — doc-coverage was 4 validators (`validate-doc-completeness`/`-registry`/`-index-completeness`/`-references`) + 2 prose rules + a manual pre-tag gate, **overlapping** (README/CHANGELOG governed 3×) yet **gap-ridden** (design.md, glossary.md, memory-lifecycle-map.md + ~10 more living docs had NO check); (3) *"there are more docs than these"* — the source-of-truth table listed ~18 docs but the repo has ~30 LIVING docs (of 159 total; the other ~125 are frozen records). **Proven by the fix itself:** v0.4.3 shipped THREE stale docs — design.md (missing the 182/183 index-contract), glossary.md (missing every 151 term: recurrence-gate/trust-score/demote-not-evict), memory-lifecycle-map.md (still described the pre-151 user-tier write-lock) — none caught by any mechanism; all found + fixed only via the user's interrogation. **The fix (both halves):** (a) JUDGMENT layer = ONE binding per-change walk over the source-of-truth table (now completed as the full living-docs manifest + an explicit frozen-RECORDS exemption list — records like `docs/research/`/`docs/adr/` are history, never "updated to match code"), run as a self-review step + re-confirmed at the pre-tag gate (the *same* walk, not two lists); (b) STRUCTURAL layer = Task 186 (revised) consolidates the 4 validators into one manifest-driven `validate-docs.mjs`. **Honest boundary:** a validator checks existence/link/registration/verb-coverage; content-staleness (design.md-describes-old-behavior) is not lintable → stays the walk's judgment. So the walk is the primary rule; the validator removes machinery-redundancy + closes existence-gaps. The old "Document user-facing capabilities" (D-17) rule is now a *row* of the walk (kept for its precedent + timing nuance), not a separate mechanism. **Chosen over** patching a 4th mechanism (a `validate-design-coverage.mjs` for design.md alone — would have made the fragmentation worse, the exact anti-pattern). _Provenance: the user's 2026-07-01 pre-tag doc audit. Relates D-17 (subsumed), D-120 (validate-doc-completeness), D-160 (validate-index-completeness), the "Single source of truth" + "Prose rules vs enforcement" kernels, Task 186. D-249._

## 2026-07-01 — the backlog has no forcing function: deferred tasks need a NAMED trigger + a cut-time sweep (D-248)

- **✅ DECISION (2026-07-01) — D-248: every deferred task must carry a NAMED, checkable trigger, and every minor cut sweeps the backlog for a verdict (build → CLAUDE.md binding rule).** **The problem (the user's catch):** laning tasks as "decide when it's ready" / "backlog-no-version-yet" has NO forcing function — "ready" never arrives on its own, so tasks pile up (verified: ~18 open tasks in `research-then-decide` / `needs-deeper-design` / `GO-NO-GO` / `backlog-no-version-yet` limbo, some since v0.1, with NO section anywhere scheduling when they get decided). The user 2026-07-01: *"it's never ready to ship until we decide on it — this is why we have a lot of tasks since v0.1 still not shipped; when are we supposed to decide?"* **The insight:** the kit ALREADY invented the right pattern — design §16's v0.1.x candidates carry an explicit **"Ship trigger: <concrete condition>"** (a bug surfaces in X / a 4th consumer needs Y / a user reports Z). That pattern works for deferred CODE but was never applied to the design/research backlog, which used non-triggers ("later", "when ready"). **The fix (2 halves):** (1) **named trigger, never "later"** — a deferral must state a checkable condition ("when Task 66 ships", "when 3 users ask"), generalizing the §16 Ship-trigger convention to ALL deferrals; (2) **cut-time backlog sweep** — before tagging any MINOR, walk the deferred tasks and give each a verdict (pull-in / keep-deferred-with-trigger / kill), with a hard rule that no task crosses TWO consecutive minors without a verdict (auto-flag kill-or-commit). Manual interim; a `validate-backlog-triggers.mjs` is the structural graduation if the backlog keeps rotting (per "Prose rules vs enforcement"). **Chosen over** a build-the-validator-now option (named-trigger is fuzzy to lint — start with the discipline, add the validator on evidence it's needed) and a decide-the-18-now-no-rule option (fixes today, not the recurrence). _Provenance: the user's 2026-07-01 "when are we supposed to decide?" during the v0.4.3 laning of the cut-gate findings. Relates design §16 (the Ship-trigger pattern this generalizes), D-157 (the digit tracks shipments — the sibling rule), the "Decision-trail preservation" + "Prose rules vs enforcement" rules._

## 2026-07-01 — v0.4.3 cut-gate Session 3: cold-open PASSES, but exposes two real search bugs (→ Tasks 182 + 183)

- **🐛 BUG + NOTE (2026-07-01) — D-247: the Session-3 cold-open (E1, "the gate that matters most") PASSED — a brand-new project scaffolded the user's uv/ruff/.venv/layered/TDD way with no prompting, driven by the injected persona — but the user's pushback ("search underperformed is an understatement — retrieval is the WHOLE point") drove a diagnosis that found TWO real, pre-existing search bugs.** **Bug 182 (the real one): promoted persona facts are UNSEARCHABLE.** `listObservationSources` (`index-rebuild.mjs:71-77`) indexes `<tier>/MEMORY.md` + `<tier>/{memory,fragments}/`, but `cmk lessons promote` writes the trait into the user-tier `HABITS.md`/`USER.md`/`LESSONS.md` scratchpads — which are in NEITHER indexed location. So the index source and the promote target don't overlap → the persona is invisible to `cmk search`, even in-session. PROVEN: in `cut-gate19`, `cmk search "always use uv never pip"` returns the PROJECT-tier fact but never the `HABITS.md` copy (`U-JXaKDYXT`); `fragments/` is empty. Masked until now because same-project search still finds the ORIGINAL project-tier fact; only the cold-open (a DIFFERENT project, where the persona is the ONLY place the rule lives) exposed it. **Bug 183: the scaffold `(example)` bullets are indexed + returned** — in a fresh project with no real facts, `mk_search` for the user's preferences returned ONLY the example placeholders (`P-KU3aNBX9` "deprecate /api/v1", score 0.008), actively misleading. **CRITICAL — NEITHER is a v0.4.3 regression, and the cold-open still WORKS:** cross-project persona is delivered by INJECTION (the SessionStart snapshot loads `HABITS.md` into context — that's how the cold-open scaffolded correctly), NOT by search. Task 151 didn't touch or break search; these are old gaps the fresh-project cold-open surfaced. The design-line "Cross-project search deferred to v0.2" (tasks.md:1041) is the SEPARATE `--all-projects` feature — 182 is the distinct in-project-persona-unsearchable bug. **DECISION: ship v0.4.3 (the persona works via injection, the headline is proven); 182 + 183 are the follow-up bugs.** **Also filed Task 184** (the user's catch): the `--all-projects` cross-project search deferral had sat as an un-scoped v0.1.0 one-liner (tasks.md:1041) — the cold-open made its case (a fresh project can't SEARCH prior-project facts, only the hand-promoted persona slice), so it's now a real trackable design task. 184 ≠ 182: 182 is "the persona isn't indexed in-project" (a bug); 184 is "search across DIFFERENT projects' indexes" (a deferred feature). **Honest framing correction (self-flagged):** the assistant's first framing ("search underperformed here, a nit") was the lazy-framing class — retrieval IS the product; the user was right to reject it. The correct frame: "promoted persona facts are structurally unsearchable + example bullets pollute a fresh project." _Provenance: the user's v0.4.3 cut-gate Session-3 catch. Relates Task 76 (the promote writer), 46/65 (search), 182, 183, D-246 (the sibling 151 gap the same session found)._

## 2026-07-01 — v0.4.3 cut-gate: Task 151 verified live + a recurrence-vs-adherence gap found (→ Task 181)

- **✅ NOTE (2026-07-01) — D-246: the v0.4.3 cut-gate ran clean through §4d (Task 151 = PR1–PR5 all PASS live), AND surfaced a real design gap in the recurrence gate — filed as Task 181, NOT a v0.4.3 blocker.** The gate was run against the REAL installed 0.4.3 (`cmk` global, packed from main): §0–1 scaffold (G0–G7), §2 Session 1 (18 rich facts captured, correct user-explicit-vs-auto-extract classification, ZERO username leak despite `C:\Users\<name>\…` all over the session), §3 capture (B3–B7 graduation reactive + proactive), §4 explicit (C1–C6 + FQ1), and **§4d the Task 151 headline: PR1 recurrence-bump, PR2 demote-not-evict/Hole-B, PR3 trust_score migration, PR4 topic-routing/Hole-C, PR5 invisible-Unicode — ALL green.** The live audit trail even showed 4 real `persona-promote` events during Session 1 with the `promotedVia` provenance (`via confidence-high`) — Move-1's plumbing working end-to-end. **THE GAP (the user's insight, the real find):** the recurrence gate counts **fact RE-CAPTURES** (`write-fact.mjs:240` `existingIdAtPath === id` → `bumpRecurrence` — the ONLY bump site; no behavioral detector exists, verified), so it measures *"how often did the user have to RE-ASSERT this?"* = **FRICTION/FAILURE**, not adherence. The user's reasoning: *"I tell you once, it's in memory, you follow it every time without fail — so I never repeat myself; the only recurrence comes from the times you DIDN'T follow it. A rule that works perfectly stays at recurrence_count 1 — the BEST rule scores LOWEST."* So the "promote what you silently demonstrate" pitch is narrower than it sounds: a well-followed unspoken rule is exactly what recurrence can't see. **NOT a regression** — 151's declared-rule path (`via confidence-high`) and the genuine fact-re-surface path (`via recurrence-N`) both work and shipped; this is a MISSING capability. **Options to research (Task 181, v0.4 curation lane):** (a) behavioral-adherence counting (risky — the behavioral inference the kit deliberately avoids); (b) stability/longevity promotion (a fact un-contradicted for N sessions earns in on stability — the cleanest D-169 fit, likely recommendation); (c) correction-as-signal (the user's "if I say STOP, trigger it" + the friction signal = "the rule is FAILING → surface, don't silently promote"). Overlaps Task 180 (memclaw's `repeat-recall = first-answer-failed` is the SAME friction insight) + Task 97 (dynamic trust). **DECISION: ship v0.4.3 as-is; Task 181 is the follow-up.** _Provenance: the live cut-gate session 2026-07-01. Relates Task 151, 97, 177, 180, D-169, D-245._

---

## 2026-06-30 — v0.4.3 pre-merge: whole-branch review = MERGE; 2 review Minors fixed

- **✅ NOTE + FIX (2026-06-30) — D-245: the FINAL pre-merge whole-branch `code-review-excellence` pass over the full v0.4.3 production diff (Task 151 + 70.4 + 74; 17 modules, ~810 insertions) returned MERGE — 0 Blocking / 0 Important / 2 Minor — and the 2 Minors were fixed (the user's "fix everything").** The per-sub-task reviews had already caught the hard bugs (the doomed reinforce-overlay, the sweep-re-eval drift); this holistic pass verified the CROSS-CUTTING integration the slice-reviews couldn't see, and it's coherent: (a) the trust_score SEED (recurrence term, durable) and the OVERLAY (dampen) never double-count or contradict — they target different lifecycle states (a re-surfaced LIVE fact seeds high; a superseded fact moves to `archive/superseded/` so its dampen STANDS, un-reseeded); (b) no WAL lock contention (better-sqlite3 is sync/single-thread — sequential opens, design §2512); (c) all 5 recurrence_count readers default to 1× consistently; (d) promote-gate + seed consume recurrence in the same direction; (e) the new invisible-Unicode Poison_Guard adds NO false-positive on 151 write-path content (routed promotes, the mention string, unicode-heavy prose all pass); (f) every changed shared-function contract (assembleProjectCorpus, lessonsPromote `to`-default, consolidate evicted-shape, initTrustScore signature) is fully threaded — no missed caller; (g) the frozen-snapshot invariant holds (trust_score is index-only, routing/condense are write-side, mention is a tool-result field — nothing mutates the SessionStart inject mid-session). **The 2 Minors fixed (not deferred):** (1) `index-rebuild`'s recurrence default was `isFinite ? ## 2026-06-30 — Task 74 verify-and-lock-in (branch): post-compaction re-injection already works; now contractually pinned

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-244: Task 74 = verify-and-lock-in, NOT a feature build (the LAST v0.4.3 task before merge).** The original task imagined a new PreCompact hook to restore the frozen snapshot after Claude Code auto-compacts a long session (the kit's own cross-session-amnesia failure, applied mid-session). **But the mechanism ALREADY WORKS by luck (D-218 deep-read):** `settings-hooks.mjs` registers `SessionStart: cmk-inject-context` with NO `source`/`matcher`, and Claude Code fires `SessionStart` with `source:"compact"` after a compaction → the matcher-less hook re-runs `cmk-inject-context` and re-injects the snapshot. `inject-context.mjs` is source-agnostic (never reads the `source` field), so the re-fire restores memory regardless of WHY SessionStart fired — through the EXISTING wiring, no new event. **The gap was "works by luck, not verified contract":** the property was UNasserted (`grep compact tests/` had 0 relevant hits). **So 74 shrank to three deliverables:** (1) **lock-in tests** — `cli-install-hooks` pins SessionStart is matcher-less in both `KIT_HOOKS_BLOCK` AND the installed settings.json (a future `matcher` that would exclude `compact` now fails the test); `cli-inject-context` pins injectContext is source-agnostic; (2) **ADR-0006 corrected** — the stale "PreCompact declined as experimental in v0.1" note now explains no PreCompact hook is NEEDED (the matcher-less SessionStart handles it; PreCompact/PostCompact are stable now but unnecessary); (3) **the honest live-confirm caveat** — verified against the CC hooks doc + the code + the lock-in tests, but NOT a live compaction; a real auto-compact + snapshot-reappears check is the maintainer's manual cut-gate step (can't be auto-triggered). No new feature code. **Gate:** full suite green. _Relates Task 75.2 (the per-prompt hint — the OTHER compaction-surviving layer), the Stellman ERR pattern (the research dossier), D-218 (the deep-read that found it works-by-luck), ADR-0006 (corrected). **With 74, the v0.4.3 scope (Task 151 + 70.4 + 74) is CODE-COMPLETE on the branch.** NEXT: the pre-merge skill-review of the whole 151.x diff + stress 5/5 → merge to main → cut v0.4.3 (the maintainer's outward step)._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 70.4 shipped (branch): Poison_Guard rejects invisible/zero-width/bidi Unicode (v0.4.3 hardening)

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-243: Task 70.4 BUILT — Poison_Guard now rejects invisible/zero-width/bidi Unicode at write time (the v0.4.3 security rider).** A hidden-instruction vector the kit's COMMITTED memory makes worse than any DB competitor: an invisible char (zero-width joiner, a Trojan-Source bidi override) smuggles text past a human reviewer AND past the other Poison_Guard patterns, then ships to every teammate via `git clone`. **Build:** a new `injection_invisible_unicode` pattern matching 17 explicit code points — zero-width (U+200B ZWSP / U+200C ZWNJ / U+200D ZWJ / U+2060 word-joiner / U+FEFF BOM), bidi controls + isolates (U+202A–U+202E LRE/RLE/PDF/LRO/RLO + U+2066–U+2069 LRI/RLI/FSI/PDI), + soft-hyphen U+00AD / Arabic-mark U+061C / Mongolian-separator U+180E. **Built review-safely (a real implementation choice):** the code points live in an EXPLICIT `INVISIBLE_UNICODE_CODEPOINTS` array (each commented) + a `buildInvisibleUnicodeRe()` helper constructs the regex at load — NO literal invisible chars in source (those are unreadable + editor-mangleable; the first draft used literals + tested green, but the literal-in-source form is a maintenance hazard, so it was refactored to the array+builder). **Verified:** all 17 code points rejected + ZERO false positives on ordinary whitespace (space/tab/newline), ASCII, accents (café/naïve), CJK (北京), emoji (🚀) — legitimate prose never blocked (the guard's documented cost is a false positive = a silently-lost memory, so the no-false-positive proof is load-bearing). **Composition:** 145 caller tests green (auto-extract / memory-write / write-fact — the write paths that gate every capture). **Grounded:** Hermes parity (the lone primary source that scans stored memory for invisibles) + the kit's own kiro-design §699 / kiro-requirements char set (the research that flagged the gap). **Gate:** full suite green. _Relates Task 70 (the parent inject-defense task — 70.1/70.2/70.3 stay backlog), D-218 (the split that pulled 70.4 forward as a security patch), the v0.4.2 security-patch precedent. Ships in v0.4.3 with Task 151 + 74. NEXT: 74 (re-inject-after-compaction) → pre-merge skill-review + stress + cut v0.4.3._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.5 re-eval RESOLVED: the sweep keeps the enum; trust_score is floor/protection, not a sweep-ranking driver

- **✅ DECISION (2026-06-30) — D-238: the binding 151.5 sweep RE-EVAL is resolved — the cap-relief sweep KEEPS the `trust` ENUM proxy and does NOT consume the evolved `trust_score` float. NO new sweep code.** Context: 151.6's task entry made it binding to re-evaluate the 151.5 sweep order once a real `trust_score` existed (151.6-151.8 now landed it). The maintainer asked "what about research and code?" before accepting — so the verdict is grounded in both, not asserted. **Research:** the systems that EVOLVE trust (memclaw `_adjust_weights`, letta, graphiti) use the score as a **FLOOR + never-delete protection**, NOT as an active sweep-ranking driver; the systems that rank-and-sweep BY a score (MemoryOS-LFU access-frequency, MemOS top-N) are the **CAUTIONARY** ones — *exactly the Task-151 bug*. So wiring `trust_score` into a hot-path sweep ranking would drift TOWARD the documented bug. **Code:** (a) the protection the score gives is already wired in the ARITHMETIC — `TRUST_SCORE_FLOOR 0.05` (never-zero → never auto-deleted) is enforced in `updateTrustScore`/`initTrustScore`; (b) the sweep already protects high-trust STRUCTURALLY via the enum (`scratchpad.mjs` "preserve high-trust regardless of age" + `inject-context.mjs` "never evict a high-trust bullet before a lower one") — the float would only re-order WITHIN the medium/low band, a refinement not a missing protection; (c) RELIABILITY — `inject-context.mjs` doesn't open the index-db, so a `trust_score` lookup would put DB I/O on the 500 ms SessionStart inject path AND rank on an overlay value that resets on a full reindex (D-237) = non-deterministic across a repair; the enum is read from the always-present committed `.md` provenance, no such failure. **So both axes agree:** the enum sweep ORDER (151.5) + the `trust_score` FLOOR (151.7) + demote-not-evict (151.4) already deliver the research-faithful protection; the score's job is floor + protection (dampen lowers it, floor stops it, never-delete store keeps it), NOT hot-path sweep ranking. Updated design §20.3 with the full verdict; the two `// 151.6: re-evaluate` code markers are now resolved decision-trail pointers; no behavior change. _Relates D-237 (151.8, the overlay-durability posture), D-233 (151.5, the enum sweep), D-234 (151.6, the field), the [research note](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md) (floor-not-rank, the cautionary systems), ADR-0016 §20.3. With this, Move 1-3 + the Move-2 re-eval are CLOSED. NEXT: Move 4 (151.9 topic-routing / 151.10 auto-drain / 151.11 mention) → 151.12 → 151.13._

---

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.8 shipped (branch): the 3 passive trust signals (+ a research-caught reinforce fix)

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-237: Task 151.8 BUILT — the 3 passive signals move trust_score, with a TWO-mechanism split the review forced (dampen=overlay, reinforce=durable seed term).** Move 3 completes (folds Task 97). **The durability fork (decided WITH the maintainer, research- + code-grounded):** trust_score is a RUNTIME OVERLAY on the rebuildable index (a "regenerable read-cache") — a delta survives the boot reindex (unchanged files skipped) but a FULL reindex reseeds from the committed enum; accepted because trust_score is the LOCAL protection signal while the committed `trust` enum is the PORTABLE one (the two-fields design). The research backs this: every system that evolves trust (memclaw `_adjust_weights`, MemoryOS, honcho, EverOS, captain-claw) keeps it in the runtime DB store, none replay/commit it. **The wiring:** a new best-effort `applyTrustSignal({projectRoot,id,event})` (`trust-signal.mjs`, open→SELECT→updateTrustScore→UPDATE→close, swallows every error — a trust nudge must NEVER break the primary write) dampens at the **contradiction** site (`memory-write doAdd` conflict-queue route → existing fact) + the **supersession** site (`memory-write doReplace` → old fact; covers direct replace + auto-persona's persona-supersede which routes through it). **THE REVIEW CATCH (Blocking, the load-bearing correction):** the third signal — restatement/recurrence — was first wired as the same overlay (`applyTrustSignal('reinforce')` in write-fact's bump branches). The `code-review-excellence` pass + a live probe proved it WIPED on the very next reindex (0.45→reinforce 0.55→reindexBoot→0.45) — because `bumpRecurrence` rewrites the fact's file, which triggers a reseed. **The maintainer asked "what does the research say?" — and it was decisive:** MemoryOS (`N_visit` term), MemOS (`min(count·w, 2)` term), honcho (`times_derived`, "retrieval sorts by it") all make the recurrence COUNT a TERM IN THE SCORE, never a separate event; memclaw's asymmetric ±deltas are for trained-OUTCOME reports (`report_outcome`), a DIFFERENT signal I'd conflated. **The fix:** fold a CAPPED recurrence term into `initTrustScore` (reconstructed from the committed `recurrence_count`, 151.1) → a re-stated fact seeds higher DURABLY-by-construction (survives every reindex, because it's rebuilt from the durable count) → removed the doomed overlay-reinforce calls. The cap is load-bearing (a high-recurrence LOW-trust fact must never outrank a once-stated HIGH-trust one — the value-blind-LFU bug). **So the final shape: dampen = runtime overlay (memclaw outcome-delta); reinforce = durable seed term (MemoryOS/MemOS/honcho recurrence-as-score).** **Important #2 (honest scope):** two OTHER supersession writers (`conflict-queue mergeScratchpadBullets`, `merge-facts moveToSuperseded`) set `superseded_by` without routing through doReplace → don't dampen yet; deferred to 151.12 (supersede-hooks) with a tracked note + an honest in-code comment (not a false "single chokepoint" claim). **Tests:** new `trust-signal.mjs` unit tests (best-effort/over-mutation/floor) + the recurrence-term seed tests + INTEGRATION tests through the real writeFact/memoryWrite chains, incl. a **signal→reindexBoot→assert durability regression** (the test the review's gap demanded). Caller-map: applyTrustSignal wired into 2 hot write paths, best-effort, 216 write-path caller tests green. **Gate:** full suite green (2452+). _Relates D-236 (151.7 the update rule), D-234 (151.6 the field), Task 97 (folded), ADR-0016 §20.2, the [curation research note](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md) (recurrence-as-score-term, the decisive line), 151.12 (the deferred merge-path dampen). NEXT: the 151.5 sweep RE-EVAL (now a real evolved trust_score exists to consume) → 151.9-151.13._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.7 shipped (branch): the asymmetric trust update rule

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-236: Task 151.7 BUILT — `updateTrustScore` is the asymmetric, clamped, floored, EVENT-driven trust update (memclaw `_adjust_weights`).** Move 3 continues (the rule that EVOLVES the 151.6 `trust_score` seed). **What shipped:** `updateTrustScore(current, event)` in `trust-score.mjs` — `REINFORCE_DELTA = +0.1` / `DAMPEN_DELTA = −0.15`, clamped to `[TRUST_SCORE_FLOOR 0.05, TRUST_SCORE_CEIL 0.95]`. **The asymmetry is the point** (`|−0.15| > |+0.1|`): a contradicted/superseded fact sinks FASTER than a restated one rises — the conservative, fail-loud posture (one failure outweighs one success; a reinforce-then-dampen nets negative). **Floor is load-bearing:** 20 consecutive dampens settle at exactly 0.05, never zero → a fact is never auto-deleted by trust decay (demote-not-evict, §20.3). **NO time-decay of the stored value** (event-driven, not clock-driven — recency decay stays a read-time search-ranking concern, computed at read, never mutating the stored score). Pure + deterministic; an unknown event is a no-op so a not-yet-wired signal can't silently corrupt a score. **Verification:** 9 unit tests (deltas, asymmetry, floor-over-20-dampens, ceil, no-time-decay determinism, defensive garbage-clamp, composes-with-init) + an adversarial probe confirming float accumulation from floor lands EXACTLY on CEIL (no `0.9499…` drift) + boundary-idempotence. **Grounded in the primary source:** memclaw `evolve_service._adjust_weights` — the research note's exact "asymmetric `+0.1`/`−0.15`, floor `0.05`, NO time-decay" line. **Two-pass review: 0 findings** (pure function, no I/O, no callers yet — 151.8 wires it). **Gate:** full suite 2443/2443. _Relates D-234 (151.6, the field this evolves), Task 97 (folded), ADR-0016 §20.2, design §20.2, memclaw (the reference). NEXT: 151.8 — wire the 3 PASSIVE signals (contradiction-queue hit → dampen; `superseded_by` set → dampen the old; 151.1 re-surface → reinforce) onto these events, zero ritual (D-169)._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 150 pulled into v0.4.3 + a binding interim: auto-commit the dogfood memory at every task boundary

- **✅ DECISION (2026-06-30) — D-235: memory-commit becomes automatic — Task 150 PULLED into v0.4.3, + a binding CLAUDE.md interim so the user never reminds me to commit `context/` again.** **Trigger:** during the Task-151 session the user had to say "commit the memories" / "commit all the memories" TWICE, then: *"we need something that makes you do it automatic, and not me reminding you."* This is the kit's OWN thesis (manual rituals get forgotten — D-169) turned on the build process. **Recalled, not re-derived (the memory-recall rule worked):** this exact gap is already **Task 150** ("AI-judged memory-commit flow"), filed 2026-06-14 from the user's identical observation, design-first, with the design already settled: **AI proposes / user one-tap approves** (Claude notices durable memory accrued and offers to commit; the user keeps the *whether* gate). This HONORS **SETTLED D-126** ("no auto-git-commits; the user owns the publish gate") rather than overturning it — a hook that silently commits would violate D-126 + the no-surprise-in-git-history constraint. **Independent validation (D-218):** `basic-memory`, the most git-native competitor, arrived at the same propose-in-chat / leave-the-git-to-the-user answer. **The decision (the user's pick of 3 options):** (1) adopt a MANUAL interim NOW + (2) BUILD Task 150 in v0.4.3. **(1) The interim (binding):** a new Durable-state-first checkpoint #4 in CLAUDE.md — at every task boundary (the same checkpoint that flushes docs), run `git status --short context/` and, if dogfood memory accrued, stage `context/` + commit it in the SAME batch (with the binding pre-commit screen: maintainer-name validator + home-path/secret scan + gitignored-tier exclusion, since the repo is public). This makes next-session-me do it unprompted — the durable fix for "in-context intention dies at session end." **(2) The feature:** Task 150 re-laned from "v0.3.x/v0.4 design-gated" to a committed lane — **a RIDER in v0.4.4 (with Task 66), NOT its own minor and NOT in the in-flight v0.4.3.** _(Corrected same-day after the user's follow-up "we can take minor tasks and add them to laned versions with bug tasks?" — yes: a laned version carries non-headline riders beside its differentiator, exactly as v0.4.3 already rides 70.4+74 under the 151 headline. So 150 doesn't need its own minor; it rides a lane. It rides 66's not-yet-started v0.4.4 lane rather than the in-flight v0.4.3 because 150 is DESIGN-FIRST — the D-126 ADR gates the build and must not delay the persona release; thematic fit too: 66 = facts-stay-true-as-they-age, 150 = facts-actually-persist.)_ Build: the D-126 reconciliation ADR (recommend propose-and-approve) → the conversational-surface prompt. Once 150 ships, the kit prompts the user itself and the prose interim is subsumed by the structural feature (prose → enforcement). **Scope note:** this is the FIRST instance where a "user reminded me twice" became a structural rule THIS session — exactly the interval-flush class, extended to the dogfood-memory tier. _Relates Task 150 (the pulled-in feature), D-126 (the no-auto-commit line it honors via propose-and-approve), D-108 (the dogfood that accrues the files), D-169 (no manual ritual — the thesis this restores), basic-memory (D-218, the propose-don't-auto-commit validation), the CLAUDE.md Durable-state-first checkpoint #4. NEXT (build): finish 151 → 70.4 → 74 → Task 150 → cut v0.4.3._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.6 shipped (branch): the trust_score field (the evolving protection signal; folds Task 97)

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-234: Task 151.6 BUILT — `trust_score` is a FLOAT in the rebuildable index (NOT committed frontmatter, D-218), seeded from source on (re)index.** Move 3 of Task 151 (the protection field the Move-2 sweep order needs; folds Task 97). **What shipped (151.6 = the FIELD + INIT only; the update rule is 151.7, the passive signals 151.8):** (1) a new `observations.trust_score REAL NOT NULL DEFAULT 0.5` column in the index-db schema; (2) a new pure module `trust-score.mjs` with `initTrustScore({trust, writeSource})` — base from the committed trust ENUM (high 0.8 / medium 0.5 / low 0.3) + a SOURCE adjustment so a user-attested write (`user-explicit`/`manual-edit` +0.1) seeds HIGHER than a machine-derived one (`auto-extract`/`compressor` −0.05) at the same enum — the design's "user-explicit > auto-extract" (memory-os source-based init); clamped to `[TRUST_SCORE_FLOOR 0.05, TRUST_SCORE_CEIL 0.95]` (floor = memclaw `_adjust_weights`, never zero → never auto-deleted; ceil leaves reinforcement headroom); (3) computed at INSERT in `index-rebuild.mjs` (one place, a `withTrustScore` wrapper over both the fact + scratchpad observation builders) so it's reconstructed deterministically on every full reindex and the committed `.md` files carry NO such field; (4) a **non-destructive column migration** in `openIndexDb` (`PRAGMA table_info` → `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN`, idempotent — `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` does NOT add a column to a pre-existing table) so a pre-151.6 index gains `trust_score` in place + keeps its rows (no forced rebuild; the next full reindex reseeds real values, existing rows carry the DEFAULT 0.5 until then). **Caller-map (binding):** only `index-db.mjs` (schema) + `index-rebuild.mjs` (the two INSERTs, both updated) write `observations` — no other module inserts with an explicit column list, so the schema change is contained; `forget`/`trust` UPDATEs are column-count-insensitive. **The 151.5 re-eval trigger fired:** 151.5's sweep keys on the trust ENUM + capture-age as a proxy *because no continuous score existed* — 151.6 now provides the real `trust_score`, but the sweep CONSUME is deferred to after 151.7/151.8 (the score must first be EVOLVING from passive outcomes before the sweep should key on it; reseed-only-on-rebuild isn't yet a meaningful protection signal). **Test-fixture note:** the reconstruction tests initially failed because the fixture ids (`P-EXPLICTA`/`P-AUTOXTRA`) contained `I`/`O` — excluded from the kit's base32 alphabet, so `reindexFull` skipped them as "invalid id" (a fixture bug, NOT a code bug — the trust_score wiring was correct from the first run, proven by the seed rows getting 0.6); fixed to valid ids. **Gate:** 151.6 tests green (trust-score init + index-db schema/migration + index-rebuild reconstruction + DB-consumer regression across search/forget/reindex = 149 green in the targeted run). _Relates D-233 (151.5, the re-eval trigger), Task 97 (folded), ADR-0016 §20.2, design §20.2, D-218 (trust-in-index-not-frontmatter). NEXT: 151.7 (the asymmetric/clamped/floored update rule) → 151.8 (wire the 3 passive signals) → THEN the 151.5 sweep re-eval._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.5 shipped (branch): the cap-relief sweep is value-ordered on both surfaces

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-233: Task 151.5 BUILT — the cap-relief sweep is VALUE-ordered (low-trust first, high-trust never swept) on BOTH the inject + write surfaces, a two-axis CONJUNCTION. Research-grounded, NOT the lower-risk guess.** **The scope was settled by reading the research, not by caution** (the maintainer: *"does the research/tests say?"*): the curation note + ADR-0016 say the sweep drops **low-trust AND long-unaccessed** (a CONJUNCTION, two axes) and explicitly flag the SINGLE-axis sweeps — MemoryOS-LFU (access-only), MemOS-top-N (rank-only) — as *"exactly the Task-151 bug — don't replicate."* So the tempting "low-trust at ANY age" option was itself the bug class (trust-only). **What was already built:** the INJECT surface (`truncateTierToBudget`, §19.3/D-66) already drops lowest-`maxTrust` section first → 151.5 added the missing trust-VARYING regression tests (the prior test dropped by FILE order, never varied trust) — 2 tests pinning "low section drops, high survives" + the 3-tier low→medium→high order. **What had a gap:** the WRITE surface (`consolidate`) — its drop GATE was already a two-axis conjunction (`trust !== high` AND age > 14 d, so high-trust is exempt at any age and recent low-trust is spared), but it pushed the `evicted[]` list in FILE order, leaving low/medium-stale undifferentiated. 151.5 sorts the eviction list **low-trust-before-medium, then oldest-first**; the file-removal set (`removeIdx`) is UNCHANGED, so only the archive + audit ORDER now reflects value (a debugger / a future partial-drop sees the cheapest bullets first). **Deferred to 151.6 (binding re-eval, the maintainer's call):** both surfaces key on the `trust` ENUM (high/medium/low) + capture-`at` as the "long-unaccessed" proxy — the only signals a scratchpad bullet carries today (no last-access field on bullets). When 151.6 lands the real `trust_score` FLOAT + a genuine access/recurrence signal, the sweep is upgraded to rank on those; `// 151.6: re-evaluate` markers are at both code sites + a binding note sits in 151.6's task entry. The CONJUNCTION shape is invariant across the upgrade. **Two-pass review:** self-review confirmed no `evicted[]` consumer breaks (the array is private to scratchpad.mjs; consumers use `.id`/`.block` only) + the sort can't desync `removeIdx`; the `code-review-excellence` pass returned **0 Blocking / 0 Important / 2 Minor** — both Minors fixed inline per the maintainer's "fix all" (added the inject-side ordering test for symmetry + a comment isolating the trust axis from the recency tiebreak). **Honest framing (recorded so it's not overclaimed):** on the write side the removal SET is identical — the only behavioral delta is eviction ORDER; the genuinely-new protection (recent-low spared, value-ordering) mostly pre-existed on the inject side. 151.5 is "verify the invariant on both surfaces + close the write-side ordering gap," correctly scoped, not a big behavioral change. **Gate:** full suite green (151.5 adds 3 tests). _Relates D-232 (151.4), ADR-0016 §20.3, design §19.3/§20.3, the [curation research note](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md) (the single-axis = bug finding), 151.6 (the binding re-eval). NEXT: Move 3 = 151.6 trust_score field (folds Task 97) — which TRIGGERS the 151.5 sweep re-evaluation._
