## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.4 shipped (branch): demote-not-evict — the persona condenses, never strands to fragments

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-232: Task 151.4 BUILT — the user-tier persona CONDENSES at cap instead of graduating high-trust traits to un-injected `fragments/` (Hole B closed). PIVOT: reverses the tier-U half of D-60/D-61.** **The bug (confirmed real, not theoretical):** the pre-fix test showed `bulletsGraduated===1` — when a persona scratchpad (USER/HABITS/LESSONS.md) exceeded its ~1800 B cap, `graduateForCapRelief` (D-61's all-tiers graduation) moved the OLDEST high-trust persona bullets to `<userDir>/fragments/`, which `inject-context` NEVER reads → a freshly promoted trait VANISHED at cold-open (the v0.3.1 cold-open regression — Hole B). **The fix (mechanical, no LLM — decided WITH the maintainer, who couldn't see the option detail and asked for the recommendation):** for tier U, BOTH cap-relief sites (`appendScratchpadBullet` + the session-end `sweepScratchpadForCapRelief`) now call a new pure `condenseScratchpadForCapRelief` (trim trailing whitespace + collapse blank runs, CRLF-tolerant per Task 139, **drops no bullet**) and NEVER graduate to `fragments/`. If condense can't reach cap, the file grows past the inject budget (the D-61 load-cap-not-write-cap invariant already permits this) and the snapshot's importance-aware load-cap (§19.3 `truncateTierToBudget`, drops lowest-aggregate-trust SECTION first) keeps the high-trust traits injected — so the loss does NOT move to inject time (verified). **Tier P graduation to `context/memory/` is UNCHANGED** — those facts are recall-reachable, so no Hole-B there. **PIVOT / decision-trail (binding):** this reverses 94.2's "the user tier graduates too" (D-60/D-61) — the INTENT (never-lose-memory) is preserved, only the MECHANISM changes for the persona; the old path is preserved with the dated reversal in design §19.2 + §20.3 + the 2 flipped tests (94.2 in cli-load-cap + the 94.2-path in cli-graduate-session), each carrying a DECISION TRAIL comment (not silently "fixed to pass"). **Why no LLM (composition):** an inline Haiku rewrite (letta's agent-condenses) on the synchronous `appendScratchpadBullet` hot path — called from hooks + auto-extract — would be a cooldown/timeout/latency hazard; the genuine LLM tighter-rewrite is **Task 95** (re-curation, async). **Two-pass review:** self-review verified both relief sites + no third tier-U→fragments path; the `code-review-excellence` pass caught a real **CRLF no-op bug** (the helper used `split('\n')`, leaving a trailing `\r` so blank-collapse + trailing-trim did NOTHING on a Windows-authored file — the maintainer's platform) — fixed to `split(/\r?\n/)` + a CRLF regression test, 0 Blocking otherwise. **Gate:** 2419/2419 + validators green. _Relates D-231 (151.3), D-60/D-61 (the reversed graduation), ADR-0016 §20.3, design §19.2/§19.3/§20.3, Hole B (D-177). NEXT: 151.5 (sweep order — low-trust AND stale first; high-trust never swept), the protection signal Move 3's trust_score (151.6-151.8) feeds._

## 2026-06-30 — Task 151.3 shipped (branch): the cite-and-sum recurrence gate is live

- **✅ FIX (2026-06-30) — D-231: Task 151.3 BUILT — the form-gate is replaced by the cite-and-sum recurrence gate (Hole-A closed).** Implemented D-230's wiring TDD on branch `task-151-recurrence-promotion`: (1) `assembleProjectCorpus` now exported + returns `{corpus, factIndex}` — each fact headed `### [P-XXXXXXXX] title` so the classifier has a citable handle, `factIndex` = `Map<id, recurrence_count>` built only from corpus-resident facts (truncated facts aren't citable AND aren't indexed — they can't disagree); (2) `parsePersonaCandidates` peels a trailing `| source_fact_ids=[…]` (regex `$`-anchored, robust to pipes/brackets/decoys in the restatement; ids upper-cased to tolerate a lowercase LLM echo); (3) new pure `resolveRecurrenceSum({sourceFactIds, factIndex})` — dedups cited ids, drops hallucinated, sums real `recurrence_count`; (4) the facts-path classifier prompt gains the `source_fact_ids` output format + a CITE-don't-COUNT instruction block (transcript path unchanged — no citable ids); (5) the gate at `promoteCandidatesToUserTier` is now `confidence=high` (explicit-imperative fast-path, preserved) **OR** `recurrenceSum ≥ PROMOTE_THRESHOLD (3)` (the demonstrated-but-not-declared path — the Hole-A fix). The promote flow after the gate (section-ensure → detectConflicts → memoryWrite) is untouched. The `persona-promote` audit `reasonText` now carries `via recurrence-N` / `via confidence-high` (Door 4 — a recurrence-gated promotion is distinguishable). **The other 3 callers** (inline auto-extract, `lessons-promote`, `drainPersonaReviewQueue`) don't attach `recurrenceSum` → `?? 0` → they hit the `confidence=high` clause exactly as before (no silent behavior change — verified). **Two-pass review:** self-review surfaced + fixed a Door-4 audit gap (the recurrence path was unnamed in the trail); the `code-review-excellence` pass returned 0 Blocking / 2 Important / 4 Minor — actioned Important #1 (Door-3 test: the id-bearing corpus actually reaches `backend.compress`'s input — else a stripped corpus silently reopens Hole A), Important #2 (transcript-path medium candidate does NOT promote — guards the D-44 asymmetry), Minor #4 (lowercase-id echo resolves), Minor #2 (double-floor marked intentional). **Gate:** full suite 2415/2415 + all ~20 validators green; stress 5/5 on the first invocation. 151.3 checkbox flipped. _NEXT: Move 2 (151.4 condense-not-evict, 151.5 sweep order). Relates D-230 (the wiring), D-229 (Option B), ADR-0016, design.md §20.1, D-177 (Hole A). The maintainer's autopilot directive ("research what others did in code before inventing") held — the gate shape came from the 5-system bridge read, not invention._

## 2026-06-01 — the road to a product: ship-one-wow-at-a-time, video-parity is the done-bar

### Settled decisions (do NOT re-open without new evidence)

- **✅ DECISION (2026-06-29) — D-230: Task 151.3 WIRING = cite-and-sum (the classifier cites source_fact_ids; code sums their recurrence_count to gate). The LLM NEVER counts — 5/5 bridge study unanimous.** D-229 settled THAT recurrence gates (Option B); D-230 settles HOW the LLM-born trait gets its recurrence number. A 6th workflow (wv99dhd5d) code-read the gate→synthesis handoff of the 5 strong-yes systems (MemoryOS/honcho/memclaw/EverOS/captain-claw): **UNANIMOUS — arithmetic counts+selects the unit; the LLM never counts recurrence** (4/5 don't even pass the number into the LLM context). **The asymmetry that made this non-obvious:** their gated unit PRE-EXISTS the LLM (segment/cluster carries its own count); our trait is LLM-BORN (synthesized, no pre-existing row to ORDER BY). **The faithful adaptation (cite-and-sum / B-strict via citation):** the classifier emits `PERSONA CANDIDATE | … | source_fact_ids=[…]` (cites which facts it drew from — NOT a count); code resolves+validates the ids, SUMS their `recurrence_count` (151.1), gates on the sum ≥ 3. **Rejected Option A** (LLM emits recurrence=N) — 5/5 reject LLM-counting; grading a number ≈ grading phrasing (the bug). **Honest caveat (recorded):** the sum is deterministic, but trait MEMBERSHIP is the LLM's grouping choice — acceptable (grouping coherent facts IS synthesis, the LLM's job), NOT the arithmetic-pre-clustering guarantee the 3/5 cluster systems have (we'd prefer that with an embedding-cluster primitive pre-LLM; we lack one, so cite-and-sum is the pragmatic faithful pick). Lands in design.md §20.1 + the [research note ADDENDUM 2](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md) + Task 151.3's wiring note. Build state unchanged: 151.1+151.2 committed (53c1bbf, suite 2387/2387 green); 151.3 is the next TDD step (extend PERSONA_CANDIDATE_RE + parsePersonaCandidates for source_fact_ids; add resolveRecurrenceSum; swap the gate at auto-persona.mjs:534). _Relates D-229 (Option B), ADR-0016, design.md §20.1, the bridge study (wv99dhd5d, backed up). The maintainer "research what others did in code before inventing" — the asymmetry was caught by reading the real handoff, not assumed._

- **✅ DECISION (2026-06-29) — D-229: Task 151.3 promotion gate = Option B (recurrence GATES promotion, the LLM only SYNTHESIZES the trait wording), validated by a WIDE 15-system code-read — honest count, NOT inflated.** The maintainer pushed for 5+ real samples, same-shape AND different-shape, and explicitly *"even more projects is better"* + *"it doesn't have to be the same — projects that have a mechanic that deals with this."* Code-read 15 systems on the broad durability-earning question (recurrence vs LLM-judged vs trained-trust vs pure-self-edit vs event-time): MemoryOS, MemOS, memclaw, graphiti, cognee, claude-mem, honcho, memobase, MIRIX, EverOS, TencentDB, letta, langmem, basic-memory, captain-claw. **The honest result (the studies refused to inflate it):** **5 strong-yes parallels to B** (MemoryOS heat≥5.0 / memclaw cluster≥3 / honcho `times_derived` / EverOS cluster≥2 / captain-claw `dream_cycles≥2`) + MemOS partial — **but NONE are our exact shape** (all server/DB/SQLite). **Among systems actually shaped like us** (markdown/git/local — basic-memory, claude-mem, iwe, the awrshift cluster): **ZERO auto-promote by recurrence; our two closest twins have no persona tier at all.** So "5+ similar projects did B" is FALSE; the truth is two-layered: **the mechanism is proven across 5 diverse architectures, but our class hasn't done it — we'd be FIRST.** **Why B is still right for US** (reasons the code revealed, all mapping to our constraints): (1) no per-turn LLM — we're not an observer-LLM architecture, recurrence is free; (2) no ritual (D-169) — recurrence needs no human feedback signal (unlike the `helpful_count`/`report_outcome` the LLM-judged systems need); (3) deterministic/fail-closed/auditable vs an LLM hallucinating confidence on thin evidence; (4) it is the PRECISE fix for the v0.3.1 cold-open bug — a demonstrated-but-not-declared philosophy stranded by a PHRASING gate; recurrence catches it because the evidence was in the recurrence, not the wording. **Honest framing recorded so it's never overclaimed:** NOT "5 similar projects do it" (the peer read kills that); rather "the field's scoring systems converge on recurrence + our peers leave it on the table → we adapt the proven primitive to lead our class, layered on safety they lack (Poison_Guard/conflict-queue/decision-trail)." **The LLM is NOT removed** (the earlier overstatement, corrected mid-discussion): it stays as the SYNTHESIZER of trait wording (MemoryOS pattern: arithmetic heat gates, LLM writes the profile) — what's removed is the LLM from the GATE. **Build status:** 151.1 (recurrence_count field) + 151.2 (computeHeat) shipped on branch `task-151-recurrence-promotion`, full suite 2387/2387 + lint green; 151.3 is the resume point. _Full study → the [curation-cluster research note ADDENDUM](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md); the maintainer "even more projects is better" + "it doesn't have to be the same, just a mechanic that deals with it" + "i am not the smartest man… seeing how others did it makes it solid." Relates ADR-0016 (the decision this validates), D-228 (the 7-system design lock), the v0.3.1 cold-open bug (D-177), D-169 (no ritual — why recurrence not LLM-feedback), Task 151.3._

- **📐 DESIGN LOCKED (2026-06-29) — D-228: Task 151 persona-promotion redesign settled by a 7-system CODE-read; folds Task 97; design lives in design.md §20 + ADR-0016 + a research note (NOT a standalone docs/design/ file).** The maintainer asked to "deep research all the version tasks from sources we researched — actual code, then best practice." Ran an 8-agent parallel workflow reading the ACTUAL CODE (not note-summaries) of 7 memory systems — MemoryOS, mem0, letta, langmem, caura-memclaw, graphiti, MemOS — for the curation cluster (promotion 151 / trust 97 / re-curation 95 / loop 179 / skill 180). **The 3 architectural decisions (→ ADR-0016):** (1) **promotion = CAPPED RECURRENCE, not phrasing** — `heat = min(recurrence_count, CAP)·W + lazy exp(-Δh/τ)`, promote at count≥3; the cap is load-bearing (MemOS); NO LLM on the hot path (mem0 ABANDONED its per-fact judge for hash-dedup = evidence it's too costly/unstable). Replaces the form-based `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE` (fixes Hole A). (2) **trust = a SEPARATE evolving passive-outcome field (folds Task 97)** — `+0.1/−0.15` floor `0.05`, event-driven from contradiction/supersession/restatement (zero ritual, D-169), in the rebuildable INDEX not committed frontmatter (D-218). Two fields not one (the maintainer's call) — recurrence gates promotion, trust gates protection; MemOS proves a unified score lets a noisy fact rank high. (3) **DEMOTE-NOT-EVICT** — the snapshot is a validity-filtered VIEW over a never-deleted store; at cap CONDENSE the file (letta) not fragment-split; sweep drops low-trust-AND-unaccessed first; high-trust persona never swept (fixes Hole B — the cold-open bug). Cross-system consensus: never-delete + status-flip; the MemoryOS-LFU / MemOS-top-N value-blind sweeps ARE the Task-151 bug — don't replicate. **Process notes:** (a) Task 97 ceases to be standalone → ships as Task 151.6–151.8; (b) the design was FIRST written as a standalone `docs/design/` file, which VIOLATES the kit's "design.md is the sole Spine HOW" kernel — the maintainer caught it; corrected to design.md §20 (canonical) + ADR-0016 (decision) + a research note (evidence) — the kit's existing ADR+research link-out pattern, adopted as a working convention because design.md is now 324 KB and should link-out evidence rather than inline it; (c) the standalone was BACKED UP (`C:\cut-gate-backups\`) before removal + content verified copied (the maintainer: "don't just delete docs… I don't want to lose info"). 151 broken into 13 granular sub-tasks (151.1–151.13), each with a Done-when criterion. v0.4.3 = 151 + 70.4 + 74. _The maintainer: "deep research all from sources, actual code, then best practice" + "two fields" + "all of what you said needs its own subtasks" + "backup first, don't delete willy-nilly" + the design.md link-out policy. Relates ADR-0016 (the decision), design.md §20 (the HOW), the [7-system code study](../research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md) (evidence), D-177 (the holes), D-178 (full-redesign-once), D-154 (the down-payment), D-169 (no ritual), D-218 (trust-in-index), Task 151/97/95/66/179/180._

- **📝 REGISTRY PRIOR-ART SWEEP → the space is now CROWDED (positioning update) + 3 sibling projects (2026-06-29) — D-227: a `patent`-tool registry sweep + 3 git-native-markdown-memory siblings (nestwork / pulse8-cortex-vault / nt) → revisit-notes on Tasks 146/176/80/50/148, AND a real positioning correction.** The user wanted to check if anyone's already built our ideas (via the `patent` CLI — a semantic-search over npm/PyPI/GitHub/crates registries). The tool itself is too noisy to adopt (38 fuzzy blurb-matches per query; misses buried-in-code gems — our deep-read is better), but ONE search ("git-native markdown memory for AI agents") delivered the load-bearing finding:
  - **POSITIONING CORRECTION (supersedes the D-224/6-frameworks "the gap is us" note):** the git-native/markdown-memory space is **NO LONGER EMPTY — it's CROWDED.** The sweep surfaced a cluster of direct siblings: **synpulse8/pulse8-ai-cortex** (markdown typed-graph knowledge OS), **songth1ef/nestwork** (git-sync multi-agent memory), **navbytes/nt** (plain-text agent memory), + tomdwipo/claude-soul, codesstar/loci (Memory Palace), clawsouls/soulspec, opencode-graphiti. **So the differentiator is NO LONGER "we're the only markdown/git-native one"** — it's EXECUTION DEPTH (automatic auto-extract capture, trust/Poison_Guard/dedup/conflict-queue, the v0.4 breadth, the cross-project wedge). README/About positioning must shift from "category-novel" to "depth-of-execution" (the 6-frameworks article's "the gap is us" was true weeks ago; the long tail has filled in since).
  - **3 sibling deep-reads → revisit-notes (no new tasks):** **`nestwork`** → Task 146 (PARTITION-BY-WRITER concurrency — each agent owns its dir, writes never collide, no locks; a cheaper answer than lock-the-shared-file) + Task 50 (AGENTS.md-canonical + thin CLAUDE/SOUL/GEMINI mirrors — INDEPENDENT confirmation of our cross-agent shape, handles our exact tail) + Task 148 (a `desensitization contract` — redact-before-commit + optional AI-semantic pass — so 148's "unmatched" claim is corrected: a 10th project does it). **`pulse8-cortex-vault`** (Apache-2.0) → Task 176 read-list: a markdown typed-graph with AUTO-MAINTAINED EDGES on file change + a `vault_context` ranked-subgraph query — the closest reference for "derive/maintain edges from the markdown we already write" (both halves of 176). **`nt`** (MIT) → Task 80: a NEW capture source we lack — a PostToolUse hook mirroring Claude's `TodoWrite` list into memory (we capture turns + edits, NOT the agent's live task-state).
  - **The honest meta-call (the user: "lets write this all up and go back to developing our kit"):** we've thoroughly canvassed the space — each new project is now mostly CONVERGENCE-CONFIRMATION (our architecture is right) + one small idea; marginal value is dropping. Survey winding down; back to kit dev (Task 66/151). _The user: "you want to check them now?" → "lets write this all up and go back to developing our kit." - **📝 BATCH SURVEY — 2 projects + 8 articles → revisit-notes on recall/graph/fusion tasks (2026-06-29) — D-225 (sift-kg, Elastic) + D-226 (8 MLM articles), with a real PREMISE CORRECTION on Task 178.** Batched survey (the user: "wait with the commit until we finish a couple"). So 178's benchmark carries a HYPOTHESIS (RRF ≥ weighted-avg) not a blind sweep. Covers only fusion, no rerank.
  - **D-226 — 8 MachineLearningMastery articles** (mostly 101-level confirmation; the real gems): **(→178)** k=60 standard RRF constant, retrieve-ALL-before-fuse (avoid truncation bias), **post-retrieval filtering** (re-score candidates vs the live query, drop low scorers before injecting — we lack this), **HyDE/query-expansion** (embed a hypothetical answer — a paraphrase-recall lever for Task 99); **(→176/95)** **RAPTOR** (recursive cluster→summarize→cluster the summaries — a memory summary-HIERARCHY for big-picture recall; the one genuinely-new idea) + the GraphRAG/Leiden community-summary mechanism + Cognee flagged as the priority clone; **(→149)** "memory as a TOOL the agent chooses to call" is a NAMED recognized pattern — external validation our judgment-pulled `memory-search` skill is a design, NOT a workaround; **(→74)** static-vs-dynamic two-pass context (= our frozen snapshot, confirmed) + "anchored iterative summarization" (preserve decisions/state when compressing) + "Lost in the Middle" (attention favors start+end → injection order matters); **(metadata)** filter-BEFORE-scoring — our keyword path already does (`search.mjs:322` SQL WHERE before rank), verify the vec KNN path does too.

- **📝 NOTE + RESEARCH TASK + SEARCH-NOTE (2026-06-28) — D-217: surveying `rohitg00/pro-workflow` (the most credible competitor yet) — we're AHEAD on the core memory loop, they're ahead on ONE thing we don't attempt (training the behavior doc from corrections → Task 177); RRF-search noted, not tasked.** `pro-workflow` (npm, TypeScript, better-sqlite3+FTS5, 34 skills / 37 hooks / 24 events, Claude Code + Cursor + 32 agents via SkillKit) is the closest thing to the kit surveyed so far — same pitch ("gets smarter every session"), same stack. **The read-past-the-README payoff (decisive, code-verified):** its headline "corrections auto-loaded on session start" is **terminal-only** — `session-start.js` writes every learning via `console.error` (stderr) and **NO hook anywhere emits `additionalContext`/`hookSpecificOutput`** (the documented CC context-injection mechanism). So the model NEVER sees the memory unless the human reads the console + re-types it. **Our frozen-snapshot SessionStart injection actually puts memory in the model's context** — they show it to the human. **Two places we're clearly ahead:** (1) recall INJECTION (above — the load-bearing gap); (2) capture is regex-detect + manual `[LEARN]` markup (the user must tag corrections), where ours auto-extracts each turn (D-85/D-169). Plus the maturity gaps: no dedup (same correction = 2 rows), no trust/decay, no contradiction handling, no privacy screen on learnings, no pruning. **Where THEY'RE genuinely ahead (the buried gem the README never mentions):** a **DSPy-style offline skill OPTIMIZER** (`src/optimizer/`) — treats `SKILL.md` as trainable text-space state, corrections as training trajectories, holds out 20% as a validation set, Reflect→Aggregate→Clip→Apply→Evaluate (LLM-graded, accept-on-improvement, budget-capped, periodic consolidation rewrite). It TRAINS the behavior doc; we store FACTS. That's a real bet we don't make → **filed as Task 177** (research+ADR; sibling to Task 55 behavioral-patterns + 151 promotion — a correction may be a signal to UPDATE a rule, validated, not just a fact to store). **Also notable (not borrowed):** their auto-research wiki loop (seed-BFS → fetch → summarize → grow overnight) = OFF our thesis (build topic KBs, not memory-of-you — same skip as awrshift's `/close-day`); and their **Reciprocal Rank Fusion** (BM25+vector, k=60) **possibly cleaner than our hybrid** (Task 65). **RRF decision (the user's call):** do NOT breadcrumb it onto the SHIPPED Task 65/99 (`[x]` tasks — dead weight); log it as a data-point + a note in the recall lane, and evaluate it against the Task 99 benchmark IF/WHEN a v0.4 hybrid-search-tuning task opens. Numbers decide, not vibes. _The user: "add research task" (the optimizer) + "breadcrumb on tasks we already did? v0.3.x already shipped, we're at v0.4.2" (the RRF correction — right, no breadcrumb on closed tasks). - **📝 NOTE + RESEARCH TASK (2026-06-28) — D-216: surveying `iwe-org/iwe` surfaced the graph-recall question — should the kit add a relational/graph query mode beside keyword + semantic? Filed as Task 176 (research + ADR, NOT commit-to-build).** `iwe` (Rust markdown knowledge-graph + LSP + MCP, 1.2k★, Apache-2.0) bills itself as a "markdown memory system" but the CODE tells the real story (the read-past-the-README lesson): **it has ZERO auto-capture** — the human authors every note; the AI only queries/refactors. So it's a different PRODUCT (developer PKM, not agent memory) and we're NOT behind it on memory (it isn't doing memory). **Its buried gem (README undersells it):** link-integrity-preserving structural refactoring — a real `Graph` + `RefIndex` edge map so renaming a doc auto-updates all 1000 references, extract/inline are transactional at the graph level, and the same core serves LSP+CLI+MCP. That gem doesn't transfer (it solves hand-authored-note-web problems our auto-capture model means our users don't have). **What DOES transfer is the QUESTION:** `iwe` makes graph traversal a first-class recall mode (`$includes`/`$referencedBy` bounded-depth BFS) — and we answer EVERYTHING with flat similarity (FTS5 + semantic). **Confirmed no existing task asks this:** graphiti/Zep graph-memory is in our research base (2026-06-06 deep-dive; Task 66 borrowed their bi-temporal model) but we only mined those for TEMPORAL + PROMOTION lessons, never "do we want a graph QUERY layer." Task 149 asks WHEN to recall; this asks WHAT recall MODES — complementary, not duplicate. **Decision: file the research task, don't commit to building.** Adding a graph layer is a real architectural bet — and the HARD CONSTRAINT is that any edges must be AUTO-DERIVED from the markdown we already write (fact↔fact, decision↔file, `[[wikilink]]`-style), rebuildable like the FTS5/vec index — NOT a hand-authored graph (the `iwe` model presupposes human-authored links auto-capture means we don't have). The ADR decides ADOPT (+derive-edges design +lane) / DEFER / REJECT. _The user: "do we have a task to research this? if not lets add it, maybe it's a good fit to add graph recall." Relates Task 176 (the new research task), Task 149 (WHEN-to-recall sibling), Task 65 (semantic), Task 66 (the bi-temporal borrow from the same graph systems), the read-past-the-README discipline, the markdown-native + derive-don't-hand-author constraint._

Fix: exported `setDeep` (a legitimate security-invariant boundary) + added a direct guard test AND a catch-path test → `config-core.mjs` 100% lines. **Versioning (the patch-digit rule):** a security fix has no differentiator → it's a patch → takes the next number (v0.4.2), and Task 151 (persona) slides to v0.4.3. - **✅ FIX + RESOLUTION of D-212 (2026-06-27) — D-213: prompt-free capture is delivered by a `PermissionRequest` HOOK that auto-approves the kit's own tools/skills — NOT by allow-list rules (Task 172).** This RESOLVES the D-212 open investigation. **Verdict on cause:** the capture popups are a **Claude Code 2.1.x change, not a kit regression** — git shows the skill + allow-list config byte-stable since Task 108/117; it started prompting the day CC updated. **External proof (the user found it):** anthropics/claude-code **#17499** (auto-approving MCP tools via a skill's `allowed-tools` is undocumented + unreliable — another developer hit the identical "still asks for permission" symptom; Anthropic clarified general syntax but left the MCP case **explicitly unaddressed**) and **#18837 → #14956** (cluster incl. #13048/#16389: `allowed-tools` "not enforced / ignored entirely"). So **neither Task 169 (`Skill(:*)`) nor Task 171 (specific `mcp__cmk__` names in `permissions.allow`) suppresses these prompts on 2.1.195** — disproven live across cut-gate-v041d→l. **The documented, working mechanism is a `PermissionRequest` hook** (code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks-guide#auto-approve-specific-permission-prompts): it fires when CC is about to show a permission dialog and a hook that writes `{"behavior":"allow"}` answers it. **LIVE-PROVEN (cut-gate-v041l):** hooks matching `mcp__cmk__.*` + `Skill` → the popup flashes then auto-dismisses ("Allowed by PermissionRequest hook") and the fact saves with NO click (disk: `feedback_run-black-before-committing.md`; audit `action:created, writeSource:user-explicit`). **Two gates, two fixes:** the per-TOOL/skill gate → the PermissionRequest hook; the SERVER-approval gate → `enabledMcpjsonServers:["cmk"]` (narrow, NOT `enableAllProjectMcpServers`). **The automatic Stop-hook capture path was already prompt-free** (in-process `writeFact`, headless `claude --print`, no MCP/skill) — this fixes the agentic/explicit path. **Shipped (Task 172, additive):** new `cmk-approve-permission` bin + `approve-permission.mjs` (`evaluatePermissionRequest` — approves ONLY kit tools/skills, two-layer safety: narrow matcher + handler self-check, fail-silent); `writeKitHooks` wires the `PermissionRequest` hooks + `enabledMcpjsonServers:["cmk"]` (one write-site, npm + plugin + `repair --hooks`); **KEEP all existing layers** (the full `permissions.allow` + skill `allowed-tools`) as belt-and-suspenders that activate natively when CC fixes #17499/#14956 (the user's call — "maybe everything that worked till now and the rest we added will work someday"). - **🐛 CUT-GATE FIND + FIX (2026-06-26) — D-210: `cmk install --with-semantic` verified npm's EXIT CODE instead of the embedder's actual import → falsely disabled semantic (the D-199 class; Task 170).** The v0.4.1 cut-gate (fresh `cut-gate-v041b` install) printed *"semantic recall NOT enabled"* — but the embedder was installed, importable, and `cmk search --mode semantic` returned results. **Root cause (install.mjs:579):** `enableSemantic` bailed on `npm.status !== 0`; on Windows that non-zero exit was a **benign cleanup-EBUSY** (npm couldn't unlink a leftover temp DLL — `sharp-win32-x64`/`libvips-42.dll` held by a running process) AFTER a SUCCESSFUL install. So the kit conflated npm's noisy exit with an install failure and skipped `default_mode: hybrid` — leaving the user silently keyword-only despite doing everything right. **The user's two catches:** *"are you sure semantic is not working?"* (it was — pushed past my premature "it failed") and *"the install needs to be automatic, users are not supposed to do anything"* (the manual `cmk config set` I used to unblock the gate is a workaround, not the fix). **Fix:** on a non-zero npm exit, PROBE the embedder import (`checkEmbedderBinding`, the HC-8 probe); if it imports, enable hybrid regardless of npm's exit — only `nonzero-exit AND import-fails` is a real failure. `enableSemantic` gains an injectable `probeEmbedder` seam. **This is the SECOND D-199-class find this gate** (the first was Task 169's prompt — both "the command's report ≠ reality"), and both were caught only by the LIVE gate (no unit test drives a real npm-with-locked-DLL or a real CC skill-approval). _Relates D-199 (the kiro-cli verify-the-thing lesson this repeats), Task 46 (the original --with-semantic), HC-8 (the embedder probe reused), the live-test-every-task rule._

One write-site covers npm + plugin (both call `writeKitHooks`). **The cut-gate did its job** — a real prompt-free break that unit tests structurally couldn't see (no test drives a live Claude Code skill-approval) was caught by the live gate, exactly per the live-test-every-task rule. _Relates Task 90 (the original allow-list), Task 169 (this fix), the Kiro upstream-format-tracking precedent, the v0.4.1 cut-gate._
- **🔬 LIVE-TEST REVISION (2026-06-26) — D-208: the SessionStart SYNCHRONOUS drain (Q4) is INFEASIBLE — reverted; the detached roll + the cron-liveness gate (167.A) is the real fix.** During the Task 167 autopilot build, the `npm run live-verify:now-roll` agent-loop (real `claude --print`, the automatic path, NO manual command) FAILED: the sync drain fired + detected stale-now correctly, but a **real now→today Haiku roll takes 18–37 s** while the **SessionStart hook ceiling is 30 s**, so it reliably TIMED OUT and fell back to the detached path anyway (live `lazy-compress.log`: `sync-drain timed-out` → detached `compress-session success`). **Re-reading the research closed it:** claude-mem/mem0/Letta compact synchronously at session **END** (the Stop hook, no user waiting), NOT session start — and the kit already has that (the SessionEnd `compress-session` hook). So Q4's PRINCIPLE (correctness > speed) holds, but its MECHANISM (sync-at-start) was wrong — overturned by the live test (the primary source) + a closer research read. **The fix:** keep the now→today roll on the DETACHED SessionStart path + the SessionEnd hook; 167.A (cron-liveness) makes that detached roll reliable (a dead cron can't suppress it) → now.md heals next session and NEVER compounds. `runSyncDrainIfNeeded` + the inject-bin wiring were reverted; 167.B's (a) `now-too-big` verdict proved redundant (stale-now ⊇ it) and (c) sync-catch-up was the reverted code — 167.B ships as "covered by 167.A + 167.F." **Re-verified GREEN** by the live scenario (both single + multi-session: a bloated now.md + dead-cron heartbeat heals from one SessionStart fire). _This is the live-test-every-task rule + the lazy-framing rule applied to our OWN grilled decision: a green unit suite + a confident grilling still shipped an infeasible mechanism; only the real `claude --print` run caught it. Relates D-207 (Q4 revised), the cron-liveness research note, Task 105 (the detached roll it relies on)._
- **🧭 DESIGN RESOLVED (2026-06-25) — D-207: Task 167 = the `compaction-state.mjs` deep module (also architecture-review candidate #1), settled via a 7-question grilling + the marker-vs-derive research + the EverOS/OpenWolf peer-CODE sweep.** **(Q1)** a deep module absorbs the whole verdict — owns `isCompactionNeeded` (replaces `detectStaleness`; the `cron-registered` sentinel + `cronSentinelPath` retire). **(Q2)** marker-vs-derive = HYBRID (the GNU make "Empty Target Files" rule): DERIVE `now`/`daily`/`weekly` from existing artifacts (NO new marker — ADR-0002, the derive logic was never the broken part); STAMP cron-liveness with ONE anacron-style `cron-heartbeat` the cron bins write per fire, gated on AGE not existence. _Peer-validated: OpenWolf's `last_heartbeat`-by-age + EverOS's in-process APScheduler — both schedule reliably ONLY because they have an always-on process the kit lacks → the kit must derive + stamp-per-fire._ **(Q3)** interface = TWO methods — `isCompactionNeeded()` returns a RICH `{verdict, cronStale, heartbeatAge}` (lazy roll reads `.verdict`; doctor/dev reads the rest) + `recordCronHeartbeat()` (single writer). NO standalone `isCronAlive` — one source of truth, can't drift (a 3rd predicate = the exact "two sources disagree" class 167 fixes). **(Q4)** **"we're in the memory business" — correctness > startup speed (binding, P-9V3K7KEA):** stale content + dead cron → drain SYNCHRONOUSLY before inject (THIS session reads clean, not the old heal-next-session); a TIME BUDGET caps the sync portion + finishes detached so it never hangs (offline/huge-file). **(Q5)** cooldown touched on SUCCESS only (failed call must retry); the sync-drain BYPASSES the cooldown (cost guard yields to correctness; it still gates the opportunistic compress). **(Q6)** testing = agent-run, user does NOTHING — unit tests + a live agent-loop scenario in the existing `live-verify.mjs` (trap state → SessionStart-only → assert healed + multi-session-heals-in-one; FORBID any manual drain call — the masking that shipped the original bug green). _The user is on a Claude SUBSCRIPTION → no per-token $ cost gating live tests (P-SW5R69QS)._ **(Q7)** `cmk doctor` HC-10 KEPT as a DEV/diagnostic nice-to-have (helps US during kit dev; informational, never "run X to fix"), NOT a required part of the heal. Memory: P-YZQD9K4U/P-9V3K7KEA/P-UPJDK2UN/P-6PGKSVT3/P-DDRMSBPC/P-SW5R69QS. _Relates D-206 (the bug), the architecture review (candidate #1), the 2026-06-25 research notes (cron-liveness + EverOS), Task 105/106/35._
- **🐛 ROOT CAUSE + TASK (2026-06-25) — D-206: the stale-injection is the lazy now.md→today roll (Task 105) failing to recover a SEVERELY-bloated `now.md` → filed as Task 167, laned v0.4.x, bundled with the 105 lineage (the user: "we need a task for this and lane it for the next version, and do 105 with it").** D-205 found the SYMPTOM (stale "pending" line injected); this is the diagnosed CAUSE. **Task 105 IS shipped + works as designed** (lazy-roll on SessionStart, PR #127 + race-fix #128) — but built/tested against a ~10 KB `now.md`. **The dogfood broke it at scale:** across the v0.4.0 gate sessions (06-20→06-25, many VS Code restarts) `now.md` grew to **410 KB** and the latest `today-*.md` froze at **06-20** — so `inject-context.latestDaySession()` served a 5-day-old day-file. The user's sharp question — *"I restarted VS Code and started a new session, how can it not roll?"* — is exactly right: 105's lazy-on-SessionStart roll SHOULD have fired. **Why it didn't — PROVEN from `lazy-compress.log`, which CORRECTED my first guess (I wrote "times out on 410 KB"; the log says it NEVER RAN — skipped every SessionStart):** two compounding gates, NEITHER size-related. **(1) `cron-active` short-circuit (PRIMARY).** `detectStaleness` (lazy-compress.mjs L216-219) *"Cron sentinel short-circuits everything"* — if `context/.locks/cron-registered` exists → `cron-active` no-op, BEFORE the `stale-now` bloat check (precedence `cron > … > now`). `cmk register-crons` wrote the sentinel → lazy roll defers to "the cron" → **but the host cron NEVER FIRED** (live-confirmed: `Get-ScheduledTask cmk-daily-distill` State "Ready", `LastRunTime` BLANK — machine asleep at the 23:00 trigger). The sentinel disabled the only working path while pointing at a dead primary. **(2) `cooldown` (06-23 on).** The shared 120 s cooldown kept skipping the roll; journal-syncs touch the same marker, holding it fresh. **So `now.md` grew because the roll was GATED OUT, not because it failed** (forced `cmk-compress-session` drained 410 KB→1386 b in 26 s — the roll WORKS; it was never allowed to run). **This PROVES the user's "105 wasn't a real fix, just postponed the problem"** — 105's lazy roll turns itself OFF the instant a cron sentinel exists, with no check the cron is alive. **SCOPE (the user's catch: "the cron isn't registered by default, right?" — correct):** `cmk install` does NOT register crons (`register-crons` is OPTIONAL — README: "otherwise self-heals lazily"). So the **default user is NOT affected** (no sentinel → lazy roll works). This bites ONLY a `register-crons` user whose cron doesn't actually fire — and the nasty part is that **opting into the cron makes it WORSE than not** (the sentinel disables the working lazy fallback, then points at a dead primary). Medium severity, but a trap on the careful-user path. _Sibling to D-179 (2026-06-20, same week): the daily-distill itself went 4 days stale via a cron/timeout issue — the same "trust-the-cron / if-it's-not-automatic-it's-a-bug" class, caught by the same user instinct._ **Fix (Task 167, split into 3 sub-bugs, TDD, 105 lineage):** 167.A cron-LIVENESS gate (short-circuit only if the cron actually ran recently, not sentinel-exists — the highest-leverage one-line cause); 167.B size-triggered `now-too-big` verdict outranking `cron-active` + cooldown carve-out + chunked/sync catch-up; 167.C observability WARN + a `cmk doctor` HC-10 for bloated-now.md / stale-today / dead-cron. **Immediate data fix done this session** (ran `cmk-compress-session` by hand → fresh `today-2026-06-25.md`; inject verified clean: `RESEARCH-FIRST` count 0). **RE-LANED (the user, 2026-06-25): Task 167 = the NEXT version (v0.4.1); Task 151 persona = the version after; Cursor (was v0.4.1) postponed further out.** _Relates D-205 (the symptom), Task 105 (the roll it extends) / 106 (the rename-race a sync catch-up must preserve) / 35 (the cron path), `lazy-compress.mjs` `detectStaleness`, `inject-context.mjs` `latestDaySession`, `compress-session.mjs`, §6 rolling-window._

The user caught it: *"why is it stale? this is the whole point of this kit."* **Root cause (diagnosed, not guessed):** TWO injected tiers behaved differently. (1) **MEMORY.md auto-capture WORKED** — its Active Threads are current (06-25 timestamps: IDE-1.0.52-download, chose-to-upgrade, clean-test-folders). (2) **`context/sessions/recent.md` (the rolling-window summary) is FROZEN at 06-20** — its "Active Threads" still lists *"v0.4.0 Kiro adapter: RESEARCH-FIRST against kiro.dev §5.1 (use RESUME-HERE.md)"*, written BEFORE the campaign started. Until automated, a session that ships a major lane should correct `recent.md`'s Active Threads. _Relates the whole-kit thesis (kill cross-session amnesia — this is it, applied to the kit's OWN summaries), D-203n (the ship this stale line contradicted), the rolling-window compression (§6) which has no resolution-reconciliation step._

- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-22) — D-195: the `memory-write` SKILL.md `description` was INVALID YAML (an unquoted `: ` colon-space) — Claude Code tolerated it, Kiro REJECTED the skill ("Invalid SKILL.md frontmatter"); fixed with a YAML block scalar + a strict-parse validator (the 7th live-found cross-agent cut-blocker).** The cut-gate-kiro live test surfaced it the moment Kiro loaded the project: a red "Invalid SKILL.md frontmatter: …/.kiro/skills/memory-write/SKILL.md". **Root cause:** the `description:` was a plain (unquoted) YAML scalar containing the phrase `"update memory: X is now Y"` — and in YAML a `: ` (colon-space) inside a plain scalar starts a new mapping key, so a strict parser throws `mapping values are not allowed here` (line 3, col 607) and rejects the whole frontmatter. **Independently confirmed by two strict parsers:** my js-yaml AND Kiro's own PyYAML (the user asked Kiro why, and its `yaml.safe_load` threw the identical error at the identical column). **The Claude-tolerated/Kiro-strict class (same theme as D-185..190/194 — the 7th):** Claude Code reads SKILL.md frontmatter LENIENTLY (cares about name/description as text, doesn't strict-parse the block), so the invalid YAML shipped LATENT and "worked" for months; Kiro strict-parses the frontmatter for progressive skill-loading and rejects it. `memory-search` happened to parse (no `: ` in its description) — fragile by luck, not design. **The fix (the more robust one — Kiro itself suggested it over my first em-dash rephrase):** convert BOTH skills' `description` to a YAML **folded block scalar** (`description: >-`), which treats `:`, quotes, and apostrophes as literal text — immune to the whole class, not just this one phrase (the description is full of `"…"` and `don't`, so neither double- nor single-quoting works; the block scalar is the clean fix). **Single-source discipline (the user's "aren't we working with a template?"):** fixed ONLY the canonical `template/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md`, then `sync-plugin-skills.mjs` for the plugin copy + re-copied to the dogfood `.claude/skills/` — one source, both agents inherit it (Claude Code scaffolds it verbatim; Kiro via `kiro-skills.mjs` translating `context:`/`allowed-tools:` away — composition VERIFIED: the translated output parses + drops the right keys). **The structural guard (so it can't recur):** `validate-skill-sources.mjs` had its OWN naive line-split frontmatter parser (as lenient as Claude Code's — which is why the validator never caught it); replaced with a **strict js-yaml parse** that fails the gate naming the YAML reason. PLUS the integration guard: `cli-kiro-skills.test.js` now strict-parses the TRANSLATED `.kiro/skills/` output (what Kiro actually consumes) — the test that would have caught it originally. Also migrated `cli-skill-scaffold.test.js`'s naive frontmatter parser to js-yaml (it returned an empty description on the block scalar). **Both agents, one fix:** the canonical block-scalar fix + the strict-parse validator protect Claude Code AND Kiro scaffolding at once. Test-first: `scripts-validate-skill-sources.test.js` (real-skills-pass / colon-space-fails / colon-without-space-ok) + the kiro-skills integration test. Full suite 2239/0. _Relates D-185/186/187/188/190/194 (the Claude-tolerated/Kiro-strict cross-agent theme — the 7th), KG4 of the gate (which only checked Claude-only keys were ABSENT, never that the YAML PARSES — the gate gap this closes), the single-template / sync-plugin-skills discipline (one canonical source), the primary-source rule (two independent strict parsers confirmed the diagnosis), the live-test discipline (only a real Kiro project-load surfaced the reject)._

- **🔎 RECONCILED — on Kiro IDE 1.0, `permissions.yaml` is AUTHORITATIVE; `.vscode/settings.json` trust is auto-MIGRATED into it (2026-06-25) — D-203i. (Kiro's own assistant gave the LEGACY `.vscode` answer — the convergence-vs-primary-source trap, settled by disk.)** The user asked Kiro IDE "how do I add commands to permissions / what about MCP?" and Kiro's assistant answered with the OLD model: `.vscode/settings.json` `kiroAgent.trustedCommands` (shell) + `kiroAgent.trustedMcpTools` (MCP). **But the disk contradicts that for 1.0:** the gate project's `.vscode/settings.json` has ONLY `trustedCommands` (NO `trustedMcpTools`, NO skill) — yet MCP tools ran PROMPT-FREE. The `~/.kiro/workspace-roots/<hash>/.trust-migration.json` proves why: Kiro MIGRATED the `.vscode` trust → `permissions.yaml` (`{root: c:\Temp\kiro-ide-gate, rulesWritten: 2, completedAt: 11:27}`), and `permissions.yaml` carries all three capabilities (`shell` + `mcp` + `skill`). **So `permissions.yaml` is the live authority on 1.0; `.vscode` works only because Kiro migrates it (once, at first open).** **CONSEQUENCE for 50.N.5:** (a) the kit's existing `.vscode` `trustedCommands` write still works (Kiro migrates it) — so hooks stay prompt-free; (b) BUT there is NO `.vscode` setting for SKILL trust in Kiro's model, so the only reliable pre-trust for the skill-load is to write `permissions.yaml` DIRECTLY at `~/.kiro/workspace-roots/<hash>/` (hash = sha256(norm(projectRoot)).slice(0,16), D-203h). 50.N.5 writes permissions.yaml directly (shell+mcp+skill), making the kit's trust self-contained from install rather than dependent on Kiro's one-time migration of `.vscode`. **The lesson (again):** Kiro's IN-IDE ASSISTANT is an LLM describing docs/old-model — NOT a primary source for live 1.0 behavior; the `permissions.yaml` + `.trust-migration.json` on disk are. _Relates D-203h (the canonical format), D-203f/D-196 (Trust v2 — now fully reconciled: migrated, not broken), Task 50.N.5 (writes permissions.yaml directly), the primary-source-over-(even-the-tool's-own-LLM) rule._

- **🔬 DEEP-RESEARCH + 🚨 LATENT CUT-BLOCKER (2026-06-25) — D-203: the Kiro IDE 1.0 release (2026-06-25 — TODAY) DEPRECATED the legacy `.kiro.hook` format the kit's EXISTING IDE hooks use → they will SILENTLY STOP FIRING on Kiro IDE 1.0+. Found resolving the 50.N.3 verify-first contradiction.** The kit's `kiro-ide-hooks.mjs` emits `cmk-capture.kiro.hook` + `cmk-inject.kiro.hook` in the **0.x format** (`when:{type:'agentStop'|'promptSubmit'}` + `then:{type:'runCommand'}`). Per kiro.dev/docs/whats-new-1-0 + the changelog, **Kiro IDE 1.0 replaced `.kiro.hook` ENTIRELY** with a consolidated `.kiro/hooks/*.json` v1 format: `{"version":"v1","hooks":[{name, trigger, matcher?, action:{type:'command'|'agent', command|prompt}, timeout?, enabled?}]}` with **PascalCase `trigger`** values (`SessionStart`, `UserPromptSubmit`, `PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, `PostFileSave`, `PostFileCreate`, `PostFileDelete`, `PreTaskExec`, `PostTaskExec`) and **`action.type:'command'`** (NOT `then.type:'runCommand'`). Legacy 0.x hooks "appear with an upgrade badge — they won't execute until migrated." **This RESOLVES the 50.N.3 contradiction:** the 2026-06-21 survey's "IDE hooks are askAgent-only, never deterministic" was TRUE for 0.x; **v1 added a first-class deterministic `{type:'command'}` shell action** ("executed locally on your PC, do not use an LLM") — so the 2026-06-25 deep-research was right (the convergence-vs-primary-source trap: the survey saw 0.x convention, the docs describe v1 capability). **What v1 UNLOCKS (all primary-source-confirmed):** ☑ deterministic shell commands on IDE hooks; ☑ **`PreToolUse` CAN BLOCK** (non-zero exit blocks the tool — so an IDE delete-guard IS possible, closing the Task-165(b) "IDE has no guardrail" gap); ☑ **`PostFileSave`** for observe-edit; ☑ files are **installer-writable** ("write a JSON file directly" is a documented creation method). **⚠️ 5 things STILL need a LIVE PROBE (the kit-burned-before discipline — docs silent/ambiguous):** (1) does Kiro auto-LOAD an installer-written `.kiro/hooks/*.json` without a GUI "create"/reload; (2) what argv/env/stdin a `PreToolUse` command receives (the file path the guard must inspect — UNSPECIFIED); (3) exit-code 1-vs-2 for blocking; (4) the exact IDE tool-name `matcher` tokens (`fsWrite`/`executeBash`/…?); (5) whether v1 has a session-END trigger to replace `agentStop` capture (the type list has `SessionStart` but no obvious `Stop`/`SessionEnd` — the kit's end-of-turn capture may need to move to `PostTaskExec` or another mechanism). **SCOPE IMPACT:** 50.N.3 is no longer "add 2 IDE legs" — it's a **v1 migration of the IDE hook writer** (capture+inject MUST move to v1 or they break on IDE 1.0), with the new guard+observe legs coming along in the same format. The CLI agent-config format is SEPARATE + unaffected (kiro-cli uses STDIN-JSON-in-agent-config, not `.kiro/hooks/`). Sources: kiro.dev/docs/hooks/ + /actions/ + /types/ + /whats-new-1-0 + /changelog. _Relates 50.N.3 (the verify-first leg this researches — now reshaped), Task 165(b) (the "IDE has no delete-guard" claim — now OVERTURNABLE via v1 PreToolUse, pending live probe), D-200's deep-research (which first flagged the IDE-has-10-triggers correction), the primary-source-over-convergence rule (the survey was convention, the docs are capability)._
