- **🚨 BUG×2 + 🔧 FIX + 🔬 DEEP-RESEARCH (2026-06-25) — D-200: kiro-cli AUTOMATIC capture (the Stop-hook → read transcript → extract → promote-the-wedge chain) NEVER worked — TWO independent breaks, both fixed + live-proven. D-199's "ALL THREE surfaces fully work" was premature: it proved INJECT + EXPLICIT; the live cut-gate (the user driving real kiro-cli) caught that the AUTOMATIC legs were dead.** The wedge (a "in every project, always X" rule auto-promoting to the user tier) did not land. Root-caused to two separate bugs, each the same D-198 class ("is it even reading the right place?"):
  1. **The transcript reader was IDE-only.** `readKiroTurn` (kiro-transcript.mjs) read ONLY the Kiro IDE path (`%APPDATA%/…/globalStorage/kiro.kiroagent/workspace-sessions/<base64(cwd)>/` via `CONTINUE_GLOBAL_DIR`). **kiro-CLI uses a DIFFERENT location AND schema** (primary-source verified on a real file): `~/.kiro/sessions/cli/<uuid>.json`, matched by `cwd`, with the assistant text at `session_state.conversation_metadata.user_turn_metadatas[].result.Ok.content[].data` — NO `history[]`, and the CLI never sets `CONTINUE_GLOBAL_DIR`. So `readKiroTurn` returned empty for every kiro-cli stop → capture wrote an empty turn → nothing extracted. **Fix:** new `parseKiroCliSession` + `readKiroCliTurn` (read `~/.kiro/sessions/cli`, pick the latest file whose `cwd` matches, normalize separators — NOT `path.resolve()`, which re-roots a value that ever looks relative), wired as a FALLBACK in `readKiroTurn` (IDE path stays primary; CLI fires when the IDE path yields nothing → IDE unaffected).
  2. **The kiro stop hook never spawned auto-extract.** `runHook` (subcommands.mjs) called `captureTurn({payload, projectRoot})` WITHOUT `autoExtractPath` — and `captureTurn`'s in-module default is `null`, so `spawnAutoExtract(null)` short-circuits `no-auto-extract-path`. Capture wrote `now.md` but NEVER extracted facts. The Claude Code bin (`cmk-capture-turn.mjs`) passes the resolved sibling-bin path; the kiro path didn't. **Fix:** new `resolveKiroAutoExtractPath()` (env `CMK_AUTO_EXTRACT_PATH` → `../bin/cmk-auto-extract.mjs` sibling — mirrors the Claude bin), passed into the kiro capture dep.
  **LIVE-PROVEN end-to-end:** after both fixes (global rebuilt), running `cmk hook stop` as kiro-cli does → capture reads the REAL CLI transcript (uv/ruff turn, no pollution) → auto-extract spawns + calls Haiku → **the wedge PROMOTED**: a fresh "always squash, never commit to main, in every project" rule landed in `~/.claude-memory-kit/HABITS.md` (`U-3FFLPSVH`/`U-EWGEGAW5`). **The wedge rides on the per-turn Stop hook, NOT SessionEnd** — Task 61 made auto-extract do INLINE cross-project promotion every turn (the SessionEnd batch sweep is a top-up). **🔬 DEEP-RESEARCH (the user: "can you do a deep research about it?")** — primary-source sweep of kiro.dev confirmed + CORRECTED the kit's assumptions: (a) **NO Kiro surface has a SessionEnd event** (CLI, IDE, or V3) — so the per-turn wedge is the ONLY path, which is fine since it already works; (b) **Kiro IDE exposes 10 hook triggers, NOT 2** (the kit uses only `promptSubmit`+`agentStop` — it's leaving Pre/Post-Tool-Use, File Save/Create/Delete, Task hooks on the table → the IDE observe-edit + delete-guard gaps ARE closable, contradicting the kit's "IDE = 2 triggers" note); (c) **IDE hooks CAN run deterministic shell commands** (the kit wrongly believed askAgent-only — the "convergence-across-surveyed-repos ≠ primary-source" trap); (d) **V3 = CLI 2.8.0 (2026-06-17), opt-in + non-breaking** (kit said 2.9.0) → v2 agent-config is the correct DEFAULT, v3 is forward-compat; (e) `max_output_size` is NOT in the vendor docs (kit asserted it from Rust source). **STILL OPEN for full Claude-Code parity (the v0.4.0 goal "make Kiro == Claude Code"):** observe-edit (PostToolUse) + prompt-capture (`<private>`-strip half of UserPromptSubmit) are unwired on Kiro CLI+IDE; the IDE delete-guard is unwired — all now KNOWN to be closable per the research (Kiro has the triggers). Test-first: `cli-kiro-read-turn.test.js` (+5 CLI-schema cases incl. cwd-match, recency, malformed, IDE-precedence) + `cli-kiro-hook-bin.test.js` (Door-3 autoExtractPath-resolves). Full suite 2272/0. _Relates D-199 (the explicit-memory sibling — this is the AUTOMATIC sibling; together they make kiro-cli's CORE memory work), D-198 (the same "reading the wrong location" class — third instance), Task 61 (inline per-turn promotion — why no SessionEnd is needed), the live-test discipline (only the user driving real kiro-cli surfaced that "works" meant inject+explicit, not automatic), the primary-source rule (the deep-research corrected 5 kit assumptions that convergent internal notes had wrong)._
- **🚨 BUG + 🔧 FIX + 🧹 CLEANUP (2026-06-24) — D-199: kiro-cli explicit memory (`cmk remember`/`cmk search` in chat) silently did nothing — the agent reported `✅ Remembered` but NOTHING wrote to disk. THE root cause was ONE missing line: the kiro-cli agent config had no `tools` capability field, so a custom agent had ZERO tools enabled and could not run ANY shell command — the model was FABRICATING success.** This took **hours** and four wrong diagnoses to find, all blaming Kiro: (1) MCP tools not wired to custom agents (#5873), (2) the Windows allowlist rejecting matching commands (#5376/#7431), (3) a `cd` prefix breaking the allowlist (#4579), (4) env not flowed to stdio servers. I built MCP→CLI→`--project`→env workarounds for each and even drafted a "documented kiro-cli limitation" for the release. **All misdiagnoses.** The real cause: per kiro.dev/docs/cli/custom-agents/configuration-reference, `tools` is the agent's CAPABILITY SET ("lists all tools the agent can potentially use") — and **our agent had no `tools` field at all**, while Kiro's own example agent lists `tools: [read, write, shell, grep, glob, …]`. With no tools, the agent can run nothing; the model role-played `cmk remember` + invented a tool name + fabricated the `✅ Remembered` result. **The fix: `tools: ['*']`** (proven live — a real rich fact `P-DTRaa79G` landed in a kiro-cli chat). **The tell I walked past four times:** a tool call with a *fabricated* result and *zero* side-effect (no audit entry, no file) = "the tool never ran" = a missing capability declaration in the agent's OWN config, NOT a platform bug. **The user's reframe cracked it** — *"cmk remember is just a tool like ls — how do you make it run tools in chat?"* — reframing from "why is this command blocked" to "is the agent even allowed to run commands at all." **The working kiro-cli config (all proven live):** `tools: ['*']` (run shell commands) + `includeMcpJson: false` (no MCP — kiro-cli doesn't wire MCP tools to custom agents AND every stdio MCP server pops a `cmd.exe` console window on Windows; the terminal uses the `cmk remember`/`cmk search` shell commands instead, which ALSO removes the popup) + the agent prompt instructs the model to pass `--project "<abs>"` and NOT prefix with `cd` (a `cd …` prefix makes the command start with `cd`, failing the start-anchored `^cmk remember` trust match → an approval prompt) + `cmk remember`/`cmk search` gained a `--project <dir>` flag (+ `normalizeProjectPath` for a git-bash `/c/Temp`→`C:/Temp` path). **🧹 CLEANUP (the user: "no useless code"):** a systematic audit removed the now-dead MCP project-root machinery from the prior misdiagnoses — the IDE `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` is back to plain `cmk mcp serve` (no `--project`/env: the IDE launches from the workspace; kiro-cli doesn't use MCP), `mcp serve --project` + a `readFlag` helper removed, `resolveMcpProjectRoot` simplified to `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR → walk-up-to-context/ → cwd` (net −46 lines). **Two-pass review** (self + `code-review-excellence` skill, approved no-Blocking): the skill caught a stale cut-gate checklist (KCG5/KC4/inventory still asserted the old MCP shape → a tester would mark the correct config as FAIL) + flagged that the *approval gate* (allowedCommands + preToolUse), not the `tools` set, is the security boundary (so a future reader must not "tighten" `'*'` to a scoped list — a hardcoded `execute_bash` would silently drop the shell tool across the V2→V3 `execute_bash`→`execute_command` rename). Both addressed. Full suite 2266/0; real `kiro-cli agent validate` passes. **NET v0.4.0 Kiro state: ALL THREE surfaces fully work** — Claude Code (MCP), Kiro IDE (MCP + autoApprove), kiro-cli (automatic hooks + `cmk remember`/`cmk search` explicit + no popup). _Relates D-198 (the agent-location sibling, already merged #225), the D-185..190 cross-agent theme (this one was NOT a Kiro bug though — it was ours), the CLAUDE.md binding lesson added ("check the agent's capability/enablement config FIRST when a tool call fabricates success"), the live-test discipline (the fabricated `✅ Remembered` is exactly the gap unit tests can't see)._
- **🚨 BUG + 🔧 FIX + 📌 PARTIAL-DEFER (2026-06-24) — D-198: the kit wrote the kiro-cli agent config to the WRONG LOCATION (`~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/`) — kiro-cli never loaded it, so NO hooks fired. The TRUE root cause behind D-197's symptom (D-197's "matcher" fix was a right fix to a dead file).** Found by instrumenting the cut-gate KG-guard: a diagnostic probe wired to the agent's `agentSpawn` + `preToolUse` hooks showed **NEITHER fired** — then `kiro-cli agent list` revealed the active default was the built-in **`kiro_default`**, with agents living in **`~/.kiro/agents/`** (global) + `<project>/.kiro/agents/` (workspace). The kit wrote `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/q_cli_default.json` — the OLD Amazon-Q location kiro-cli 2.8+ does NOT read. So our config sat ignored; the guard, agentSpawn, and stop hooks all silently never ran. **Our own research had it right** ([2026-06-20-kiro-automatic-memory-deep-research §3](../research/2026-06-20-kiro-automatic-memory-deep-research.md): *"Sets `{"chat.defaultAgent":"kiro_memory"}` in `~/.kiro/settings/cli.json` … the load-bearing step the kit is missing"*) — the implementation dropped the verified finding (the "read the authoritative docs before implementing" rule, applied to our OWN research). **The fix:** `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` now writes (1) `~/.kiro/agents/cmk.json` and (2) `~/.kiro/settings/cli.json` `{"chat.defaultAgent":"cmk"}` (the load-bearing registration, managed-merge byte-preserving other keys). Agent name `cmk` (not `q_cli_default` — that name doesn't exist; the built-in is `kiro_default`). **Live-validated with the real `kiro-cli agent validate`**, which caught TWO more bugs unit tests couldn't: (a) the old top-level `managedBy` marker is REJECTED (`unknown field`) → moved the ownership marker into the valid `description` field; (b) `includeMcpJson` + `useLegacyMcpJson` are the SAME setting → supplying both is a `duplicate field` error → kept only `useLegacyMcpJson:false`. Also dropped `file://AGENTS.md` / `file://.kiro/steering/cmk.md` refs: kiro-cli resolves a config's `file://` paths RELATIVE TO THE AGENT-FILE DIR (`~/.kiro/agents/`), not the project root (kiro.dev/docs) — so a project-relative ref can't resolve from the global agent; AGENTS.md auto-loads from the workspace anyway, and an INLINE recall/persist `prompt` travels with the agent. **PROVEN LIVE:** after the fix, `kiro-cli agent list` shows `* cmk Global` (resolved default) and the **`agentSpawn` hook FIRES** (probe captured the stdin `{"hook_event_name":"agentSpawn","cwd":…,"session_id":…}`, env `KIRO_VERSION=2.9.0`) — so **capture + inject (the core automatic-memory value) now work on kiro-cli.** **📌 THE GUARDRAIL LEG IS DEFERRED on kiro-cli V3 (a Kiro platform shift, NOT a kit bug):** the same probe showed `preToolUse` does NOT fire on kiro-cli 2.9.0 with ANY matcher (`'*'` or the literal `execute_command` — 2.9.0 ALSO renamed the shell tool `execute_bash`→`execute_command`). Primary source ([kiro.dev/docs/cli/v3](https://kiro.dev/docs/cli/v3/)): **Kiro CLI V3 redesigned hooks as a BREAKING CHANGE** — embedded agent-config hooks moved to standalone `.kiro/hooks/*.json` (PascalCase triggers), and tool-blocking moved from `preToolUse` to a new `permissions.yaml`. So our V2-style embedded `preToolUse` is unsupported-for-blocking on V3 (V2 `agentSpawn`/`stop` still fire, which is why capture/inject work). The banner warns it: *"Migration tooling to bring your V2 configurations to V3 is coming soon."* On V3, the delete-guardrail relies on **kiro-cli's OWN shell-approval gate** (which prompted "shell requires approval" every time in the gate) until the kit adds V3 hook support. **The Claude Code + IDE guardrails are unaffected** (different mechanisms). **Shipped regardless:** `execute_command` added to `guard-memory.mjs` SHELL_TOOLS (correct for when the guard DOES fire). **Follow-up (Task 166):** V3 hook support (`.kiro/hooks/*.json` PascalCase + `permissions.yaml`), possibly emitting both V2+V3. _Relates D-197 (matcher — a real-but-secondary fix; superseded as "the" root cause by this), D-187 (BOM-tolerant reads — kiro-cli's OWN reader is NOT BOM-tolerant, so the kit must never WRITE a BOM; a PowerShell `ConvertTo-Json` probe-edit injected one and broke the live agent mid-diagnosis), the live-test discipline (an instrumented probe found what 3 black-box KG-guard runs couldn't), the "read our OWN research first" rule (the location was in the research, dropped at impl)._
- **🚨 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-23) — D-197: the memory delete-guardrail did NOT FIRE in kiro-cli — its `preToolUse` matcher was a pipe-alternation, but kiro-cli matchers are LITERAL strings → it matched nothing → a `Remove-Item -Recurse -Force context/sessions` DELETED memory unblocked (caught live by the cut-gate-kiro KG-guard; the D-193 I3 risk realized).** The headline data-loss guardrail (D-192/193) silently did NOT protect a kiro-cli user. **Live sequence:** asked kiro-cli to `rm -rf context/sessions` → model cautioned + asked → on "yes" it queued the shell command → kiro-cli's OWN "shell requires approval" gate (good — kiro-cli warns independently) → the `rm -rf` failed on Windows → model rewrote to `Remove-Item -Recurse -Force context/sessions` (our guard's dual-pattern coverage anticipated this) → approved → **"Done — context/sessions has been removed."** The guard NEVER fired. **Root cause (primary-source, kiro.dev/docs/cli/hooks):** the `preToolUse` `matcher` is a **LITERAL string, NOT a regex/glob** — pipe alternation is NOT supported. Our matcher `'execute_bash|executeBash|shell'` looked for a tool literally named that (= nothing), so the hook never matched the real `execute_bash` tool. **This is EXACTLY the I3 risk D-193 flagged** ("Kiro matcher alternation unverified — KG-guard covers it") — the live gate covered it. **The fix:** matcher `'execute_bash|executeBash|shell'` → **`'*'`** (match ALL tools — the docs' all-tools matcher). Safe + future-proof: `decideGuard` already filters to destructive+memory commands regardless of tool name, so matching all tools costs nothing and catches every shell-tool variant + future tools. Test-first (the matcher must be `'*'`, never contain `'|'`). **Scope honesty (a SEPARATE finding, NOT code-fixable):** the Kiro **IDE** has NO kit `preToolUse` delete-guardrail at all — only the kiro-cli agent-config can carry `preToolUse` (the IDE's auto-firing hooks are `agentStop`/`promptSubmit` only; per the research, IDE hooks are "defined in the IDE UI, no file an installer can write"). So the kit's delete-guardrail is a **kiro-cli-only** protection; the IDE relies on Kiro's own native confirm-before-destructive behavior (which DID prompt). Documented as a known Kiro-platform limitation, not a kit bug. **A v0.4.0 cut-blocker** — fixed before the tag. _Relates D-192/193 (the guardrail this repairs), D-183 (the preToolUse stdin shape — correct; only the matcher was wrong), the live-test discipline (the gate caught a silently-broken headline safety feature unit tests couldn't — the matcher's real-CLI behavior), the primary-source rule (kiro.dev/docs/cli/hooks: matchers are literal, the doc we should have checked when writing the alternation)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-23) — D-196: the kit auto-approves Kiro's HOOKS (D-194) but NOT its MCP TOOLS — so `mk_remember` (and every MCP call) prompts "Reject / Trust / Run" in a Kiro session; fixed by adding `autoApprove` (IDE) + `allowedTools` (CLI) to the MCP wiring (the 8th cross-agent finding, found LIVE in cut-gate-kiro Session 1).** The user ran the real Kiro live test and hit it: the capture/inject HOOKS ran silently (D-194 trusted-commands works — "Command executed successfully with no output", no prompt) AND Kiro correctly CALLED `mk_remember` with a full rich payload when the user stated a preference (M1 works) — but the MCP tool call itself popped a **Reject / Trust / Run** approval. **Root cause:** Kiro gates **MCP-tool calls** through a DIFFERENT trust system than **shell-command hooks**. D-194 wired `kiroAgent.trustedCommands` (hooks) but nothing wired the MCP-tool approval. **The fix (two surfaces, two DIFFERENT mechanisms — primary-source verified):** (1) **IDE** (`.kiro/settings/mcp.json`) → an **`autoApprove`** array INSIDE the server entry (`kiro.dev/docs/mcp/configuration`), **bare** tool names — added the explicit 11-tool list (`mk_remember`…`mk_queue_resolve`) to `install-kiro.mjs` `MCP_ENTRY`. (2) **CLI agent-config** (`~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/*.json`) → **`allowedTools`** at the agent top level (`kiro.dev/docs/cli/custom-agents` — the Amazon-Q agent uses `allowedTools` with the `@server/tool` format, NOT `autoApprove`), set to **`["@cmk"]`** (allow the kit's own server's tools). **Scoped, never a `"*"` blanket** — only the kit's tools; `mk_forget` is safe to auto-approve the CALL because it carries its own two-step confirm-token before deleting. The two surfaces genuinely diverge (same as the D-194 IDE-wildcard-vs-CLI-regex split, and the mcp.json-shape split D-182 noted) — do not unify them. Test-first (install-kiro autoApprove + kiro-cli-agent allowedTools assertions, both "never `*`"); full suite 2253/0. cut-gate-kiro KG2 extended to verify both + M1 made the live prompt-free confirmation. **What the same live session PROVED works:** D-194 (hooks silent), D-195 (valid SKILL.md YAML, no reject), KH1 (capture fired), M1 (Kiro called mk_remember rich). **Two-pass review — skill-review I1 (Important):** the IDE `autoApprove` is an EXPLICIT 11-tool list, so a future 12th MCP tool would silently ship un-auto-approved (prompting Reject/Trust/Run for that one tool — the bug, recursed). The list matched the 11 tools exactly, but nothing enforced it. **Fixed with a structural guard:** `validate-cli-mcp-parity.mjs` (which already enumerates the registered MCP tools) gained `checkAutoApprove` — every registered tool must be in `MCP_AUTO_APPROVE` and vice-versa (both directions), wired into `npm test`/CI Lint. Proven to bite (a synthetic 12th tool fails it). Considered + rejected switching the IDE side to `autoApprove:["*"]`: the kiro.dev docs don't explicitly confirm `"*"` is server-scoped (only structurally implied), and the explicit list is provably correct — the guard removes the drift risk without the ambiguity. _Relates D-194 (the hook-trust sibling — this is the MCP-tool analog), D-182 (the IDE-mcp.json vs CLI-agent-config shape divergence), the primary-source rule (two different kiro.dev doc pages gave the two mechanisms; the `"*"` scope was ambiguous so the explicit-list+guard won), the prose-rule→validator discipline (the drift guard), the live-test discipline (only a real Kiro chat-capture surfaced the MCP prompt; unit tests asserted the server entry, not that a tool call is prompt-free)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔬 RESEARCH (2026-06-22) — D-194: a Kiro install's hooks PROMPT "Run/Reject" on every fire — they aren't auto-trusted; `cmk install --ide kiro` must ALSO write `kiroAgent.trustedCommands` so the kit's own hook commands auto-run (the 6th live-found cross-agent cut-blocker).** The cut-gate-kiro live test (50.M) surfaced it the moment a real Kiro IDE session fired the inject hook: Kiro showed a **"Hook Command … Run / Reject"** approval prompt for `cmd.exe /c cmk hook promptSubmit` instead of running it silently — so "automatic memory" isn't automatic; the user must click Run every turn. **Same Claude-Code-shaped-assumption class as D-185/186/187/188/190:** on Claude Code a registered hook just fires; on Kiro a hook's shell command is gated by Kiro's **command-trust** system and prompts unless pre-trusted. **Primary-source diagnosis (kiro.dev, the "did you check the docs?" rule):** (a) [Hook actions](https://kiro.dev/docs/hooks/actions/) + [Hook examples](https://kiro.dev/docs/hooks/examples/) confirm our hook DESIGN is correct — a Prompt-Submit→shell-command hook is a documented, supported shape (their own `curl` logger example), runs "locally on your PC … each time the hook is triggered," no approval step *in the hook spec*. So the prompt is NOT a hook-shape bug. (b) The Run/Reject is the **command-permission gate**: [permissions](https://kiro.dev/docs/cli/chat/permissions/) — trusting a command stores it (CLI side) as regex in the agent's `allowedCommands`; the **IDE side** uses **`kiroAgent.trustedCommands`** in `settings.json` (user scope `…/Kiro/User/settings.json` OR workspace `.vscode/settings.json`), wildcard-prefix matched (`npm *` trusts anything starting `npm`). The user found the IDE settings mechanism by trial-and-error (the docs bury it); confirmed against kiro.dev search. (c) **Autopilot is NOT the gate** — the screenshot had Autopilot ON and it still prompted; Autopilot governs file-edit approval, command-trust is separate. **The gap in the kit:** `kiro-ide-hooks.mjs` + `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` wire the hooks but the kit writes **NO `kiroAgent.trustedCommands` / `allowedCommands` anywhere** (grep-confirmed: zero hits in `src/`). **THE FIX (to build):** `cmk install --ide kiro` writes a managed `kiroAgent.trustedCommands` entry into the **workspace** `.vscode/settings.json` (project-scoped — travels with the repo, never touches the user's global trust) pre-trusting ONLY the kit's own hook commands — the SPECIFIC prefixes (`cmd.exe /c cmk hook *`, `cmd.exe /c cmk-guard-memory*` on Windows; the bare `cmk hook *` / `cmk-guard-memory*` on POSIX), **NOT** an over-permissive `cmd.exe /c *` (the docs warn wildcards over-trust, and trust matches only the command PREFIX — a broad prefix would trust chained commands after it). CLI side: the agent-config's `allowedCommands` gets the same kit-only patterns so the guarded default agent's hooks don't prompt either. Conservative + idempotent + over-mutation-safe (merge into an existing `trustedCommands` array, never clobber a user's entries; BOM-tolerant read via `read-json.mjs`). Cut-gate-kiro gets two new checks: **KG11** (trustedCommands + allowedCommands written on disk) + **KH-trust** (the live IDE hook fires with NO Run/Reject prompt). Test-first: `cli-kiro-trusted-commands.test.js` (install/uninstall/idempotent/corrupt/BOM/over-mutation) + install-kiro + kiro-cli-agent assertions; full suite 2235/0. **Two-pass review — the skill-review caught 3, one Important:** (**I1**) the orchestrator copied the MCP-leg's halt-on-corrupt-config pattern to the trust leg, but trust runs LAST (after MCP/steering/AGENTS.md/skills/ide-hooks succeeded) and is the LEAST critical surface — so a user's pre-existing malformed `.vscode/settings.json` would abort an otherwise-good install. **Fixed: the trust leg is now NON-FATAL** — on a corrupt settings.json it records a `warnings[]` entry, skips the surface, and continues to the CLI agent (the hooks still fire, they just prompt until trusted); added the I1 regression test. (**M2**) the CLI `allowedCommands` regex was unanchored — `cmk hook .*` could match a command that merely CONTAINS the phrase; **fixed: start-anchored (`^cmk hook .*`)** to mirror the IDE's prefix-from-start semantics. (**M1**) uninstall removes a pattern byte-identical to ours even if the user added it — inherent to marker-less array-membership ownership, near-zero collision; documented as a code comment, not structurally fixed (over-engineering for this surface). **Security assessment (the focus question): the prefix/regex trust is broad-by-the-docs but safe-in-context** — the kit AUTHORS the hook commands (fixed strings, never user/model-controlled at the pattern level), and Kiro only runs the exact `command` from the hook definition, so the "prefix trusts chained commands" warning doesn't create an injection path (an attacker who could inject into `.kiro/hooks/` already has write access = game over); the patterns explicitly avoid the blanket `*`/`.*` the docs warn against (tests pin it). _Relates D-185/186/187/188/190 (the cross-agent "Claude-Code-only mechanism / assumption not carried over" theme — this is the 6th), D-183 (the IDE hook surface this makes actually-silent), D-187 (the BOM-tolerant read-json this reuses), the primary-source rule (kiro.dev hook + permissions + agent-config-reference docs — the IDE-wildcard-vs-CLI-regex distinction came from there), the two-pass-review rule (skill-review's I1 non-fatal fix), the live-test discipline (only a real Kiro IDE turn surfaced the prompt; unit tests asserted the hook file, not that it fires silently)._
- **🛡️ BUILD (2026-06-22) — D-193: the memory delete-guardrail ships kit-wide for BOTH agents — a `PreToolUse` hook (`cmk-guard-memory`) that BLOCKS a destructive shell command aimed at a memory path before it runs; the Kiro payload shape was CORRECTED from a guess by checking the real oh-my-kiro/vibekit sources.** The structural enforcement of D-192's prose rule. **Shared core:** `guard-memory.mjs` — `decideGuard(cmd)` blocks iff the command is BOTH destructive (`rm`/`Remove-Item`/`del`/`git clean`/`git reset --hard`) AND aimed at a memory path (`context/`, the `~/.claude-memory-kit` persona tier, `MEMORY.md`/`DECISIONS.md`). Broad by intent: a false block is recoverable, a false allow is the data loss. **The bin `cmk-guard-memory`** reads the PreToolUse stdin payload `{tool_name, tool_input:{command}}`, exits 2 to BLOCK (fail-OPEN on any error — a broken guardrail must never wedge the session). **Wiring (the per-agent thin shim):** Claude Code — `KIT_HOOKS_BLOCK.PreToolUse` (matcher `Bash|PowerShell`) wired by `cmk install`; Kiro CLI agent-config — `preToolUse` (matcher `execute_bash`) calling `cmk-guard-memory` directly. **THE PRIMARY-SOURCE CORRECTION (the user's "don't we have an example from the research?"):** I first GUESSED Kiro's `preToolUse` passes the command via argv/env (extrapolating D-183's "Kiro hooks use argv+env not stdin" — true for agentSpawn/stop/promptSubmit). Reading the actual cloned `oh-my-kiro/hooks/security/block-dangerous.sh` (a real Kiro `preToolUse` guardrail — header literally "PreToolUse[Bash] (Kiro + CC)") + `vibekit/vibenotif.py` DISPROVED the guess: Kiro's `preToolUse` reads **STDIN JSON `{tool_name, tool_input.command}` — IDENTICAL to Claude Code** (`INPUT=$(cat); jq '.tool_input.command'`), tool name **`execute_bash`**, matcher `execute_bash`. So **one bin guards both agents** — no Kiro-specific adapter; the speculative argv/env adapter was removed. The lesson: a `preToolUse` payload is NOT the same surface as the capture/inject hooks; checking the real survey clones (we HAD them at `/c/tmp/kiro-survey/`) beat extrapolating from a related-but-different finding. **The Kiro `preToolUse` FIRING is still flagged for the cut-gate-kiro live test** (KG-guard) — schema-accept + does-it-actually-block on a real `kiro-cli` — but the payload shape is now verified-from-precedent, not guessed. Test-first: `cli-guard-memory.test.js` (incident + false-positive guards + execute_bash + fail-open) + dispatcher/runHook guard-branch tests (block→exit2, allow→0, no-guard/crash→fail-open) + the Claude-Code install-hooks update (6th hook, coexists with a user PreToolUse). Full suite 2205/0. **Dogfood false-positive caught immediately:** the guardrail BLOCKED its OWN feature commit (`git commit -m "...rm...context/..."` — the message PROSE mentions a delete) — first fixed with a whole-command EXEMPT list. **The two-pass review then caught a BLOCKING BYPASS that the exemption opened:** a start-anchored whole-command exempt let `echo "cleaning" && rm -rf context/sessions` through — the leading `echo` exempted the WHOLE compound command including the chained `rm` (a *natural* announce-then-act agent shape; the original incident command `rm -f context/sessions/*` + any `echo` prefix → allowed). Plus 3 under-block classes: a delete in a `$(...)` inside an exempt commit arg (I1), and delete mechanisms with no `rm` verb — `find … -delete` / `truncate` / `> file` redirection-truncate (I2), and a Kiro `executeBash`/`shell` matcher gap (I3). **Fixed (per the skill-review):** `decideGuard` now SPLITS the command into segments (on `&&`/`||`/`;`/`|`/newline + surfaces `$(...)`/backtick substitutions as their own segments) and blocks if ANY non-exempt segment is destructive+memory — so an exempt verb in front can't launder a chained delete; exemption is PER-SEGMENT, never whole-command. Added `find -delete`/`truncate`/`>`-redirect to the destructive set, and the Kiro matcher covers `execute_bash|executeBash|shell`. 17 bypass vectors added as blocked-fixtures (the test gap that let it ship green). The lesson: a guardrail's exemption must survive shell composition — a whole-command exempt is a bypass; per-segment is the only safe granularity. **This is the second user-data-loss-class bug the two-pass skill-review caught in this branch family (after the D-191/B1 husk regex) — the discipline earning its keep on exactly the bugs self-review's mental model hides.** **Parked follow-ups (Minor, not data-loss — tracked here, not blocking):** (M1) the bin's fail-open is SILENT — a persistently-broken guard stops guarding with no signal; add a best-effort NDJSON guard-log line on the catch paths (Door-4 observability) so a disabled guard is diagnosable. (I3-live) the Kiro `preToolUse` matcher alternation (`execute_bash|executeBash|shell`) + the firing+block are unverified on a real `kiro-cli` — the cut-gate-kiro **KG-guard** check covers it. (M3) DONE this session — this repo's local `.claude/hooks/block-memory-deletes.mjs` was rewritten to DELEGATE to the shipping `guard-memory.mjs` (was a drifted hand-written copy), so the dogfood guard is now byte-identical to what ships. _Relates D-192 (the incident this hardens structurally), D-183 (the argv/env input model that DOESN'T apply to preToolUse — the correction), the full-research-base-check rule (the user's prompt to use the survey clones; reading them corrected the guess), the cross-agent shared-core/thin-shim pattern (one guard bin, two thin wirings)._
- **🚨 INCIDENT + 🧠 LESSON (2026-06-22) — D-192: the assistant ran `rm -f` after a `cd` that SILENTLY FAILED, deleting the dev repo's `context/sessions/` + `context/transcripts/` (gitignored → not git-recoverable); recovered from the user's off-machine Google Drive sync. Two durable safeguards adopted.** While trying to reset the gate project's runtime state, the Bash tool's `cd /c/tmp/kiro-gate` failed (case/path: the real dir is `/c/Temp/kiro-gate`) and — because the shell's cwd PERSISTS across calls — the subsequent `rm -f context/sessions/* context/transcripts/*` ran in the **dev repo's** `context/` instead. The durable tiers were unharmed (`MEMORY.md`, `DECISIONS.md`, all 575 fact files, queues — those survived), but the **raw rolling-window layer** (daily session logs + verbatim transcripts) was deleted. These were **gitignored on this PUBLIC repo by design (D-108, name-privacy)** → `git restore` could not bring them back. **Recovery:** the user had a **Google Drive sync of the repo** and restored from it — the off-machine backup was the real safety net (the durable lesson: redundant off-machine backup beats any in-repo scheme). **Root cause = a destructive command after an UNVERIFIED `cd`** — exactly the class the working rules already warn about; the harness even blocked the equivalent PowerShell glob-delete first, and the agent worked around it into Bash without re-verifying the working directory. **Two safeguards adopted:** (1) **binding agent rule** — `pwd`-verify (and confirm the path exists) BEFORE any destructive command (`rm`/`Remove-Item`/`del`/reset/`git clean`); never rely on a persisted cwd for a delete; treat a blocked destructive op as a STOP signal, not a reroute. (2) **a structural delete-guardrail** — a Claude Code `PreToolUse` hook that blocks `rm`/`Remove-Item`/`del` targeting `context/` (memory paths) before execution, so the mistake can't run even if the rule is forgotten. **Decision on git-tracking memory (D-108 re-confirmed, NOT changed):** the user's first instinct was "no more gitignore — commit sessions/transcripts so they can't be lost," but committing raw transcripts on THIS public repo would (a) publicly expose raw dev-chat + the maintainer name and (b) FAIL `validate-maintainer-name-confined`. Since the Google Drive sync already provides the resilience, the D-108 gitignore stays as-is here; the SHIPPED kit template already commits users' sessions/transcripts by default (private repos → git-recoverable for users). The git-tracking-with-name-redaction path is parked, not adopted. _Relates D-108 (the public-repo gitignore deviation, re-confirmed), the "destructive ops need a safer alternative / confirm first" working rule (the rule this incident violated + hardens), the off-machine-backup lesson (Google Drive sync = the real recovery)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-22) — D-191: `cmk uninstall --ide kiro` left empty HUSK files (empty `AGENTS.md`, `{}` `mcp.json`, frontmatter-only `steering/cmk.md`) — found by the user dogfooding the command; fixed with a conservative `removeIfHusk`.** While cleaning a stray Kiro install off the dev repo, the user asked *"are you sure uninstall actually works?"* — and it didn't, fully: `uninstallKiro` removed our *content* (managed blocks, MCP key, hooks, skills, CLI agent) and correctly preserved `context/` + user content, but left the now-empty SHELLS of files the kit created (`AGENTS.md` empty, `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` = `{}`, `.kiro/steering/cmk.md` = dead `---\ninclusion: always\n---` frontmatter). Substantively safe (nothing dangerous lingered, nothing wrong deleted) but messy + could read as "uninstall failed." **The fix:** `removeIfHusk(path)` deletes a kit-created file IFF uninstall left it with no real content — empty, `{}`, or only-YAML-frontmatter — and is called for AGENTS.md + steering + mcp.json after their block/key removal. **Conservative by construction:** a file with ANY user content (prose outside our markers, a sibling MCP server, user frontmatter+body) is never a husk → never deleted. **The two-pass review caught a BLOCKING data-loss bug in the first cut of this fix (B1):** the only-frontmatter check was a naive regex `/^---\r?\n[\s\S]*?\r?\n---\s*$/` whose non-greedy `*?` BACKTRACKS to a *later* `---` (a user's horizontal rule) to satisfy `$` — so a steering/AGENTS.md file with USER NOTES bordered by `---` matched as "only frontmatter" and got DELETED (reproduced live: user adds notes to the steering doc ending in `---` → uninstall nukes them). Fixed to a ReDoS-safe **line-scan** (`isOnlyFrontmatter`: opener `---`, the FIRST `---` after it is the close, only blank lines may follow) — proven to KEEP both trap shapes the old regex deleted while still removing genuine husks. Plus **B2 defense-in-depth:** each `removeIfHusk` is now GATED on "the kit's removal step actually changed THIS file," so a pristine never-kit-managed file is never even a deletion candidate. **I1:** added the regression tests (user steering/AGENTS.md content bordered by `---` must survive) — the over-mutation guard the first cut lacked. Test-first (RED: husks remained; GREEN after) + **live-verified end-to-end**: a real install→uninstall leaves 0 `.kiro/` files / no `AGENTS.md` / no `~/.aws` agent / `context/` intact, AND a user-edited steering file with trailing-`---` notes SURVIVES with content intact. **The skill-review earned its keep again — self-review shipped a user-data-loss bug; the adversarial pass caught it before merge.** _Relates D-189 (the uninstall verb this completes — the husk gap was latent in it), D-188 (the AGENTS.md/overlay surfaces being uninstalled), the live-test/dogfood discipline (the user running the real command is what surfaced it — unit tests asserted content-removal, not file-cleanup)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-22) — D-190: the Windows console-popup (Task 81) fix was Claude-Code-only — the Kiro `cmk hook agentSpawn` path flashed a `node` console window; fixed by self-resolving the lazy-compress bin path inside `injectContext`.** 5th live-found cross-agent cut-blocker. A `"node" "...\cmk-compress-lazy.mjs"` window popped during the gate's Kiro-hook exercise. **Root cause (the same Claude-Code-only-mechanism class as D-185/186/187/188):** the Task-81 no-popup spawn (`process.execPath` node-direct + `windowsHide`, NOT the `shell:true` `.cmd` shim) only kicks in when `injectContext` RECEIVES a real `compressLazyPath`. The Claude Code bin (`cmk-inject-context.mjs`) resolved + passed it; the Kiro `cmk hook agentSpawn` path (`subcommands.mjs runHook` → `injectContext({cwd,userDir})`) passed NOTHING → `lazyCompressSpawnDescriptor` fell to the `shell:true` fallback, which `windowsHide` can't fully suppress (it hides the `cmd.exe`, not the `node` grandchild the `.cmd` shim launches) → the visible console. **Confirmed the Kiro agentSpawn path reaches `spawnLazyCompress`** (agentSpawn→inject→injectContext→spawnLazyCompress), so a real Kiro user hits it, not just a manual run. **The fix (defense-in-depth, fixes EVERY caller):** moved path resolution INTO `injectContext` — a new `resolveCompressLazyPath()` (`$CMK_COMPRESS_LAZY_PATH` override → `import.meta.url`→`../bin/cmk-compress-lazy.mjs`) is the DEFAULT for the `compressLazyPath` param, so the Claude bin, the Kiro hook, and any future agent all get the node-direct no-popup spawn without each remembering to pass it. Test-first (resolver finds the real bin; the resolved default → a node-direct/no-shell descriptor; `$CMK_COMPRESS_LAZY_PATH` override honored). Descriptor-level VERIFIED node-direct (`shell: undefined`, `windowsHide: true`); **on-screen no-popup CONFIRMED by the user** ("No popup — clean") after the fix, vs. the visible `node` window before. _Relates D-185/186/187/188 (the cross-agent "Claude-Code-only mechanism not carried over" theme — this is the 5th), Task 81 (the original Claude-side popup fix this extends), the live-test discipline (only a real hook-trigger surfaced the visible window; unit tests asserted the descriptor, not the cross-agent caller gap)._
- **🔬 RESEARCH + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-21) — D-188: the Kiro install must be a clean per-agent OVERLAY (write Kiro's real files incl. AGENTS.md, never create or clobber Claude-Code files), so a project can carry BOTH agents — settled by 5 primary/near-primary sources after the cut-gate found `.claude/skills/` leaking + a broken `AGENTS.md` reference.** The cut-gate-kiro live-test found `cmk install --ide kiro` left a dead `.claude/skills/` (Claude-Code-only) AND its CLI agent-config referenced `prompt: file://AGENTS.md` while **nothing ever wrote AGENTS.md** (broken ref ships). The user then raised the real scenario the "just skip Claude files" framing missed: **a project used by BOTH agents** (two people, or one person switching tools on the same repo/machine). **Researched + VERIFIED across 5 sources (primary-source rule):** (1) **kiro.dev/docs/steering (PRIMARY)** — Kiro auto-loads `AGENTS.md` from the **project root** (or `~/.kiro/steering/`), "always included, no inclusion modes"; it does NOT read `.claude/`. (2) **AWS agent-toolkit rules-files doc (PRIMARY)** — the per-agent rules-file home table: **Claude Code → `CLAUDE.md`**, **Kiro → `.kiro/steering/*.md`**, Codex → `AGENTS.md` (each agent reads its OWN file). (3) **Claude→Kiro migration guide** — "Kiro does NOT read `.claude/` folders — no backward compatibility"; `.claude/skills/`→`.kiro/skills/`, `CLAUDE.md`→steering, `AGENTS.md` = the cross-tool bridge. (4) **AI-DLC article** — `AGENTS.md` is the agents.md.io / Agentic-AI-Foundation standard read on session-init. (5) **AWS's own `aws/graph-explorer` repo (a real Kiro project)** — has `AGENTS.md` + `.kiro/`, **NO `.claude/`**, and its `CLAUDE.md` is literally `@AGENTS.md` (a 1-line import pointer). **The user was right on both counts:** Kiro doesn't need `.claude/` or `CLAUDE.md`; `CLAUDE.md` is Claude Code's, `AGENTS.md` is Kiro's (+ the cross-tool standard). **THE SETTLED DESIGN (per-agent overlay, additive + idempotent + over-mutation-safe):** (a) `--ide kiro` does NOT create the Claude-Code-only `.claude/skills/` or `CLAUDE.md` (they're dead weight on a Kiro-only project — the gate find); (b) but it NEVER clobbers existing `.claude/`/`CLAUDE.md` (if Claude Code was installed first, those are another agent's LIVE config — must survive); (c) `--ide kiro` WRITES a managed `AGENTS.md` block at project root (Kiro's real always-loaded instruction file — fixes the broken `prompt:file://AGENTS.md` ref AND gives Kiro its instruction surface); (d) the shared brain `context/` is written once + REUSED by both agents, never re-scaffolded/duplicated; (e) `cmk install` (Claude) likewise must not clobber existing `.kiro/`/`~/.aws`. **The four switch workflows all become one idempotent command:** CC→+Kiro = `cmk install --ide kiro` (leaves `.claude/` alone); Kiro→+CC = `cmk install` (leaves `.kiro/` alone); each direction's cleanup = `cmk uninstall [--ide kiro]` (D-189). **`--with-semantic` is agent-NEUTRAL** (it writes `context/settings.json` `default_mode:hybrid` — shared-brain config), so `cmk install --with-semantic --ide kiro` enables it identically, and a later second-agent install REUSES the existing hybrid setting (must not downgrade it — composition to verify). _Relates D-182/183/184 (the Kiro surfaces this completes), D-185/186/187 (the gate's other live-found cut-blockers — same "Claude-Code-shaped assumption in the cross-agent path" theme), D-189 (the symmetric uninstall verb), the primary-source rule (5-source verification, incl. AWS's own repo), the live-test discipline (the leak + broken-ref only showed on a real install)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-21) — D-189: `cmk uninstall` gains a symmetric per-agent `--ide` flag — `cmk uninstall --ide kiro` removes ONLY the Kiro managed surface, mirroring how `--ide` scopes install; both stay CONSERVATIVE (never touch the shared `context/` brain).** The user asked "uninstall usually does everything — sure we want `--ide`?" — checked the code: today's `cmk uninstall` is ALREADY narrow + conservative (it strips only the `CLAUDE.md` managed block + Claude hooks; it deliberately does NOT delete `context/`, the user tier, or `.gitignore` — "users delete `context/` themselves"). So a per-agent uninstall is the CONSISTENT extension, not a new destructive mode: `cmk uninstall` → Claude-Code managed surface; `cmk uninstall --ide kiro` → Kiro managed surface (`.kiro/` blocks via `uninstallKiro` — already built but unwired to a CLI verb — + the guarded `~/.aws` agent); **neither touches `context/`** (the shared brain is sacred to both, the same conservative principle). Needed for the switch-and-clean-up workflows (D-188 cases C/D): without it, going Kiro→Claude-only leaves orphaned `.kiro/` + a stray `~/.aws` agent with no clean removal path. _Relates D-188 (the dual-agent overlay this completes the uninstall half of), the existing conservative-uninstall contract (this preserves it), uninstallKiro (the orchestrator this finally wires to a verb)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-187: the Kiro CLI default-agent guard was BOM-fragile — a Windows-editor `settings.json` (UTF-8 BOM) made the guard miss an existing `chat.defaultAgent` and CLOBBER the user's default; found by the cut-gate-kiro live-test, fixed kit-wide.** Third live-found cut-blocker of the gate (after D-185/D-186). The KG7 guarded-default probe seeded `settings.json` via PowerShell `Set-Content -Encoding utf8` — which writes a **UTF-8 BOM** (`EF BB BF`). `readDefaultAgentSetting` did a bare `JSON.parse(readFileSync(...))`; the leading BOM makes `JSON.parse` throw → the `catch` returned `null` → the guard concluded "no default agent set" → it wrote `q_cli_default.json`, **taking over the user's default** instead of the guarded `cmk.json`+skipped-existing path. **Unit-green-but-broken-live** (the live-test class): the existing guard unit test seeded BOM-free JSON, so it passed while the real Windows path failed — a BOM on a Windows config file is common, so this is a realistic clobber of a real user's default (the D-184 class again). **Audit found the kit had NO BOM handling anywhere** — `mutate-agent-config.mjs` (which reads the user's `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` + Claude `settings.json`) had the same bare `JSON.parse`, so a BOM'd config there would falsely read as "corrupt" and trigger the refuse-to-clobber error. **The fix (kit-wide, the user's call — "fix it so it is inline with the rest of our code"):** a new shared `read-json.mjs` — `stripBom()` + `parseJsonFile(path, {fallback})` (BOM-tolerant, never-throws). Routed **every USER-AUTHORED config reader** through it (7 sites — the skill-review I-1 caught that the first pass fixed only 2 and the "kit-wide" claim outran the diff, the lazy-framing class; the sweep was then completed): **swallow-to-fallback readers** use `parseJsonFile` — `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` (`isOurAgent`, `readDefaultAgentSetting`), `config-core.mjs` (`readSettings` — `cmk config get`), `semantic-backend.mjs` (`resolveDefaultSearchMode` — a BOM was silently downgrading hybrid→keyword); **distinguish-missing-vs-corrupt readers** use `stripBom` before their existing parse (preserving the refuse-to-clobber / specific-error contract) — `mutate-agent-config.mjs`, `settings-hooks.mjs` ×2 (`writeKitHooks` + `writeKitMcpServer` — the highest-impact: a BOM there made `cmk install` REFUSE to wire hooks / register MCP on a valid file), `doctor.mjs` HC-1 (BOM → false HC-1 parse-error FAIL). Kit-authored / tool-authored file reads (package.json, kit scratchpads, transcripts) are correctly out of scope — they never carry a BOM. Test-first: `cli-read-json.test.js` (8) + a kiro-cli-agent guard test + a `writeKitHooks` BOM regression (hooks wire on a BOM'd-but-valid settings, not a false error). Verified LIVE: KG7 with a BOM'd `settings.json` → "you already have a Kiro CLI default agent" + `cmk.json` (no clobber). Full suite 2151/0. **Two-pass review:** self-review built the shared module; the `code-review-excellence` skill-review (I-1) caught the incomplete sweep + the "kit-wide"-claim-vs-2-sites gap (would have shipped a false decision-log claim + 5 still-fragile readers incl. the install-blocking `settings-hooks` ones) + an M-1 citation drift — all addressed. _Relates D-184 (the clobber class), D-185/D-186 (the gate's other live-found cut-blockers — all unit-green-but-broken-live), the live-test discipline (the BOM only shows on real Windows input), the shared-module discipline (one BOM-tolerant reader, not N inline strips)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-186: the D-185 doctor fix re-introduced the same bug one level down — HC-1 checked only the IDE-hook surface, so a kiro-cli-only install false-FAILed — caught by the skill-review (B1) before merge.** D-185 made HC-1 check `.kiro/hooks/` instead of `.claude/settings.json` — but Kiro wires capture/inject through TWO independent surfaces: the **IDE hooks** (`.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook`, the GUI user) AND the **CLI agent-config** (`~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/{q_cli_default,cmk}.json` with `agentSpawn`/`stop` hooks, the kiro-cli user). D-185 checked only the IDE half → a **kiro-cli-only user** (memory fires via `~/.aws`, no IDE hooks) got a wrong HC-1 FAIL + a heavy `cmk install --ide kiro` hint for a working install. Worse on a clone: `~/.aws` is machine-local and doesn't travel, so the surfaces can legitimately diverge. **This is literally the same separately-correct-jointly-broken class as the original D-185 bug, recursed** — the first fix swapped one hardcoded surface for another instead of checking the CAPABILITY across all surfaces. **The fix:** HC-1 is a capability check — `hc1KiroHooks` PASSes if the IDE hooks OR a cmk-owned CLI agent is present (new exported `hasOurCliAgent({awsDir})` in `kiro-cli-agent.mjs`, keyed on the `managedBy` marker; `awsDir` injectable for tests), FAILs only when NEITHER, and the FAIL names both surfaces. - **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-185: `cmk doctor` was Claude-Code-only; HC-1 false-FAILed on every `--ide kiro` install — found by the v0.4.0 Kiro live-test gate, fixed as a cut-blocker.** Running `cmk doctor` on a real `cmk install --ide kiro` project reported `[FAIL] HC-1: .claude/settings.json missing — hooks not wired → cmk repair --hooks`. **The bug:** HC-1 hard-checked `.claude/settings.json` (Claude Code's hook file) unconditionally — but a Kiro install wires `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook`, and there IS no `.claude/settings.json`. So HC-1 false-FAILed on EVERY Kiro install with a repair hint (`cmk repair --hooks`) for the wrong agent — a scary red FAIL on the headline feature of the release. **Same class as D-184** (the `~/.aws` write bug): the Kiro *installer* was unit-tested in isolation and correct, but the *diagnostic* layer was written before cross-agent install existed and nobody taught it which agent a project was installed for — separately-correct, jointly-broken; only `cmk doctor` on a REAL Kiro install surfaced it (unit tests structurally couldn't — they only ever fed `.claude/settings.json` shapes). **The fix:** `detectInstallKind(projectRoot)` — `.claude/settings.json` present → Claude Code; else `.kiro/` present → Kiro; neither → Claude Code (historical default, so a not-yet-installed project still reports the Claude-shaped hint). HC-1 routes to a Kiro variant (`hc1KiroHooks`) that verifies `cmk-capture.kiro.hook` + `cmk-inject.kiro.hook` and, on a miss, points at `cmk install --ide kiro` (NOT `cmk repair --hooks`). **Scope contained:** audited the other `.claude/`-touching checks — HC-6 (native Anthropic Auto Memory) checks `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/`, an Anthropic-global feature independent of which agent the kit installed for, so it does NOT misfire on Kiro (verified PASS on the live gate project). HC-1 was the only false-fail. Test-first (3 new tests: Kiro PASS, missing-Kiro-hook FAIL with the right hint, Claude-Code-unaffected), RED→GREEN, verified live on the real `C:\Temp\kiro-gate` install (`[PASS] HC-1: Kiro IDE hooks wired`). Folded into v0.4.0 (the cut-blocker the gate exists to catch). _Relates D-184 (same separately-correct-jointly-broken class), D-182/D-183 (the Kiro surfaces doctor must now understand), the live-test discipline (this is exactly what live-testing the headline feature surfaces that unit tests can't), VD1/HC-9 (the other doctor cross-agent-adjacent check)._
- **🚧 BUILD (2026-06-21) — D-184: Kiro rework PR-2 (the CLI agent-config `hooks{}` surface + the guarded default-agent) BUILT — the 5th install surface for `kiro-cli` terminal users; the IDE hook surface (D-183) covers the GUI.** PR-2 of the D-182 rework, the follow-up D-183 flagged. **What it ships:** `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` — `installKiroCliAgent({awsDir})` writes `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/q_cli_default.json` in the **authoritative Amazon-Q Rust contract** (D-182): `hooks{agentSpawn→inject(timeout_ms:10000), stop→capture(timeout_ms:30000)}` keyed by trigger → array of `{command, timeout_ms}` (NOT the stale `agent-v1.json` `{command}`-only shape), plus `mcpServers` + a `prompt` pointing at `AGENTS.md`. The hook command is platform-correct via the shared `kiro-hook-command.mjs` (`cmd.exe /c cmk hook <event>` on Windows — the WSL-no-node finding, extracted from `kiro-ide-hooks` so BOTH surfaces share one source). **Guarded default-agent (the D-182 non-clobber rule):** a fresh install names the file `q_cli_default.json` (Kiro's auto-default convention) and reports `defaultAgent:'set'`; if the user already has a default (`chat.defaultAgent` in settings.json, OR a `q_cli_default.json` they authored), it installs a NAMED `cmk.json` instead and reports `defaultAgent:'skipped-existing'` — their default is byte-untouched. `installKiro` now wires this as the **5th surface** (`cli-agent`) and surfaces `cliDefaultAgent` so the CLI install notice can tell the user to set the default themselves when skipped. **Both hook surfaces reuse the SAME `cmk hook <event>` dispatcher** → the same `captureTurn()`/`injectContext()` core (the shared-core architecture, P-7QBE6A6M); the CLI agent-config is only another input adapter. **CRITICAL bug caught by the live-test discipline (not unit tests):** the install routing passed `options.userTier` (undefined in the real CLI) so `installKiroCliAgent` fell back to `homedir()` and wrote `q_cli_default.json` into the user's **real** `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/` during a live-check. Caught it, verified it was ours, removed it + the empty dirs, and fixed with a `MEMORY_KIT_AWS_DIR` env override + an explicit `awsDir` param — tests + live-checks ALWAYS sandbox the `~/.aws` write now (P-3Y6MCN2B). Two-pass review: self-review made the `hook` verb exit-0 explicit (`process.exitCode = 0`, I1); skill-review pending in the PR. **Honest edge (live-test rule):** the CLI agent-config + default-agent resolution + `stop`/`agentSpawn` firing in a real `kiro-cli` session is flagged for the batched manual live-test (50.M) after all v0.4.0 code lands — not claimed from unit tests. _Relates D-183 (PR-1, the IDE surface this complements — same dispatcher, forked only at the hook leg), D-182 (the settled spec: Rust contract + default-agent + the `~/.aws` path), the cross-platform rule (the shared `kiro-hook-command`), the live-test discipline (firing flagged; the `~/.aws` bug it caught), P-7QBE6A6M (shared core), P-3Y6MCN2B (the `~/.aws` sandbox rule)._
- **🚧 BUILD + 🔬 LIVE-VERIFY (2026-06-21) — D-183: Kiro rework PR-1 (shared 3 surfaces + IDE hooks) BUILT + live-verified; the IDE `.kiro.hook` surface is REINSTATED as a first-class deterministic-capture target (D-182's "IDE disqualified" was wrong).** PR-1 of the D-182 rework. **The key correction to D-182:** its "IDE `.kiro.hook` is disqualified for capture (askAgent-only)" conflated OBSERVED USAGE with CAPABILITY — the user's own Kiro-IDE-GUI-created hook is `{when:{type:agentStop}, then:{type:runCommand, command, timeout:60}}`, i.e. the IDE GUI itself emits `runCommand` on `agentStop` = **automatic deterministic capture, NO default-agent needed.** So the IDE surface is the PRIMARY target for IDE users (simpler than the CLI default-agent path); the survey repos used `askAgent` by *choice* (LLM-task-tracking), not because `runCommand` was unavailable. **What only LIVE-TESTING on the user's real Kiro could find (none of it in any doc):** (a) the `.kiro.hook` on-disk format (`{version,enabled,name,description,when:{type},then:{type:runCommand|askAgent,command|prompt,timeout}}` — docs deliberately omit it; the user's GUI hook was the only primary source); (b) **Kiro on Windows runs hook `runCommand` through WSL, and WSL has NO node** → a bare `cmk hook stop` fails (`node: not found`); the fix is **`cmd.exe /c cmk hook <event>`** (LIVE-PROVEN: a `.kiro.hook` running `cmd.exe /c cmk --version` output `0.3.5` in the Kiro chat) — emitted per-platform via the binding cross-platform rule; (c) **Kiro's hook INPUT model is argv(event) + env(`USER_PROMPT`) + cwd(project) + the transcript FILE, NOT a stdin JSON payload** like Claude Code (the probe hung on a stdin read; the AWS "Mastering Agent Hooks" article then CONFIRMED `$USER_PROMPT` + the rule that a non-zero hook exit BLOCKS the tool — hence the always-exit-0 invariant). **PR-1 ships:** `install-kiro.mjs` (the dedicated orchestrator — D-182's "Kiro needs its own installer branch") wiring 4 surfaces — MCP (`.kiro/settings/mcp.json`) + steering (`.kiro/steering/cmk.md`, `inclusion:always`) + skills (`memory-search`/`memory-write`→`.kiro/skills/`, ports 1:1) + IDE hooks (`.kiro/hooks/cmk-{capture,inject}.kiro.hook`, platform-correct command); `kiro-hook-dispatch.mjs` (router) + `kiro-hook-bin.mjs` (adapter) + the `cmk hook <event>` verb (always exit 0); `readKiroTurn` (reads the real transcript via `CONTINUE_GLOBAL_DIR` env + base64url workspace key); `managed-block.mjs` (shared marker-block + json helpers, self-review dedup). **The kit is the FIRST project to do deterministic `runCommand` memory capture on Kiro** (40+ surveyed real hooks are all `askAgent`) — which is precisely why every layer was live-verified, not copied. Two-pass review: self-review deduped `managed-block`; skill-review made exit-0 explicit (I1) + the recency tie-break deterministic (M2); the stress prerun caught a malformed `@doors` header. **Honest edge (live-test rule):** `cmk install --ide kiro` lands all 4 surfaces live-verified, and the hook *runs* (probe-proven), but the hook *firing-and-capturing-a-real-turn* end-to-end is flagged for a final manual Kiro session — not claimed from unit tests. **PR-2 (separate):** the CLI agent-config `hooks{}` surface + the guarded default-agent (for `kiro-cli` terminal users) — genuinely different files + activation from the IDE surface (the user's "cli hooks folder and ide hooks folder are not the same, right?" — correct: IDE = `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook` files; CLI = `hooks{}` inside `.kiro/agents/<name>.json`). _Relates D-182 (the spec this builds; its IDE-disqualified call corrected), D-181/D-180 (the superseded design), the cross-platform rule (the WSL `cmd.exe` finding), D-85/D-164 (deterministic auto-capture), the live-test discipline (firing flagged), the all-4-surfaces + both-surfaces decisions (P-YKG4GF25/P-F4WFAXAQ), the verified facts (P-WJRUQVSW format, P-PM2CD6CB Windows cmd, P-CJYGTQYR input model, P-XaPRJFWE AWS confirmation)._
- **🔬 RESEARCH + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-21) — D-182: the Kiro install path is SETTLED by a 14-real-project survey + the AUTHORITATIVE Amazon-Q Rust contract — and it REVISES the D-180/D-181 Kiro design on every axis. The shipped Kiro profile (D-181) is wrong against the live CLI and must be reworked before v0.4.0.** The user pushed hard + correctly: *"check more than 15 projects"* → *"if needed clone them"* → *"check actual files"* → *"the projects we checked have kiro install too?"* → *"what about steerings?"* → *"in kiro you have hooks, steerings, skills and mcp"*. Each push fixed a real error in my model. **The five corrections (all from REAL files / the Rust source, not docs):** **(1) Kiro CLI IS Amazon Q Developer CLI** — so the authoritative hook contract is the `aws/amazon-q-developer-cli` Rust source, and **the published `schemas/agent-v1.json` is a STALE SUBSET** (lists 2 triggers + `{command}`-only; the real contract has 5 triggers `agentSpawn`/`userPromptSubmit`/`preToolUse`/`postToolUse`/`stop` + `Hook{command, timeout_ms(u64 default 30000), max_output_size(10240), cache_ttl_seconds(0), matcher}`, camelCase keys). My D-180 conclusion targeted the wrong schema. **(2) The dominant real install = CLI agent-config with a `hooks{}` block** (9/14 repos; 3/4 memory repos — Auriti/kiro-memory, oh-my-kiro, vibekit), NOT the IDE `.kiro.hook` files D-180's correction had swung toward. **(3) IDE `.kiro.hook` is DISQUALIFIED for capture** — across ALL surveyed repos, ZERO use `then:runCommand` for lifecycle capture; every automatic IDE hook is `then:askAgent` (hands the LLM a prompt + hopes it calls the tool = non-deterministic) AND IDE-only (doesn't fire for `kiro-cli`). That's the exact non-determinism the kit exists to kill — so IDE hooks are OPTIONAL user-triggered convenience only, never the capture spine. **(4) Automatic activation needs the default agent** — 5/14 repos reach "fires with no `--agent` flag" by either setting `chat.defaultAgent` (2: naas, coder/registry) OR naming the agent `default`/`q_cli_default` at the user tier (3: vibekit, oh-my-kiro, Auriti). Hooks fire automatically (Rust `conversation.rs:581`) ONLY for the resolved-active agent — there is NO global hook path. So the kit MUST set the default (guarded — don't clobber a user's existing default; merge or surface a `cmk doctor` notice). The D-181 profile NEVER did this → its hooks would never auto-fire (the bug the user predicted). **(5) Kiro has FOUR surfaces, not three** (the user's correction): hooks + **steering** + **skills** + MCP. The kit's adapter omitted SKILLS entirely. Verified from real files: Kiro skills = Claude-Code-style `<name>/SKILL.md` (`.kiro/skills/` project + `~/.kiro/skills/` user — the user's own install has python-pro/systematic-debugging/…), so the kit's `memory-search`/`memory-write` skills PORT DIRECTLY. Custom **steering** with `inclusion: always` auto-loads in base mode but is DROPPED under a custom agent unless re-added via the agent's `resources:["file://.kiro/steering/<f>.md"]` (proven: 3fn/DesignerPunk's 8 agent JSONs all re-list each steering file). **THE SETTLED SPEC (D-182):** write a CLI agent-config (`q_cli_default.json` or `cmk.json`+guarded activation) to `.amazonq/cli-agents/` + `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/` with `hooks{agentSpawn→'cmk hook agentSpawn'(inject, cached whole-conversation = SessionStart analog), stop→'cmk hook stop'(capture)}` (one dispatcher, usalu/semio pattern) + `mcpServers.cmk` + `resources[AGENTS.md, steering]` + `prompt:file://AGENTS.md`; PLUS the other 3 surfaces (steering `.kiro/steering/cmk.md`; skills `memory-search`/`memory-write`→`.kiro/skills/`; MCP `mcp.json`). **The user chose ALL FOUR surfaces incl. hooks** (deterministic capture, not model-compliance) + **rework Kiro PROPERLY before v0.4.0** (not ship-broken-fix-later). **8-point live-test checklist** before claiming automatic (default resolves w/o `--agent`; inject+capture FIRE not just register; non-clobber guard; MCP reachable; timeout composition). _Relates D-181 (the profile this reworks — wrong on schema/path/default-agent/skills), D-180 (the seam — its Kiro-hook conclusion superseded), D-85/D-164 (the automatic-capture thesis hooks serve), §8.5 (the `timeout_ms` composition), the all-4-surfaces + rework-now decisions (P-YKG4GF25/P-55ZLLX6T), the install-path fact (P-P9FL3NYB). Settled by a 14-project survey — do NOT re-open without new real-project evidence._

  **⚠️ CORRECTION (2026-06-21, same day) — D-182's "IDE `.kiro.hook` is DISQUALIFIED for capture (askAgent-only)" was WRONG; the IDE is a FIRST-CLASS capture target.** The user caught it: *"why are you only talking about kiro cli and not kiro ide?"* — I'd let the research collapse to CLI-only. The survey claim conflated **observed usage** with **capability**: it saw repos use `then:askAgent` (Taskmaster 7×, because their hooks are LLM-task-tracking) and concluded `runCommand` was unavailable for lifecycle events. **The user's own Kiro-IDE-UI-generated hook DISPROVES this** — it is `{when:{type:'agentStop'}, then:{type:'runCommand', command, timeout:60}}`: the IDE GUI itself emits `runCommand` on `agentStop`, i.e. **deterministic shell-command capture on turn-end, automatically, with NO default-agent needed.** So the corrected picture: **(a) Kiro IDE is the PRIMARY target** (it's the user's main work surface — the original v0.4 reason, P-DGN6ZNXZ), not a secondary convenience. **(b) BOTH surfaces support deterministic capture** — IDE via `.kiro/hooks/cmk-capture.kiro.hook` (`agentStop`→`runCommand` — automatic, simpler, no default-agent clobber risk) AND CLI via agent-config `hooks{stop}` (needs the guarded default-agent). **(c) 3 of 4 surfaces are SHARED IDE+CLI** (MCP `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` + steering `.kiro/steering/` + skills `.kiro/skills/`) — one install covers both; only the HOOKS leg forks (IDE `.kiro.hook` file vs CLI agent-config). The rest of D-182's spec stands (default-agent for the CLI side, AGENTS.md/steering/skills, Rust contract for CLI hooks); what changes is that the **IDE hook path is co-equal, not dropped** — the kit should install IDE `.kiro.hook` files for IDE users + the CLI agent-config for CLI users, sharing MCP/steering/skills. IDE hook format verified from the real file (P-WJRUQVSW): `{version:'1.0.0', enabled, name, description, when:{type}, then:{type:'runCommand', command, timeout}}`. _Relates P-WG6SMMV7 (the correction), P-WJRUQVSW (the real IDE hook format), P-N39ZJ69D (the earlier "IDE is a better fit" finding the survey wrongly overrode)._

- **🔬 RESEARCH + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-20) — D-180: the Task 50 cross-agent adapter research-revisit (the binding D-157 gate) ran a FULL-corpus survey + cloned-source deep-read + kiro.dev primary verification — output is the seam architecture + a load-bearing Kiro hook-system CORRECTION.** The user pushed twice to widen the lens (*"you should check more products than just this 2"* → *"please clone and check all of them"* → *"these are not the products we researched… which research are you using?"* → *"why not also do a pass on other products?"*) — the right call: my first pass leaned on only Taskmaster + claude-mem, and asserted (rather than verified) that the rest of the corpus didn't help. **Did the broad pass change the answer? NO — but it VERIFIED it instead of assuming it.** Swept all 66 research notes through the multi-agent-install lens: **only claude-mem actually installs the three legs we install (hooks + MCP + instruction-block) into multiple agents, and even it is bespoke-per-agent code, not a clean adapter.** The rest split into instruction-file-only (project-memory/GBrain/OpenClaw), MCP-connector ("multi-agent" = clients hit one running server, not an installer), a per-host-handcraft NEGATIVE example (TencentDB hand-built 2 integrations — exactly what our seam avoids), and single-agent/core-only (mem0/Letta/Zep/memsearch/mempalace/memory-os/OpenHands/AgentCore/…). So most of our corpus shaped the kit's CORE, not the adapter — which is WHY the adapter corpus was genuinely thin (now confirmed, not guessed). **THREE load-bearing findings:** (1) **Don't build a uniform `Installer` base class** — claude-mem proved it breaks the moment agents differ in format (Goose YAML, Codex TOML) or mechanism (Cursor whole-file vs Gemini surgical-merge vs Codex plugin-marketplace). The reusable seam is a shared, TESTED `mutateAgentConfig(path, format, keyPath, entry, {merge|replace})` primitive (touch-only-our-keys, refuse-to-clobber-on-parse-error, idempotent `changed`-boolean) + per-agent metadata as **DATA, not classes** — which maps onto the kit's existing marker-block byte-preservation + over-mutation-guard rules. Do NOT registry-ize the matrix yet (single-digit N; opencode's registry pays off at N≈75). (2) **🔴 Kiro has TWO hook systems and only ONE fits (primary-verified correction).** Target **Kiro CLI agent-hooks** — `agentSpawn` (=SessionStart-inject) + `stop` (=turn-end-capture), defined inside `.kiro/agents/<name>.json` — NOT the IDE "Agent Hooks" surface (file-event-centric, no documented session-start trigger, no documented on-disk format). **The Taskmaster `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook` claim was the WRONG hook system** (the §5.1 convergent-third-party-≠-primary precedent, caught exactly as the rule predicts). Good news: the kit's inject-at-start/capture-at-end model PORTS CLEANLY to the CLI surface. Steering → `.kiro/steering/` (`inclusion: always`); MCP → `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` (`mcpServers`) — both primary-verified. (3) **Highest UNVERIFIED risk: Kiro's transcript format is unknown.** The kit's extract/compress hardcodes Claude-Code touchpoints (`~/.claude/projects/<slug>/<session>.jsonl`, `env -u CLAUDECODE`); kiro.dev docs don't cover Kiro's transcript-on-disk shape → must be parameterized per-agent + discovered LIVE at build (the capture half of the model gates on it). **Build order (the note's §6):** `mutateAgentConfig` primitive FIRST (+ over-mutation test) → per-agent profile data-shape → adapter-parity validator → Kiro profile → AGENTS.md breadth rung → `cmk install --ide` routing → live verification (hook-firing + transcript format flagged for a real Kiro session, NOT claimed verified from docs). Output committed as [research note `2026-06-20-cross-agent-adapter-seam-task50.md`](../research/2026-06-20-cross-agent-adapter-seam-task50.md); facts captured via `cmk remember` (P-AGV23NTY/P-SAX2JDHY/P-RT2G5VAY). **Meta-lesson: the user's "check more than 2 / clone all / which research?" forced the full-corpus verification that turned "the adapter corpus is thin" from an assumption into a verified finding — and the cloned-source read is what surfaced the don't-build-a-base-class lesson a docs-only survey would have missed.** _Relates D-157 (the research-revisit gate this satisfies), D-127 (Kiro-first), ADR-0012 (cross-agent future), design §16.49/§16.50, Task 50 (the build this feeds), the §5.1 primary-source precedent (the Kiro hook-system correction is a textbook instance), the live-test discipline (hook-firing + transcript flagged, not claimed)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-19) — D-175: Task 161's fix is a BOUNDED, TRANSIENT-ONLY RETRY — grounded in a full-field code read (9 systems), placed only on the ceiling-free paths. The plan was RE-ESTABLISHED after winging it (the user: "this is getting out of hand… read the code, all of it, then go back to research, and then restart the task with an established and well thought out plan").** After D-174 inverted the size-bound design to a retry, I (a) read the WHOLE compression subsystem end-to-end (compress-session / compressor / lazy-compress / session-end-tasks / daily-distill / weekly-curate / the bins), and (b) read how the field ACTUALLY retries — not 1 system (the first pass tunneled on OpenHands; the user: "why only OpenHands?" / "only 6?"), but **9 systems' real retry code** → [retry-patterns research note](../research/2026-06-19-llm-call-retry-patterns-cross-system.md). **Unanimous convergence (7 of 7 retrying systems):** bounded attempts (2–4), backoff (exponential majority / linear memclaw), **retry ONLY the transient class (rate-limit / 5xx / timeout / empty-response) keyed on the error TYPE, NEVER the deterministic class (4xx / context-length / policy-violation / ENOENT), reraise after exhaustion.** graphiti's `is_server_or_retry_error` predicate + Letta's `ValueError`(retry)-vs-`RuntimeError`(don't) split are the model. **Decisive negative result:** **claude-remember — the precedent the kit's compress was COPIED from — does NOT retry** (single attempt, raises `RuntimeError`, moves on); claude-mem doesn't either. So the kit inherited the *no-retry* gap from its precedents, exactly as it inherited the unbounded-input gap (D-174). **THE PLAN (Task 161.8–161.11):** a `compressWithRetry(backend, opts, {maxAttempts≤2, baseBackoffMs, isRetryable})` helper — `isRetryable` true for `HaikuTimeoutError` + a transient `HaikuFailedError` (classified via the `exitCode`/`stderr` that 161.6a now captures — this is WHY observability shipped first), false for ENOENT / deterministic exit. **Placement keyed to the verified composition budgets:** the CEILING-FREE paths (`dailyDistill`, `weeklyCurate`, the detached lazy `compressSession`) get the retry; the **SessionEnd-hook `compressSession` gets NONE** — it runs under the 60s ceiling CONCURRENT with `autoPersona` (D-42) where a 50s attempt + 50s retry = 100s blows the ceiling, so it keeps its existing restore-on-failure (D-79) and DELEGATES the retry to the now-retrying lazy path one session later (the field's "two valid placements" — explicit loop vs delegate). **REOPENED items from the set-aside D-173:** input-capping (A) is NOT in the plan (D-174 falsified its premise); it returns only if a future huge-buffer case is ever measured. _Relates D-174 (the inversion that made this a retry problem), D-173 (the set-aside size-bound), D-79 (restore-on-failure — the hook path's delegated-retry mechanism), D-42 (the 60s concurrent ceiling that bars an in-hook retry), 161.6a (the observability fix the transient/deterministic classification depends on), §8.5 (timeout/ceiling composition), the [retry research note](../research/2026-06-19-llm-call-retry-patterns-cross-system.md) + the [19-system note](../research/2026-06-18-session-buffer-compaction-under-latency-growth.md). The user's process correction (read-all-code → re-research → re-plan) is itself the lesson: don't improvise a design mid-conversation — establish it from the code + the field first._
- **🐛 BUG + FIX (2026-06-20) — D-179: the ceiling-free compress callers used the hook-sized 50s timeout → needless `haiku_timeout` → `recent.md` went 4 days stale on the dogfood repo (Task 163, fixed).** Surfaced live: after the Claude Code + cmk update, `cmk doctor` HC-2 showed `recent.md` 4d stale. **The user's instinct was the catch — "if it's not automatic, it's a bug"** — and stopped me from papering over it with a manual `cmk daily-distill`. **Investigated with real data** (not guessed): the daily-distill INPUT is tiny (4.7 KB), yet it timed out at 50s; a measurement of the REAL input showed `claude --print` taking **18–27s when fast but 78s in a slow window** — pure ENVIRONMENTAL slowness (confirms D-174: not size-driven), and the slow window can be SUSTAINED, so the v0.3.4 retry (50s + 50s, both inside the same slow window) didn't help. **Root cause:** `daily-distill`, `weekly-curate`'s curate call, and the lazy `compressSession` all used `timeoutMs: 50_000` — the value sized for the **60s SessionEnd HOOK ceiling** — despite being **CEILING-FREE** (cron / detached-lazy children with NO outer ceiling). The D-92/F-2 composition rule (a ceiling-free caller must NOT inherit a ceiling-sized bound) was applied to `weekly-curate`'s PERSONA call (120s) but MISSED on the other three. The v0.3.4 retry comment itself said "ceiling-free path" while the timeout stayed 50s. **FIX (Task 163):** the three ceiling-free sites → **120s** (matching weekly-curate's persona call); `compressSession` gains a `timeoutMs` param (default 50s = the hook contract; the lazy caller passes 120s) — mirrors the `maxAttempts` param. **Composition VERIFIED:** the lazy child is `detached:true` + unref'd, so the 120s×2≈240s worst case runs in the BACKGROUND after the 30s SessionStart hook returns — no ceiling violation; cron is standalone; the SessionEnd-hook `compressSession` keeps 50s (it HAS the 60s ceiling). **LIVE-PROVEN on the real stale repo:** the patched daily-distill ran the real input in **77.9s** (would have died at 50s, succeeded at 120s) and `recent.md` refreshed. Full suite 2029/2029. **Secondary finding (filed, NOT fixed here):** on a busy cron-less repo the lazy cascade can ALSO starve daily/recent — `now.md` keeps refilling → verdict stays `stale-now` → rarely advances to `stale-daily`; the DESIGNED mitigation is `cmk register-crons` (HC-5 was SKIP on this repo). **Process note (mine):** I initially mis-diagnosed this as cascade-starvation, then as an input-size issue — the real-data measurement (78s on 4.7KB) corrected both to "ceiling-free timeout mis-sized"; the user's "dig deeper" + "it's a bug if not automatic" forced the measurement over the guess. **▶ SECOND LEVER — the BACKOFF was also misconfigured (the user's two follow-ups: "escalating timeout?" then "backoff tuning?").** Checked the escalating-timeout idea against **19 cloned systems** — **NONE escalate the per-attempt timeout; ALL use a fixed timeout + exponential backoff BETWEEN attempts** (graphiti `wait_random_exponential(min=5,max=120)`, Letta cap 10s, mempalace `2**attempt`s — all in SECONDS). So escalation was rejected (no prior art, adds cost for no measured gain). **But the field-check surfaced a real bug:** the kit's `compressWithRetry` backoff default is **600 MILLISECONDS** — the field waits 5–120 SECONDS. D-174's slowness is a transient WINDOW; a 600ms backoff retries INSIDE the same slow window, so attempt 2 hits the same slowness. **FIX (added to Task 163):** a `CEILING_FREE_BACKOFF_MS = 5_000` constant (field low-end) on the ceiling-free retrying paths so a retry lands AFTER the window; `compressSession` gains a `baseBackoffMs` param (default 600ms; lazy caller passes 5s). Both timeout (120s) + backoff (5s) extracted to named constants in `compress-retry.mjs` so the family can't drift back. Safe on every path (hook = maxAttempts:1, backoff never fires; ceiling-free = detached/cron, a 5s wait is free). **Meta-lesson: the user's "don't check just one, check at least 15" forced the broad survey that both KILLED the escalation idea AND found the backoff bug — a single-system check would have missed both.** _Relates D-174/D-175 (the retry this complements — retry handles a blip, the right BUDGET handles a sustained slow call, the right BACKOFF lands the retry after the window), D-92/F-2 (the ceiling-free-timeout composition rule this completes across the family), §8.5 (timeout policy), Task 105/D-75 (the lazy-cascade-starvation secondary finding), HC-5 (cron — the designed mitigation), the 19-system retry research (escalation rejected, backoff-too-short found)._
