(2) **CRLF blindness:** default Windows git (`autocrlf=true`) rewrites committed memory files at clone; the strict-LF frontmatter boundary and `split('
')` readers left `
` on every line — the clone indexed 0 of 18 facts. The kit's PORTABILITY promise (H1, "another computer") was broken on the most common Windows config. Fix: tolerant reads (`/
?
/` + `
?` boundary), writes re-join LF (self-healing); `.gitattributes` prevention parked as follow-up. **Meta:** the implementer's own tooling discipline (heredocs for code edits) caused #7 — heredocs are now banned for code edits in favor of the Edit tool (the lesson fired three times before sticking). _Relates D-125, Task 137 (the gate-vs-automation program), CLAUDE.md tooling traps._
- **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-125: imported bullets broke the next reindex — Task 138 (cut-gate9 F-13, gate-day bug #5).** The F-sweep's seeded real-input import applied cleanly, then `cmk search` reported "index refresh failed: NOT NULL constraint failed: observations.write_source" (graceful stale-index degradation — the message worked). - **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-124: the output cap wrote a CORRUPTED memory — Task 136 (cut-gate9 Session 2).** The user's recall probe surfaced P-BaTM3L42 with body "The `clau" (9 chars): a dense Session-1 turn emitted 3 rich facts (>2000 bytes), `compressor.mjs` defensively slices at `maxOutputBytes`, and `parseRichFacts` accepted the clipped trailing block — the parser had no concept of a truncated fact. The model worked around it live (read the file, inferred from the title) — the ladder degraded gracefully — but a corrupted fact on disk violates the never-lose-context promise's quality half. **Fix:** an EOF-unterminated BEGIN_FACT block (the slice's unique signature — well-formed output always closes) is dropped + counted (`clipped_facts_dropped` in extract.log); the extraction budget raised 2000→8192 (3-4 rich facts ≈ 2.5-4KB legitimate). Losing the clipped fact beats storing a mangled one. **Today's gate total: FOUR bugs** (D-122 dedup self-poisoning, D-123 skill allowlist, the C3 guide probe, D-124 clipped facts) — the manual gate keeps out-finding 1700+ green tests. _Relates Task 103 (rich facts), design §6.4, D-122._

- **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-122: auto-extract dedup SELF-POISONING — organic capture suppressed since Task 87; found by the user's cut-gate8 run, fixed as Task 132 (CUT BLOCKER).** The user pushed back twice ("something definitely broke somewhere", "even our own project's MEMORY.md hardly has any memories") — and was right. Investigation: gate7-vs-gate8 same-script comparison → extract-chain byte-diff vs published 0.2.4 (IDENTICAL — not a v0.3.0 code regression) → controlled A/B: the EXACT failing turn extracted 3 observations with empty now.md, ZERO with now.md's last entry = the current turn. **Root cause:** capture-turn appends the turn to now.md (Task 87) BEFORE spawning the extractor; the extractor read "the last now.md entry" as dedup — "do not re-emit facts already here" + its own input. Haiku obeys → nothing_durable. Stochastic obedience explains why older gates extracted sometimes (scratchpad bullets across gate dirs: 6/2/1/2/1/0 — the fingerprint); explicit mk_remember + persona promotion were immune (different paths). **Fix (Task 132):** the dedup snapshot is taken PRE-append by capture-turn and rides the turn file as `DEDUP_CONTEXT:` (design §6.4 shape); the extractor never reads now.md (missing marker = no dedup section, never a re-read). Plus: the concurrent-run early-exit unlinks its turn file (gate8's orphan-.tmp leak), and validate-references skips context/sessions + transcripts + context.local (the dogfood Stop hook grew now.md MID-STRESS and broke the prerun — conversation capture is data, not corpus). **Meta:** shipped through ~10 releases because no test asserted the COMPOSITION (capture-turn's now.md append × auto-extract's dedup read) — each surface unit-green; composition-verification instance #7 (CLAUDE.md). - **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-118: Task 104.2 + 104.3 shipped (PR #158, merged `1541efa`) — TASK 104 COMPLETE; the recall waterfall has its floor (the L3 raw tier is searchable).** Build: `transcript_chunks` + FTS + `vec_transcripts` (the embedding cache is SHARED — content-addressed, the same text embeds once regardless of scope); the chunker (`## ` turns → ≤1500-char windows, every window keeps its heading); sync rides `reindexBoot`/`reindexFull` via per-file sha1 checkpoints in the shared `files` table (`transcript:` key prefix). **Two composition hazards caught before they shipped:** (1) reindexBoot's orphan-prune would have eaten the `transcript:` checkpoints every boot (they're not observation sources) — the prune now skips the prefix and the transcript sync prunes its own orphans; (2) a flaky test exposed a REAL mtime-resolution race (two appends within the filesystem's mtime granularity made the second invisible — rapid Stop hooks are the production shape) — the mtime fast-path was dropped, sha1 is the authority. **Search surface:** `search()` scope param ('facts' default | 'transcripts'); fact-only filters (tier/minTrust/since) are REJECTED under the transcripts scope (honest, not silent); hits carry synthetic `T:<file>:<line>` ids (chunks are locations, not facts — no [PUL] identity, no trust; the id keys hybrid RRF fusion and is the drill-back handle); `cmk search --scope transcripts` + `mk_search {scope}` parity; the memory-search skill gains Step 4 (LAST RESORT, with the capture-back nudge: "if something found here is durably useful, say so"). **104.3 retention settled in design §19.4.1:** full history, growth bounded at the source (the 104.1 caps), knob deferred with the repo-size trigger. _Relates D-117 (104.1), Task 65 (the semantic machinery generalized), Task 75.1 (the skill), §19, D-70/D-72._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-117: Task 104 sub-structured (2 PRs, the Task-108 precedent) + 104.1 shipped (PR #157) — the kit's transcript now records TOOL ACTIVITY (the L3 raw tier's capture half).** **The ordering insight: capture is time-sensitive, search is not** — every turn that passes uncaptured is unbackfillable, while the index can be built over the accumulated record any time; so 104.1 (enriched capture) ships first, 104.2 (the `--scope transcripts` L3 search) next. **Sub-decisions settled:** (a) detail = +tool calls/results (compact, capped: 300-char result snippets, 4000-char block, honest "…N more truncated" overflow), NOT thinking (bulky, rarely recall-worthy, privacy-heavier); (b) the L3 index = a SEPARATE scope, never mixed into L1 results (the MemPalace last-resort contract); (c) retention = full history (the differentiator vs native's ~30-day machine-local expiry; growth bounded by the per-turn caps; a retention knob deferred, trigger = transcripts dominating repo size). **Build:** new pure [`turn-tools.mjs`](../../packages/cli/src/turn-tools.mjs) (`extractTurnToolActivity` + bounded `readTranscriptTail`, 768KB tail) reads the current turn from the Stop payload's `transcript_path` (Anthropic's live JSONL — extracting the turn at capture time is NOT the JSONL-copy crutch the user rejected 2026-06-06); capture-turn appends a privacy-sanitized `**Tools:**` block under the assistant entry; now.md + the auto-extract turn-file stay TEXT-ONLY (tool noise must not feed the compressor/extractor). **The format is not a documented contract — the user's push ("there are several projects you can examine and the docs") drove a 6-session/4-project empirical survey that caught two variants a single sample missed:** `message.content` can be a plain STRING (not only a block list) and `tool_result.content` comes as STRING or LIST; the parser handles both + degrades to null on anything else (a format shift can degrade the enrichment, never the capture). **Live-tested on the most real input available: this session's own 7.8MB JSONL** — the bin extracted the session's actual tool calls (PR merges, doc edits) into a capped, readable block. _Relates Task 104/65/75, §19 (the L3 floor), D-70/D-72 (the waterfall), the 2026-06-06 user directive._

So: `cmk install --with-semantic` = npm-installs the embedder globally + writes `search.default_mode: hybrid` (only after npm succeeds — no half-state) + pre-warms the model (the one-time download happens at INSTALL, not as a surprise on first search); from then on bare `cmk search` and `mk_search` run hybrid with no flags. `--no-semantic` pins keyword; bare install prints a one-line tip. **Degradation contract:** configured-default-unavailable → graceful keyword fallback + stderr note (a default must never break every search); explicit `--mode=semantic` unavailable → exit 2 + install hint (you asked, you get the truth). **Composition fix found by TDD:** the default-mode resolution initially rode the same dynamic import as the heavy prepare → suspended the KEYWORD path’s synchronous contract (caught by cli-subcommands-dispatch); fixed by statically importing the light resolver (module top-level = node builtins; the embedder stays lazy). - **🏁 DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-109: Task 65 shipped (PR #150) — the Layer-5b semantic backend is REAL and the §9.3.1 deferral is RESOLVED ([ADR-0015](../adr/0015-semantic-backend-sqlite-vec-plus-local-onnx-embedder.md)). Wow #2 (recall with reasoning) = video parity.** Decision: **sqlite-vec (v0.1.9, ~300KB regular dep) inside the kit’s EXISTING SQLite index + `Xenova/bge-base-en-v1.5` via the OPTIONAL `@huggingface/transformers` embedder** (lazy import; ~258MB with onnxruntime → never a hard dep; absent → actionable hint; `CMK_DISABLE_SEMANTIC=1` force-disables). **The ladder decided it (D-105 honored exactly):** spike passed first try (sqlite-vec loads on Windows via better-sqlite3; the named zvec fallback was never needed) → bench rungs: bge-small hybrid 0.765/0.800 → bge-small semantic 0.824/0.900 → bge-base hybrid 0.882/0.900 → **bge-base semantic 0.941/1.000 (R@5/paraphrase) — WINNER** → bge-m3 0.765/0.800: **the 5×-heavier multilingual giant LOST to the English-tuned base on short memory facts; the ladder found its ceiling at rung 2** (the user’s bigger-reliable-beats-small-flaky bias satisfied at minimum weight). Architecture: content-addressed embedding cache (sha256(model+body) — the memweave pattern; only-changed re-embeds), model-derived dims (vec table auto-rebuilds on model change), the sync `semanticBackend` seam PRESERVED (async lives in `prepareSemanticBackend` — Task 120’s contract untouched); CLI + MCP auto-prepare on `--mode=semantic|hybrid`. - **📋 DECISION (2026-06-09) — D-105: the v0.3 recall-lane plan APPROVED (the user: "i approve of the plan, you can start"). Five PRs, strict order: 75.0 → 99 → 52 → 65 → README.** Key calls, each SETTLED: **(1) 75.0 pulled forward** of 65 — instruction-first (D-64), no backend dependency, cheapest recall lever. **(2) Task 99 lands BEFORE 65** and carries TWO baselines: one-shot FTS5 AND **agentic/iterative multi-query keyword (rung 0b)** — the embedder must beat rung 0b, not just one-shot keyword, per Anthropic's "start with agentic search and only add semantic if you need it" (the 2026 agentic-search shift; verify the primary sources at ingest). **(3) Embedder = a LADDER, tests decide:** start bge-small-en-v1.5 (NOT all-MiniLM — degrades past ~128 tokens vs our ≤1500-char chunks), go up a rung per benchmark run (bge-base / nomic / EmbeddingGemma-class → bge-m3); **the user's bias: bigger-and-reliable beats small-and-flaky; install weight is an axis, quality wins ties.** **(4) Task 52 (dogfood) pulled into the lane** before 65 — the kit's own repo is the real bake-off corpus; the public-repo privacy decision (what `context/` content commits) gets settled at task start. **(5) sqlite-vec stays the primary backend candidate (§9.3.1 fit); [alibaba/zvec](https://github.com/alibaba/zvec) = the NAMED fallback** (embedded, Node bindings, Windows — but bindings only ~v0.4.0/May-2026-old; verify in the spike). **(6) memweave = reference implementation** for build details (content-addressed embedding cache, temporal decay with evergreen exemption, min-score gate, Jaccard-MMR dedup) — **code-dive before adopting** (author-written article); its 0.7/0.3 weighted merge vs D-72's RRF k=60 is a bake-off question the harness answers. **(7) README professional upgrade closes the lane**, publishing raw-vs-reranked benchmark numbers. - **🧭 DIRECTION CONFIRMED (2026-06-09) — D-104: the LLM-capture architecture is RIGHT; it's a layered hybrid, NOT "LLM-capture vs store-everything+semantic".** The user asked (concerned LLM-per-turn capture is token/context-heavy): *"are we going the right way with the llm capture? and not just taking everything, putting it in a file and then just use a semantic search?"* **Verdict: right direction.** The kit already does BOTH in layers: **(1) raw transcripts** (`context/transcripts/`) = the lossless "store everything" (proof: the async rule the grader MISSED in cut-gate7 IS in `transcripts/2026-06-09.md`); **(2) LLM auto-extract** = the curation layer that turns raw turns into small high-signal facts; **(3) semantic search over raw** (Layer 5b, v0.3) = the retrieval/safety-net. **Pure "store-everything + semantic" (naive RAG) REJECTED** because: (a) memory is INJECTED at session start into a budget-constrained coding agent — you must inject *small + high-signal*, and raw similarity chunks are noisier per token than a `**Why/How**` fact; (b) curation (deciding what's durable) IS the differentiator vs native auto-memory; (c) semantic isn't free anyway — Anthropic has no embeddings API, so it needs a local embedder (the deferred sqlite-vec). Field-validated: **mem0** (leading agent-memory) does extract-then-store + vector, NOT pure RAG. **KEY STEER for v0.3 (ties to D-103's async variance):** the per-turn grader is ~80% on AMBIGUOUSLY-phrased rules and can't be cheaply perfected — so **DON'T over-engineer the capture grader; invest v0.3 in semantic-recall-over-raw-transcripts as the backstop** (the raw already holds what the grader missed → catch misses at read-time, no extra capture tokens). Capture cost itself is tunable (Haiku already; could batch / only-substantive-turns). _Relates D-103 (async variance), Task 65/75 (v0.3 recall), design §9 (search) + §6 (auto-extract)._

  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-95: Task 113 — `cmk queue review` / `conflicts` verified on REAL queued items (F-9); no command-layer bug.** The cut-gate sweep only ran these on EMPTY queues (D-84 hollow pass). **Investigation finding (same shape as Task 112):** the unit RESOLVERS (`resolveReviewQueue` / `resolveConflictQueue`) were ALREADY fully covered on real items + all actions (review: promote/discard/skip + drain + audit reasons; conflict: keep-old/keep-new/merge-both→`mergeFacts`/skip + over-mutation). The real gap was the **interactive CLI wiring** `runQueueReview` / `runQueueConflicts` — readline over `process.stdin` + `process.cwd()`, so untestable → the sweep could only run them empty. **Fix:** dep-inject + export both (`{projectRoot, prompter, log, logError}`; defaults = readline + cwd + console, prod unchanged) + 4 CLI-path tests driving real promote / discard / keep-old / keep-new end-to-end with effect assertions. **Result: the command layer works — no bug.** **Contract clarified by writing the test** (the value of real-input testing): conflict resolution MARKS an entry resolved (rewrites its `resolution` field; `listConflictQueue` filters `pending`) rather than deleting it — so the correct Door-2 assertion is "a 2nd pass finds nothing pending," not "the id is gone" (my first assertion was wrong; the resolver was right). 3rd D-84 re-audit finding to land (after 110, 112): pattern holds — sound core, untested command/integration layer; the fix is a real-path test, occasionally surfacing a contract nuance. _Relates D-84, Task 116._
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-94: Task 112 — `cmk weekly-curate` 7-day-archive path verified on REAL input (F-4); no bug.** The cut-gate sweep had only ever seen weekly-curate "skipped (cooldown)" / same-day-nothing-to-archive (D-84 hollow pass). **Investigation finding:** the gap was NOT the unit logic (already well-covered by `cli-weekly-curate.test.js` 34.4 — 14-day fixture, archivedDays:7, archive.md written, OLD-deleted/CURRENT-preserved + over-mutation guard) NOR the cooldown (already overridable via `weeklyCurate({cooldownMs})`). The gap was **mock-only verification**: every archive test injects `MockHaikuBackend`, so the REAL `claude --print` archivist call was never exercised on aged input, and the cron-chain smoke only asserted the bin *logged* (hollow on non-aged data). **Fix = a live-Haiku smoke** ([`tests/spawn-smoke-weekly-curate.test.js`](../../tests/spawn-smoke-weekly-curate.test.js)): seed aged `today-*.md` (>7d) → real `HaikuViaAnthropicApi` (cooldownMs:0, skipRecentRebuild to pin the archive call) → assert archive.md non-empty + aged rotated + current preserved. **Result: green on a ~48s real round-trip — the feature WORKS; no code fix needed.** This is the right shape for the whole D-84 re-audit lane: when the unit logic is sound but only mock-verified, the missing piece is a REAL-backend smoke, not more mock tests. _Relates D-84, Task 116._
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ LIVE-VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-100: Task 117 — free-speech intent→action coverage (D-85); the LAST v0.2.3 task. 🎉 v0.2.3 fix-lane COMPLETE (108–117).** **Audit:** every user-expressible memory intent now has a free-speech path — capture/correct/forget were already covered (memory-write skill + `mk_remember`/`mk_forget`, plus automatic auto-extract); the ONE open gap D-85 named — **"trust this / not important"** — is now closed by adding an **"Adjust trust"** action to the `memory-write` skill (description triggers + `allowed-tools: mcp__cmk__mk_trust` / `Bash(cmk trust *)` + body, routing "trust this"→high / "not important / not sure"→low to `mk_trust`).   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-99: Task 116 — coverage hardening + the persona-portability flake ROOT-CAUSED & fixed (116.x).** Two halves: **(a)** added the **★★ real-input rule** to [`cut-gate.md`](../process/cut-gate.md) — a check passes ONLY on real input; cooldown-skip / empty-queue / dry-run-nothing / same-day-nothing-to-archive = `unverified`, re-run for real (the D-84 lesson, now in the process doc, not just the decision log). The automated real-input TESTS were Tasks 112–114; live-verification was D-96/D-97. **(b) 116.x flake — found a real fragility, not just a timing race:** `rollbackImport` restored a backed-up file with `renameSync(bkp, dest)` where `dest` already held the half-applied NEW content — renaming ONTO an existing file intermittently throws EPERM/EBUSY on Windows under heavy parallel FS load, and the **fully-silent catch** then left the un-rolled-back NEW file (= the `expected 'ORIGINAL B' got 'NEW imported'` flake). **Investigation first ruled out** the cross-contamination theory (per-test mkdtemp; reindex takes explicit userDir; vitest default file-isolation; deterministic apply/rollback) → narrowed to the renameSync restore. **Fix:** `restoreBackup()` uses `copyFileSync` (reliable cross-platform overwrite) + a 5× retry for transient locks; backup removed only after a confirmed copy. 14/14 persona-portability green. **Lesson:** a "rare flake" that's silently caught is worth root-causing — this one was a genuine rollback-reliability bug (a real mid-import failure on a user's Windows box could have left a half-applied persona), not just test noise. _Relates D-84, D-93 (the flake's filing), Tasks 109–115 (the lane this hardens)._
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ LIVE-VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-98: Task 115 — transcript temp-file hygiene (cut-gate5 H1).** The cut-gate's portability test committed a `context/transcripts/.extract-<ts>.tmp` via `git add -A` — the auto-extract turn buffer (`capture-turn.mjs:284`) isn't gitignored, so a crash-orphaned partial could travel with `git clone`. **Fix:** added `context/transcripts/.extract-*.tmp` to `template/.gitignore.fragment` (the source `cmk install` builds the managed `.gitignore` block from — install reads the fragment, not hardcoded lines). The buffer is normally consumed + deleted by the detached auto-extract child; the gitignore covers only the crash-orphan case. `cli-install.test.js` now asserts the pattern. **LIVE-verified:** scaffolded a real project, created `.extract-99999.tmp`, `git check-ignore` returned it + `git add -A` staged no `.tmp`. Minor but real (a partial extract buffer is un-Poison-Guarded raw turn content — same reason `*.extract.log` is gitignored). _Relates D-83 (the sweep that found it), Task 92 (the extract.log gitignore precedent)._
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ LIVE-VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-97: Task 114 — `cmk import-anthropic-memory` verified on REAL input (F-13); no bug.** The sweep only ran `--dry-run` with native memory OFF (nothing to import). **Same shape as 112/113:** the CORE (`importAnthropicMemory`) was already tested on real input (non-dry-run apply with `write_source: imported` + `trust: medium` + dedup, via its `harnessRoot` seam) — so the literal "add a test" ask already existed; the gap was the CLI WRAPPER (`runImportAnthropicMemory`, only ever run dry-run-with-nothing). **Fix:** dep-inject + export the wrapper (`{projectRoot, harnessRoot, log, logError}`; defaults unchanged) + 4 wrapper tests (applied / no-source / dry-run / requires-confirmation). **LIVE test (the user's "live test every task" directive):** seeded a real native `MEMORY.md` at the actual `~/.claude/projects/<sandbox-slug>/memory/` path + ran `cmk import-anthropic-memory --yes` (current repo code) → **"applied 2 proposal(s)"**, both bullets in `context/MEMORY.md` with `write_source: imported, trust: medium, source: anthropic-auto-memory`; cleaned up the sandbox slug dir. **Works on real input — no bug.** **Side question answered (the user, mid-task — "why are we reading native auto memory?"):** native Auto Memory (Claude Code v2.1.59+) writes to `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/` — machine-local, uncommitted, ~30-day ephemeral — and is winner-take-all (D-74: the agent can save to native instead of the kit). `import-anthropic-memory` is the one-way bridge that reclaims those bullets into the kit's committed/tiered/searchable `context/`. It's an optional coexistence convenience (pure file ops, no Haiku), not core. 4th D-84 re-audit finding landed (110/112/113/114) — pattern fully holds. _Relates D-84, D-74, ADR-0011, Task 116._
  - **✔ LIVE-VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-96: ran the v0.2.3 fixes LIVE from the CLI (current repo code via `node packages/cli/bin/cmk.mjs`, real Windows + real Haiku, sandboxed `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR`) — the user asked "did you do live tests until now?" and the honest answer was "live-Haiku unit smokes yes, but not the actual broken commands."** So I ran the three I'd flagged as logic-verified-not-live: **Task 109** — `register-crons --dry-run` on real Windows → **exit 0**, well-formed schtasks command with the quoted path triple (the D-83 bug was even `--dry-run` failing exit 2; gone). **Task 110** — rich `cmk remember` → `cmk search "pnpm"` finds it → `cmk forget <id>` → `cmk search "pnpm"` returns **"no results" with NO manual reindex**, while the other fact survives (the headline auto-reindex + over-mutation guard, end-to-end live). **Task 111** — `cmk persona generate` with real Haiku → completed in **16s** (bug was a 50s timeout), **promoted 2** cross-project doctrine facts (uv + lint) to the user tier, correctly left the project-specific fact unpromoted. **Finding (not a bug):** terse `cmk remember "text"` writes a SCRATCHPAD BULLET, but `cmk forget` only tombstones FACT FILES (`context/memory/*.md`) — so forget-by-query against a bullet correctly says "no matching fact"; the first live attempt used the wrong capture mode (re-ran with rich `--why/--how` → fact file → forget works). **Still needs the user's live SESSION (can't drive from CLI):** Task 108 MCP tools driven by Claude in-session; Task 113 interactive `cmk queue` over a real TTY.   - **🧭 DECISION (2026-06-08) — D-93: merge Task 111 on isolation-green + single-run-green; defer two PRE-EXISTING stress-only flakes to Task 116.x.** Task 111's 5× stress gate surfaced two concurrency flakes, BOTH passing in isolation + on a single clean `npm test`, BOTH unrelated to the F-2 change (auto-persona corpus/timeout): (1) `cli-capture-turn` spawn-latency under saturation — root-caused (detached child cold-start > the 3s `pollFor` window; `r.spawned` was already true) + FIXED in-PR (3s→12s); this is the exact flake PRs #22/#23 wrongly DISCLAIMED.   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-92: Task 111 — `cmk persona generate` timed out on a real project (F-2); root cause was prompt-overload, not a hang.** The cut-gate sweep first mis-reported F-2 as "PASS (cooldown)"; on a real cooldown-cleared run it errored `claude --print did not return within 50000ms`. **Root cause:** `assembleProjectCorpus` (the `facts` source) joined EVERY tier-P fact + scratchpad into ONE unbounded classifier prompt — while the SessionEnd `transcript` path was already 40KB-capped. On a project with substantial memory the prompt ballooned and Haiku blew the 50s timeout. Compounding it, the 50s was hardcoded even though `cmk persona generate` is a one-shot with NO outer hook ceiling (unlike the 60s-bounded SessionEnd path it shares `autoPersona` with). **Fix (3 parts):** (1) cap the facts corpus at `PERSONA_CORPUS_BYTES` (60KB, accumulate WHOLE facts up to budget + a truncation marker — never split a fact); (2) parameterize `autoPersona({timeoutMs})` — SessionEnd keeps the 50s default (composes with the 60s ceiling per design §8.5 / D-42), and the ceiling-free `facts` callers (`runPersonaGenerate` + `weekly-curate`) pass 120s; (3) the CLI surfaces a clear "timed out — re-run" hint instead of the raw internal error. **§8.5 composition:** the inner timeout must NOT exceed any outer ceiling — but the CLI has none, so a generous inner bound is correct there; the SessionEnd path is the one that stays 50<60. **Tests:** the "real generates candidates" test the task asked for ALREADY existed (mock backend returns `PERSONA CANDIDATE` lines, asserts `action:'promoted'` + the bullet lands in the user tier — not a cooldown-skip); added corpus-cap (Door 3: input ≤ cap + marker via `onCompress`), timeout default-vs-override, CLI 120s + hint. **Known limitation (documented):** facts past the cap drop in file-iteration order — value-ordered (trust/recency-first) accumulation is the follow-up if a large corpus drops doctrine. **Meta:** this is the 2nd of the D-84 "ran-on-trivial-input ≠ feature-works" re-audit findings to land (after Task 110); the unbounded-corpus bug only surfaced because the re-run used REAL project memory, not the empty/cooldown-skipped sweep input.

  - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-90: Task 110 — `cmk forget` (and any removal) now auto-propagates to search; no manual `cmk reindex` (F-7).** **The bug (D-84 re-class):** `forget` tombstoned the fact file correctly but never touched the search index, and `reindexBoot` (which every index reader lazy-runs before reading) only ADDED/UPDATED files that still existed — it never PRUNED rows for a file that vanished. So a forgotten fact lingered in `cmk search` until a manual `reindex --full`. **Root cause:** reindexBoot was add/update-only, not a full sync. **Fix (2 parts):** (1) **reindexBoot now prunes orphans** — any `files`-checkpoint row whose source no longer exists is deleted with its observations (the FTS5 delete trigger fires per row); since `search`/`get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recent-activity` all lazy-call reindexBoot, the WHOLE deletion class (forget, queue-discard, supersede-archive, manual delete) self-heals on the next read with zero command. (2) **forget() reindexes IN-BAND** after tombstone+scrub so the index is correct the instant it returns; both `cmk forget` (CLI) + `mk_forget` (MCP) call the same `forget()`, so both surfaces get it; best-effort try/catch (the on-disk tombstone is authoritative). **Audit (trust / lessons / queue — the task asked):** NO gap — in-place edits (`trust` rewrites the file → mtime/sha1 diff → re-indexed) + adds (`lessons promote` = new source file) already self-heal via the existing lazy reindex; only DELETIONS needed the prune. Locked by a test running the REAL `overrideTrust` → `reindexBoot` chain. **inject was never broken for facts:** `injectContext` reads scratchpads (not fact files, not the index), and forget already scrubs the scratchpad bullets — the "may still be injected at SessionStart" line was a severity frame; the concrete, reproducible bug was `cmk search`. **Boundary (design §9.2.1):** a forgotten fact's row is pruned, so it's recoverable via `cmk get`/the tombstone file but NOT `cmk search --include-tombstoned` (forget = gone-from-search; the flag surfaces rows with `deleted_at` set *in the index*, which move-to-archive doesn't feed). Before this, forget left the row as a LIVE observation (`deleted_at` null) → it surfaced in DEFAULT search: the actual bug, not a working `--include-tombstoned`. **Tests:** reindexBoot orphan-prune (+over-mutation guard +no-false-positive), forget in-band (+graceful no-projectRoot), trust audit-lock. design §6.5 + §9.2.1; CHANGELOG Fixed.
  - **🐞 BUG (cut-gate5 live run, 2026-06-07) — D-81: explicit `cmk remember` SILENTLY corrupts rich facts that contain backticks.** A `--how`/`--why`/`--text`/`--title` value with backtick code-spans is eaten by **bash command-substitution** before `cmk` (node) ever reads argv → the spans are saved as empty `()`. Confirmed on disk: `feedback_use-venv-for-all-python-packages.md` How = `Create .venv if absent (), always install packages into it (), never use system pip` — both `` `python -m venv .venv` `` and `` `.\.venv\Scripts\pip install ...` `` gone; the `..venvScriptspip: command not found` line in the run is the substitution firing. **Silent** — cmk + the agent both saw success. **Blast radius:** the explicit `cmk remember` shell path only; **auto-extract (the v0.2.2 headline) is IMMUNE** (Haiku → `writeFact`, no shell). **Pre-existing** — rich `--why/--how` predates Task 103, so this lives in 0.2.1 too; NOT a v0.2.2 regression. **This is NOT R2-class / not an accept-the-edge.** The user (2026-06-07): *"this is not good at all… if this continues all our memory will be garbage… we never want this to happen."* Silent corruption of memory is the one failure a memory kit must never have. **Root cause is unrecoverable at the binary** (bash destroys the content before node starts), so the FIX must move rich content OFF the shell argv: a non-shell input channel — e.g. `cmk remember --from-file <fact.json>` (agent writes the JSON via the Write tool → zero shell parsing of content) — plus remember-skill guidance to never inline backticks/`$()`. Detection-only is weak (the evidence is already destroyed). **Owner decision PENDING:** fix as a pre-cut blocker, vs. cut v0.2.2 now (headline path immune) + fix as an immediate v0.2.3 fast-follow task. Needs a §16 design candidate + a cut-gate known-edge note once the fix shape is settled.
  - **📋 NEXT TASK (decided 2026-06-07) — D-82: unify CLI+MCP over ONE shared memory-op core + RESILIENT structured input + a parity guard.** Ships as **v0.2.3, AFTER the user cuts v0.2.2** (decision-2 settled: v0.2.2's CHANGELOG is sealed around the 5 shipped tasks + its headline auto-extract path is immune — do NOT re-open it). Scope: (a) fix D-81 resiliently — CLI `remember --from-file <fact.json>` + `--json -` (stdin) → `JSON.parse` → the SAME structured object the MCP tool passes; rich content never touches argv, so `fs.readFileSync`+`JSON.parse` is byte-total; (b) close the CLI↔MCP drift — MCP gains the write/mutate tools, CLI gains `get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recent-activity` (the 4 read verbs it lacks today), both as thin adapters over the shared core; (c) a `validate-cli-mcp-parity.mjs` guard wired into `npm test`. **Decision-1 (APPROVED):** MCP gets the destructive ops too, but `forget`/`purge` over MCP require an explicit **confirm-token param** (mirrors CLI `--yes`) so the auto-invoking model can't silently tombstone. Carries **ADR-0014** + a **design §10/§12 revision** (decision-trail-preserved: §10.3 framed MCP as retrieval-first with writes flowing through the memory-write skill→`cmk remember`; we APPEND the write-parity extension + the why — both §10 and §12 are ALSO stale vs the code, re-sync them) + a DECISION-LOG entry. **RESEARCH-FIRST (user directive 2026-06-07):** before designing, do REAL primary-source research on the ACTUAL CURRENT code of the dual-surface / structured-input products — top target **basic-memory** (open-source Python CLI+MCP memory tool = our exact architecture), co-top **mempalace** (Python CLI `init/mine/search/wake-up/sweep` + a **29-tool MCP** server — a 2nd real dual-surface analog; NB ~5 CLI cmds vs 29 MCP tools ⇒ likely NOT 1:1, the CLI is a thin subset — confirm the shared-core + subset pattern in their source), then claude-mem (TS CLI+MCP+hooks), claude-remember (stdin-from-file input channel), gstack (single-quoted-JSON-arg→binary), memsearch (pipe), Hermes (memory action-model tool). NOT Cursor/Kiro/ChatGPT/Antigravity (closed or spec-methodology-only — no studiable dual-surface code for THIS question). **CHECKED-AND-EXCLUDED for THIS question (2026-06-07, real-repo verify):** `memory-os` (ClaudioDrews) — a backend memory-OS for the Hermes agent (Docker/Qdrant/Redis/ARQ), **no standalone CLI, no MCP** (integrates only via the Hermes Icarus plugin hooks), so nothing to teach on CLI↔MCP parity or shell-safe input; it stays relevant only to Task 75 (authoritative-injection) + Task 97 (dynamic trust), already filed. Our existing `docs/research/` notes answer the CAPTURE question, not the CLI-MCP-parity + shell-safe-input question, so this is net-new research. **Honesty note (the assistant, 2026-06-07):** I do NOT already know their live source — prior citations were from our notes (some code-level, some survey); training data on these niche products is unreliable. Each repo read gets an adoption-verification note (concrete gain vs counterfactual). Formal `tasks.md` entry created at task-start (post-cut). (ADR-0014 written 2026-06-07 at task-start: [docs/adr/0014](../adr/0014-unify-cli-mcp-shared-core.md).)
  - **🐞 BUG (cut-gate5 full CLI sweep, 2026-06-07) — D-83: `cmk register-crons` is broken on Windows.** Even `--dry-run` fails (exit 2): `error — command: must not contain double quotes (Windows schtasks /TR quoting contract)` for BOTH daily-distill + weekly-curate. The builder emits a schtasks `/TR` value containing double quotes, which the kit's own guard rejects → cron can NEVER register on Windows. **Non-★, optional** (the lazy-on-read SessionStart fallback covers compression — doctor HC-6: "cron not registered (optional) — using the lazy-on-read fallback"), **pre-existing** (Task 33, NOT a v0.2.2 regression) → does NOT block the v0.2.2 cut per the verdict ★-list.   - **🔁 CORRECTION + META (2026-06-07) — D-84: the cut-gate5 CLI sweep conflated "the command didn't crash" with "the feature works" — a lazy-framing instance from the ASSISTANT, in a live-test report.** The user caught it on F-7 (I wrote "not a bug, just a stale index" → they pushed: *"this is bad… users will not run commands; the regular user will want everything to happen automatic"*) and asked *"are there more hiding behind code words?"* — there were. (2) **F-2 `persona generate`**, reported "PASS (cooldown)", actually ERRORS on a real cooldown-cleared run (`claude --print did not return within 50000ms`) → Task 111. (3) **F-4 / F-9 / F-13** "passes" were hollow — they ran against cooldown / an empty queue / a dry-run-with-nothing, i.e. "trivial input didn't crash," NOT feature-verified → Tasks 112 / 113 / 114. (4) **register-crons** (D-83) + all of these shipped untested because no suite test or cut-gate check ever exercised them on REAL input → Task 116 (coverage hardening). **Meta-rule (graduates toward CLAUDE.md):** a sweep verdict MUST distinguish "ran without error on trivial input" from "the feature works on real input" — cooldown-skip / empty-queue / dry-run-nothing is NOT a pass; mark it "unverified" and re-run for real. This is the **5th instance of the lazy-framing class** in the build (CLAUDE.md anti-patterns) — the first sourced from a live-test sweep report. All 8 findings → v0.2.3 Tasks **108–116** ([`tasks.md`](../../specs/tasks.md) §"v0.2.3"); lane in [`RELEASE-PLAN.md`](../../docs/RELEASE-PLAN.md).
  - **🧭 PRODUCT PRINCIPLE (binding, 2026-06-07) — D-85: the regular user NEVER runs a `cmk` command — they live in free speech.** Every memory operation reaches the kit one of two ways: **AUTOMATIC** (hooks — capture / inject / compress / auto-extract / persona-promotion — the user does nothing) or **CLAUDE-MEDIATED** (the user voices an intent — *"forget the API key"*, *"what did we decide about X"*, *"always use uv"* — and Claude translates it into the kit action via a skill trigger or an MCP tool). **The `cmk` CLI is Claude's + power-users' tool, NEVER the regular user's interface** — if a regular user ever has to type `cmk` or run `reindex`, the kit failed. Consequences: (a) every user-expressible intent MUST have an automatic OR Claude-mediated path — a CLI verb with no skill-trigger / MCP-tool is **invisible** to the regular user; (b) once triggered, the action must **complete automatically** (F-7 / Task 110: *"forget X"* → gone from search AND inject, zero follow-up command); (c) the **MCP tool surface + skill layer IS the real user-facing surface** (via Claude) — so Task 108's CLI↔MCP parity is the *free-speech action surface*, not symmetry-for-its-own-sake. **Gaps today (intents with NO reliable free-speech path):** *"forget X"* (no forget skill/tool — memory-write is remember-only; MCP has no `mk_forget`), *"trust this / not important"* (none), reliable recall-on-a-question (partial — Task 75 active-recall). → **Task 117.** Source: the user 2026-06-07: *"the regular user will not run commands, at all… they assume that if they tell Claude in free speech, then it will happen or it happened automatic… this is what they think about every command."* **Clinching evidence (same day): the MAINTAINER himself drove this entire cut-gate CLI sweep by telling Claude *"if you think we should run all the commands we didnt run, you could do it"* — then *"even i dont run commands and tell you to do it."* Even the author, who knows every command exists, uses free-speech→Claude rather than typing `cmk`. So the model is UNIVERSAL, not a novice accommodation — the conversation IS the interface for everyone; the CLI is the substrate Claude drives.** Graduates toward a design principle + CLAUDE.md.
  - **♻️ REVISIT (2026-06-07) — D-80 (R2 `cd`-compound permission edge) gets its "simple solution" via Task 108's MCP-first surface.** D-80 parked R2 ("won't fix unless a simple solution arrives") because the bash path is un-allowlistable — Claude Code matches a compound `cd "…" && cmk …` PER-SUBCOMMAND, so the `cd &&` prefix dodges `Bash(cmk:*)`. **New evidence (the user, 2026-06-07):** the MCP path dissolves it by construction — an `mk_*` call is a JSON-RPC tool, NOT a shell command, so there's no `cd`, no compound, no `Bash()` matcher; and the MCP server already knows the project root (launched per `.mcp.json`). **Simple fix (rides Task 108):** `cmk install` allowlists `mcp__cmk__*` (mirroring the existing `Bash(cmk *)` + `Skill(memory-write)` allowlists from Tasks 79/90) → the Claude-mediated path is pre-approved, ZERO prompts, none of the 3 rejected hacks (`Bash(cd:*)` / leading-`*` wildcard / PreToolUse hook). Same move that fixes D-81 (get the op off the shell). **Tracked as its own Task 118** (lands with/after 108 — a checkbox won't get lost the way a "revisit later" note would; the no-lugging principle).   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🎓 LESSON (2026-06-07) — D-86: Task 108a merged (PR #130); real-binary subprocess tests don't count for line coverage — extract pure, dep-injected helpers.** 108a (`cmk remember --from-file`/`--json` — the **D-81** fix: rich content read from a file/stdin never touches the shell) shipped. **The lesson (reusable):** the PR's SonarCloud gate failed at *"12.5% coverage on new code"* even though the `--from-file`/`--json` logic was thoroughly tested — because the kit's CLI tests spawn the **real binary** (`spawnSync(cmk.mjs)`, Door 3), and a subprocess's execution is invisible to the parent process's coverage instrumentation. **The fix is also better design:** extract the logic into a PURE, dependency-injected helper (`parseFactInput`) + make the action dep-injectable (`runRemember(…, {projectRoot, log, logError})`, mirroring `runRememberRich`) and unit-test those **in-process**; keep the real-binary test for the wiring (Door 3). **Apply going forward:** when new CLI logic is only real-binary-tested, add in-process unit tests on an extracted pure helper / dep-injected action — don't rely on the subprocess test for coverage. Two-pass review fixes also landed (field allowlist so a crafted JSON can't forge provenance, 64 KB input cap, `readHookStdin` reuse, bare-remember guard). Graduates toward CLAUDE.md (Engineering discipline). Next: **108b** (MCP write/read parity + `validate-cli-mcp-parity` guard + skill/install R2 fix).
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ♻️ RESOLVED (2026-06-08) — D-87: Task 108 COMPLETE (108b, PR #131) — full CLI↔MCP parity + enforcing guard + install MCP registration; R2 / D-80 / Task-118 RESOLVED.** 108b shipped the whole parity surface over shared in-process cores (`remember-core.mjs` + `read-core.mjs`): MCP gained rich `mk_remember` + the mutate tools (`mk_trust` / `mk_lessons_promote` / `mk_forget` two-step-confirm-token) + queue tools (`mk_queue_list` / `mk_queue_resolve`); CLI gained the 4 read verbs; `validate-cli-mcp-parity.mjs` fails the build on drift; `cmk install` writes `.mcp.json` + allowlists `mcp__cmk__*` and the skill prefers the MCP tools — so the Claude-mediated path is prompt-free (R2 dissolved: a tool call isn't a shell command). **VERIFIED primary-source findings (the "did you check?" rule, code.claude.com/docs):** Claude Code's `permissions.allow` supports the **`mcp__cmk__*` tool wildcard** (and server-level `mcp__cmk`) — `/en/permissions`; project-scoped `.mcp.json` is a committed stdio config and Claude Code sets **`CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`** in the spawned server's env — `/en/mcp`. **Two-pass review caught SR-1:** `mk_queue_list` mutated the queue file because it listed via the resolve-walker (which `writeFileSync`s unconditionally) → fixed with pure-read `listReviewQueue` / `listConflictQueue`. **SonarCloud new-hotspot gate caught** a sha1 in the confirm-token (a preview-fingerprint nonce, not crypto) → switched to sha256 to clear it honestly with no NOSONAR. **Lessons reaffirmed:** the D-86 in-process-coverage discipline held (new-code coverage came in at 80% = pass); primary-source verification before generating user config (didn't guess the permission wildcard). **Deferred (non-blocking housekeeping):** design §10/§12/§16.57 re-sync, SOURCES entry, research-note OPEN→VERIFIED close, journey retrospective. Next: **Task 109** (register-crons Windows fix).
  - **🧹 SHIPPED (2026-06-08) — D-88: Task 77 done — version-named-but-general docs renamed to version-agnostic (the misnomer class the user raised 3×).** `specs/v0.1.0/` → `specs/` + `docs/journey/v0.1.0-build-log.md` → `docs/journey/build-log.md`, one atomic refactor: ~200 internal references updated in lockstep (docs, README, CLAUDE.md, DOCUMENTATION-MAP, the validators' path constants, 3 test files); `validate-references` + full suite green. **The principle (naming hygiene):** version-AGNOSTIC names for the **living Spine** (one cumulative doc that grows across versions — a `v0.X` label there *lies* about scope); version-STAMPED names for **point-in-time history** (a *series* of per-release records — `v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md`, `archive/specs/v0.1.0/`, etc. — where the version IS the doc's identity, not a stale label).   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-89: Task 109 — `cmk register-crons` fixed on Windows (broken since v0.1) + a macOS sibling bug found & fixed.** D-83's bug: the win32 path built schtasks as a pre-quoted shell string `/TR "${command}"` where `command` = the quoted path triple `"<node>" "<script>" "<projectRoot>"` (Task 36 B1/B2) — so the inner quotes double-wrapped AND `registerCron`'s own guard *rejected* the `"` → cron could NEVER register on Windows (even `--dry-run`, exit 2). **Root-cause class:** a single pre-quoted command STRING can't serve three platforms' quoting — Linux nests it in `echo '…'`, Windows re-wraps in `/TR "…"`, macOS splits on whitespace. **Fix:** win32 now execs `schtasks` with an ARGS ARRAY (no `shell:true`) → the `/TR` value reaches schtasks verbatim (CreateProcess arg-quoting); cmd.exe parses the quoted paths only when the task FIRES. Removed the self-contradictory double-quote rejection; `buildWindowsSchtasks` returns + exports the argv array, unit-tested via a new `platform` test seam on `registerCron` (since `detectPlatform()` can't vary on a single CI host — the gap that let this ship). **macOS sibling, found the same pass:** the plist `command.split(/\s+/)` kept the wrapping quotes → `<string>"/path/node"</string>` → launchd exec'd a literally-quoted path → ENOENT. Silently broken, never reported because the crons were never checked since v0.1 (the user: *"we didn't check the crons since the first version"*). Now strips the wrapping quotes. Linux was already correct. **HC-6:** no change needed — once the command works, its "Run `cmk register-crons`" advice is valid (it already points at the lazy-on-read fallback too). **Remaining edge (backlog, v0.2.x):** a node/project path that itself contains a SPACE breaks the macOS whitespace-split — the real fix is the `command:string` → `argv:string[]` API refactor (each platform quotes from raw argv); rare for node/project paths, so not a blocker. **Lesson:** dry-run-only tests + a "platform-tested by the user at install" Door-3 N/A note let a broken Windows AND macOS path ship for two minor versions — cross-platform builders must be tested directly (pure functions, platform-seam-injected), not deferred to manual install-time checks.

- **D-80 NOTE (2026-06-07) — explicit-capture R2 prompt on a `cd <abs-path> && cmk` compound is a KNOWN, ACCEPTED edge — DOCUMENTED, deliberately NOT fixed. SETTLED.** The user (2026-06-07): *"lets just document it as an edge case we wont 'fix' unless we have a working simple solution."* Surfaced by the v0.2.2 cut-gate live run: the agent captured a preference richly (`cmk remember "…" --type feedback --why … --how … --title …`, no "remember this" — F1 working) but Claude Code popped *"Allow this bash command?"* because the agent wrapped it as `cd "c:/Temp/cut-gate5" && cmk remember …`. **Verified root cause against the primary source ([code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions)):** (1) `cd` is a built-in **read-only** command (auto-approved) — but only when the target is *inside the working directory*; a `cd` to an **absolute path** Claude Code doesn't recognize as inside the WD doesn't qualify. (2) Compounds are **split per-subcommand** ("a rule must match each subcommand independently") — so the whole `cd … && cmk …` prompts because the `cd`-to-absolute-path subcommand didn't qualify, NOT because of `cmk`. (3) `Bash(cmk:*)` (≡ `Bash(cmk *)`) already covers the **bare** `cmk remember …` — which is the normal case → no prompt. So **R2 substantially passes**; the friction is only the agent's redundant `cd <abs>` wrapper. **Two false fixes ruled out by the docs (verify-before-shipping paid off):** `Bash(cd:*)` is a **no-op** (cd is already read-only); `Bash(*cmk:*)` doesn't help (the `cmk` subcommand already matches; the `cd` subcommand is the issue) AND would be a hole. **Why we're NOT fixing:** the only two real options both have a catch — a behavioral skill/CLAUDE.md nudge ("run `cmk` directly, never `cd` first") which the docs themselves say *"doesn't change what Claude Code allows"* (the weak kind), OR a **PreToolUse hook** to auto-approve `cmk` capture calls (the docs' endorsed mechanism) which **re-opens ADR-0006's deliberate PreToolUse-drop** ("fires on every tool invocation") — an architectural decision, not a quick patch. **Trigger to revisit:** a *simple, reliable* solution (e.g. if Claude Code later treats `cd`-to-WD-root as read-only in all forms, or a cheap non-PreToolUse mechanism appears). Filed as a deferred candidate (design §16.57). _Relates R2 cut-gate check, ADR-0006 (PreToolUse drop), Task 79/90 (cmk + skill allow-listing), the v0.2.2 cut-gate; primary source verified._

- **D-79 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 106: the §16.27 `now.md` compress race is CLOSED via the file-rename pattern (for BOTH callers). SETTLED.** Surfaced by Task 105 self-review (D-78): `compressSession` read `now.md` → ~5–10s Haiku → `truncateSync(0)`, so a turn the (new) session appended in that window was dropped. **Fix:** `compressSession` now CLAIMS the buffer by atomic rename (`now.md → now.md.rolling-{ts}`) before the Haiku call (`claimNowBuffer`), compresses the claimed copy, and on success `discardRolling` (unlink) — `now.md` is owned by the session's appenders, never re-touched, so a concurrent append is never clobbered. On Haiku failure/timeout, `restoreRolling` puts the un-compressed buffer back (prepended to anything appended meanwhile), preserving the old "leave now.md intact → retry next roll" contract. **Design decisions:** (1) **Pure rename, no re-create** — an uncontended roll leaves `now.md` ABSENT (not truncate-to-0-bytes); re-creating an empty `now.md` would re-open a (tiny) clobber race against a concurrent append, so we don't. The 3 honesty/unit tests asserting `size === 0` were corrected to "no leftover (empty OR absent)" — exactly the size-vs-existence correction §16.27 had predicted (the note claimed the tests would survive unchanged; they needed this one-line contract correction, which is consistent with the note's INTENT: pin the OUTCOME, not the impl). (2) **Restore-on-error prepends** (claimed buffer is older → leads) so both the un-rolled buffer + any concurrent append survive. (3) **`cmk roll --scope now` inherits it free** (it delegates to `compressSession`). **Verified:** a deterministic race test (backend appends mid-compress; the turn must survive + error-path restore + no orphan rolling file) + a **12/12 live-Haiku end-to-end run** (real `claude --print`: a turn appended ~1.5s into the real Haiku call survived while the prior content rolled). **Honesty correction carried from D-78:** D-78's first claim "the §16.27 race composes fine" was WRONG; this task is the fix, and the corrected D-78 line + §16.27 both reflect that. _Relates §16.27 (now SHIPPED), D-78, Task 105, Task 27 (I4, the original §16.27 finding), `compress-session.mjs`._

- **D-78 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 105: the now→today roll now ALSO fires lazily at SessionStart, so rolling compression no longer depends on a clean SessionEnd. SETTLED (implements the D-75 fix).** D-75 found the `now.md` → `today-{date}.md` roll (`compressSession`) was SessionEnd-only, and Claude Code fires SessionEnd only on a clean window-close — so a never-cleanly-closed session left `now.md` unbounded with no `today-*.md`/`recent.md`. Fix: `detectStaleness` gains a `stale-now` verdict (now.md `trim() !== ''`) at **highest precedence after cron/no-context-dir**; `runLazyCompress` dispatches it to `compressSession`; `inject-context` adds `stale-now` to its detached-spawn condition. **Design decisions:** (1) **Detached, not inline** — a Haiku roll can't run in the 500ms SessionStart budget, so THIS session injects pre-roll state and the next gets the rolled state (the standard §8.2.1 lazy tradeoff; the spec's "roll THEN inject" wording is aspirational — the real mechanism mirrors the already-working daily-distill lazy pattern). (2) **One-verdict-one-cycle, cascading** — `stale-now` takes precedence over weekly/daily because now→today is the FIRST pipeline level; the today→recent + weekly levels self-heal on subsequent SessionStarts once now.md drains. (3) **Cooldown composes** — `runLazyCompress` gates 120s up front and passes `cooldownMs:0` to the inner `compressSession`, so a clean SessionEnd immediately followed by a reopen doesn't double-roll. (4) **Scope: now→today ONLY** — MEMORY.md graduation already has a reactive-on-write path (Task 94), so it never grew unbounded; the now-roll was the *unique* gap, so Task 105 does NOT add graduation to the lazy path. **§16.27 race — does NOT fully compose (self-review finding, corrected):** my first read said "the roll fires at session start, before the new session's appends, so it composes fine." Deeper review proved that WRONG — `compressSession` reads now.md, spends ~5–10s in Haiku, then truncates to 0, so a turn appended by the NEW session during that window is dropped from `today-*.md`. It's MORE likely than the SessionEnd §16.27 case (a starting session actively appends; an ending one doesn't) and opens a minor new loss path (the dropped turn is transcript-recoverable, not durable-memory loss; and timing usually avoids it — the first append lands after the ~10s roll). Net still strongly positive (before Task 105 now.md grew UNBOUNDED). Documented in §16.27 as the concrete "visible user pain" trigger for the file-rename fix (§16.27 candidate #1) — recommended as a focused follow-up PR (the rename touches the shared compressSession + needs a race test). **Read-the-docs-first note:** the user asked mid-task whether I'd read the rolling-compression docs first; I read design §8 + §8.2.1/.2 + §16.27 + D-75 BEFORE writing implementation — and the §16.27 read is exactly what flagged this race on self-review. _Relates D-75, Task 35 (lazy-compress mechanism this extends), Task 86c (SessionEnd persona pass — still SessionEnd-only, a known smaller gap), design §8.1/§8.2.2, §16.27 (now.md truncate race — file-rename follow-up)._

- **D-77 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 103: `cmk-auto-extract` now synthesizes RICH Why/How fact files on the native-immune Stop-hook path. SETTLED.** Implements the D-74 fix: rich capture rode ONLY the explicit `cmk remember` path, which native Auto Memory can hijack (winner-take-all); the immune Stop-hook auto-extract wrote only terse bullets. Now the SAME per-turn Haiku pass (no second LLM call) emits a third output type — a fenced `BEGIN_FACT…END_FACT` block for durable project KNOWLEDGE (triggers 3–6: setup/config, conventions, workflows, quirks) — routed via `writeFact` to the fact store. Lighter signals (triggers 1–2) stay terse `MEMORY.md` bullets. **Four design decisions, all settled:** (1) **trust:medium** (spec-settled) — auto-extract is a Haiku synthesis = proposal-grade; explicit `cmk remember` stays high + supersedes. (2) **Direct-to-fact-store, NOT the review queue** — deliberate deviation from the terse "medium → queue" convention; the point is *automatic* native-parity capture (native writes its files with no approval step), the fact store is searchable-but-not-full-trust-injected, writeFact screens every write, and explicit-high supersedes. (3) **Rich-vs-terse split + XOR** — each fact is EITHER a rich block OR a terse line (prompt-enforced; a terse candidate whose canonical id matches a rich fact's body is dropped as a safety net). (4) **Shared `rich-fact.mjs`** — `buildRichFactBody`+`slugifyFact` extracted from `subcommands.mjs` so explicit + automatic paths build identical files. **It's BOTH/AND (D-74 addendum):** git-portability/provenance/3-tier STAY differentiators; this makes the memory itself native-parity-then-better — the LIVE parity check confirmed real Haiku emits a STRUCTURED body (Architectural Pattern + Tech Stack breakdown) + Why/How that matches/beats native. **Parser robustness surfaced by that live check:** Haiku formats multi-line bodies as a YAML block scalar (`body: |` + indent) → `cleanFieldValue` strips the indicator + dedents (a mocked test would never have caught this — the manual live check earned its keep). REJECTED (still): PreToolUse hard-block + disable-native-default (D-74). _Relates D-74, Task 21/23 (auto-extract), Task 63 (rich capture), ADR-0011, design §6.4 (rich-fact synthesis), the §19 graduation composition (rich facts land in the graduation TARGET, reducing scratchpad pressure)._

- **FIX (2026-06-07) — Task 101: extended the manual-run stdin-hang fix (Task 100) from `cmk-compress-session` to ALL hook bins.** Every hook bin drained stdin with a raw blocking `readFileSync(0)` that hangs forever on a manual TTY run (no piped payload → the console never sends EOF), before any body runs — the same class Task 100 fixed for only the SessionEnd bin. Routed `cmk-capture-prompt`, `cmk-capture-turn`, `cmk-inject-context`, `cmk-observe-edit` (npm + plugin twins) and the plugin-only `cmk-version-check` through the existing `readHookStdin({ isTTY: process.stdin.isTTY })` helper (returns `''` for a TTY). Each bin loads the helper via the SAME guarded dynamic-import block as its main module, so a corrupt install still emits its hook envelope + exit 0 (graceful-degradation preserved); plugin `observe-edit` keeps its envelope-FIRST ordering via a split import (drain-helper before the envelope, heavy append module after). Regression-locked by `tests/cli-hook-stdin-drain.test.js` — structural (every bin delegates to the helper, injects `isTTY`, and contains no raw `readFileSync(0)`) + behavioral (empty stdin exits 0 within a hard timeout). **`cmk-compress-session` folded into the structural lock too** — the user caught the "out of scope" framing on its leftover comment token: it wasn't out of scope, the test just hadn't covered the already-fixed bin (lazy-framing class, corrected). _Relates Task 100, NFR-5 spirit, the twin-bin lockstep hazard._

- **D-76 FIX (2026-06-07) — `cli-index-rebuild.test.js` 29.4 #2 ("boot after editing one fact") was a load-induced mtime-granularity flake (stress 4/5); made deterministic with `utimesSync`.** `reindexBoot`'s fast path skips files whose `floor(mtimeMs)` matches the indexed checkpoint (intentional + documented — a content change that preserves mtime isn't re-read). The test seeds a fact, boots, then edits + boots again expecting `filesReindexed === 1`; it writes the seed and the edit <1ms apart, so under 5x stress the two mtimes collided → fast-path skip → `filesReindexed === 0`. **Test fix, not code fix (stated explicitly per the anti-pattern rule):** the production fast-path is correct by design (it avoids re-reading every file's content on every boot — a deliberate perf choice); the test was relying on the wall clock advancing between two synchronous writes, which isn't guaranteed under load. Forced a strictly-later mtime on the edited file (`utimesSync(factPath, now+10s)`) to simulate the real-world edit-gap. Surfaced as a Task 101 stress detour — problem-forced, and structurally unrelated to the hook-bin change (the test imports `reindexBoot`, never a hook bin). _Relates `index-rebuild.mjs` mtime caveat, the stress-gate non-jitter rule, D-68 (stress logging that NAMED the failing test)._

- **D-75 FINDING (2026-06-06) — rolling compression (`now.md` → `today-*.md`) is SessionEnd-only, and Claude Code fires SessionEnd ONLY on a clean window-close, not on new-chat-same-window → it silently never ran in the not-cleanly-closed cut-gate runs. NOT a wedge blocker; fix = Task 105 (lazy-roll on SessionStart).** Surfaced at the cut-gate Session-1→2 boundary. **What's verified:** the SessionEnd chain WORKS — on a clean close of `mem-test3` it fired fully (Haiku `compressSession` → accurate `today-2026-06-06.md` summary, `now.md` 10 KB→0, the §19 graduation sweep, and `context/sessions/{date}.compress.log`, all at 21:02). **But across cut-gate2 + cut-gate3** (never cleanly closed) `now.md` accumulated ~10 KB/22 turns over multiple sessions and **never rolled** — no `today-*.md`, no `recent.md`, no Task-86c SessionEnd persona pass. The wedge still worked there because the **Stop-hook inline path** (capture + persona) is independent of SessionEnd. **Consequence if a user never cleanly exits:** unbounded `now.md`, no injected rolling summary (`recent.md`), no 86c second-grade for queued persona candidates. **Fix (Task 105):** lazy-roll a stale `now.md` at SessionStart (in `cmk-inject-context`), mirroring the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart precedent; keep the SessionEnd path too (idempotent). **Self-correction logged (5th of this thread):** the assistant first reported "`compress.log` empty everywhere → SessionEnd never fired" — but was looking in `context/.locks/`; the compress log actually lives at **`context/sessions/{date}.compress.log`**. The *conclusion* (no compression before the clean close) held, but the path claim was wrong — verify the artifact location before asserting absence. _Relates Task 105, Task 86c (SessionEnd persona pass), §6 (rolling-window compression), the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart precedent; surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate._

- **D-74 FINDING (2026-06-06) — a cut-gate run captured to Claude's NATIVE Auto Memory instead of the kit; investigation says VARIANCE not regression, and the whole field captures via the Stop hook (immune). NOT a v0.2.0 blocker. Full write-up: [research note](../research/2026-06-06-native-auto-memory-coexistence-investigation.md).** In `cut-gate3` (Claude Code v2.1.167) the agent saved stated preferences to Claude Code's **native Auto Memory** (`Write ~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/feedback_*.md`) and **never called `cmk remember`** — the kit's `context/memory/` ended up empty, vs `cut-gate2` which produced 3 rich `cmk remember` fact files. **Verdict (decisive): VARIANCE, not regression.** A same-version re-run (`mem-test3`, also v2.1.167) used the kit correctly (`cmk remember --why/--how` → rich fact file, no native). Same version → both outcomes ⇒ the host-version-causation theory is dead (the assistant leaned on it twice, too confidently; the maintainer pushed back; the primary source — [code.claude.com/docs/en/memory](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/memory) + changelog — shows native is the agent writing notes itself, on by default since v2.1.59, **no documented behavior change in 2.1.160–2.1.167**, and CLAUDE.md is *"context, not enforced configuration"* that *"won't reliably hold"*). **What's at risk when native wins a turn is BOUNDED:** the kit's Stop-hook `cmk-auto-extract` captured the cross-project persona (5 promotions) + terse `MEMORY.md` bullets in `cut-gate3` anyway — the **wedge is immune by construction** (the hook reads the conversation; the agent's tool choice is irrelevant). Only the **rich project fact files** are lost (auto-extract writes terse; only explicit `cmk remember` writes rich Why/How). **What the field does (10 competitor READMEs fetched + our deep-dives):** NONE disable native; NONE even mention it (MemPalace/supermemory explicitly "complement"); the **entire field captures ONLY via the Stop hook** (memsearch/claude-mem/claude-remember/Hermes) with **no agent-invoked "remember" command** — so native has nothing to compete with. Our `cmk-auto-extract` is the *same shape*; the kit's explicit `cmk remember` is an *addition* (our differentiator) and the *only* surface native can win. **DECISION:** (1) **ADR-0011 coexist-default STANDS** — the case for disable-by-default is *weaker* than it looked (intermittent + costs only the rich-fact tier); make `cmk disable-native-memory` prominent/recommended instead. (2) **Real fix = Task 103:** enrich `cmk-auto-extract` to write rich fact files so rich capture rides the immune Stop-hook path; explicit `cmk remember` becomes a bonus and native winning a turn costs nothing. (3) A PreToolUse hard-block (the only *forced* redirect) was **REJECTED by the user (2026-06-06)** — intercepting Claude Code's own tool calls is too invasive/fragile for an intermittent loss of the least-critical tier; do NOT re-propose it. **Honesty note:** logged the twice-over-reached version theory deliberately — correlation-as-cause is the lazy-framing class; `mem-test3` (same version, kit won) is the empirical disproof. _Relates ADR-0011, Task 103 (enrich auto-extract), Task 60 (`disable-native-memory`), Task 21/23 (auto-extract), Task 63 (rich capture), the 2026-06-06 competitor README survey._
  - **Addendum — two strategic directives (the user 2026-06-06), both binding:**
    1. **It's WINNER-TAKE-ALL, not coexistence (corrects the FINDING's softer framing).** The cross-tab is exclusive: kit fact files **XOR** native files, never both (cut-gate 4/0, cut-gate2 3/0, cut-gate3 0/5, mem-test3 1/0). When one wins the explicit save, the other writes **nothing** that session. (The kit's always-on auto-extract still runs underneath — that's why the persona fills regardless — but the explicit-save layer is exclusive.) Native ALSO now writes rich Why/How fact files (side-by-side: native's `user_backend_philosophy.md` was MORE structured than our one-shot `cmk remember`) — **our v0.1.1 "we capture richer" moat is GONE.**
    2. **Memory QUALITY must lead — but it's BOTH/AND, not either/or.** The user: *"leaning on this 3 [git-portability / citation-IDs / provenance] are idiotic cause this project is supposed to deliver memory, not gimmicks"* — clarified 2026-06-06 to *"it's not wrong, we didn't say we're not doing that also; it's not mutually exclusive."* So the 3 **STAY real differentiators** (native is machine-local + ephemeral → structurally can't do them) — they are NOT dropped. The correction is narrower: don't pitch the win **solely** on them while the memory itself lags. **Keep the differentiators AND make capture+recall native-parity-then-better.** Task 103's bar reflects this.

- **ISSUE (2026-06-06) — `cmk-compress-session` TIMES OUT (exit 124, ~60s) on the real global install when the SessionEnd Haiku passes have input; the proactive graduation sweep (Task 94.3) then never runs. NEEDS INVESTIGATION (potential v0.2.0 blocker — do NOT tag until resolved).** Surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate deterministic probes (B7). Repro: `cmk install` a throwaway, `cmk remember` ~14 facts, lower `MEMORY.md` cap below current size (but **above** the ~1146 B scaffold floor, e.g. 1400), `CMK_PROJECT_DIR=<dir> timeout 60 cmk-compress-session` → **exit 124, MEMORY unchanged, 0 session-end graduated events, ZERO stderr** (hung before `summarizeSessionEnd` printed). **What's confirmed working:** empty-project compress-session = fast skip/skip/graduation (exit 0); **reactive** graduation on write (B5) = ✅ 9 graduated on the real install; cmk-compress-session does NOT hang in general. **The hang correlates with the Haiku pass having input** (fact corpus / transcript) → it spawns `claude --print`, and the test shell has **no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / no Claude auth** → the spawn hangs. **CORRECTION (the no-auth theory was WRONG):** the kit's Haiku backend is **`claude --print`** (authed by the Claude **subscription** / logged-in CLI, NOT `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`). Verified `echo … | claude --print --model haiku` → replies fast, **exit 0** in this same shell. So the hang is **NOT** the Haiku spawn / auth. **Corrected lead:** the hang appears only when **graduation does REAL work** (over-cap with eligible bullets → `writeFact` → `reindex` per bullet); the empty case (graduation 0) is fast. **Prime suspect = the reindex/index path or a lock**, NOT Haiku — and note the maintainer has **memsearch 0.4.3 installed but Milvus almost certainly NOT running** (HC-7: "milvus reachability is Layer 5b"), so a reindex/writeFact step that touches memsearch/Milvus could block. **NEXT STEP for the resuming session:** (1) read `reindex.mjs` + `write-fact.mjs` + `graduation.mjs` — does graduation's per-bullet `writeFact`→`reindex` shell out to `memsearch`/Milvus or take a lock that can hang? (2) repro with memsearch removed / `CMK_SKIP_*` to isolate; (3) confirm whether `runSessionEndTasks` printed NO stderr because it hung in graduation (after the concurrent block) vs in the Haiku passes — add/inspect a per-stage log; (4) fix before tagging v0.2.0. _Earlier (a)/(b) Haiku-timeout framing is SUPERSEDED by this correction; the `claude --print` spawn is fine._ **CORRECTION #2 — memsearch is ALSO ruled out (grep is decisive):** `reindex.mjs`/`write-fact.mjs`/`graduation.mjs`/`index-db.mjs`/`index-rebuild.mjs` only do `db.exec(...)` (SQLite FTS5) — **no `memsearch`, no Milvus, no `spawn`/`child_process`.** The kit's ONLY memsearch reference is `doctor.mjs` HC-1 (`spawnBinSync('memsearch',['--version'])` for detection). So the graduation→reindex path is **pure SQLite** — memsearch/Milvus is NOT the cause; do NOT uninstall memsearch (won't help; the test suite mocks HC-1 anyway). **Remaining suspects (narrowed):** (1) a **lock** — the 14 `cmk remember` writes + the SessionEnd writes contending in `lock-discipline.mjs` / `.locks/`; (2) the **better-sqlite3 reindex** blocking on a locked/large index DB during the per-bullet `writeFact`→`reindex` loop; (3) `autoPersona` making a real (slow but valid) `claude --print` pass over the 14-fact corpus. **NEXT: add a per-stage timing/log to `runSessionEndTasks` (or run compress/persona/graduation in isolation on the repro) to see which of the three actually blocks; the zero-stderr means it never reached `summarizeSessionEnd`.** Other deterministic checks PASSED: G2/G3/G4, B5, C3 (poison exit 2, 0 leak), C4 (0 username leak, ~ shown), F-3b persona export/import (exit 0, 0 leak). _Relates Task 94.3 (proactive sweep), design §8.5 (inner-timeout/kill-chain composition), PR-A (the same class), the v0.2.0 gate._

- **FIX / RESOLVED (2026-06-06) — root cause was the bin BLOCKING ON STDIN, not graduation/Haiku/lock/memsearch. All four earlier theories were wrong because they assumed the bin's BODY ran — it never did.** `cmk-compress-session.mjs` (both twin bins) drains stdin via `readFileSync(0, 'utf8')` at the very top (then `void`s it — the content is discarded; the read only exists to drain the hook pipe). When the bin is invoked MANUALLY without redirecting stdin — exactly what the B7 probe does (`cmk-compress-session | Out-Null` pipes stdout but leaves stdin on the interactive console, which never sends EOF) — `readFileSync(0)` blocks forever, before compress/persona/graduation ever run. The 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling then kills it → **exit 124, MEMORY unchanged, 0 graduated events, ZERO stderr** (it never reached `summarizeSessionEnd` because it never reached ANY of the body). In the REAL hook this never happens: Claude Code pipes the hook JSON to stdin → `readFileSync(0)` gets EOF → returns instantly (this is why "empty project = fast" — those runs had stdin fed). **Decisive evidence:** (a) repro of the full SessionEnd pipeline against repo source with per-stage timing = **47ms total** (compress skip/empty, persona skip/no-transcript, graduation 5 graduated in 39ms) — NO hang; (b) the installed global bin with stdin=`/dev/null` (EOF) → exit 0, full output, ~0ms; with stdin=a pipe that never EOFs → **exit 124** (blocked). The maintainer was right the install is NOT stale (uninstall+reinstall from main); the staleness theory (a 5th) was also wrong. **FIX:** (1) extract the stdin drain into a testable `readHookStdin({ isTTY })` helper that returns `''` when stdin is a TTY (interactive) instead of blocking; both twin bins call it — a manual run now degrades gracefully. (2) cut-gate B7 probe feeds stdin (`'{}' | cmk-compress-session`). **LESSON:** four theories chased the code I was READING; none reproduced first. The reproduce-with-instrumentation step (47ms) falsified all of them in one shot and pointed at the bin wrapper — which I'd skimmed past because `void rawInput` made the read look inert. _The v0.2.0 gate is now UNBLOCKED pending the helper PR._

Findings → fixes: (1) **search-id vs fact-id wart** — `cmk search` lists ids for BOTH facts AND scratchpad bullets, but `lessons promote`/`forget` act on facts only → a pasted bullet id gave a flat "no matching fact". **Fixed (Task 102, PR #124):** `bullet-lookup.mjs` + actionable errors. (2) **cut-gate doc drift** — the guide listed v0.1.x stubs (`cmk view`, bare `cmk compress`, `cmk purge --hard`, `cmk config get/set`) as runnable, omitted `forget --yes`, and showed `transcripts extract <file>` (it takes 0 args and crawls the WHOLE `~/.claude/projects` history — many MB). **Fixed (docs commit `1bae70f`):** stubs marked "expect not-yet-implemented", `--yes` added, F-15 0-arg scope flagged. **NOT fixed (intentional):** the stubs themselves stay v0.1.x deferrals (design §16); `transcripts extract`'s whole-history crawl is the feature, now documented.
