- **D-68 DECISION — test logging is ALWAYS ON: every vitest run (stress + standalone) writes a json result file; the old opt-in stdout-tee capture stays as a DEEP opt-in. SETTLED (2026-06-05, the user: "from now on all tests will have logging… logging written down to file").** Trigger: the Task 92 stress gate hit a 4/5 whose FAILING run predated logging (FAST mode discarded output), so the failing test was unidentifiable — exactly the cross-session-amnesia failure the kit fights, applied to our own gate. **Decision:** (1) `scripts/stress-test.mjs` now ALWAYS writes a per-run vitest json result to `.stress-logs/<stamp>_run-N.json` and, on failure, parses it to PRINT the failing test names; (2) `vitest.config.js` gained a `json` reporter (`outputFile` at `test.outputFile.json` so the CLI per-run override wins) → standalone `npm test`/`test:file` always log to `.test-logs/last-run.json`; (3) both dirs gitignored. **Why this doesn't re-introduce the old problem:** the previous capture mode was OPT-IN precisely because it tee'd stdout through `bash`, forcing vitest non-TTY → verbose reporter → ~2x slower, which MANUFACTURED new timing flakes (PR #45 / fix-stress-os-level-tee). The json reporter is a **side channel** — it writes a result file without changing console output, TTY detection, or test timing — so it's safe always-on. `CMK_STRESS_LOG=1` survives as the DEEP opt-in that additionally tees full stdout (for hard crashes / prerun failures the json can't capture). Verified end-to-end: 5 per-run json files land per stress run; standalone runs land the config file; the CLI `--outputFile.json` override beats the config default. Stress 5/5 under the new regime. _Relates the stress-gate rule (CLAUDE.md "Workflow"), D-55 (the kit's whole reason: don't lose state)._
- **D-67 FIX — Task 92 (G6) shipped: LOW-trust auto-extract drops now leave a recoverable trace in extract.log; the diagnostic log is gitignored to keep the raw excerpt out of git. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-92-low-trust-trace).** Auto-extract LOW (and assistant-demoted-to-`discarded`) candidates were dropped with no content record — only a `nothing_durable` COUNT — so a fact Haiku mis-graded LOW vanished with no auditable trace (the §6.5 "don't lose without trace" principle had a hole at the capture edge: MEDIUM got a review queue, LOW got nothing). Fix: the routing-loop else branch ([auto-extract.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/auto-extract.mjs)) writes one `low_trust_discarded` NDJSON entry per drop (excerpt capped 200 chars + reason + trust + `demoted_from` + origin), Door 4. **Log-only by decision** — NOT routed to the review queue (would flood it with low-signal noise; MEDIUM→review stays the "needs human" path). Fires inside the loop so it lands in both the all-low `skipped` branch and the mixed `extracted` branch. **The load-bearing finding (security composition, caught in self-review):** the new entry writes a RAW, un-Poison-Guarded excerpt — and the scaffolded `.gitignore.fragment` ignored `context.local/` + `.index/` + `.locks/` but NOT `context/sessions/*.extract.log`, so in a user's project the extract.log is **committed**. Today harmless (counts only); the excerpt change would make it an F1-class leak (a dropped secret reaching git). Fixed by gitignoring the extract.log (it's local diagnostic, same class as the `.locks/` logs), with a cli-install assertion locking it. **Verified vs ADR-0010** (read-before-flagging): the broader raw-`transcripts/{date}.md` committed surface is a *separately decided + accepted* tradeoff (mitigated by `<private>` stripping + Poison_Guard-at-write + documented awareness), so not re-opened here; the excerpt is a subset of that already-accepted content and the fix adds no second committed copy. **Two-pass review** confirmed (b) the else branch catches both `low` + double-demoted `discarded`, (c) `<retain>` force-promotes before routing so it's never mis-traced, (e) no over-mutation of the HIGH/MEDIUM path. Full suite 1422 green. _Relates G6, §6.5 (trace principle), Task 91.2 (the eviction-edge analog this mirrors at the capture edge), ADR-0010 (transcript posture), D-55 (lifecycle map)._
- **D-66 FIX — Task 93 (= 94.4) shipped: inject eviction is now IMPORTANCE-aware (lowest-value section first), not tail-order. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-93-importance-aware-inject).** The inject-selection half of the §19 architecture (G7 from the lifecycle map). When a tier exceeds its per-tier byte budget at SessionStart, `truncateTierToBudget` ([inject-context.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/inject-context.mjs)) used to drop whole `## ` sections **from the tail** (file order) — so which facts reached the context window depended on section ORDER, not trust/recency; a high-value fact in a late section could be dropped while a lower-value early section survived. Now it ranks sections by **aggregate value** (MAX bullet trust per section → newest `at` → later-in-file tiebreak) and drops the lowest first. The value map (`collectBulletValues`) is parsed from the **RAW** bodies before `cleanScratchpadBody` strips provenance; truncation then resolves ids on the cleaned block (bullet `(P-..)` ids survive cleaning). **The load-bearing design choice:** the later-in-file tiebreak makes this a **strict generalization** of the legacy tail-drop — when no provenance is present every section ranks equal and it drops from the end exactly as before, so **all 32 pre-existing inject tests pass unchanged** (no behavior change on the id-less path; importance-order only engages when provenance exists). **Granularity (accepted approximation):** eviction is section-granular (per §7.1.1 + the task's "whole sections by aggregate value" sanction), so a low-trust bullet bundled with a high-trust one survives over a standalone medium section — a bullet-level inversion, asymmetric with §19.2 graduation's per-bullet oldest-first. Locked as intentional by a mixed-section test; bullet-granular is the v-next stricter option. **Two-pass review:** skill-pass confirmed the strict-generalization claim, flagged the section-granularity limitation (documented in code + design §19.3) + the orphaned-valueById-entries question (inert — lookups only hit present lines, commented), and surfaced an out-of-scope **follow-up**: the total-cap fallback (Step 2 of `enforceCap`, fires only when Σ budgets > cap) still drops whole tiers from the priority tail (persona FIRST) — filed as a v-next importance-aware candidate in design §19.3. Door 4: the `tier_truncated_to_budget` event now carries `strategy: 'importance-ordered'` + `dropped_sections`. Full suite 1420 green. **Closes 94.4; Task 94 remaining: only 94.5 (live cold-open re-test, the user's outward action).** _Relates D-61/D-65 (the §19 architecture), G7 (lifecycle map), §7.1.1 (per-tier budgets), the wedge cold-open (US-2)._
- **D-65 FIX — Task 94.3 shipped: graduation now also runs PROACTIVELY at SessionEnd, not only reactively-at-write. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-94.3-proactive-graduation).** The reactive relief inside `appendScratchpadBullet` only fires when a write pushes a scratchpad over cap. That misses two cross-session cases: (1) a file that drifts over its load-cap between sessions with no new write, (2) low/medium bullets that AGE past the 14-day stale window while idle. New `graduateAllScratchpads()` ([graduate-session.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/graduate-session.mjs)) sweeps all fact-bearing scratchpads (P: MEMORY.md/SOUL.md; U: USER/HABITS/LESSONS; L excluded — machine config isn't durable facts) via a new `sweepScratchpadForCapRelief()` export in scratchpad.mjs that runs the SAME relief as append (consolidate stale-drop+archive → graduate high-trust overflow), but only when over cap and writing back ONLY if content changed (over-mutation safe, no churn). **Composition (the load-bearing decision):** wired into `runSessionEndTasks` **sequentially AFTER** the concurrent `allSettled([compress, persona])` block — because autoPersona WRITES the user-tier persona scratchpads and graduation READS+rewrites them, so running it as a third concurrent task would race (the §6.8/§7.1 disjoint-input rule). After `allSettled` resolves, autoPersona's writes are complete → no window. It's local file I/O (no spawn/network), best-effort (SessionEnd exits 0 on overrun), so it doesn't threaten the 60s hook ceiling on top of the ~50s Haiku block. **Why net-positive even pre-recall (Task 75):** an over-cap persona would otherwise be SILENTLY tail-dropped by the inject layer at SessionStart (G7/Task 93); graduation is strictly better — oldest-first, archived, audited, dedup'd, recoverable + searchable. **Two-pass review:** skill-pass surfaced (a) the consolidate-inside-sweep wasn't tier-gated (only safe because the caller filters L → added a `tier !== P && tier !== U` guard for defense-in-depth), (b) the "<<1s" cost comment understated the reindex-per-graduated-bullet cost (tempered + justified vs. the accepted reactive cost). Full suite 1416 green. **Closes 94.3; Task 94 remaining: 94.4 (= Task 93 importance-aware inject) + 94.5 (live cold-open re-test).** _Relates D-61 (architecture), D-63 (94 core), Task 91 (mechanism), Task 93/G7 (inject-side selection), Task 75 (recall, v0.3)._

- **D-61 DECISION (ARCHITECTURE, binding) — memory is LOAD-cap not WRITE-cap + overflow GRADUATES to the searchable store + Claude RECALLS it, across ALL tiers/files. Invariant: never lose memory; always retrievable. SETTLED (2026-06-04, the user).** The user's directive: *"we definitely need to do 'load-cap not write-cap' but memory needs to move somewhere when it overflows, and then our mechanism moves it somewhere else and Claude knows to search for it, this needs to be in all files, so we wouldn't lose memory, because the whole point of this kit is memory retention and the ability to retrieve it when needed."* **The model (= Anthropic's own, generalized to all tiers — D-60):** (1) **Load-cap, not write-cap** — writes ALWAYS succeed (files grow on disk); the cap governs only how much is INJECTED, never whether you can save. The `cap_exceeded` write-reject path is DELETED. No write-lock, ever, anywhere. (2) **Overflow graduates** — content beyond the injected window moves into the searchable fact store (Task 91's mechanism, generalized). (3) **Recall** — Claude searches for graduated memory when needed. (4) **ALL files/tiers** — MEMORY.md, USER/HABITS/LESSONS, SOUL — not just project MEMORY.md. **This supersedes D-57's "defer user-tier graduation" and extends Task 91 (project-only) to universal.** **Honest two-half split (binding on the roadmap):** the STORAGE half (load-cap + graduate-everywhere + never-reject) is deterministic + buildable now and ALONE satisfies the "never lose memory" invariant (everything stays on disk + searchable); the RETRIEVAL half ("Claude knows to search") is the ~50/50 active-recall problem (Task 75) and is v0.3 — until it lands, graduated memory is on-disk-searchable but not always auto-recalled. Pairs with G7/Task 93 (importance-aware inject → keep the BEST in the window, graduate the long tail → minimizes the recall dependency). **LANE DECISION (the user lost/overwhelmed, asked for a recommendation; accepted direction): do NOT cut a hollow v0.2.0 the maintainer won't use.** The user 2026-06-04: *"this is not a good product right now for my or my friends use… I will continue to do all the tasks until we have everything this kit promises."* So: **build this architecture next (bounded — extends working Task 91), then the v0.3 recall lane (75/84/80c); tag v0.2.0 when the architecture lands as a real milestone (no write-lock anywhere, zero loss), but the FRIEND-HANDOFF bar is the recall-lane finish, not the tag.** The path to friend-ready is FINITE: ~1 architecture task + ~3-4 recall tasks. **Process: design-section in `design.md` first (preserve the old write-cap design beside it per decision-trail), reviewed, THEN TDD build.** _Relates D-60 (cap research + spectrum), D-57 (superseded: user-tier graduation no longer deferred), Task 91 (mechanism to generalize), Task 75 (recall, v0.3), Task 93/G7 (importance-aware inject), D-24/D-25 (the friend bar reframed: friend-ready = post-recall-lane, not v0.2.0)._

- **D-57 DECISION — v0.2.0 scope LOCKED: fix the write-lock with a minimal graduation safety valve, ship, move on. In-project heavy-session recall is explicitly v0.3. SETTLED (2026-06-04, the user: "lets just fix v0.2.0 enough, ship it, and move forward, my friend can wait for v0.3.0 or even later").** Resolves the graduation-vs-recall coupling surfaced this session. **The coupling (so it's not re-derived):** MEMORY.md is byte-capped because it's *injected whole* into context (finite budget ≈ 12 facts / P-tier 4300B). So the moment a user works hard enough to exceed the inject window — an hour or two of intense Claude Code — the overflow MUST be found by search/recall, wherever it lives. Graduation moves *where* the overflow sits; it does not remove the need to recall it. **80c filed** — the DETERMINISTIC half the template already promises (`Environment Notes — "picks these up from PostToolUse hook events"`): observe-edit detects concrete config from tool I/O (ports from run commands, versions from install output, paths, URLs, env vars) and routes to Environment Notes **independent of Haiku's judgment**, with 80b's prompt nudge kept as best-effort complement. **Lane:** v0.2.x, but a CONDITIONAL cut-blocker — if §5 R3-quality fumbles port-8000 recall in the manual run, 80c pulls into v0.2.0 (Task 80's own severity clause: "if recall fumbles, it's fix-before-cut"). **Lesson (checkpoint-verification, again):** a prompt-only fix marked done while the gap reproduces is the exact trap — an LLM instruction isn't "done" until the behavior is reliable; deterministic mechanisms beat asking the classifier nicely. _Relates lifecycle-map G8 (config under-capture compounds the 7-day session-loss), D-36 (80b generality), D-47 (the status-audit discipline), Task 78 (the sibling prompt-tuning that DID work because promotion is gated, not LLM-judged)._
- **D-55 NOTE — the memory-lifecycle map: a systematic intent-vs-code audit of every edge, turning the one-at-a-time cut-gate findings into one complete list. SETTLED (2026-06-04).** The user, after the 4th silent-loss finding in a row: *"are there any more like this? i am starting to think we need a map of the code/logic."* Right instinct — the findings are one CLASS (*a designed invariant the code doesn't enforce → silent loss / duplication / blocked write at a composition boundary*), not isolated bugs. Built [`specs/memory-lifecycle-map.md`](../../specs/memory-lifecycle-map.md) (Zone-1 Spine support) by reading the code at **15 lifecycle edges** (capture→route, explicit capture, MEMORY.md append/consolidate/graduation/supersede, fact store, index, inject, the sessions pipeline, queues, tombstone, user tier), pinning design intent against code reality per edge. **10 gaps catalogued (G1-G10):** G1-G3 already filed under Task 91; G4 (high-trust supersede just-appends — design line 1956 "drops by AGE not VALIDITY") + G5 (literal canonical-ID dedup misses rewordings) → F-D/§16.18; G8 (session >7d lossy-Haiku into 4KB archive + source today-file UNLINKED → a durable fact never extracted is gone from active memory after 7d, recoverable only via manual `cmk transcripts extract`) → relates Task 80/84; G10 (fact store + queues unbounded, disk-only) → v0.2.x. **THREE surfaced only by walking every edge:** **G9 — verified NOT a gap** (looked like "consolidate() removes a bullet but doesn't reindex → stale search hit", but [subcommands.mjs:268-286](../../packages/cli/src/subcommands.mjs) runs `reindexBoot` mtime+sha1-diff BEFORE every `cmk search`/`mk_search` query → self-heals; the authors already knew + compensated — check-the-code again). **G6 — LOW-trust drops leave no trace** (discarded with only a count, not the content; §6.5 trace-principle applied to the capture edge) → **Task 92** (log excerpt to extract.log; v0.2.x). **G7 — inject drop is tail-order, not importance** (`truncateTierToBudget` drops whole `## ` sections from the file tail, so what reaches the window depends on section ORDER not trust/recency; can drop a high-value late section while keeping a low-value early one) → **Task 93** (value-ordered eviction, never drop high-trust before low-trust; v0.2.x). **The map's payoff (and why it's Spine, not history):** its "how to use" rule — before adding a lifecycle invariant, check the rows it COMPOSES with — is exactly the composition-verification discipline; graduation (Task 91, edge #5) composes with consolidate/append-dedup/fact-store/index, and the map names those edges so the build respects them. **Sound half (not all red):** explicit `forget` tombstones correctly (the contrast that flags consolidate()'s hard-delete), transcripts are a verbatim never-pruned backstop (nothing truly unrecoverable), fact-file dedup+reindex-on-write is consistent, inject/session caps compose. _Relates D-54 (G1/graduation), Task 91/92/93, F-D, Task 80/84, D-38 (the index-consistency class G9 belongs to). Verification status: read from code 2026-06-04._
- **D-54 ISSUE+DECISION — MEMORY.md "graduation" (the 3rd shrink mechanism) is NOT implemented → the hot index write-locks; this is a v0.2.0 BLOCKER (Decision A). Filed as Task 91. SETTLED (2026-06-04, cut-gate run, code-verified).** Surfaced while investigating the cut-gate double-capture (.venv + architecture each exist BOTH as a `cmk remember` fact file AND an auto-extract MEMORY.md bullet). The design intent — stated in THREE places ([design.md §987](../../specs/design.md), [2026-06-01 lifecycle research](../research/2026-06-01-memory-lifecycle-and-competitive-position.md) lines 56+60, chatgpt-design.md) — is that **MEMORY.md is a small HOT INDEX kept bounded by THREE mechanisms: (1) byte cap, (2) stale-drop >14d, (3) GRADUATION — durable facts move OUT into granular `context/memory/*.md` fact files (the permanent brain).** **Code reality (verified, not inferred):** the kit ships (1) + (2) only. `scratchpad.mjs::consolidate()` does stale-drop (low/medium bullets >14d, hard-deleted) — `grep graduat` returns ZERO source hits; `daily-distill` touches only the sessions pipeline (`today-*.md→recent.md`), never MEMORY.md→fact-files. **Graduation, the drain, is unbuilt.** **Consequence (quantified from the live run):** cut-gate `context/MEMORY.md` = **2059 bytes after ONE session** (cap 2500, consolidation trigger 2375), all **6 bullets `trust: high`** → `consolidate()` is forbidden from dropping high-trust (line 227 `if (prov.trust==='high') continue`) → frees nothing → ~1 more session pushes past cap → next high-trust write returns `CAP_EXCEEDED` (no silent truncation) → **the kit silently stops remembering.** For a kit whose identity is "fixes per-session amnesia," project memory that write-locks after ~2 sessions is a core-promise failure. **This is the single root cause beneath BOTH cut-gate findings:** the double-capture (graduation would move the bullet INTO a fact file and dedup against the existing one) AND the cap-lock (graduation is the missing exit for high-trust facts). **Secondary gap noted (same investigation):** `consolidate()` HARD-DELETES low/medium stale bullets with no tombstone — inconsistent with `cmk forget`'s tombstone-don't-delete principle (§6.5); graduation/eviction should archive, not vanish. **DECISION A (the user, 2026-06-04):** BLOCKER — build graduation before the `v0.2.0` tag; NO stopgap (raising the cap is the band-aid the user rejected before; "is a stop gap, not a fix"). The wedge (cross-project cold-open) ships on the SEPARATE user-tier promotion path and works, but the project tier cannot ship with a 2-session write-lock. **Filed as Task 91** (v0.2.0 BLOCKERS section). **Meta-lesson (check-the-code, fired again):** I first wrote that consolidation "drops bullets to stay under cap" with "no way to know real vs duplicate" — WRONG; reading `consolidate()` showed it's selective (high-trust + <14d are never dropped). The user's instinct ("doesn't it move memory out?") was right — graduation IS the designed behavior; they only had the destination wrong (fact files, not `memory-<date>.md`; dated files are the episodic session diary, a separate track). _Relates D-53 (cut-gate run), the duplicate finding; design §7.1/§987, §6.5; F-D (fact-layer auto-supersede shares the machinery)._

SETTLED (2026-06-04, committed 2adc861 + efb21aa + 036d294).** Trigger: the user pushed back that `live-verify` (wedge-only, shimmed DEV bins) "isn't a real verify of the actual workflow" — it never exercised Task 69's skill path and tested dev source, not the artifact. [`scripts/live-test.mjs`](../../scripts/live-test.mjs) is the scripted equivalent of [`docs/process/v0.2.0-self-test-guide.md`](../process/v0.2.0-self-test-guide.md): installs the **REAL packaged tarball** into an isolated global prefix (`npm install -g --prefix`, never touches the user's global cmk), then drives `claude -p` through the whole flow asserting **files AND tool-use at every stage** — install + `cmk doctor` 0-fail + reads every scaffolded file (safe skill, slim CLAUDE.md, hooks+allowlist, no leak); SESSION-1 staged build where the agent ACTUALLY builds + per-stage artifact checks; explicit `cmk` probes (terse/rich/Poison_Guard-reject+no-write/home-path-sanitize); skill-path safety via **tool-use inspection** (no hand-edit of memory, no leak, audited); SESSION-2 recall (tool-use proves memory vs code-read); SESSION-3 cold-open (reads built files). **Two findings the automation surfaced (the value of repeatable runs):** (a) **`--permission-mode acceptEdits` is NOT honored when `claude -p` is driven through node `spawnSync({shell:true})` on Windows** — writes fall back to interactive approval → silently denied → the agent "describes" builds instead of doing them (early runs showed "scaffold-only, no source"). **`--dangerously-skip-permissions` IS honored** (safe in the isolated sandbox). Verified via a focused probe, not a guess. (b) **In-project recall is ~50/50** — one run answered "what are my rules" from the injected persona with 0 tool calls, the next globbed the code — **the known Task-75 / D-35 active-recall gap reproduced** (passive injection isn't a reliable trigger; reading code for IN-code facts is fine per D-40, but re-deriving NOT-in-code preferences from code is the miss). So D1/D2 recall are classified as **non-gating PROBES** (reported, not failing the suite — the gate is the shipped deterministic capabilities; the gap is tracked as Task 75, deferred to v0.3). The **cold-open wedge passed every run.** Findings are a **timestamped per-run trail** at [`docs/journey/live-test-runs/`](live-test-runs/) (a subdir the doc-registry validator scans non-recursively, so per-run files need no registration) so run-to-run drift (like the recall variance) is visible across runs. On-demand, real tokens, NOT in `npm test`. _Relates D-45 (Task 89 feasibility), D-35/D-40 (recall), Task 69 (verified end-to-end on the real artifact)._

- **D-46 DECISION — Task 87 (compression input): capture-turn APPENDS the conversation to now.md, chosen over an offset-based transcript-read. SETTLED (2026-06-03, shipped PR #108).** The SessionEnd compression buffer `now.md` was fed ONLY by observe-edit's file-write lines (`[ts] Write file=X lines=N`), so the compressor summarized filenames and hallucinated content the dialogue never contained (live-test-6: "Flask app: app.py"). **Two designs were on the table:** **(A, chosen) capture-turn appends the turn's conversation to now.md** — keeps compress-session's existing read→truncate buffer contract intact; the dialogue now dominates the summary so the hallucination dies at the root (a framework can no longer be inferred from a lone filename); now.md is truncated per compress so it stays a transient buffer, not a second store. **(B, deferred) offset-based transcript-read** — compress the new transcript span since a stored byte-offset, making the transcript the single source and dropping now.md's role. (B) is architecturally cleaner but needs offset tracking + touches observe-edit/daily-distill; (A) is the smaller, lower-risk change for the cut. **Decision-trail:** (B) stays the v0.2.x escalation if mega-sessions bloat now.md. **Skill-review I1 (fixed inline):** compress returns on cooldown BEFORE truncating now.md, and auto-extract refreshes the shared cooldown every turn, so during an active session now.md is NOT truncated and accumulates; appending full turns (vs the old short file-write line) can bloat it — so the per-turn ASSISTANT contribution is capped (4000 chars + marker); the USER turn stays FULL (it carries the standing rules we must not truncate). Both turns are privacy-sanitized upstream. **Verified:** suite 1372, stress 5/5, and live-verify confirmed now.md carries the conversation + the compressed summary is grounded in the dialogue with no hallucinated framework; the wedge stayed 2/2+2/2. Follow-up noted: observe-edit's file-write lines in now.md are now redundant (dialogue + the 84a grounding rule neutralize them) — dropping that write is a separate hook-removal.
- **D-41 DECISION — Task 86 fix: persona promotion must be a DEDICATED, FREQUENT pass (detached at SessionEnd over the clean fact list), NOT an overloaded per-turn extraction call. SETTLED (2026-06-03, primary-source-verified).** The prompt tweak (require per-fact emission; branch `task-86-multi-rule-promote`, f4f0976) is **necessary-but-insufficient** — live-verified: a CLEAN all-rules turn promotes 3/3, but the REALISTIC MIXED turn (rules stated while building) still emits **0 in 2 of 3 runs**. Root cause is structural, not wording: one Haiku call can't reliably do extraction AND persona classification when the turn is busy. **Primary source (cloned NousResearch/hermes-agent, read the source — The user: "clone the product and search how they do it"):** Hermes runs a **dedicated forked review** (`background_review.py`, memory-tools-only) on a **nudge interval of ~10 turns** (`agent_init.py:1067` `_memory_nudge_interval=10`; gated `conversation_loop.py:519`), with a **persona-focused single-purpose prompt** ("has the user revealed preferences / work-style / expectations?"). memsearch corroborates (dedicated `claude -p` per turn). **None overload one call; all run the dedicated pass frequently.** Our kit HAS the right-shaped tool — `auto-persona.mjs` `buildClassifierInstructions` (focused classifier over the CLEAN accumulated fact list via `listObservationSources`, immune to the busy-turn problem) — but only fires **manually** (`cmk persona generate`) or **weekly** (`weekly-curate`), which the user flagged ("not good"). **Fix:** wire a **detached `autoPersona` run at SessionEnd** (the SessionEnd hook = `cmk-compress-session`; spawn detached to dodge the 60s ceiling + cooldown contention). SessionEnd (not SessionStart) because the persona must fill from project-A's facts BEFORE cold-opening project-B — A's session end, not A's next start (which lags a session). Keep the inline emission as a best-effort fast-path. **Lesson (two-pass + lazy-framing caught this):** the clean-turn 3/3 demo + the tautological prompt-content test gave FALSE "fixed" confidence; the skill-review's "verify the mixed case" + the user's "are you sure about the Minor?" exposed it. Full primary-source note: [2026-06-03-hermes-dedicated-review-primary-source.md](../research/2026-06-03-hermes-dedicated-review-primary-source.md). Implementation pending (TDD + two-pass); re-verify on mixed-turn → cold-open (live-test-9).
- **D-45 FINDING — the live wedge test is SCRIPTABLE: `claude -p` fires the kit's SessionStart / Stop / SessionEnd hooks, so live-test-N can be automated (→ Task 89). VERIFIED 2026-06-03 (the user's idea + empirical probe).** The user: "why can't you run interactive Claude sessions on my machine? … why can't we make a script that is exactly like the live tests I do manually?" (ref: the Ralph Wiggum loop article — `claude -c -p` drives Claude Code headlessly; [CLI reference](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/cli-reference)). **CLI evidence:** `--bare` exists to *skip* hook auto-discovery (so normal `-p` runs hooks); `--include-hook-events` streams hook lifecycle; `--init-only` runs Setup+SessionStart then exits; `--session-id`/`--continue` give multi-turn; `--settings`/`--output-format json` allow scripted config + parseable answers. **Empirical probe (the decisive check, not training):** `cmk install` into a temp project, ran `claude -p "Reply with the word hello"` with `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR` isolated → disk side-effects proved ALL THREE load-bearing hooks fired: `transcripts/{date}.md` captured the turn **verbatim** (Stop/capture-turn), `sessions/{date}.compress.log` `scope:"session-end"` (SessionEnd/compress), user-tier scratchpads scaffolded (SessionStart/inject). Isolation via `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR` worked (no pollution of the real tier). **Implication:** the full wedge loop — capture→promote (project-A `claude -p` stating rules) → cold-open recall (project-B `claude -p` asking for the rules, parse the JSON answer) — is fully automatable as `npm run live-verify`. Unblocks me running live-test-9 myself AND becomes a permanent wedge regression test. **Caveat for the REAL test:** the probe used the GLOBAL published `cmk`; the harness must install the DEV build (npm pack → install tarball, or npm link) to exercise 86b/86c. Costs real tokens per run → on-demand script, NOT in default `npm test`. Output-styles (also flagged by the user) NOT needed — formatting only, irrelevant to hook-driven memory. Filed as Task 89.
- **D-44 FINDING — the SessionEnd persona classifier must read the RAW TRANSCRIPT, not the distilled fact corpus. The wedge's real second-stage gap. (2026-06-03, primary-source-verified: hermes + claude-mem; the user: "check the code in other products.")** Investigating the 86b watch-item (the dedicated classifier emits all candidates but graded them medium→queued, promoting 0) traced to the **input**, not the classifier. `autoPersona` classifies over `assembleProjectCorpus` = the **distilled fact files** (`context/memory/*.md`, title+body only). But auto-extract distills a user's *universal* rule into *project-scoped* text: the real live-test-8 `uv` fact body reads "Use uv … **pip is not used in this project**" and the venv fact reads "**For Python projects**, always create a local .venv" — the cross-project signal ("from now on", "in every project") is GONE, and `assembleProjectCorpus` also **discards the frontmatter** (`trust:high` + `write_source:user-explicit` — which already encode "explicitly-stated rule"). So the classifier re-grades from degraded input and correctly declines to promote a fact that says "in this project." **The raw signal is intact in the transcript:** `transcripts/2026-06-03.md` carries the verbatim user turn "i want that **from now on** create .venv" — "from now on" is exactly the high-confidence marker. **Primary source (the user's "check other products"):** (1) **hermes** `agent/background_review.py` `_MEMORY_REVIEW_PROMPT` = *"Review the **conversation above** … Has the user **revealed** … preferences …"* — it forks an agent over the RAW conversation snapshot, never over distilled memory; (2) **claude-mem** `cli/handlers/summarize.ts` reads from `transcriptPath` (`extractLastMessage(transcriptPath, …)`) — the RAW transcript. **Both mature products classify over the raw conversation; NONE classify over already-distilled facts.** Our 86b copied the right *pattern* (frequent dedicated single-purpose pass — D-41) but fed it the wrong *input*. **Same root as Task 87** (compress reads file-write logs, not the conversation) — the kit's secondary passes keep reading degraded derivatives instead of `transcripts/{date}.md`. **Fix (Task 86c):** `autoPersona` classifies over the recent transcript window (bounded, like hermes' "snapshot" / claude-mem's last-message), where universal-scope phrasing survives — not (only) the fact corpus. The 86b concurrency infrastructure (session-end-tasks.mjs) is correct and stays; only autoPersona's input source changes. **This is why 86 is NOT done at 86b** — without 86c the SessionEnd pass queues instead of promotes, so the cold-open still won't inherit the rules. Reframes the parent-checkbox gate: live-test-9 will PASS only after 86c.
- **D-43 ISSUE — the Haiku-compressor sandbox uses the WRONG CLI flag: `--allowed-tools ''` (an auto-approve allowlist) instead of `--tools ''` (the actual disable-all). FILED as Task 88 (2026-06-03, primary-source-verified against the CLI reference).** Checking [code.claude.com/docs/en/cli-reference](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/cli-reference) (the user pointed me there): `--allowedTools` = *"Tools that execute **without prompting** for permission … to restrict which tools are **available**, use `--tools` instead"*; `--tools` = *"Restrict which built-in tools Claude can use. Use `""` to disable all."* Our [compressor.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/compressor.mjs) passes `--allowed-tools ''` with a comment claiming it makes "the tightest possible sandbox; the sub-Claude can only respond, not act" — but that flag is an **auto-approve allowlist** (empty = nothing auto-approved), NOT an availability restriction. The comment is factually wrong about the mechanism. **Honest severity: live exposure ≈ nil** — in `--print` + `--max-turns 1` there is no approver and the prompts only ask for text back, so a tool call can't actually execute; the real safety today comes from print-mode + max-turns, not from the flag. So this is **defense-in-depth + comment-accuracy, not an active vulnerability** (stated plainly to avoid the lazy-framing trap in either direction). **Fix (Task 88): use `--tools ''`** (the documented disable-all) so the sandbox matches its stated intent, and correct the comment. **Cross-cutting** — every Haiku call inherits this argv: compress-session, daily-distill, weekly-curate, auto-extract, auto-persona — so it gets its OWN focused PR with a spawn-smoke re-verification, NOT bundled into Task 86. (Casing note: docs spell it `--allowedTools`; the installed binary accepts the kebab `--allowed-tools` — the live spawn-smokes pass — so the casing isn't the bug; the flag CHOICE is.)
- **D-42 PIVOT — the SessionEnd persona pass runs CONCURRENTLY inside the hook, NOT detached as D-41 planned. SETTLED (2026-06-03).** D-41 settled "run the dedicated `autoPersona` classifier at SessionEnd"; the open question was HOW to fit a SECOND ~50s Haiku call into the 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling alongside `compressSession`'s own ~50s call. _Original plan (D-41, pre-2026-06-03): **detach** the autoPersona spawn so it outlives the hook and dodges the ceiling + the shared Haiku cooldown._ **Pivoted to: run both passes CONCURRENTLY inside the hook** (`Promise.allSettled`), each with its own backend instance, awaited before the hook returns. **Why concurrent-in-hook beats detached:** (1) a detached child re-introduces the **Task 81 Windows console-flash class** — the exact bug just fixed; (2) detached gives **no completion guarantee** before a cold-open in project-B (the whole point is A's persona is ready before B opens); (3) detached needs another bin + is hard to test. **Why it's safe to compose in-hook:** the two passes have **disjoint inputs/outputs** — `compressSession` reads `sessions/now.md` → writes `today-*.md`; `autoPersona` reads the `context/memory/` fact corpus (written per-turn by auto-extract, NOT by compress) → writes user-tier scratchpads; neither takes a lock the other needs — so overlapping them yields wall-clock `max(~50s) ≈ 50s` under the 60s ceiling. **The composition bug this fixes (self-review caught it):** the first 86b cut ran them **sequentially** → worst case `50+50=100s` > 60s ceiling → OS kills the hook mid-persona-write (half-written user-tier INDEX = HC-5 corruption, shared across every project) AND drops `{"continue": true}`. compressSession is correct alone (50<60), autoPersona is correct alone (50<60); only the SEQUENTIAL composition was broken — textbook "separately-correct-jointly-broken" (CLAUDE.md composition rule, instance #4 class). Extracted the orchestration to [session-end-tasks.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/session-end-tasks.mjs) (`runSessionEndTasks` + `summarizeSessionEnd`) — ONE testable place, no twin-bin drift; both bins thin-wrap it. `cooldownMs:0` on the persona call so the shared 120s cooldown the concurrent compress touches doesn't skip it. 11 orchestrator tests (deterministic concurrency proof via event-ordering, per-call backend isolation, allSettled isolation, summarizer). **Trigger: the user — "why not 2 threads instead of 1?"** Re-verify on mixed-turn → cold-open (live-test-9) still gates the parent Task 86 checkbox.
- **D-40 NOTE — recall reframe: the kit recalls DECISIONS/RATIONALE/PREFERENCES (not-in-code), and reading code for in-code facts is correct, not a failure. SETTLED (2026-06-03, live-test-8).** Two recall passes in live-test-8 gave opposite results, and the contrast is the lesson. **Pass 1 (factual/in-code: "which model? what version?")** → the agent **read the code** every time, even though the Gemini answer was in the injected snapshot. **Pass 2 (decision/why/preference: "why the reflection loop? my standing rules?")** → the agent **led with memory** (*"let me check the project memory before re-deriving anything"*), quoted the user's exact words from the transcript, listed all 8 rules from the fact files, and — crucially — when asked *why* the reflection loop, **refused to invent a rationale** (*"the reasoning wasn't discussed… that would be my inference, not something we established"*): anti-hallucination at the recall layer. **Conclusion:** for facts that live IN the code (model, version, entry point), a good agent reads the code — it's ground truth and can't go stale (and memory CAN go stale — see the F-D contradiction). The kit's recall value is the stuff NOT in code (decisions, why, cross-project preferences), and THAT works. Implication for testing: recall tests must ask not-in-code questions; "which model" is the wrong probe. Implication for the wow: if the goal is "it just KNOWS the facts too" (D-26), that needs the agent to LEAD with memory then verify — the current passive injection + D-35 instruction didn't override Claude's read-the-code default for in-code facts. Full write-up: [v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md](v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md) (2026-06-03 RE-TEST 3). Bugs filed: Task 86 (wedge multi-rule promote), Task 87 (now.md compression input = the real Task 84 root), Task 80 (capture gap, concretely), F-D (auto-supersede stale facts).
- **D-39 DECISION — the SonarCloud "Security Hotspots Reviewed" gate condition is ACCEPTED as a cosmetic red; not worth fixing. SETTLED (2026-06-03, the user).** The `SonarCloud Code Analysis` quality-gate check is `ERROR` solely on `new_security_hotspots_reviewed = 0% (< 100% required)`. The 27 hotspots are all **false-positives** on kit-internal trusted input: 19 "regex could be ReDoS" (regexes run only on the kit's *own generated* text — IDs, scratchpads, kit-written files — never attacker input), 2 sha1 (content *fingerprints* for provenance/dedup, not crypto), 6 `PATH` on `node`/`bash`/`launchctl` spawns of fixed trusted binaries. **Why we don't fix it:** (a) the check is **non-blocking** — it has never stopped a merge (all 6 Dependabot PRs merged red); real security is gated GREEN by **CodeQL (SAST) + gitleaks + osv-scanner + npm-audit**. (b) The clean fix (remove the condition via a custom gate) is **paywalled** — SonarCloud's Free plan refuses to assign a custom Quality Gate to a project; the built-in "Sonar way" is read-only. (c) Code-side alternatives rejected: **NOSONAR** on 27 lines = recurring source noise (the user dislikes the clutter); **dashboard hotspot review** = manual click-through that re-fails on every future regex PR. The **coverage** half of the same gate WAS fixed (`new_coverage` 77.9% → 82.2% via `tests/cli-subcommands-dispatch.test.js`, in-process handler coverage — that file stays). **Net:** treat the lone red SonarCloud check as known-cosmetic. Do NOT spend effort greening it (no NOSONAR sweep, no plan upgrade) unless SonarCloud changes its free-tier gate policy. If a future contributor sees the red, this is why.
- **D-38 BUG+FIX — INDEX.md consistency: HC-5 false-fail + capture leaving the index stale. FIXED (2026-06-03, Task 85).** live-test-7's first rich capture produced a persistent `cmk doctor` HC-5 FAIL that `cmk reindex` couldn't clear. The user: *"we reinstalled everything, so there shouldn't be a problem unless we made it, and running 'cmk reindex' is not a solution, cause users suppose to get it working from the start."* Two composing bugs: **(B)** HC-5's regex matched id-shaped filenames (`[PUL]-XXXXXXXX.md`) the kit never generates — real fact files are `<type>_<slug>.md` — so it flagged every real fact as missing; the HC-5 *test* had fixtured the unreal `P-AAAAAAAA.md`, enshrining the wrong contract and keeping CI green while production failed (test-genuinely-wrong: rewrote it to realistic naming). **(A)** `cmk remember`→`writeFact()` wrote the fact file but never refreshed INDEX.md. **Fix:** HC-5 matches the markdown link target `](type_slug.md)`; `writeFact()` calls `reindex()` after a successful create (the writer owns the derived index, best-effort since the fact is already durable). Works from the first capture, no manual step. **Lesson:** an unrealistic test fixture is worse than no test — it actively certifies a broken contract; fixtures must mirror what the code actually produces (it's the boundary-test discipline applied to filenames). Side effect noted: reindex replaces the rich scaffold INDEX guidance with the pointer list on first capture (the index's job; slim-header-preserve is a possible follow-up).
- **D-37 DECISION — Audit every LLM-facing guardrail by READING each file in full, never by grep-for-symptoms. SETTLED (2026-06-02, the user).** After D-36's two fixes (84 + 80), the user caught me still symptom-hunting: *"you are doing it again … why? you need to read all the files, see what in it, see what is written."* and earlier *"this Holistic crap, using grep, finding exact things, it not working for me."* **The principle:** grep can only find strings I think to search for, so it structurally cannot catch a scenario-assumption phrased a way I didn't predict — which is exactly how "code" survived three of my own edits (grep `re-read the code` missed `code inspection` and `this app's port`). **The method:** open every guardrail the kit sends to an LLM (or injects into Claude's context) and read it top-to-bottom. Locating-with-grep is still symptom-hunting — banned for this audit class. **The full comb (every prompt-builder + skill + template + MCP tool description read in full) found:**
  - **A new behavioral bug grep could never have surfaced: `weekly-curate.mjs` (`buildCurateInstructions`) had the SAME missing grounding rule as compress/distill** — a THIRD hallucination layer (→ `archive.md`). The live-test-6 Flask test only exercised the first two layers (it fires weekly), so symptom-search for "Flask" would never reach it. Fixed: same example-free grounding rule, mirrored across all three layers. Door-4 test added.
  - **Three more "code"/leaked-example domain assumptions** the `grep code` pass missed: auto-extract trigger #4 (`discovered through code inspection`), auto-extract persona line (`NOT … like a port number or file name`), auto-persona classifier (`IGNORE … this app's port, this repo's file names`). All neutralized to property-defined, domain-neutral phrasing.
  - **Clean on the domain axis (read + confirmed):** the shared `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE`, both SKILL.md (bootstrap, memory-write), all 6 MCP tool descriptions, SOUL/INDEX/machine-paths/overrides/journey-log scaffolds, all 4 plugin context-templates.
  - **Class B (cosmetic, flagged for the user's call, NOT auto-fixed):** the scaffold seed bullets (MEMORY/USER/HABITS/LESSONS) + the injected `cmk remember` worked examples are *uniformly* coding/git ("PR #142", "git push/reset --hard", "fix the code not the test", "FastAPI/Kamal"). They're illustrative placeholders the user replaces (don't change capture behavior), but a non-coding friend opening the scaffold sees "a tool for programmers." Decision deferred to the user — neutralize the examples vs. keep them (defensible for a Claude Code tool).
  - **Class C (consistency):** npm `template/` scaffolds carry seeded example bullets w/ provenance; plugin `context-template/` ones are bare — two scaffold sources drifted. Low priority.
  - All shipped on branch `task-84-compressor-grounding`; full suite 1334 green.
- **D-36 DECISION — Recall-cluster fixes must be GENERAL, not scenario-fit; "preserve framework/port/path verbatim" was rejected as over-fit. SETTLED (2026-06-02, the user).** The user caught the proposed Task 84 fix: *"Task 84 sounds like the wrong fix … 'preserve framework/port/path identifiers verbatim, never infer' … this will only work for that scenario … we are suppose to be working on a general solution, not one that will only work for this guide."* Then: *"please check now that you didnt just 'fixed' things by tiping the bowl! that makes all the tasks and this win in question."* **Audit run on the whole recall/cleanup cluster (76/78/79/80/81/82/83 + D-35):**
  - **Task 84 (proposed, not shipped) — over-fit, corrected.** Root cause confirmed: `buildCompressionInstructions` HARD RULES protect *citation IDs* (`never invent new IDs`) but have **NO faithfulness/grounding rule** — nothing forbids emitting content absent from the buffer, which is why Haiku invented "Flask". **General fix (replaces the whitelist):** one example-free HARD RULE — *every bullet must be grounded in the session buffer; do not infer or guess any fact not explicitly stated in the buffer; do not carry forward content from earlier summaries; if unsure, omit it.* No example categories — The user caught that naming "framework / port / path" even as examples anchors the model and leaks the scenario back in (*"you need to remove 'framework/library/tool names, file roles, ports'"*). Kills Flask AND every invented-fact class. tasks.md Task 84(a) rewritten.
  - **Task 80 — PARTIAL tip-the-bowl, filed as 80b.** The prompt change is defensibly general (names categories, not just one value), BUT the unit test is **tautological** (`toMatch(/port 8000/)` checks the literal example I typed) and the live win reused the SAME scenario (port 8000/FastAPI) — generality **asserted, not proven**. Filed 80b: assert the category instruction not the literal, and prove on a different config (port 3000 + Postgres).
  - **Tasks 81 / 79 / 83 / 82 / 76 / 78 — clean, structural, NOT scenario-fit.** 81 = `windowsHide` on spawn (general); 79 = `Bash(cmk:*)` allow-list (general); 83 = delete the Files-Touched section (kills the noise class for every project); 82 = template scrub (general); 76/78 = the promote code path (general). No over-fit smell.
  - **The principle (binding going forward):** a recall/quality fix that only resolves the *specific scenario in the live test* is a tip-the-bowl, not a fix. The fix must address the *class*. A test that asserts the literal example string I typed into a prompt is tautological — assert the *instruction/behavior category*, and prove generality on a DIFFERENT input than the one that surfaced the bug. This is the "did you check?" rule applied to my own fixes: convergence-on-one-scenario is not proof, same as convergence-on-one-source is not primary-source verification.
- **D-35 DECISION — Recall must be ACTIVE (agent consults memory on demand), not just PASSIVE injection. SETTLED (2026-06-02, the user).** live-test-5 Session-2 recall: Claude got the right answer ("port 8000, layered structure") but by **re-reading the code** (globbed `**/*.py`, read `config.py`), NOT from the injected snapshot — even though the snapshot WAS delivered (verified: 2116-char inject containing all 4 persona rules + project facts). The user: *"what i want is that not just inject the memory.md but he know to go and check it when needed."* **The model:** passive injection alone loses to code-reading because (a) the snapshot is bounded (can't hold the granular archive / old sessions), and (b) the model treats injected text as background, not a source to *query*. **Recall feels real only when the agent, on hitting "what did we decide / what's our X / how does the user work," GOES AND LOOKS IT UP** (`cmk search`, reads `context/memory/<id>.md`, checks the persona) instead of re-deriving. This is what every mature memory product does (D-29: Hermes `memory_tool`, memsearch CLI, gstack `/learn` — a tool + an instruction to query on demand). **The parts exist** (`cmk search`, the `context/memory/` archive + `INDEX.md`, MCP `mk_search`/`mk_get`, Tasks 75 recall-trigger + 69 recall-skill); **what's missing is the behavioral wiring:** (1) the injected `CLAUDE.md`/skill must instruct Claude *when to READ* memory ("recall a decision/config/preference → query it, don't re-derive from code") — today the block only covers how to *write*; (2) the snapshot becomes a hot index that POINTS to the queryable archive, not a dump that tries to be everything. **Reframes the recall work:** v0.2.0 = snapshot-quality (dedup the Files-Touched bloat — the snapshot was ~50% repeated `## Files Touched` noise burying the persona; Task 80 env capture) + the "go check memory" instruction; the auto-triggering recall skill + semantic search backend = 0.3.0. This is the wedge-completing half (capture B1–B4 is proven; this is recall).
- **D-34 NOTE — the WEDGE is verified working on real Haiku (live-test-5 B4, 2026-06-02).** The fresh re-test closed the D-30 auto-half gap end-to-end: a stated universal rule (*"always use a project-local .venv …"*) auto-promoted to `USER.md § Working Style` at **`trust: high` / `write: user-explicit`**, with **no command and no prompt** (`extract.log persona_promoted:1`). This is the thing Task 78 fixed — pre-Task-78 it queued at medium and never landed. F1 (rich capture) also confirmed. **Two follow-ups from the run:** (1) **Task 79** — `cmk install` should allow-list `Bash(cmk *)` so the agent's *explicit* `cmk remember`/`cmk lessons promote` don't trip Claude Code's per-command permission prompt (the auto path is already seamless via hooks). (2) the user-tier re-init fixed a stale `{{TODAY}}` from an old install (already-patched in current code; the old tier predated the fix). **Still open before the cut:** Session-2 recall (D1) + Session-3 cold-open (E1) — 78.4 not fully closed. Full write-up in [v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md](v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md) (2026-06-02 section).
- **D-33 FIX — vitest 2 → 4 bump (real fix for the Critical CVE), via a filter-as-bridge. SETTLED (2026-06-02).** osv-scanner flagged GHSA-5xrq-8626-4rwp (Critical) in `vitest` 2.1.9 — a dev-only test runner, never in the published package. Rather than override the gate or filter-and-defer (the "amortize later" pattern the user distrusts), the agreed path (the user 2026-06-02): add a *temporary* osv filter to unblock the wedge merge (#100), then take the real `vitest → 4.1.8` bump **immediately** (#101) and delete the filter. Done — `npm audit` 0 vulns; osv green with no filter. Two durable config consequences, both documented in `vitest.config.js`: (a) `testTimeout` 10s → 30s (vitest 4 has higher per-op overhead; heavy I/O + spawn tests need headroom; one 200-file test carries an explicit 120s budget); (b) coverage `branches` ratchet 70 → 69 — a **measurement re-baseline, NOT a regression**: vitest 4's v8 provider counts branches more granularly (AST-aware), so the same code reads ~69.3% vs ≥70% under v2; ONLY branches moved (lines/funcs/statements still 70), the tell that the ruler changed not the code. Do not "restore 70" without re-measuring under the current tool.
- **D-32 DECISION — 45.4 invariant refined to "latest explicit wins" for the explicit-high path. SETTLED (2026-06-02).** The original 45.4 — *an auto/medium promotion never overwrites a hand-curated `trust:high` rule* — was written (Task 45) when the auto path was always `medium`, so a same-topic collision was `medium < high → queue` and curated highs were safe from inferred noise. Task 76 (`cmk lessons promote`) + Task 78 (inline grading of an explicitly-stated rule) now write at `trust:high`, so a same-topic collision is `high ≥ high → supersede`: an explicit, user-attested rule **can** replace a hand-curated high. Surfaced by the Task-78 skill-review (B-INV). **the user chose "latest explicit wins"** over preserving 45.4 strictly — an explicitly-STATED rule is the newest user intent and should win; the residual risk (Haiku mis-grading a casual mention as `high` → clobbering a curated rule) is bounded by the sharpened `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE` (`high` = explicitly-stated only). **Refinement, not substitution:** the original protection is UNCHANGED for inferred/medium writes (still queue against a high); only an explicit `high` can replace a `high`. Documented in the `promoteCandidatesToUserTier` docstring (preserve-old + add-new per the decision-trail rule).
- **D-31 DECISION — Ship the wedge in two sequential PRs (explicit half first, auto half on top), not one combined PR. SETTLED (2026-06-02).** The EXPLICIT half (Task 76, `cmk lessons promote`) merged first (PR #99) because the AUTO half (Task 78) builds **on its plumbing**: Task 76 added the `trust`/`source` policy param to `promoteCandidatesToUserTier`, which is exactly the lever the auto half needs (promote an explicitly-stated universal rule at `trust:high` instead of queuing at medium). Both halves also edit `auto-persona.mjs`, so combining them = a self-inflicted merge conflict in the wedge's most sensitive file. Nothing reaches a USER until the `v0.2.0` tag (D-24), and that tag is gated on the end-to-end live re-test which needs BOTH halves — so sequential merges to `main` don't ship a half-wedge, they bank the reviewed foundation. **Task 76 EXPLICIT half: DONE. Task 78 AUTO half: the remaining D-30 cut-blocker.** (Two-pass review on #99 earned its keep — skill-review caught a Blocking: rich `--why/--how` bodies, the actual live-test case, silently failed to the queue; the single-line happy-path test had masked it.)
- **D-24 DECISION — Release cadence: ONE differentiator → live test → publish → next. Never shelve. SETTLED.** The user 2026-06-01, after the v0.1.1 + v0.2.0 self-tests: *"this is still a model of a car and not a car… but if i just shelf it until we 'finish' this will never go out."* So we do NOT wait for full completion to release. Each wow feature ships as its own version: build it → live-test it → publish the version → start the next. Incremental, always-shippable, never a big-bang. Resolves the build-vs-ship tension by doing both.
- **D-25 DECISION — The "worth giving to a friend" bar = everything the Simon Scrapes video described (video parity). SETTLED.** The user: *"until i have everything that the youtube video talked about, this is not good enough."* The bar is a **feel** bar, not a time bar — *"i will give this to my friend when it feels right and not because we are working on it a long time."* Concrete parity checklist = the video's 6 layers ([`docs/sources/simon-scrapes-master-claude-memory.md`](../sources/simon-scrapes-master-claude-memory.md)): L1 in-repo location ✅ · L2 granular archive ✅ · L3 bounded scratchpads ✅ · L4 memory-aware hooks ✅ · **L5 memsearch / semantic *Recall* ⚠️ (keyword FTS5 built; semantic Layer 5b NOT — Task 65)** · L6 cron self-curation ✅ · frozen-snapshot ✅. **The single true gap to video parity is L5b semantic recall** — the video's own headline ("recall is the most important function"). Everything else the video described is built.
- **D-26 DECISION — Why it doesn't excite yet (and the fix). SETTLED framing.** The user: *"when i give it to somebody i want him to be excited as me, and i am not excited at all."* Diagnosis: we built the **skeleton**, and skeletons don't demo. Excitement lives in the *wow moment* — the thing no other tool does, in front of you, unprompted. Three identified wows, sequenced by shippability: **(1) cross-project cold-open** — open Claude on a brand-new project and it already knows how you work (our *wedge*; nobody else does it; unlock = F2/Task 64, nearly the next task); **(2) recall with reasoning** — "what did we decide about X 3 weeks ago and why" → the answer + rationale (needs L5b/Task 65); **(3) currency / contradiction-catch** — kit notices "you said Postgres, now SQLite — which is current?" (needs temporal-validity §16.18, beyond-video). The roadmap delivers these *one at a time*, each felt before moving on — not a feature checklist.
- **D-27 NOTE — The niche wedge (why anyone picks us over more-mature tools). SETTLED positioning.** claude-mem = single-user local capture+recall; native Auto Memory = single-project, opaque, Anthropic-controlled; GBrain = enterprise entity-graph, heavy. **Nobody owns "your coding persona + project memory, committed to git, portable across machines, shareable with your team, that gets sharper the more you use it."** That is the kit's reason to exist. It only pays off once recall is good (L5b) AND the persona tier actually fills (F2) — which is exactly why those two are the front of the roadmap. See the cross-system competitive + lifecycle synthesis: [`docs/research/2026-06-01-memory-lifecycle-and-competitive-position.md`](../research/2026-06-01-memory-lifecycle-and-competitive-position.md).
- **D-30 CONCLUSION — v0.2.0 is NOT ready to cut: the WEDGE doesn't fill end-to-end (live-test-4 baseline, 2026-06-02). SETTLED.** The fresh live test proved the core loop (F1 rich capture ✓; auto-extract ✓ after the 25→90s timeout fix, finding #5) — but the **cross-project persona (the wedge, the whole reason the kit exists per D-27) does NOT reliably reach the user tier.** Both feed paths are broken: **(auto)** an *inferred* cross-project pref is queued to persona-review at medium confidence, not promoted (Stage-1 turn); **(explicit)** `cmk lessons promote` is a **stub** + `--tier U` unimplemented, AND the scaffolded CLAUDE.md + the 69.0 skill point the agent at that stub → it **hand-edited the user tier** (finding #7, Task 76). So "Task 64 fixed F2" was half-true: the section-*creation* fix is real, but the *promotion* feeding it doesn't fire. **v0.2.0 cut now requires: Task 76 (implement `cmk lessons promote` + `--tier U` via the safe path) + tuning the auto-promote so an EXPLICITLY-stated cross-project rule promotes at high confidence + fix the docs pointing at stubs.** The live test earned its keep: it found the one thing that would make a friend say "it doesn't actually learn how I work." Full findings #1–#7 in the live-test-4 baseline thread; tasks 64/67/76 + this conclusion.
- **D-29 DECISION — Source-level deep dive of every memory product → conclusions SETTLED (2026-06-01).** Cloned + read the actual source of Hermes / memsearch / gstack / claude-mem (+ antigravity-awesome-skills, Honcho, Hermes user-docs). Two research notes: [skills survey](../research/2026-06-01-how-products-implement-skills.md) + [source-level deep dive + divergence](../research/2026-06-01-deep-dive-product-memory-implementations.md). **Settled conclusions:**
  1. **Our foundations are sound or BETTER — do NOT change them.** Markdown source-of-truth (committable/auditable) ; consolidate-at-cap (Hermes hard-rejects — ours better) ; content-addressed IDs (Hermes substring — ours better) ; 3-tier project/user/local (everyone else single-store — ours is the wedge) ; committed-to-git (everyone else machine-local — the wedge). Nothing in the dive says change the core.
  2. **Storage/search: keep FTS5-first + optional vector.** claude-mem validates it verbatim ("SQLite is source of truth; vector OPTIONAL + opt-out-able"); Hermes `session_search` is **SQLite FULL-TEXT not vector**. **Reject Milvus** (memsearch's): `milvus-lite` is `sys_platform != 'win32'` — no lite path on Windows. **Layer-5 lean: `sqlite-vec` + ONNX `bge-m3`** (local/CPU/no-API/cross-platform), chunk-by-`##`-heading + clean-before-embed. → Task 65.0.
  3. **Universal safe-write pattern: route through a tool/CLI, NEVER hand-edit.** Hermes (memory_tool, scans + **refuses hand-edits** via drift detection), gstack /learn (binary), memsearch (Bash CLI). → validates Task 69.0 (skill uses `cmk remember`, not Edit/Write).
  4. **Nobody injects into the USER's CLAUDE.md** — every product delivers memory via skills+hooks; their CLAUDE.md (240–2800 lines) is their OWN dev doc. → Task 69.3 (slim our block).
  5. **Security gaps we lack (committed-to-git memory = supply-chain vector):** inject/output injection-defense + fencing (Hermes scans at write+inject+output) → **Task 70**; external-drift detect+refuse → **Task 71**; invisible-Unicode scan → **Task 70.4**.
  6. **Don't-adopt (wrong weight class / license):** memsearch+Milvus (Windows-hostile), Honcho (AGPL service + async workers — but its reasoning-first user-modeling is the v0.3+ direction for our persona tier), GBrain entity-graph.
  7. **Candidate features filed (post-v0.2):** numeric confidence 1-10 + `files[]` linking (gstack → §16.52/Task 55), pinning + inactivity-triggered no-cron curation (Hermes → Task 68/33-35), recall progressive disclosure (memsearch → Task 65), fork-full-agent auto-extract + agent-created-skills (Hermes → v0.3+).

### Roadmap (the cadence, concrete — also a milestone in [`tasks.md`](../../specs/tasks.md) "Road to 1.0")

- **0.2.0** — **GATED (binding, the user 2026-06-01: *"dont cut to 0.2.0 until we fix the problems and then do live test again, on a new project"*):** do NOT push the `v0.2.0` tag until ALL of — (1) F1 rich capture done (✅ Task 63), (2) F2 persona-fill done (Task 64), (3) a **fresh live test on a NEW project** confirms MEMORY.md/fact-files are rich AND HABITS.md fills. Only then cut + publish. Delivers **wow #1 (cross-project cold-open)** + kills the empty-MEMORY.md feel.
- **0.3.0** — L5b semantic recall (Task 65) → live test → publish. Delivers **wow #2 (recall with reasoning)** = **video parity reached**.
- **0.4.0+** — temporal validity / §16.18 (shape field + validity windows + `expires_at` enforcement) → **wow #3 (currency / contradiction-catch)** = past-the-video differentiator.
- **1.0** — video parity complete + it *feels right* to hand to a friend (the user's call, not a date).

### Issues / notes

- **ISSUE — `expires_at` is a defined provenance frontmatter field with ZERO enforcement (verified 2026-06-01).** No code under `packages/cli/src/` references `expires_at`/`expiresAt`. Facts that should age out don't. Folded into the §16.18 temporal-validity task (0.4.0+). Surfaced while answering the user's "what happens to memory after days/weeks/months/years" — which the two-track lifecycle (session-diary rolling-window + durable fact archive) answers for *volume* but not for *currency*.
- **D-28 DECISION — Deliver kit guidance as SKILLS, not a fat CLAUDE.md block; both install routes equivalent. SETTLED (the user 2026-06-01) → Task 69.** The user spotted the npm tarball ships `template/.claude/skills/memory-write/SKILL.md` but `cmk install` never scaffolds it. Archaeology (what/why/when): the memory-write skill is a *requirement* (FR-10/11) + planned-as-package (OS-2, gstack research D-16); the **original `install.sh` (initial commit) DID scaffold it** (`mkdir .claude/skills/memory-write` + copy); **Task 24 (#30)** rewrote `plugin/skills/memory-write/SKILL.md` but froze the `template/` copy (→ drift); **Task 49** (`cmk install`, node) replaced `install.sh` and **silently dropped skill-scaffolding** (installTier only does context tiers; writeKitHooks only writes `settings.json`). Net: skill lives only on the plugin route; npm route substitutes a **60-line memory-write PROCEDURE appended into the user's CLAUDE.md**. **Why that's wrong (Anthropic primary sources, verified 2026-06-01):** [skills doc](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/skills) — "create a skill when a section of CLAUDE.md has grown into a *procedure*… a skill's body loads only when used"; [memory doc](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/memory) — "target **under 200 lines**; longer reduces adherence; move procedures to a skill." Plus the user's `CLAUDE.md` is THEIRS (team-shared coding rules) — our block competes with their instructions for context + adherence = bad-citizen. **DECIDED:** (1) `cmk install` scaffolds skills into `<project>/.claude/skills/` (route-equivalence, travels with git); (2) ONE source per skill + a drift validator; (3) slim the CLAUDE.md loader block to FACTS + a pointer, move the procedure into the skill. Not a v0.2.0 *blocker* but a real packaging break; sequence relative to the cut is the user's call.
- **FIX/NOTE — retired 8 superseded scripts from the shipped package, AFTER reading each against its node impl (2026-06-01, live-test finding #2).** Removed `auto-extract-memory.sh`, `run-daily-distill.sh`, `run-weekly-curate.sh`, `register-crons.py`, `refresh-distill-timestamp.py`, `.claude/hooks/{pre-tool-memory,transcript-capture}.js`, `.claude/settings.json` — all the pre-Task-21/23/33/62 LLM-prompt/bash implementations, superseded by node (auto-extract.mjs / capture-turn.mjs / inject-context.mjs / daily-distill.mjs / register-crons.mjs / writeKitHooks). **Honesty correction:** the removal commit claimed "checked every one against its implementation" when only one had been read; the user pushed back ("you read every script and corresponding node?"), so each was then actually read. Verification result: all GOALS covered, mechanisms redesigned. **Also fixed the copy script to MIRROR (clear dest first) not accumulate** — a deleted template file was lingering in `packages/cli/template/` and still shipping (same staleness class as finding #3).
- **DELTA/CANDIDATE — node `weekly-curate` lost the old script's LLM-semantic MEMORY.md pruning.** `run-weekly-curate.sh` used an LLM to detect *resolved* Active Threads (cross-checking session logs) and remove/merge them; `weekly-curate.mjs` only archives old session files, so MEMORY.md scratchpad pruning is now purely **mechanical** (memory-write's 14-day staleness + exact-dup merge). A resolved-but-fresh thread lingers until it goes stale. This was a deliberate mechanical>LLM design choice (deterministic, no weekly LLM call), but it's a real capability difference and it qualifies the "memory stays clean over time" story (§8.0 two-track). **DECIDED (the user 2026-06-01) → Task 68, validate-before-build:** through the user-operability lens this is an ACCURACY issue, not hygiene — `MEMORY.md` is injected every session, so resolved-but-fresh threads make Claude plan/answer around stale state (+ eat injection budget). Plan: (68.1) BASELINE in the current v0.2.0 live test WITHOUT it — watch whether stale Active Threads actually mislead Claude in Sessions 2/3; (68.2) build the Haiku semantic-prune pass in `weekly-curate.mjs` (infra already there); (68.3) re-test the same scenario, ship only if the before/after shows a real delta, else document the negative result + park. Not a v0.2.0 blocker; evidence-first per D-24.
- **ISSUE — user-tier scratchpad writes are not lock-serialized (pre-existing class, widened slightly by Task 64).** `promoteCandidatesToUserTier` writes the shared `~/.claude-memory-kit/*.md` scratchpads via `memoryWrite` (and now `ensureSectionExists`) with no cross-process lock. Two auto-extracts firing inline (Task 61) from *different projects* against the same user-tier file could interleave (read-old → both append). The window is narrow (detached, short writes) and pre-dates Task 64 (memoryWrite already wrote the user tier unlocked); Task 64's `ensureSectionExists` adds one more unlocked write. **Deferred:** the real fix is a user-tier lock-discipline sweep (the project tier already has `.locks/`); track for v0.2.x alongside the broader lock audit. Surfaced by the Task 64 code-review (M4).
