## 2026-05-31 — documentation-governance restructure (3-zone spine + registry harness)

### Settled decisions (do NOT re-open without new evidence)

- **D-19 DECISION — Documentation has ONE current-state home: the spine (requirements/design/tasks). SETTLED.** Across the build, every "document this" demand spawned a new/different surface instead of reusing the existing one — ~7 overlapping state surfaces (conversation-log → build-log → BOOTSTRAP → RESUME-HERE → findings-roadmap → DECISION-LOG → PHASE-3-PLAN) plus a spec spine split since day one (requirements vs requirements-revisions-proposed, both born 2026-05-22). The model: three zones — **Spine** (requirements/design/tasks = the only current state, must be cold-restart-sufficient), **Product** docs (for kit users), **History** (everything else, append-only, never current state). Registry + routing rules: [`../DOCUMENTATION-MAP.md`](../DOCUMENTATION-MAP.md). **Why structural, not just a rule:** consistency must survive a context-compact without relying on Claude's memory — the very thing that fails at every compact. Enforced by `scripts/validate-doc-registry.mjs` (dev-only, not shipped to kit users): a new unregistered doc surface fails `npm test`.
- **D-20 PIVOT — "don't archive anything" → "archive the dead/orphaned; keep living history."** the user said don't archive earlier this session, then reversed: files "just hanging there" (retired / superseded / closed) move to `archive/` so the working tree foregrounds the spine. Living history (DECISION-LOG, build-log, ADRs, research, sources) stays in place; only dead surfaces archive (conversation-log, closed v0.1.x findings, the PHASE-3-PLAN husk, the merged proposed file). Old path preserved per the decision-trail rule.
- **D-21 DECISION — Anthropic native Auto Memory: coexist by default, one-command opt-in to disable. SETTLED (ADR-0011 accepted, closes a 9-day-open decision).** Claude Code's built-in Auto Memory (v2.1.59+, ON by default — verified live on the user's machine) writes the same `MEMORY.md + <type>_<slug>.md` shape, machine-local; with the kit installed both inject at session start (~25 KB native + ~13 KB kit snapshot) → **context bloat**. The kit is **additive, not enforcing**: default = coexist (don't touch `autoMemoryEnabled`); inform at install + via `cmk doctor`; offer `cmk disable-native-memory` (writes `autoMemoryEnabled:false` to the *committable* project `.claude/settings.json`, so it travels with `git clone`) as the opt-in. Original 2026-05-22 default-A (silently disable native) **rejected** by the user: *"i dont want to inforce our kit's memory… let the user choose."* Option B (redirect via `autoMemoryDirectory`) rejected — user-level-only (not committable) + Anthropic writes its own format, not the kit's schema. Implementation: Task 60.
- **D-22 DECISION — Cross-project promotion fires INLINE (at capture), not only weekly. SETTLED (Task 61, PR #90).** Auto-persona promoted cross-project doctrine to the user tier only in the weekly `weekly-curate` janitor — so "Claude knows how I work in every project" could lag up to 7 days, invisible in a short trial (re-opens the #2 self-test gap in practice). The user 2026-05-31: *"nobody is going to wait a week, not even a day, in an age where everyone wants everything and now, the tik-tok age."* Decision: **two layers, not four** — Layer 1 (new) detects cross-project doctrine at capture time and promotes it THIS turn, riding the auto-extract Haiku call that already fires every turn (no second LLM call, no extra cooldown); Layer 2 (kept) is the weekly `autoPersona` pass, demoted to a dedup/catch-miss janitor. A briefly-considered third option (additional daily + SessionSt­art-opportunistic passes) was **rejected** — the inline insight makes them redundant. Shared `promoteCandidatesToUserTier()` is the ONE promotion path for both layers.
- **FIX — inline persona promotion is failure-isolated from project extraction (Task 61 self-review).** The secondary cross-project promotion is wrapped in try/catch inside `runAutoExtract`: a bug in the promotion path records `persona.error` + a `persona_error` extract.log field but never aborts the primary job (project facts + extract.log). Auto-extract's standing contract — never let a secondary failure take down the primary.
- **D-23 DECISION — the kit's hooks run on Node alone, no bash, on every OS. SETTLED (Task 62, PR pending).** Surfaced by the user's *"i need the kit to run on windows/mac/linux like claude code itself"* + the dev box's default `bash.exe` (Docker Desktop's distro) having no `/bin/bash`. **Primary-source check (62.1):** Anthropic's plugins-reference says path vars are *"substituted inline … in hook commands"* → Claude Code expands `${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}` itself, so `node "${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/bin/x.mjs"` runs under any shell on any OS. Plugin `hooks.json` switched `bash "…/cmk-x"` → `node "…/cmk-x.mjs"`; the 6 extensionless bash wrappers + legacy `auto-extract-memory.sh` retired; `cmk-version-check` ported to a node `.mjs` stub. The npm route (Route A) was already node-only; this aligns Route B. Old plan preserved in design §5.1 per the decision-trail rule. **Proof:** full suite **1275→1276 green with NO Git Bash on PATH** (was ~35 failing on the broken-bash machine).
- **FIX — `cmk doctor` fresh-install severities (live-test finding, 2026-05-31).** The user installed v0.2.0 in a fresh project; `cmk doctor` reported **"3 fail"** (HC-3 distill, HC-4 transcripts, HC-6 cron) — alarming first impression for the friend, and wrong severity: those are "nothing's happened yet" (HC-3/4 before any session) or "optional" (HC-6 cron, which has a lazy-on-read fallback the README already calls optional). Now they SKIP on a fresh project (a clean install reads `6 pass · 0 fail · 3 skip`, exit 0); they FAIL only on a genuine problem (stale distill; transcripts that existed but stopped). The doctor's own FAIL was inconsistent with our own README — caught only by a real fresh install, not the test suite (which seeded state). **Why it matters:** first-impression UX for a non-builder; "looks broken" vs "looks healthy" on minute one.
- **FIX — release-verification test hardcoded the version → broke on every bump (caught at the v0.2.0 cut).** `release-verification.test.js` asserted `package.json === '0.1.2'` + CHANGELOG `[0.1.2]` literally, so `npm run release -- minor` (→ 0.2.0) turned `main` red. Rewritten to read the version dynamically and assert **package.json ↔ latest-CHANGELOG-heading lockstep** — the invariant `npm run release` actually guarantees — so it self-maintains across releases instead of needing a manual edit each time. A real gap in the release mechanic, surfaced by actually cutting.
- **FINDINGS + DECISION — v0.2.0 fresh live-test (2026-05-31). DO NOT cut v0.2.0 until F1+F2 fixed.** Full write-up + Task 63/64 specs in [`docs/journey/v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md`](v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md). **F1 (headline) — capture-richness REGRESSION:** v0.1.1 agent hand-wrote rich granular fact files (Why/How/links, richer than native Auto Memory) but leaked the username path + wrong schema; v0.1.2 fixed that by routing ALL captures through `cmk remember` (sanitized) — which writes only a TERSE one-line MEMORY.md bullet + told the scaffolded CLAUDE.md to never hand-write fact files. So v0.2.0 captures one-liners where v0.1.1 captured doctrine files → "MEMORY.md feels empty." Fix (Task 63): rich `cmk remember`/`cmk fact` → granular fact file via `writeFact()` THROUGH the sanitizer (richness + safety) + CLAUDE.md guidance to capture richly. **F2 — cross-project promotion broken:** auto-extract emitted a `confidence:high` PERSONA CANDIDATE targeting `HABITS.md § Architecture Preferences` (not a fixed section) → schema error → queued, not promoted → HABITS.md empty (same symptom Tasks 45+61 meant to fix). Fix (Task 64): create-section-if-missing in `promoteCandidatesToUserTier`. **NOTE — native Auto Memory is NOT the benchmark** (the user: the kit exists to beat native; v0.1.1 did). Unit tests missed both (hard-coded valid sections + confidence=high + never compared capture richness).
- **FIX/NOTE — D-21 (ADR-0011) shipped: native-auto-memory coexistence (Task 60, PR #93).** `cmk disable-native-memory` / `enable-native-memory` write the committable `autoMemoryEnabled` flag; `cmk install` surfaces the coexistence + opt-out; doctor HC-8 enhanced to read the setting + flag the both-layers bloat. Default stays coexist (non-enforcement), exactly as D-21 settled. **v0.2.0 feature scope is now COMPLETE** — next is the fresh live test (release gate) then the v0.2.0 cut.
- **NOTE — Layer-5b semantic-search backend should be RECONSIDERED (memsearch+Milvus likely the wrong weight class). Open; revisit at Layer-5b build (post-v0.2).** Surfaced 2026-05-31 from the user's qmd/Chroma question + his personal-wiki search decision record (`C:/Projects/personal-wiki/docs/search-architecture.md`). Two independent evidence sources (the wiki, which has the same single-user-local-markdown profile + rejected Milvus as overkill; AND our own research base, where the markdown-memory consensus is SQLite FTS5 with light-embedded `sqlite-vec`/`sqlite-memory` vs heavy-server Milvus) say the kit's original `memsearch+Milvus` pick is the heaviest option — and it collides with the node-only/no-server ethos we just hardened in Task 62 (D-23). Shortlist lightest→heaviest: **sqlite-vec** (in our existing SQLite DB — best fit) < **qmd** (Node/MCP, file-granularity caveat) < **Chroma** (Python embedded; we need *less* than the wiki since FTS5 already filters) < **memsearch+Milvus**. Anthropic has NO embeddings API (can't use Claude for vectors). Full write-up + bake-off design (recall@5 over memory-shaped facts + synonym queries) in design §9.3.1. The `semanticBackend` DI seam + `reciprocalRankFusion` are already built, so any winner drops in. **Decision: capture + continue v0.2.0 (the user chose this); do the bake-off + pick post-friend-validation.** Backlog, not a v0.2.0 task.
- **FIX — low/medium-confidence persona candidates are now durable, not response-only (Task 45 follow-up, PR #92).** The user 2026-05-31: *"response object can get lost — i dont like it."* `promoteCandidatesToUserTier` now writes queued candidates to `<userDir>/queues/persona-review.md` via `appendPersonaReviewQueue` (deduped by canonical id so repeated passes don't pile up), and surfaces `reviewQueuePath` on the result. Both the weekly `autoPersona` path and the Task-61 inline path inherit it. Plus a new `cmk persona generate` command (`runPersonaGenerate` → `autoPersona`) — a manual trigger for the same pipeline weekly-curate runs automatically, useful as a deterministic hook for the fresh-session live test. **Known limitation (tracked follow-up):** `persona-review.md` is now durable + visible but has **no consumer yet** — `cmk queue review` drains the *project* `context/queues/review.md`, and Phase-2 `autoDrainQueues` doesn't cover the user-tier persona queue. Dedup keeps it bounded; a drain/`cmk persona review` consumer is a v0.2.x follow-up. The literal ask ("don't lose them") is met — they're durable and inspectable.
- **NOTE — recurring flake class: absolute wall-clock assertions on load-variable measurements.** Two instances now, both surfaced in stress gates under test-harness concurrency: Task 61's `captureTurn() elapsed < 250ms` (spiked to 371ms) and Task 62's `cmk doctor duration_ms < 5000` (spiked to 5028ms). Both were tight absolute thresholds on inherently variable measurements (spawn return time / subprocess-bound runtime). Fix pattern: assert a *relative* property where possible (captureTurn — lock absent at return), else a *non-pathological ceiling* with documented headroom (doctor — 10s regression guard, production NFR still 5s). The other `elapsed < 500` in-process assertions across the suite have ~10× margin and have not flaked, so they were left as-is — the class to watch is tight-margin (≤~1.5×) or subprocess-bound timing bounds. A future sweep could add a lint, but it's not worth it for two instances.
- **NOTE — observe-edit's bash detach pattern was a bash-specific workaround, dropped in the node port.** The old `cmk-observe-edit` bash wrapper buffered stdin → detached a node child → echoed `{"continue": true}` immediately, so the bash parent returned fast. `cmk-observe-edit.mjs` now owns the envelope itself: emit `{"continue": true}` first, then run the append synchronously-then-exit. `async: true` already makes the hook non-blocking to Claude Code, so the detach added nothing; the append is tiny. Simpler + correct, verified by the existing detach test (loose `parentMs < 30000` + poll-for-file, both satisfied).

### Issues / fixes

- **FIX — main's `npm test` had been red since 529769b.** `validate-references` failed on PHASE-3-PLAN.md (a rogue plan surface created outside the spine) citing `Task 57-59` + `FR-31` that never existed; the docs-only commit skipped the suite. Folding the plan into the spine (Tasks 57-59 proposed + FR-31 reserved in requirements) + demoting the husk to a pointer greened it. Live proof of D-19's problem.
- **FIX — day-one requirements split healed.** FR-28/29/30, NFR-9, T7/T8, US-14/15, OS-9..13, OQ-8 merged from `requirements-revisions-proposed.md` into `requirements.md` (sole authoritative home); proposed file banner → SUPERSEDED. Also fixed dangling US-13 ref `FR-32`→`FR-25`.
- **NOTE — the dev machine's default `bash.exe` has no `/bin/bash` (2026-05-31; corrected diagnosis).** Initially mis-diagnosed as "WSL corruption"; the real cause: the ONLY WSL distro installed is `docker-desktop` (Docker Desktop's internal utility VM), and it's the *default*, so `C:\Windows\System32\bash.exe` launches it — a stripped LinuxKit image with no `/bin/bash` → every `spawnSync('bash', …)` fails with `execvpe /bin/bash failed 2` (errno 2 = file-not-found). `wsl --shutdown` does NOT fix it (the binary is genuinely absent, not a stuck VM). Git Bash (`C:\Program Files\Git\bin`) is the only real bash on the box; prepending it to PATH greens the suite (1276/1276). CI is Linux bash, unaffected; the shipping **npm route is node-only and CI's `windows-2022 — install + doctor` passes**, so this is purely a dev-test-harness artifact. **The durable fix is Task 62: convert the hook-bin tests to invoke the node `.mjs` bins directly (`process.execPath`, not ambient `bash`)** — then the suite has zero bash dependency on any machine. Until then: run with Git Bash on PATH.

## 2026-05-30 — v0.1.2 shipped; v0.2 launched; Task 45 started

### Settled decisions (do NOT re-open without new evidence)

- **D-1 DECISION — Build v0.2 (Phases 1→3). SETTLED.** The kit's core vision is "Claude remembers its own positions and stays consistent" (the FastAPI scenario: *"2 days ago you said X was a mistake; now the opposite"*). The user: *"this was an integral part of the kit … if it's somewhere in the future I want to be there in that future, and now."* Phases: 1 Foundation (done) → 2 Automatic memory → 3 the consistency engine. Source: [`v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md`](v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md) §"COMMITTED ROADMAP". **This was re-opened in error on 2026-05-30 and re-confirmed; do not re-litigate.**

- **D-2 DECISION — v0.1.x backlog folds into v0.2; NO v0.1.3 patch-sweep. SETTLED.** The ~40 design §16 candidates are overwhelmingly trigger-gated ("ship when a real need/bug surfaces"); the non-trigger-gated ones (Task 45 auto-persona, 16.18 temporal, Task 55 patterns) ARE the v0.2 feature set. A patch-sweep would manufacture a release for items with no demand. **Let real usage (the friend + the user's own use) be the trigger** for any v0.1.3. Implication: stop asking "patch-sweep first or fold?" — it's folded.

- **D-3 DECISION — Task 45 (auto-persona) is the friend-handoff gate; re-homed v0.1.1 → v0.2 Phase 2. SETTLED.** The self-test (finding #2 🟡) empirically reproduced design §16.16's predicted failure: cross-project doctrine (venv-3.13, layered-backend) was captured but filed PROJECT-tier; the USER tier stayed empty → cross-project value prop collapses. The user: *"we have to have task 45 and i need v0.2 … i dont think i can send this to my friend without it."* The friend gets the same empty user tier until Task 45 ships.

- **D-4 PIVOT — Task 45 posture: manual accept/reject gate → OPTIMISTIC AUTO-PROMOTE. SETTLED.** Original design (tasks.md 45.2 `cmk persona accept/reject` + 45.3 `--auto` opt-in **default-off**) is a manual-confirmation shape. Superseded for v0.2 by the user's *"i dont want to do anything, i want it to be automatic"* + his choice **Optimistic**. New posture (tasks.md 45.6): high-confidence cross-project doctrine auto-promotes to the user tier at `trust:medium` with NO manual step; low/medium-confidence routes to the auto-drained review queue; auto-supersede on contradiction (reuse Task 25). **Old manual design preserved** in tasks.md 45.1-45.5 as decision-trail + fallback if optimistic proves too aggressive.

- **D-5 DECISION — Auto-persona uses Design B (piggyback the weekly-curate consolidator). SETTLED.** It already runs the CompressorBackend (Haiku) with no extra API call; extend its prompt with a "Step 3: persona candidates" classification. Source: claude-remember code-dive + tasks.md 45.1. Fallback: Design A (standalone `cmk persona generate` pipeline) if the consolidator prompt budget can't absorb it.

- **D-6 DECISION — auto-drain the review/conflict queues (no manual `cmk queue *` in the common case). SETTLED.** The user 2026-05-30: *"i dont want to do anything, automatic."* Posture: Optimistic — auto-promote; auto-supersede on contradiction (reuse Task 25 conflict detection); the daily-distill (Task 33) + weekly-curate (Task 34) passes drain the queues. Manual `cmk queue *` stays available, just not required.

- **D-7 DECISION — Code-quality CI = "Both" (coverage now + SonarCloud). SETTLED, SHIPPED.** Vitest v8 coverage gate (70% ratchet, lcov) PR #75 + SonarCloud CI-based scan PR #78. SonarCloud **Automatic Analysis disabled** (mutually exclusive with the CI-based scan). Task 54 flipped to [x].

### Task 45 implementation design choices (2026-05-30, first increment)

- **D-8 DECISION — Classification contract.** The backend (Haiku Step-3) emits one line per cross-project candidate: `PERSONA CANDIDATE | target=<FILE> | section=<SECTION> | confidence=<high|medium|low> | <one-line restatement>`. Module parses via `CANDIDATE_RE`. Project-specific facts are NOT surfaced. Rationale: matches claude-remember's `IDENTITY CANDIDATE:` pattern, extended with routing + confidence.
- **D-9 DECISION — Routing targets + sections.** USER.md (About/Preferences/Working Style), HABITS.md (Iteration Cadence/Destructive Operations/Communication Style), LESSONS.md (Tooling Lessons/Process Lessons/Anti-patterns). A classifier-named target outside this allow-list is dropped defensively (never trust Haiku routing blindly).
- **D-10 DECISION — Provenance of promoted bullets.** `write: 'compressor'` (reused the existing valid enum — a Haiku-backend synthesis IS a compressor op; avoids a provenance-schema change this increment), `trust: 'medium'` (system-derived, not user-attested), `source: 'persona-synthesis'`, `source_line: 1`, `sha1` = sha1 of the bullet text. **Open:** a distinct `write: 'auto-persona'` enum value would be more audit-precise — deferred (schema change). Logged as I-2.
- **D-11 DECISION — Source corpus = project-tier (P) facts only.** Assembled via `listObservationSources({projectRoot, userDir})` filtered to `tier==='P'`. `userDir` is passed through PURELY to keep U-tier resolution sandbox-scoped — **never walk the real `~/.claude-memory-kit`** (design §16.36 hazard). U-tier is the DESTINATION, not a source.
- **D-12 DECISION — Confidence gate is not a manual gate.** `high` → auto-promote now; `medium`/`low` → collected in `queued[]` (response only this increment; the queue-FILE write + auto-drain lands in the next increment with its own test).

### Task 45 implementation — increment 2 (2026-05-30)

- **D-13 DECISION — auto-persona promotes THROUGH `memoryWrite`, not raw `appendScratchpadBullet`.** Delegating inherits home-path sanitization (privacy — finding #1 class; the first-increment raw-append path SKIPPED this, a latent privacy gap now closed), Poison_Guard, dedup, cap/consolidation, and audit — all already tested. auto-persona pre-calls `detectConflicts` only to pick the verb, then: **supersede** (new medium ≥ existing) → `memoryWrite` **replace** (no duplicate; closes finding #3 Gap B) + `PERSONA_SUPERSEDED` audit; **queue** (new medium < existing trust:high hand-curated) → `memoryWrite` **add** routes to `queues/conflicts.md`, never overwrites (the 45.4 invariant); **clean** → promote at trust:medium + `PERSONA_PROMOTED` audit.
- **NOTE — `memoryWrite({action:'replace'})` returns `{action:'replaced', oldId, newId, path}`** — NOT a top-level `id` (it's `newId`). Cost a failed audit-write before correction. Recorded so future callers use `newId`.

### Task 45 implementation — increment 3 (2026-05-30) — FEATURE IS LIVE

- **D-14 DECISION — dedicated classification call over project FACTS (relaxes Design B's "zero additional API call").** auto-persona runs its OWN `backend.compress` over the granular fact archive, NOT a piggybacked "Step 3" appended to the weekly-curate consolidator's *session-summary* prompt. Reason: the source corpora differ (§16.16 synthesizes persona from durable facts, not raw session summaries), separation is cleaner, and one extra Haiku call at WEEKLY cadence under the shared cooldown is negligible cost. Still triggered BY weekly-curate (Design B's integration point) — just not zero-additional-call. Decision-trail: Design B's zero-call promise is the relaxed item; the trigger-from-the-weekly-cycle part stands.
- **D-15 DECISION — weekly-curate hook placement + cooldown composition.** `weeklyCurate` gains optional `userDir`; when present it calls `autoPersona({…, cooldownMs:0})` right after its own cooldown gate passes — so persona runs on BOTH the `curated` and `no-old-files` weekly paths (persona reads facts, independent of session-file age). `cooldownMs:0` because both Haiku calls belong to ONE weekly cycle (§8.7.2, mirrors the inline `dailyDistill` call). `cmk-weekly-curate` bin passes `userDir=~/.claude-memory-kit` so it fires in production; absent `userDir`, curate runs project-only (backward-compatible — existing tests/callers unaffected). I-3 (cooldown gate) RESOLVED here.
- **STATE: the friend-handoff gate (finding #2) is now structurally closed end-to-end** — the weekly maintenance pass auto-promotes cross-project doctrine into the user tier with no manual step. Remaining for the Task 45 PR: `cmk persona generate` manual wrapper, low/medium-confidence → review-queue FILE write (currently response-only `queued[]`), full-suite + stress gate, self-review + code-review-excellence, open PR.

### External evaluation — gstack (2026-05-30)

- **D-16 DECISION — evaluated `garrytan/gstack` (the user asked "would any of these skills help?"); NOT adopting, captured as research + 2 borrowed techniques.** Read README + 4/23 SKILL.md (`context-save`/`context-restore`/`learn`/`review`). Findings: gstack is Garry Tan's **skill layer over GBrain** (the store the kit already studied — §16.19/§16.17). **`/learn`** (`{type,key,insight,confidence 1–10}` JSONL, append-only latest-wins, contradiction-prune) is an **independent second-source precedent** for the kit's supersede/conflict model + Task 55 / §16.52's numeric-confidence idea (was single-sourced to ECC). **`context-save`/`restore`** are a manual, user-home, non-committed analog of the kit's session-handoff + this decision log (the T2/T4 shape the kit improves on). **`/review`** gives two borrowable techniques. **Not adopting the code/skills** — coupled to gstack binaries + `~/.gstack` storage; wholesale = the tool-bloat rejected for Task 53's ECC repo (per the adoption-verification rule, evidence-based not feel). **Actions:** SOURCES.md entry + research note `2026-05-30-gstack-skill-layer.md`; fold the confidence-1–10 + contradiction-prune precedent into §16.52/Task 55 when it opens; apply `/review`'s **pre-emit-verification-gate** (cite-the-line-or-suppress) + **plan-completion-audit** (DONE/PARTIAL/NOT-DONE/CHANGED/UNVERIFIABLE vs diff) to the Task 45 review pass.

### Process — README/CHANGELOG discipline (2026-05-30)

- **D-17 DECISION — user-facing capabilities get documented in the README + CHANGELOG in the SAME PR that ships them (binding rule added to CLAUDE.md).** The user: *"if we add new feature and capabilities to our kit we should put it in readme… features in readme as an explanation what the kit can do."* Gap it closes: the workflow forced `tasks.md` + journey-log updates on a feature PR but NOT a README update (README was a one-time Task 41), so capabilities could ship to npm with a stale landing page. Live drift it surfaced: v0.1.2 shipped `cmk remember` + search + MCP but the README "What it does" still only named the old `memory-write` skill. **Actions:** added the binding rule to CLAUDE.md Workflow + two source-of-truth rows (README capability surface; CHANGELOG release record); added a `## [Unreleased]` (v0.2) section to CHANGELOG as the home for accruing entries; trued up BOTH READMEs' "What it does" with the already-shipped capabilities. **Timing nuance (honesty half):** README describes the *published/shipping* version — document a feature as it merges, never write up an unshipped feature as if live (lazy-framing rule applied to docs). **Applies to Task 45:** its PR will add the auto-persona capability to "What it does" + a CLI entry + the CHANGELOG `[Unreleased]` line.
- **D-18 DECISION — release/changelog = file-driven generator; not per-PR fragments, not pure hand-writing.** Per-PR changelog-fragment tooling exists only to stop many parallel contributors conflicting on one shared file — not the kit's problem (1–2 contributors, sequential PRs). But formatting + version-bump + GitHub-release is toil worth automating regardless (the v0.1.2 release-verification failure was version drift). **Built:** `scripts/lib/changelog-release.mjs` (`assembleRelease` + `extractReleaseNotes`, pure, 9 tests), `scripts/release.mjs` (`npm run release -- <patch|minor|major|X.Y.Z>`), `scripts/print-release-notes.mjs`, and a `publish.yml` step that creates the GitHub Release from the CHANGELOG section on tag push. One file (`CHANGELOG.md [Unreleased]`) → CHANGELOG + version + npm + GitHub Release. **Deferred (trigger):** per-PR `.changes/*.yaml` fragment files if the single `[Unreleased]` section ever starts conflicting — same generator. Rule: CLAUDE.md "Cutting a release — use the mechanic."

### Issues / bugs / fixes

- **B-1 BUG + FIX (shared module; surfaced by Task 45 increment 2; fix on branch `task-45-auto-persona`, ships with the Task 45 PR).** `conflict-queue.mjs` `PROVENANCE_RE` was `^<!--`-anchored, but `writeBullet`/`appendScratchpadBullet` write provenance comments **indented** (`  <!-- … trust: high … -->`). So `collectExistingBullets` failed to parse trust and **defaulted EVERY existing bullet to `medium`** — meaning a new medium fact would wrongly **`supersede` an existing trust:high hand-curated bullet** for ANY caller (memory-write's own conflict detection included), silently violating high-trust-wins. **FIX:** `PROVENANCE_RE = /^\s*<!--…/` + a regression test pinning the production (indented) format. **Why it never surfaced in tests:** `cli-conflict-queue.test.js`'s `seedScratchpad` wrote NON-indented comments — fixture-diverges-from-production, same family as PR #22's mock-only-tests-miss-spawn-breakage.
- **I-1 ISSUE (meta, root cause of today's misstep)** — assistant re-opened SETTLED decision D-1/D-2 from faded context instead of reading the durable record. **FIX:** this decision log + the new CLAUDE.md "Decision-log discipline (binding)" rule (read before re-opening; append after deciding). Also reinforced the existing "don't summarize from memory when primary source is available" verification rule — it applies to *our own prior decisions*, not just external sources.
- **I-2 RESOLVED (Task 45 increment 2)** — persona audit entries now use `paths: { after: res.path }` (object), matching the audit-log schema, not the first increment's array shape.
- **I-3 ISSUE (open, Task 45)** — cooldown gate (120s Haiku, shared marker) not yet honored in `autoPersona`. Fine for the standalone first increment (tests don't set markers); MUST be added with the `cmk persona generate` wrapper + the Design-B weekly-curate hook (which already gates cooldown at the consolidator level). Logged so it isn't forgotten.
